The two are tightly coupled: typed enforcement at runtime (G14) requires the trait-level declaration, and the amendment exists solely because tau-runtime needs it. Bundling avoids splitting one motivated change across two ADRs; future tau-ports amendments motivated by their own sub-projects will get their own ADRs (no promiscuous bundling).</p> <p>Relevant Constitution constraints: G6 (tau is a runtime, not a framework), G7 (package manager is the only way to add extensions), G9 (observable by default), G10 (solo + orchestration paths; sub-project 4 is solo only), G11 (typed addressed messages), G14 (capabilities declared at install AND enforced at runtime), G16 (overhead bounds), NG6 (no persistent agent memory), NG9 (tau does not redact for the caller), NG12 (runtime not framework), QG2 (<code>thiserror</code> everywhere), QG3 (panics are bugs), QG5 (parsers earn proptests), QG18 (ADRs for public API + trait changes).</p> <p>ADR-0006 also notes a small set of mid-implementation <strong>additive constructors</strong> added during the run-loop work: <code>Message::new</code>, <code>AgentStatus::failed</code>, <code>CompletionRequest::new</code>, <code>LlmProviderMessage::{user, assistant, tool_result}</code>, <code>ToolUse::new</code>, <code>TokenUsage::new</code>, <code>SessionContext::new</code>, <code>PackageId::new</code>. They were forced by <code>#[non_exhaustive]</code> on those types blocking struct-literal construction across crates and were registered in the same commit as Task 10 (the run loop). All are additive (no existing API broken). The kernel decisions in this ADR depend on those constructors existing.</p> <h2 id="decision-6"><a class="header" href="#decision-6">Decision</a></h2> <h3 id="1-pure-kernel-skeleton-scope"><a class="header" href="#1-pure-kernel-skeleton-scope">1. Pure kernel skeleton scope</a></h3> <p>Sub-project 4 ships a kernel testable in isolation against tau-ports' mock plugins (<code>MockLlmBackend</code>, <code>MockTool</code>, <code>MockStorage</code> under the <code>test-fixtures</code> cargo feature). Real plugin packages — concrete Anthropic / OpenAI backends, real filesystem / shell / HTTP tools — land in sub-project 5 (tau-cli) and beyond. tau-runtime accepts pre-constructed plugin instances via the builder; it does not load packages from disk at v0.1 (no cdylib, no dlopen). The integration tests at <code>crates/tau-runtime/tests/run_*.rs</code> exercise the loop end-to-end against mocks; sub-project 5 wires the same kernel to real plugins.</p> <p>Trigger to revisit: when sub-project 5+ lands real plugins and the kernel needs to surface a serve-mode protocol on top of the embeddable Rust API.</p> <h3 id="2-async-public-api"><a class="header" href="#2-async-public-api">2. Async public API</a></h3> <p><code>Runtime::run</code> and <code>Runtime::run_default</code> are <code>async fn</code>. tau-ports' <code>LlmBackend::complete</code>, <code>Tool::invoke</code>, <code>Storage::*</code> etc. are native <code>async fn in trait</code> (per ADR-0003 §1). Wrapping them in a sync facade would require <code>tokio::runtime::Handle::current().block_on(...)</code> at every call site, which fails outside a running runtime and pushes complexity onto the kernel for no value. The kernel's library code is async-runtime agnostic — bare <code>async fn</code> and <code>.await</code> only, no <code>tokio::sync</code>, <code>tokio::spawn</code>, or <code>tokio::select!</code>. <code>tokio</code> is a dev-dependency only; callers (typically tau-cli) bring the runtime at the binary level.</p> <p>Trigger to revisit: a concrete use case where async forces unwanted complexity on a small embedding.</p> <h3 id="3-builder-pattern-construction-with-name-keyed-registries"><a class="header" href="#3-builder-pattern-construction-with-name-keyed-registries">3. Builder pattern construction with name-keyed registries</a></h3> <p><code>Runtime::builder().with_*(...)*.build()</code> is the public construction path. The builder accumulates plugin instances under their <code>name()</code>; this enables dispatch by name in messages (<code>Address::Tool(String)</code>) and allows build-time detection of name collisions within a kind. The builder methods are <code>with_llm_backend(impl LlmBackend + 'static)</code>, <code>with_tool(impl Tool<Session = ()> + 'static)</code>, and <code>with_storage(impl Storage + 'static)</code> — generics, NOT <code>Box<dyn Trait></code> — because the underlying plugin traits are not dyn-compatible (native <code>async fn in trait</code> is not object-safe in Rust 1.93).</p> <p>The builder boxes through internal wrapper traits (<code>DynLlmBackend</code>, <code>DynTool</code>, <code>DynStorage</code>) with blanket impls for <code>T: Trait + 'static</code>. This is the standard "box once at the dyn-cast boundary" pattern. The wrapper types are <code>pub</code> so future tau-runtime helpers can refer to them, but they are <strong>not part of the public API contract</strong> — they are an implementation detail and will be removed when tau-ports gains a <code>trait_variant</code>-generated dyn-compatible variant.</p> <p>Build-time validations: at least one LLM backend must be registered; no name collisions within a kind (two LLM backends, two tools, or two storages with the same <code>name()</code>). Both produce typed <code>BuildError</code> variants (<code>NoLlmBackend</code>, <code>NameCollision { kind, name }</code>).</p> <p>Trigger to revisit: when tau-ports gains native dyn-compatibility (the dyn-shim becomes deletable boilerplate).</p> <h3 id="4-session---v01-tool-limitation"><a class="header" href="#4-session---v01-tool-limitation">4. <code>Session = ()</code> v0.1 tool limitation</a></h3> <p>The kernel's tool registry stores <code>Arc<DynTool></code> where the underlying trait is <code>Tool<Session = ()></code>. Stateless tools (the common case) work directly; stateful tools must wrap themselves in <code>tau_ports::StatelessAdapter</code> or wait for a future <code>DynTool</code> extension once erased associated types stabilize on stable Rust. Accepting arbitrary <code>Session</code> types from external plugins would require erased-associated-type machinery beyond v0.1's scope.</p> <p>Trigger to revisit: the first stateful tool that genuinely cannot be expressed via <code>StatelessAdapter</code> — e.g., a long-lived database connection that must persist across <code>invoke</code> calls within one agent run.</p> <h3 id="5-multi-turn-batch-loop-not-streaming"><a class="header" href="#5-multi-turn-batch-loop-not-streaming">5. Multi-turn batch loop, not streaming</a></h3> <p><code>LlmBackend::complete</code> (batch) is the v0.1 surface used by the agent loop. <code>LlmBackend::stream</code> exists in tau-ports (per ADR-0003 §2) but tau-runtime does not invoke it at v0.1. Streaming integration is purely additive (a new <code>Runtime::run_streaming</code> method) and does not break the batch surface when it lands.</p> <p>Trigger to revisit: a streaming-UX-driven use case (TUI rendering tokens as they arrive, latency-sensitive interactive flows).</p> <h3 id="6-caller-supplied-manifest"><a class="header" href="#6-caller-supplied-manifest">6. Caller-supplied manifest</a></h3> <p><code>Runtime::run(agent_def, package_manifest, initial_message, options)</code> takes the package manifest as a parameter rather than fetching it itself. tau-runtime has no <code>tau-pkg</code> dependency. Callers (tau-cli, in-process embedders) call <code>tau_pkg::read_manifest</code> and feed the result in. The dependency direction stays crisp: tau-runtime → tau-domain, tau-ports; tau-cli → tau-runtime, tau-pkg. This keeps tau-runtime embeddable in environments where tau-pkg is absent (e.g., a server consuming pre-fetched manifests over the wire).</p> <p>Trigger to revisit: an embedded use case where a caller cannot reasonably fetch the manifest itself.</p> <h3 id="7-typed-capability-enforcement-additive-amendment-to-adr-0003"><a class="header" href="#7-typed-capability-enforcement-additive-amendment-to-adr-0003">7. Typed capability enforcement (additive amendment to ADR-0003)</a></h3> <p>G14 demands runtime enforcement of declared capabilities. The kernel checks every tool invocation against the agent's package manifest: for each capability the tool declares as required, at least one capability in the manifest must satisfy it. Tools must therefore declare what they require — and the only place to declare it is on the <code>Tool</code> trait itself.</p> <p>The additive amendment to ADR-0003: a new method on <code>Tool</code> with a default,</p> <pre><pre class="playground"><code class="language-rust"><span class="boring">#![allow(unused)] </span><span class="boring">fn main() { </span>fn capabilities(&self) -> &[tau_domain::Capability] { &[] } <span class="boring">}</span></code></pre></pre> <p>is the minimum disturbance to the trait. Every existing impl (including the four mocks under <code>tau_ports::fixtures</code>) compiles unchanged; new tools opt in by overriding the method. Backwards-compatible.</p> <p>The kernel implements the satisfies-relation in <code>crates/tau-runtime/src/capability.rs</code>: variant-by-variant matching (<code>Filesystem</code> only satisfies <code>Filesystem</code>, <code>Network</code> only satisfies <code>Network</code>, etc.) with glob support for filesystem paths and HTTP hosts via the inline <code>glob_matches</code> helper (no <code>globset</code> dependency at v0.1). Mismatch produces <code>RunOutcome::Failed { status: AgentStatus::Failed { kind: FailureKind::PolicyDenied, .. } }</code> — never an <code>Err</code>. The denial detail (agent id, package id, tool name, required kind, required detail) is preserved in the failure message via the <code>CapabilityDenial</code> helper type.</p> <p>The amendment to ADR-0003 is <strong>bundled</strong> with this ADR because the trait change is solely motivated by tau-runtime's needs and would not exist without it. Future tau-ports trait changes motivated by their own sub-projects will get their own ADRs.</p> <p>Trigger to revisit: a richer satisfies-relation (semver bounds on hosts, time-windowed capabilities, regex matchers, etc.).</p> <h3 id="8-hard-fail-on-capability-denial"><a class="header" href="#8-hard-fail-on-capability-denial">8. Hard-fail on capability denial</a></h3> <p>A capability mismatch halts the agent immediately with <code>AgentStatus::Failed { kind: FailureKind::PolicyDenied, .. }</code>. v0.1 has no soft-fail mode (continue without the tool, surface a denial message back to the LLM, retry with a different tool). Soft-fail is deferred to Phase-1+ via an additive <code>RunOptions { soft_fail_capability_denial: bool, .. }</code> or similar option.</p> <p>Trigger to revisit: a workflow where partial denials are recoverable (agent retries with a different tool, or the run continues with the tool result skipped and a denial message in the conversation).</p> <h3 id="9-outcome--error-dichotomy"><a class="header" href="#9-outcome--error-dichotomy">9. Outcome / Error dichotomy</a></h3> <p>The split:</p> <ul> <li><code>Ok(RunOutcome::Completed { .. })</code> — agent ran to a terminal text response.</li> <li><code>Ok(RunOutcome::Failed { status, .. })</code> — agent ran but couldn't accomplish the task within the rules: <code>PolicyDenied</code> (capability mismatch), <code>OutOfResources</code> (<code>max_turns</code> reached). The agent's run itself was well-formed.</li> <li><code>Err(RuntimeError)</code> — kernel-level failures: a plugin returned an error, dispatch lookup failed, plugin output violates the contract. The kernel itself can't continue.</li> </ul> <p>The split makes pattern-matching at the call site clean: callers distinguish "agent done, now decide what to do with the outcome" from "kernel broken, log + retry". Forcing kernel-level errors into <code>RunOutcome::Failed</code> would conflate the two.</p> <p>The <code>RuntimeError</code> taxonomy: <code>LlmBackendNotRegistered { agent_id, backend }</code>, <code>ToolNotRegistered { tool_name, registered }</code>, <code>PluginContractViolation { plugin_kind, plugin_name, what, detail }</code>, <code>Llm(LlmError)</code>, <code>Tool(ToolError)</code>, <code>Storage(StorageError)</code>, <code>Sandbox(SandboxError)</code>, <code>Manifest(PackageManifestError)</code>, <code>Internal { message }</code> (escape hatch). Each plugin-error variant composes via <code>#[from]</code> for <code>?</code>-propagation; the <code>PluginContractViolation</code> variant is wired but not yet trigger-pathed (see Consequences).</p> <p>Trigger to revisit: a case where the dichotomy breaks down — i.e. a "soft" kernel error that should not terminate the run.</p> <h3 id="10-no-retries-at-v01"><a class="header" href="#10-no-retries-at-v01">10. No retries at v0.1</a></h3> <p>Plugin errors surface via <code>Err(RuntimeError::*)</code> and terminate the run. Callers compose retry logic externally (<code>tokio::time::timeout</code>, exponential backoff, circuit breakers). Building retries into the kernel commits to a retry strategy before real-world data informs the right one, and the kernel-as-minimum stance (G6, NG12) discourages baking in policy.</p> <p>Trigger to revisit: a Phase-1+ retry config that materially helps in a common case.</p> <h3 id="11-tracing-for-structured-logs"><a class="header" href="#11-tracing-for-structured-logs">11. <code>tracing</code> for structured logs</a></h3> <p>Per G9 (observable by default). <code>tracing = "0.1"</code> is workspace-pinned. Callers compose the subscriber (<code>tracing_subscriber::fmt()</code> + filter); per NG9 tau does not redact for the caller.</p> <p>The kernel emits ~22 events across 9 subsystems on a happy-path run (the spec originally enumerated ~45; some merged during implementation as neighboring events collapsed into one). Spans: <code>runtime.agent_run</code>, <code>runtime.turn</code>, <code>llm.complete</code>, <code>dispatch.tool</code>, <code>capability.check</code>, <code>tool.session_open</code>, <code>tool.invoke</code>, <code>tool.session_close</code>. Events: <code>runtime.run_started/completed/failed/loop_terminated/max_turns_reached</code>, <code>llm.request_built/response_received/token_usage/stop_reason/tool_use_emitted</code>, <code>dispatch.tool_resolved</code>, <code>capability.required_loaded/granted_loaded/satisfies_check/allow/deny</code>, <code>tool.args_received/result_received/invoke_failed/session_open_failed/session_close_failed</code>, <code>message.added</code>. Sensitive-data discipline: args + message contents are previewed (256 chars) only at <code>DEBUG</code>; full content only at <code>TRACE</code>. API keys / credentials are never logged by the kernel.</p> <p>Trigger to revisit: a structural change to the vocabulary (event renames, span reorganization) — additive changes are non-breaking.</p> <h3 id="12-per-runtime-storage-scoping"><a class="header" href="#12-per-runtime-storage-scoping">12. Per-runtime storage scoping</a></h3> <p><code>Storage</code> plugins are stateful (open with namespaces, get / put / list / delete). At v0.1 the runtime registry stores one <code>Arc<DynStorage></code> per name; agent-instance-scoped namespaces (e.g. <code>Namespace { agent_instance: AgentInstanceId, scope: "session" }</code>) isolate data between concurrent runs against the same backend. The kernel does not currently invoke <code>Storage::*</code> from the run loop — first-class storage use by the loop is a Phase-1+ feature; v0.1 ships the registry slot so tools can resolve storages by name when invoked.</p> <p>Trigger to revisit: tools that need per-run storage isolation guarantees beyond what namespaces give.</p> <h3 id="13-sandbox-skipped-at-v01"><a class="header" href="#13-sandbox-skipped-at-v01">13. Sandbox skipped at v0.1</a></h3> <p>The <code>Sandbox</code> trait remains in tau-ports as a forward-compat anchor (per ADR-0003 §6 provisional caveat). The kernel never invokes <code>Sandbox::create</code>. Real sandboxing requires OS-level work (Linux namespaces, seccomp, macOS seatbelt, WASI capabilities, or Firecracker VMs) that is out of scope for sub-project 4. The <code>RuntimeError::Sandbox(_)</code> variant exists for forward compat and is unused on every code path at v0.1.</p> <p>Trigger to revisit: when a real sandbox plugin lands (Phase-1+) or when an integration demands sandboxed tool execution.</p> <h3 id="14-no-runtimeshutdown"><a class="header" href="#14-no-runtimeshutdown">14. No <code>Runtime::shutdown</code></a></h3> <p><code>drop</code> is sufficient. Plugin destructors run, <code>Arc<dyn Plugin></code> reference counts drop to zero, plugin internals (HTTP clients, file handles) clean up via their own <code>Drop</code> impls. An explicit <code>shutdown(self)</code> consuming method would commit the kernel to a shutdown phase order (drain in-flight runs, flush logs, close sessions in a known order) before any consumer needs are known.</p> <p>Trigger to revisit: a long-running daemon use case where graceful shutdown ordering matters.</p> <h3 id="15-max_turns-default--16"><a class="header" href="#15-max_turns-default--16">15. <code>max_turns</code> default = 16</a></h3> <p>Empirical range for typical agentic loops. Configurable per-run via <code>RunOptions::max_turns</code>. 16 is high enough that simple single-turn responses + a handful of tool roundtrips fit comfortably; low enough that a runaway loop terminates in bounded time. Hitting the cap returns <code>Ok(RunOutcome::Failed { status: AgentStatus::Failed { kind: FailureKind::OutOfResources, .. } })</code> with the partial conversation preserved.</p> <p>Trigger to revisit: empirical evidence that the default is wrong (real agents complete in 2–3 turns and 16 is over-budgeted, or real agents need 30+ for typical work).</p> <h3 id="16-all_messages-always-included-in-runoutcome"><a class="header" href="#16-all_messages-always-included-in-runoutcome">16. <code>all_messages</code> always included in <code>RunOutcome</code></a></h3> <p>Both <code>RunOutcome::Completed</code> and <code>RunOutcome::Failed</code> carry <code>all_messages: Vec<Message></code> — the full conversation: initial message, every LLM response, every <code>tool_use</code> and <code>tool_result</code>. Callers who want to display, persist, or audit the run get full visibility for free. An opt-out (<code>RunOptions { capture_messages: false }</code> or <code>include_full_history: false</code>) is deferred — at v0.1 the storage cost is bounded by <code>max_turns × message_size</code> and is small.</p> <p>Trigger to revisit: production scale where opt-out provably helps (per-call overhead in tight inner loops, memory pressure in long-running TUI sessions).</p> <h3 id="17-structured-log-vocabulary-frozen-at-v01"><a class="header" href="#17-structured-log-vocabulary-frozen-at-v01">17. Structured-log vocabulary frozen at v0.1</a></h3> <p>The ~22 events listed in decision 11 are the v0.1 vocabulary; the <code>tests/tracing_emission.rs</code> integration test asserts a known-good event set fires on a happy-path run. Tracing event names are <strong>not</strong> considered public API in the QG18 sense — additive vocabulary changes (new events, new span fields) are non-breaking. Removal or rename of an event is a breaking change requiring an ADR.</p> <p>Trigger to revisit: a structural change (event renames, span reorganization).</p> <h2 id="consequences-6"><a class="header" href="#consequences-6">Consequences</a></h2> <h3 id="positive-2"><a class="header" href="#positive-2">Positive</a></h3> <ul> <li>Sub-project 4 ships a working solo-path kernel with 62 unit tests + 7 integration tests + 3 proptests, exercising every public surface and the core agent loop end-to-end against tau-ports' mock plugins.</li> <li>The Outcome / Error dichotomy gives callers a clean split between "agent done, examine outcome" and "kernel broken, log + retry". One <code>match</code> at the call site does both.</li> <li><code>Tool::capabilities()</code> lands as an additive amendment with zero impact on existing impls — the four mocks in <code>tau_ports::fixtures</code> and any out-of-tree <code>Tool</code> impls compile and run unchanged.</li> <li>The tracing vocabulary is frozen at v0.1 for callers; additive expansion is non-breaking, so vocabulary growth in Phase-1+ does not invalidate existing log-analysis pipelines.</li> <li>The builder + dyn-shim pattern keeps the public API ergonomic (<code>Runtime::builder().with_tool(MyTool::new())</code> — no <code>Box::new(...)</code> boilerplate at call sites) while internally bridging to the not-dyn-compatible plugin traits.</li> <li>The kernel has no async-runtime dependency — downstream consumers pick tokio, async-std, smol, or anything else.</li> </ul> <h3 id="negative-2"><a class="header" href="#negative-2">Negative</a></h3> <ul> <li>The <code>DynLlmBackend</code> / <code>DynTool</code> / <code>DynStorage</code> shim adds ~250 lines of boilerplate (a delegate trait + blanket impl per kind). It is removable when tau-ports gains a <code>trait_variant</code>-generated dyn-compatible variant, but not without breaking the v0.1 internal API surface.</li> <li>The <code>Session = ()</code> v0.1 limitation forces stateful tools to use <code>StatelessAdapter</code> — surprising to plugin authors who don't read the docs first. The compile error if they don't (<code>expected Tool<Session = ()></code>) is at least direct.</li> <li>No retries means callers compose them. Consistent with the "kernel does the minimum" stance (G6) but expects more from callers than a batteries-included runtime would.</li> <li><code>RuntimeError::PluginContractViolation</code> is wired (Task 10) but the v0.1 implementation does not have a trigger path: <code>deserialize_tool_args</code> is a passthrough today. Phase-1+ schema validation will populate this variant; until then the variant is dead code on every observed run.</li> <li>Sandbox is skipped at v0.1 — real isolation guarantees come Phase-1+. The <code>RuntimeError::Sandbox(_)</code> variant is similarly dead code today.</li> </ul> <h3 id="neutral--new-obligations-2"><a class="header" href="#neutral--new-obligations-2">Neutral / new obligations</a></h3> <ul> <li>Future tau-runtime public API additions require their own ADRs (QG18).</li> <li>The bundled tau-ports amendment (<code>Tool::capabilities()</code>) means future tau-ports trait changes that are NOT motivated by tau-runtime get their own ADRs (don't bundle promiscuously).</li> <li>Mid-implementation additive constructors (<code>Message::new</code>, <code>AgentStatus::failed</code>, <code>CompletionRequest::new</code>, <code>LlmProviderMessage::{user, assistant, tool_result}</code>, <code>ToolUse::new</code>, <code>TokenUsage::new</code>, <code>SessionContext::new</code>, <code>PackageId::new</code>) are now part of the public API surface and bound by QG18 going forward.</li> <li>The capability satisfies-relation glob matcher accepts <code>**</code>, <code>*</code>, exact strings, and a host-style <code>*.suffix</code> form. Other forms (<code>pre*.txt</code>, <code>*foo*</code>, character classes) are unsupported. Adding richer glob semantics is a satisfies-relation extension and additive (does not invalidate existing capability declarations).</li> <li>The <code>RuntimeError::Internal</code> and <code>BuildError::Internal</code> escape hatches are registered in <code>docs/explanation/escape-hatches.md</code> per the ADR-0002 escape-hatch policy; the CI registry test enforces the registration.</li> <li>Concurrent calls to <code>Runtime::run</code> against a shared <code>Storage</code> plugin rely on the storage plugin's <code>Send + Sync</code> impl and internal concurrency handling; the kernel does not serialize runs.</li> </ul> <h2 id="alternatives-considered-6"><a class="header" href="#alternatives-considered-6">Alternatives considered</a></h2> <h3 id="a-sync-public-api-with-internal-block_on"><a class="header" href="#a-sync-public-api-with-internal-block_on">A. Sync public API with internal <code>block_on</code></a></h3> <p>Rejected. The plugin traits are async; wrapping them in a sync facade requires <code>tokio::runtime::Handle::current().block_on(...)</code> which fails outside a running runtime. Forcing a kernel-managed runtime (e.g., bundling tokio inside tau-runtime) commits us to one async runtime forever. Letting the caller pick is more flexible and matches the runtime-agnostic stance ADR-0003 took for the trait surface.</p> <h3 id="b-boxdyn-llmbackend-registration-without-the-dyn-shim"><a class="header" href="#b-boxdyn-llmbackend-registration-without-the-dyn-shim">B. <code>Box<dyn LlmBackend></code> registration without the dyn-shim</a></h3> <p>Rejected. <code>LlmBackend</code> (and <code>Tool</code>, <code>Storage</code>) use native <code>async fn in trait</code> (per ADR-0003 §1) which is not dyn-compatible under Rust 1.93 (compiler error E0038). The straightforward translation of the spec did not compile. The wrapper-trait shim is the standard idiomatic workaround until tau-ports gains a <code>trait_variant</code>-generated dyn variant. See decision 3.</p> <h3 id="c-tau-pkg-dependency-in-tau-runtime-for-manifest-fetching"><a class="header" href="#c-tau-pkg-dependency-in-tau-runtime-for-manifest-fetching">C. tau-pkg dependency in tau-runtime for manifest fetching</a></h3> <p>Rejected. tau-runtime should run agents, not fetch packages. Tightening the dependency direction (tau-runtime knows nothing about installation) keeps tau-runtime embeddable in environments where tau-pkg is absent — a server consuming pre-fetched manifests over the wire, an in-process embedding in a desktop app, etc.</p> <h3 id="d-per-call-response-queue-in-mockllmbackend"><a class="header" href="#d-per-call-response-queue-in-mockllmbackend">D. Per-call response queue in <code>MockLlmBackend</code></a></h3> <p>Considered for fixtures support during the integration-test phase. Rejected for sub-project 4 because integration tests can ship an inline <code>ScriptedLlm</code> struct (see <code>crates/tau-runtime/tests/run_with_tool_calls.rs</code>). The fixture stays minimal; per-call scripting is a test-helper concern that a future sub-project can land in tau-ports if patterns demand it.</p> <h3 id="e-outcome-only-api-without-errruntimeerror"><a class="header" href="#e-outcome-only-api-without-errruntimeerror">E. Outcome-only API without <code>Err(RuntimeError)</code></a></h3> <p>Rejected. Plugin errors and dispatch errors are kernel-level — they break the agent's run because the kernel can't continue. Forcing them into <code>RunOutcome::Failed</code> would conflate "agent done" with "kernel broken" and force callers to pattern-match a tagged union for the distinction. The <code>Result</code> split is clearer at the call site and lets <code>?</code>-propagation work naturally for kernel errors.</p> <h3 id="f-top-level-runtimeerror-umbrella-with-one-variant-per-kernel-error"><a class="header" href="#f-top-level-runtimeerror-umbrella-with-one-variant-per-kernel-error">F. Top-level <code>RuntimeError</code> umbrella with one variant per kernel error</a></h3> <p>Already chosen. (This is the mirror image of ADR-0004 §12 where per-operation enums won.) For tau-runtime, the kernel's operations all flow through <code>Runtime::run</code>, so a single <code>RuntimeError</code> enum covering all kernel-error paths gives callers one type to match. Splitting per sub-operation (<code>LlmDispatchError</code>, <code>ToolDispatchError</code>, <code>CapabilityCheckError</code>) would force callers to compose three or four match arms for one logical "kernel failure" branch.</p> <h3 id="g-skip-the-additive-toolcapabilities-and-resolve-capabilities-at-install-time-only"><a class="header" href="#g-skip-the-additive-toolcapabilities-and-resolve-capabilities-at-install-time-only">G. Skip the additive <code>Tool::capabilities()</code> and resolve capabilities at install time only</a></h3> <p>Rejected. Install-time resolution alone leaves a gap: a tool's required capabilities can change as the tool ships new versions, but the agent's manifest is locked at install time. Runtime checking against the current tool's declarations catches drift between install-time and run-time state. G14 explicitly requires both halves — declared at install AND enforced at runtime.</p> <h3 id="h-sandbox-enforcement-at-v01"><a class="header" href="#h-sandbox-enforcement-at-v01">H. Sandbox enforcement at v0.1</a></h3> <p>Rejected. Real sandboxing requires OS-level work (Linux namespaces, seccomp, macOS seatbelt, WASI capabilities, or Firecracker VMs). Sub-project 4's scope is "agent lifecycle + message passing — solo path" (ROADMAP row 4); sandboxing belongs to a later sub-project where the security model is the primary concern. The trait stays in tau-ports as a forward-compat anchor (ADR-0003 §6).</p> <div style="break-before: page; page-break-before: always;"></div><h1 id="adr-0007-tau-cli--tau-runtime-amendments-capability-filter-run_with_history"><a class="header" href="#adr-0007-tau-cli--tau-runtime-amendments-capability-filter-run_with_history">ADR-0007: tau-cli + tau-runtime amendments (capability filter, run_with_history)</a></h1> <p><strong>Status:</strong> Accepted <strong>Date:</strong> 2026-04-28 <strong>Supersedes:</strong> — <strong>Amends:</strong> ADR-0006 §7 and §11 (refines typed-capability story by pre-filtering tools per-call; adds <code>Runtime::run_with_history</code> and the <code>history_len</code> span field as additive vocabulary). <strong>Refines:</strong> ADR-0002 (project <code>tau.toml</code> shares filename with package <code>tau.toml</code>; the two are distinct schemas keyed by their root tables).</p> <h2 id="context-7"><a class="header" href="#context-7">Context</a></h2> <p>tau-cli (sub-project 5, ROADMAP row 5) is the CLI binary surface for tau Phase 0 — the <code>tau</code> executable. It is the first sub-project producing a binary rather than a library, and it is the consumer that wires tau-runtime, tau-pkg, tau-domain, and the tau-ports plugin traits into a user-facing tool. Per ROADMAP row 5 the v0.1 scope is the solo path; multi-agent orchestration (G10) is Phase 1+.</p> <p>Per QG18, public API additions (the CLI subcommand surface, the project <code>tau.toml</code> schema) and additive plugin / runtime amendments require ADRs. This ADR bundles 18 tau-cli decisions plus 2 additive tau-runtime amendments per the ADR-0006 precedent (kernel + <code>Tool::capabilities()</code> amendment recorded together because the amendment was solely motivated by the kernel). Both amendments here are solely motivated by tau-cli — specifically by the capability-aware tool dispatch path and the REPL's need to thread conversation history across user turns. Bundling avoids splitting one motivated change across multiple ADRs; future tau-runtime amendments motivated by their own sub-projects will get their own ADRs (no promiscuous bundling).</p> <p>Relevant Constitution constraints: G6 (tau is a runtime, not a framework — the CLI is a thin shell), G9 (observable by default), G10 (solo path; orchestration Phase 1+), NG6 (no persistent agent memory in core), NG9 (tau does not redact for the caller and does not manage credentials), NG11 (developer tool, not end-user product), NG12 (runtime not framework), QG2 (<code>thiserror</code> everywhere), QG18 (ADRs for public API additions). This is the last sub-project before the formal Phase 0 retrospective (per PG4); decisions made here close out the Phase 0 public surface.</p> <h2 id="decision-7"><a class="header" href="#decision-7">Decision</a></h2> <h3 id="1-5-subcommand-surface-at-v01"><a class="header" href="#1-5-subcommand-surface-at-v01">1. 5-subcommand surface at v0.1</a></h3> <p><code>install</code>, <code>list</code>, <code>run</code>, <code>init</code>, <code>chat</code>. ROADMAP row 5 enumerates <code>install</code>, <code>list</code>, <code>run</code>. <code>init</code> is added per ADR-0004 §6 (the project-scaffolding verb that creates a starter <code>tau.toml</code> plus a stub agent). <code>chat</code> is added per the brainstorm's option-A REPL choice (see decision 6). Deferred to Phase 1+: <code>uninstall</code>, <code>update</code>, <code>verify</code>, <code>workflow</code> and any orchestration verbs. The deferred list is documented; v0.1 hard-rejects unknown subcommands rather than silently succeeding.</p> <p>Trigger to revisit: a real user workflow demanding any deferred verb.</p> <h3 id="2-tokiomain-async-at-the-entry"><a class="header" href="#2-tokiomain-async-at-the-entry">2. <code>#[tokio::main]</code> async at the entry</a></h3> <p>The CLI binary's <code>main</code> is <code>#[tokio::main(flavor = "current_thread")]</code>. <code>Runtime::run</code> and <code>Runtime::run_with_history</code> are async (per ADR-0006 §2); sync tau-pkg calls run inline. tokio is in dev-deps for tau-runtime tests already; the CLI as the consumer picks it. <code>Runtime::run</code> itself remains async-runtime-agnostic per ADR-0006 §2 — only the binary commits. The current-thread flavor is sufficient because v0.1 has no internal concurrency in the CLI (no <code>tokio::spawn</code>, no parallel subcommand execution); a future multi-agent orchestration step in Phase 1+ may upgrade to the multi-thread flavor.</p> <p>Trigger to revisit: a use case where async forces unwanted complexity on a small embedding (the runtime stance is unchanged; this decision only binds the binary).</p> <h3 id="3-project-tautoml-named-table-schema"><a class="header" href="#3-project-tautoml-named-table-schema">3. Project <code>tau.toml</code> named-table schema</a></h3> <p>A project's <code>tau.toml</code> has <code>[project]</code> and <code>[agents.<id>]</code> named tables (Cargo's <code>[dependencies.foo]</code> style) with optional sub-tables <code>requires</code>, <code>capabilities</code> (reserved — see decision 4), <code>config</code>, <code>prompt</code>. The project file is distinct from the package <code>tau.toml</code> defined by ADR-0002: the two share a filename modeled on Cargo's <code>[package]</code> (in a crate's <code>Cargo.toml</code>) vs <code>[workspace]</code> (in a workspace root) precedent — the root table tells the parser which schema applies. tau-cli's <code>config::read_project</code> rejects files that match neither schema with a typed <code>ProjectConfigError::AmbiguousFile</code>.</p> <p>Named tables (<code>[agents.foo]</code>) are chosen over array-of-tables (<code>[[agents]]</code> with an <code>id</code> field) because the named-table form makes the agent id visually obvious in the section header and matches Cargo's map-by-name idiom for the same role.</p> <p>Trigger to revisit: confusion between project and package files in real user reports — at which point the file extension or name should be split.</p> <h3 id="4-capability-override-intersect-only-lands-in-phase-1"><a class="header" href="#4-capability-override-intersect-only-lands-in-phase-1">4. Capability override (intersect-only) lands in Phase 1</a></h3> <p>The <code>[[agents.<id>.capabilities]]</code> array-of-tables in project tau.toml narrows — but never expands — the capabilities granted by an agent's package manifest. Each entry's <code>kind</code> discriminator must match a package-side capability; <code>allow_*</code> fields must be a glob-subset (or exact-match for hosts/commands) of the package's grant; <code>deny_*</code> fields are pure subtractions with deny-wins precedence. Validation runs at parse time AND at every runtime load, both fail-closed.</p> <p>Realized by the capability-override sub-project (Tier 2 priority 4): see <a href="decisions/../superpowers/specs/2026-04-30-capability-override-design.html"><code>docs/superpowers/specs/2026-04-30-capability-override-design.md</code></a> for the full design.</p> <p>The original v0.1 reservation (when this section was titled "Capability override is a Phase 1+ requirement") set the intersect-only invariant up-front so Phase 1 could not quietly choose expand-and-narrow — which would have let a project widen what an installed package was authorized to do, breaking the install-time security contract.</p> <p>Trigger to revisit: per-tool overrides (narrower than per-agent), hostname-glob narrowing, or <code>Capability::Custom</code> parameter narrowing — each deferred to a future sub-project.</p> <h3 id="5-per-agent-requirestools-auto-install-phase-1-active"><a class="header" href="#5-per-agent-requirestools-auto-install-phase-1-active">5. Per-agent <code>requires.tools</code> auto-install (Phase 1+ active)</a></h3> <p>Each <code>[[agents.<id>.requires.tools]]</code> array entry is a typed package declaration with <code>name</code>, <code>source</code> (typed <code>PackageSource</code>), and optional <code>version</code> (semver req, defaults to <code>"*"</code>). At <code>tau run</code> / <code>tau chat</code> time (or on-demand via <code>tau resolve</code>), missing entries are fetched + installed automatically; already-installed compatible versions are reused via the existing per-scope lockfile.</p> <p>Realized by the transitive-dependency-resolution sub-project (Tier 2 priority 5): see <a href="decisions/../superpowers/specs/2026-04-30-transitive-deps-design.html"><code>docs/superpowers/specs/2026-04-30-transitive-deps-design.md</code></a> for the full design.</p> <p>The original v0.1 reservation (when this section was titled "Per-agent <code>requires.tools</code> advisory check") committed the auto-install path as the Phase 1+ trigger so the v0.1 advisory error would convert into the auto-install hook without breaking existing call sites.</p> <p>Trigger to revisit: recursive package-level <code>dependencies</code> resolution (ADR-0004 §10 deferral) — at which point the resolver gains a second input axis; the project-level half (this section) stays unchanged.</p> <h3 id="6-one-shot-tau-run--separate-tau-chat-repl"><a class="header" href="#6-one-shot-tau-run--separate-tau-chat-repl">6. One-shot <code>tau run</code> + separate <code>tau chat</code> REPL</a></h3> <p>Two distinct verbs, two mental models. <code>tau run <id> "<prompt>"</code> is strict 1:1 with <code>Runtime::run</code> — single prompt in, single outcome out, scriptable, predictable, no detection logic. <code>tau chat <id></code> opens a REPL using <code>rustyline</code> (line editor) and <code>termimad</code> (Markdown rendering to ANSI), with in-memory-only history and a small slash-command surface (see decision 11). Overloading one verb (e.g., "if no prompt and stdin is a TTY, enter REPL") was rejected because CI scripts that forget a prompt argument would accidentally hang in a REPL; explicit verbs prevent the surprise.</p> <p>Trigger to revisit: a workflow that genuinely needs both modes from the same verb.</p> <h3 id="7-three-bucket-exit-codes-0--1--2"><a class="header" href="#7-three-bucket-exit-codes-0--1--2">7. Three-bucket exit codes (0 / 1 / 2)</a></h3> <p>The Outcome / Error dichotomy from ADR-0006 §9 maps cleanly to three exit codes:</p> <ul> <li><code>0</code> — success: <code>tau install/list/init</code> succeeded, or <code>tau run</code> produced <code>RunOutcome::Completed</code>.</li> <li><code>1</code> — <code>tau run</code> graceful failure: <code>RunOutcome::Failed</code> (any <code>FailureKind</code>). Reserved exclusively for <code>tau run</code>.</li> <li><code>2</code> — kernel/CLI broke: <code>Err(RuntimeError)</code>, parse errors, missing dependencies, unknown subcommand, IO errors.</li> </ul> <p>Three buckets give CI scripts the most common branching predicate (agent ran but failed vs. tau itself broke) without coupling exit codes to <code>FailureKind</code> variants. Finer-grained machine-readable detail comes through <code>--json</code> (see decision 8).</p> <p>Trigger to revisit: CI usage that needs finer granularity than <code>--json</code> provides.</p> <h3 id="8-strict-stdoutstderr-split----json-mode"><a class="header" href="#8-strict-stdoutstderr-split----json-mode">8. Strict stdout/stderr split + <code>--json</code> mode</a></h3> <p>Output discipline lives in the <code>Output</code> abstraction per spec §3.6:</p> <ul> <li><code>stdout</code> carries scriptable content only — agent text, list rows, JSON. Nothing else. Pipes (<code>tau run … | jq</code>, <code>tau list | wc -l</code>) must work.</li> <li><code>stderr</code> carries everything else — status messages, tracing output, errors, warnings. Tracing always goes to stderr regardless of mode.</li> </ul> <p><code>--json</code> switches stdout from human-formatted output to a schema-versioned JSON envelope per subcommand. <code>tau chat</code> rejects <code>--json</code> at argument parse time (REPL is interactive by definition). Insta JSON snapshots assert the envelopes don't drift.</p> <p>Trigger to revisit: a subcommand whose output convention legitimately breaks the split (none anticipated at v0.1).</p> <h3 id="9-verbosity-model"><a class="header" href="#9-verbosity-model">9. Verbosity model</a></h3> <p>Standard env_logger / tracing-subscriber conventions:</p> <ul> <li>Default: <code>INFO</code> scoped to <code>tau=*</code> (tau crates only — third-party noise stays at <code>WARN</code>).</li> <li><code>-v</code> → <code>DEBUG</code> (still scoped to <code>tau=*</code>).</li> <li><code>-vv</code> → <code>TRACE</code>.</li> <li><code>-q</code> → <code>WARN</code>.</li> <li><code>--debug</code> → <code>DEBUG</code> AND switches the top-level error printer from <code>Display</code> to <code>Debug</code> (see decision 12) — the single "everything" knob.</li> <li><code>RUST_LOG</code> env var, when present, overrides verbatim and ignores <code>-v/-vv/-q</code>.</li> </ul> <p>Trigger to revisit: production deployments demanding JSON-formatted tracing output (additive — a <code>--log-format json</code> flag at the binary level).</p> <h3 id="10-color-via-is-terminal----color--no_color"><a class="header" href="#10-color-via-is-terminal----color--no_color">10. Color via <code>is-terminal</code> + <code>--color</code> + <code>NO_COLOR</code></a></h3> <p>Standard CLI conventions, implemented exactly once in <code>Output</code>:</p> <ul> <li>Auto-detect: color enabled when stdout is a terminal (<code>is-terminal</code>).</li> <li><code>NO_COLOR</code> env var (any non-empty value): force-disable. Universal opt-out per the no-color.org convention.</li> <li><code>--color={auto,always,never}</code>: explicit override beats auto-detect.</li> </ul> <p>Trigger to revisit: terminals that lie about <code>IS_TERMINAL</code> and need a workaround switch.</p> <h3 id="11-repl-rustyline--termimad-in-memory-only-history-4-slash-commands"><a class="header" href="#11-repl-rustyline--termimad-in-memory-only-history-4-slash-commands">11. REPL: rustyline + termimad, in-memory-only history, 4 slash commands</a></h3> <p><code>tau chat</code> uses:</p> <ul> <li><code>rustyline</code> for line editing (arrow-key recall, emacs/vi mode, Ctrl-C / Ctrl-D handling).</li> <li><code>termimad</code> for rendering agent Markdown responses to ANSI.</li> <li>An in-memory <code>Vec<Message></code> for conversation history, threaded into each <code>Runtime::run_with_history</code> call (see decision 15). The history is dropped on exit. This aligns with NG6 (no persistent agent memory in core); REPL history is a CLI-side concern, not a runtime responsibility.</li> <li>Four slash commands: <code>/exit</code> (quit), <code>/help</code> (show commands), <code>/clear</code> (drop in-memory history), <code>/history</code> (print messages so far). <code>/save</code>, <code>/load</code>, <code>/system</code>, <code>/model</code> etc. are deferred to Phase 1+.</li> </ul> <p>Trigger to revisit: a Phase 1+ feature demanding history persistence or a richer slash surface.</p> <h3 id="12-top-level-error-message-by-default---debug-expands-to-source-chain"><a class="header" href="#12-top-level-error-message-by-default---debug-expands-to-source-chain">12. Top-level error message by default; <code>--debug</code> expands to source chain</a></h3> <p>tau-cli uses <code>anyhow</code> only at the binary boundary (each subcommand returns <code>Result<(), anyhow::Error></code> to a single top-level handler). The handler prints <code>eprintln!("error: {err}")</code> by default — anyhow's <code>Display</code> impl, which shows only the top-level message. With <code>--debug</code>, the handler switches to <code>eprintln!("error: {err:?}")</code> — anyhow's <code>Debug</code> impl, which prints the full source chain. This matches Cargo / rustc convention. Internal subcommand code uses <code>thiserror</code> (per QG2); <code>anyhow</code> lives only at the boundary.</p> <p>Trigger to revisit: rare cases where the chain is needed by default (none anticipated).</p> <h3 id="13---dry-run-on-installruninitchat-not-list"><a class="header" href="#13---dry-run-on-installruninitchat-not-list">13. <code>--dry-run</code> on install/run/init/chat (not list)</a></h3> <p><code>tau list</code> is read-only — <code>--dry-run</code> is meaningless and is rejected at argument parse time with a clear error. The other four have meaningful "would do X" semantics:</p> <ul> <li><code>tau install --dry-run</code>: clone + parse + validate, no registry write.</li> <li><code>tau run --dry-run</code>: build the <code>AgentDefinition</code>, validate <code>requires.tools</code>, but do NOT call the LLM.</li> <li><code>tau init --dry-run</code>: print the files that would be written, do NOT touch disk.</li> <li><code>tau chat --dry-run</code>: same validation as <code>tau run --dry-run</code>, then exit (do not enter the REPL).</li> </ul> <p>Stderr lines from dry-run mode are prefixed with <code>[dry-run]</code> for grep- ability.</p> <p>Trigger to revisit: a future read-only subcommand whose <code>--dry-run</code> could surface validation issues (at which point the rejection becomes selective).</p> <h3 id="14-tau-runtime-amendment-1-capability-filtered-tools"><a class="header" href="#14-tau-runtime-amendment-1-capability-filtered-tools">14. tau-runtime amendment 1: capability-filtered tools</a></h3> <p>This refines ADR-0006 §7's typed-capability story. Today the kernel checks tool invocations against the agent's manifest and denies mismatches with <code>FailureKind::PolicyDenied</code>. The amendment adds a pre-filter step before <code>LlmBackend::complete</code>: the kernel computes which registered tools are satisfied by the agent's package manifest and only those tools are sent in <code>CompletionRequest.tools</code>. Effect:</p> <ul> <li>Smaller LLM prompts (no point telling the model about a tool it can't call).</li> <li>No spurious denials when the model picks a denied tool just because the runtime mentioned it.</li> </ul> <p>Implementation: two new tracing events join the §3.9 vocabulary as additive (non-breaking per ADR-0006 §17):</p> <ul> <li><code>runtime.tool_filtered</code> at WARN, one per filtered tool, with fields <code>tool_name</code>, <code>agent_id</code>, <code>denial_kind</code>, <code>denial_detail</code>.</li> <li><code>runtime.tools_filtered</code> at DEBUG, one per turn, with summary counts (<code>requested</code>, <code>granted</code>, <code>filtered</code>).</li> </ul> <p>The defense-in-depth invoke-time check from ADR-0006 §7 is unchanged — if a tool somehow bypasses the filter (e.g., a future direct-dispatch path), the runtime still denies it. No new error variants per decision 17 below.</p> <p>Trigger to revisit: future dynamic-capability tools where per-call grants might change between filter time and invoke time.</p> <h3 id="15-tau-runtime-amendment-2-runtimerun_with_history"><a class="header" href="#15-tau-runtime-amendment-2-runtimerun_with_history">15. tau-runtime amendment 2: <code>Runtime::run_with_history</code></a></h3> <p><code>tau chat</code> needs to thread conversation history across user turns. The kernel exposes:</p> <pre><pre class="playground"><code class="language-rust"><span class="boring">#![allow(unused)] </span><span class="boring">fn main() { </span>pub async fn run_with_history( &self, agent_def: &AgentDefinition, manifest: &PackageManifest, history: Vec<Message>, initial_message: Message, options: RunOptions, ) -> Result<RunOutcome, RuntimeError> <span class="boring">}</span></code></pre></pre> <p><code>Runtime::run</code> becomes a thin wrapper that calls <code>run_with_history</code> with <code>history = Vec::new()</code>. Existing callers (sub-project 4's tests, tau-cli's <code>cmd::run</code>) are unchanged — the wrapper preserves the v0.1 signature.</p> <p>The <code>runtime.agent_run</code> span gains a <code>history_len: usize</code> field — additive per ADR-0006 §17.</p> <p>This aligns with NG6: history is a CLI-side concern threaded into each kernel call. The kernel doesn't persist anything between <code>run_with_history</code> invocations; it's the REPL's job to carry the returned <code>all_messages</code> back into the next call.</p> <p>Trigger to revisit: history-aware features at the kernel level (summarization, sliding windows, automatic compaction) — at which point a richer <code>RunOptions</code> field or a dedicated session API lands.</p> <h3 id="16-agentdefinition-construction-lives-in-tau-cli"><a class="header" href="#16-agentdefinition-construction-lives-in-tau-cli">16. <code>AgentDefinition</code> construction lives in tau-cli</a></h3> <p><code>AgentDefinition</code> is a tau-domain data type, but the logic to construct one from a project <code>tau.toml</code> (resolve a package by <code>name@semver</code>, resolve the <code>llm_backend</code> reference, read the prompt from <code>[agents.<id>.prompt.path]</code> or <code>[agents.<id>.prompt.inline]</code>, validate <code>requires.tools</code>) is tau-cli's responsibility. tau-cli's <code>config::build_agent_definition</code> is the canonical builder for the project-<code>tau.toml</code> case. Other consumers — Phase 1+ workflow runners, embedded SDKs reading from a different config — write their own builders matching their config formats.</p> <p>This keeps tau-domain free of CLI / config concerns and tau-runtime free of file-format concerns; the dependency direction stays crisp.</p> <p>Trigger to revisit: a second consumer (Phase 1+ workflow runner, IDE plugin, library SDK) that wants the same logic — at which point the builder extracts to a shared crate.</p> <h3 id="17-no-new-error-variants-without-triggering-codepaths"><a class="header" href="#17-no-new-error-variants-without-triggering-codepaths">17. NO new error variants without triggering codepaths</a></h3> <p>Per the phase-0-mid memo. Both tau-runtime amendments (§14, §15) and tau-cli's own error taxonomies (<code>ProjectConfigError</code>, <code>AgentResolutionError</code>, <code>CliError</code>) add only variants with concrete reachable failure paths backed by ≥1 test. The capability-filter amendment (§14) is silent-but-traced: no new error variants — a filtered tool simply doesn't appear in <code>CompletionRequest.tools</code>. <code>run_with_history</code> (§15) reuses the existing <code>RuntimeError</code> variants.</p> <p>This codifies the discipline that bit ADR-0006 (the <code>PluginContractViolation</code> and <code>Sandbox(_)</code> variants are wired but trigger-pathless at v0.1). Going forward, any new variant ships with its trigger path or doesn't ship.</p> <p>Trigger to revisit: never — this is a process discipline that should always hold.</p> <h3 id="18-plugin-loading-deferred-to-phase-1"><a class="header" href="#18-plugin-loading-deferred-to-phase-1">18. Plugin loading deferred to Phase 1+</a></h3> <p>tau-pkg installs packages as source trees on disk, but tau-cli at v0.1 has no mechanism to compile and dynamically load them as plugins. Real loading (in-process dlopen via <code>abi_stable</code>, out-of-process IPC, WASM/WASI) is a major design decision that benefits from Phase 1+ requirements before being committed. v0.1 ships compiled-in mock plugins gated by <code>cfg(feature = "test-mock")</code> for integration testing end-to-end. <code>tau install</code> registers source trees in the registry, but those trees do not execute against <code>tau run</code> / <code>tau chat</code> until Phase 1's loader lands.</p> <p>This is a material v0.1 limitation and is surfaced in <code>tau install</code>'s success message (a hint pointing at the Phase 1+ loader ADR slot).</p> <p>Trigger to revisit: Phase 1+ ADR for the plugin-loading mechanism.</p> <h2 id="consequences-7"><a class="header" href="#consequences-7">Consequences</a></h2> <h3 id="positive-3"><a class="header" href="#positive-3">Positive</a></h3> <ul> <li>v0.1 ships a 5-subcommand CLI with 88 unit + 64 integration + 12 snapshot tests covering every public surface and the agent run loop end-to-end (against the <code>test-mock</code> backend).</li> <li>Three-bucket exit codes give CI scripts a clean branch on the Outcome / Error dichotomy without leaking <code>FailureKind</code> into the exit-code surface.</li> <li><code>--json</code> mode plus insta JSON snapshots make schema drift impossible to ship accidentally — every JSON envelope has a snapshot test.</li> <li>Project <code>tau.toml</code> schema lays the foundation for Phase 1+ workflow / pipeline definitions; the <code>[project]</code> and <code>[agents.<id>]</code> tables give those features a natural home.</li> <li>tau-runtime amendments are additive — every existing caller (sub-project 4's tests, the tau-cli <code>cmd::run</code> path) is unchanged.</li> <li>The REPL provides the conversation-threading UX that one-shot <code>tau run</code> can't, without compromising scriptability — <code>tau run</code> stays strict 1:1 with <code>Runtime::run</code>.</li> <li><code>AgentDefinition</code> construction in tau-cli keeps tau-domain config- free and lets future consumers (workflow runners, SDKs) build agents from their own config formats without inheriting tau-cli's.</li> </ul> <h3 id="negative-3"><a class="header" href="#negative-3">Negative</a></h3> <ul> <li>Plugin loading deferred means v0.1 can install package source trees but cannot run user-supplied plugins. The compiled-in <code>test-mock</code> backend keeps integration tests viable but is not a production solution. Decision 18 makes the limitation explicit; users see a hint at install time.</li> <li>Project <code>tau.toml</code> shares a filename with package <code>tau.toml</code>. This is modeled on Cargo's <code>[package]</code> vs <code>[workspace]</code> precedent but is still a source of confusion for newcomers. Documented in decision 3 and surfaced via <code>ProjectConfigError::AmbiguousFile</code>.</li> <li>Capability override schema slot reserved but rejected at v0.1 — Phase 1 must implement intersect semantics or accept a deprecation cycle if it picks differently.</li> <li>REPL UX is minimal at v0.1: terminal-mode features (arrow-key recall verification, color rendering correctness, terminal resize handling) are not covered by automated tests; they rely on rustyline + termimad's defaults and manual smoke testing.</li> <li><code>#[tokio::main]</code> couples the CLI binary to tokio. Documented in decision 2; replaceable but only tau-cli is affected — the runtime stays async-runtime-agnostic.</li> <li>The <code>tau install</code> source-tree-only behavior means a successful install does not imply a runnable agent at v0.1; the hint at install time mitigates but does not eliminate the surprise.</li> </ul> <h3 id="neutral--new-obligations-3"><a class="header" href="#neutral--new-obligations-3">Neutral / new obligations</a></h3> <ul> <li>Future tau-cli public API additions (new subcommands, new project <code>tau.toml</code> schema fields, new <code>--flags</code>) require their own ADRs (QG18). The CLI surface is now public.</li> <li>The bundled tau-runtime amendments mean future tau-runtime changes motivated by their own sub-project (or by a library consumer that is not tau-cli) get their own ADRs (don't bundle promiscuously).</li> <li>Mid-implementation additive items in this sub-project (the <code>Scope</code> / <code>PackageSource</code> / <code>Capability</code> API findings recorded during Task 9 + Task 11) are documented in the relevant commit bodies, not in this ADR — they are tau-pkg internal API surfaces that don't change Phase-0 semantics.</li> <li>The <code>runtime.tool_filtered</code> and <code>runtime.tools_filtered</code> tracing events join the ADR-0006 §3.9 (tracing) vocabulary as additive (non-breaking per ADR-0006 §17). Future renames or removals require an ADR.</li> <li>The <code>history_len</code> field on the <code>runtime.agent_run</code> span is similarly additive vocabulary.</li> <li>tau-cli's <code>lib.rs</code> exposes internal modules for integration testing. This is NOT considered a public API in the QG18 sense — tau-cli is a binary, not a library consumed by external code. The crate name is published only so the test binary can link against the same module tree as the binary.</li> </ul> <h2 id="alternatives-considered-7"><a class="header" href="#alternatives-considered-7">Alternatives considered</a></h2> <h3 id="a-sync-tau-cli-with-block_on-at-every-async-boundary"><a class="header" href="#a-sync-tau-cli-with-block_on-at-every-async-boundary">A. Sync <code>tau-cli</code> with <code>block_on</code> at every async boundary</a></h3> <p>Rejected. Forcing sync entry would require <code>tokio::runtime::Handle::current().block_on(...)</code> at each call site, which fails outside a running runtime. tokio is in the dependency graph regardless once real LLM plugins land (the canonical <code>reqwest</code>-based clients are tokio-native). See decision 2.</p> <h3 id="b-overload-tau-run-with-prompt-vs-no-prompt-detection-for-repl"><a class="header" href="#b-overload-tau-run-with-prompt-vs-no-prompt-detection-for-repl">B. Overload <code>tau run</code> with prompt-vs-no-prompt detection for REPL</a></h3> <p>Rejected. Entering a REPL on missing prompt + isatty detection is surprising — CI scripts that forget to pass a prompt accidentally enter a REPL and hang. A separate <code>tau chat</code> verb is cleaner and gives the REPL room to grow its own surface (slash commands, future history persistence) without polluting <code>tau run</code>. See decision 6.</p> <h3 id="c-two-bucket-exit-codes-ok-vs-not-ok"><a class="header" href="#c-two-bucket-exit-codes-ok-vs-not-ok">C. Two-bucket exit codes (Ok vs not-Ok)</a></h3> <p>Rejected. CI scripts need to distinguish "agent ran but failed" from "kernel broke" — the most common branching predicate in agent pipelines. Three buckets give that distinction without coupling exit codes to <code>FailureKind</code>. See decision 7.</p> <h3 id="d-agents-array-of-tables-instead-of-agentsid-named-tables"><a class="header" href="#d-agents-array-of-tables-instead-of-agentsid-named-tables">D. <code>[[agents]]</code> array-of-tables instead of <code>[agents.<id>]</code> named tables</a></h3> <p>Rejected. Array-of-tables is visually flat and requires a separate <code>id</code> field; named tables make the scope visually obvious (the section header IS the id) and match Cargo's <code>[dependencies.foo]</code> for the same map-by-name role. See decision 3.</p> <h3 id="e-tau-init-interactively-prompts-for-name--first-agent-details"><a class="header" href="#e-tau-init-interactively-prompts-for-name--first-agent-details">E. <code>tau init</code> interactively prompts for name + first agent details</a></h3> <p>Rejected. Adds prompt-handling complexity for marginal UX value at v0.1. The stub agent gives the user a concrete starting point to edit and is friendlier to scripted use (<code>tau init <name></code> doesn't hang waiting for input). A future <code>tau init --interactive</code> is a natural Phase 1+ addition.</p> <h3 id="f-real-plugin-loading-at-v01-dlopen--abi_stable"><a class="header" href="#f-real-plugin-loading-at-v01-dlopen--abi_stable">F. Real plugin loading at v0.1 (dlopen / abi_stable)</a></h3> <p>Rejected. Plugin-loading mechanism choice (in-process dynamic linking via <code>abi_stable</code>, out-of-process IPC, WASI) is a major design decision that benefits from real Phase 1+ requirements before being committed. v0.1's compiled-in <code>test-mock</code> backend keeps integration tests viable without locking in a loading approach. See decision 18.</p> <h3 id="g-persisted-repl-session-history-at-v01"><a class="header" href="#g-persisted-repl-session-history-at-v01">G. Persisted REPL session history at v0.1</a></h3> <p>Rejected. Persistence raises "where does the file live", "garbage collection", "schema versioning", "encryption-at-rest" questions that don't have answers at v0.1 — and persistence interacts with NG6 (no persistent agent memory in core) in ways that need their own design pass. In-memory-only is the simplest correct option; persistence is additive when a real use case appears.</p> <h3 id="h-new-runtimerun-signature-instead-of-run_with_history--wrapper"><a class="header" href="#h-new-runtimerun-signature-instead-of-run_with_history--wrapper">H. New <code>Runtime::run</code> signature instead of <code>run_with_history</code> + wrapper</a></h3> <p>Rejected. Breaking the existing <code>Runtime::run</code> signature would force every existing caller (sub-project 4's tests + tau-cli's <code>cmd::run</code>) to update for a feature only <code>tau chat</code> uses today. Additive <code>run_with_history</code> plus a thin <code>Runtime::run</code> wrapper preserves source compatibility for every existing caller and isolates the history-threading complexity to the one consumer that needs it. See decision 15.</p> <h3 id="i---json-mode-on-tau-chat"><a class="header" href="#i---json-mode-on-tau-chat">I. <code>--json</code> mode on <code>tau chat</code></a></h3> <p>Rejected. <code>tau chat</code> is interactive — JSON output during a REPL would confuse both the user (they want rendered Markdown) and any hypothetical script (a script wanting JSON should use <code>tau run --json</code> in a loop). Hard-rejecting <code>--json</code> on <code>tau chat</code> at argument parse time is clearer than silently downgrading to plain text. See decision 8.</p> <h3 id="j-per-failurekind-exit-code-sub-codes-eg-10--policydenied-11--outofresources"><a class="header" href="#j-per-failurekind-exit-code-sub-codes-eg-10--policydenied-11--outofresources">J. Per-<code>FailureKind</code> exit-code sub-codes (e.g., 10 = PolicyDenied, 11 = OutOfResources)</a></h3> <p>Rejected. Coupling exit codes to <code>FailureKind</code> variants forces every new <code>FailureKind</code> to allocate an exit code and forces CI scripts to maintain a code-to-kind mapping. The three-bucket scheme keeps exit codes stable across <code>FailureKind</code> additions; precision-needing consumers use <code>--json</code>. See decision 7.</p> <div style="break-before: page; page-break-before: always;"></div><h1 id="adr-0008-plugin-loading-mechanism--ipc-over-messagepack-rpc--tau-pkg-tau-runtime-tau-domain-amendments"><a class="header" href="#adr-0008-plugin-loading-mechanism--ipc-over-messagepack-rpc--tau-pkg-tau-runtime-tau-domain-amendments">ADR-0008: Plugin loading mechanism — IPC over MessagePack-RPC + tau-pkg, tau-runtime, tau-domain amendments</a></h1> <p><strong>Status:</strong> Accepted <strong>Date:</strong> 2026-04-28 <strong>Supersedes:</strong> — <strong>Closes:</strong> <a href="decisions/0007-tau-cli.html">ADR-0007</a> §18 ("plugin loading deferred to Phase 1+"). <strong>Amends:</strong> <a href="decisions/0004-tau-pkg.html">ADR-0004</a> §3 (install lifecycle gains a build step for <code>kind = "rust-cargo"</code> plugin packages), <a href="decisions/0006-tau-runtime.html">ADR-0006</a> §17 (additive <code>RuntimeError::Plugin*</code> variants, <code>plugin_host</code> module, ten new tracing events). <strong>Refines:</strong> <a href="decisions/0005-package-source-and-kind-serde.html">ADR-0005</a> (custom serde via Display/FromStr — same pattern applied to <code>PortKind</code> and <code>PluginKind</code>).</p> <h2 id="context-8"><a class="header" href="#context-8">Context</a></h2> <p>Phase 0 sub-project 5 (<a href="decisions/0007-tau-cli.html">ADR-0007</a> §18) explicitly deferred plugin loading to Phase 1+. <code>tau install</code> already records package source trees on disk, but the v0.1 runtime had no mechanism to turn those source trees into running plugin processes the kernel could dispatch through. Integration tests instead used <code>cfg(feature = "test-mock")</code> compiled-in backends — viable for proving the kernel works end-to-end, but not a path to user-supplied plugins.</p> <p>This ADR closes that gap as the first sub-project of Phase 1 (ROADMAP Phase 1 priority 1). It commits the plugin-loading mechanism, ships the two new workspace crates (<code>tau-plugin-protocol</code>, <code>tau-plugin-sdk</code>) and the per-port host module (<code>tau-runtime::plugin_host</code>), exercises the mechanism end-to-end with two toy plugins (<code>echo-llm</code>, <code>echo-tool</code>), retires the <code>test-mock</code> feature, and bundles the four ports the kernel defines (<code>LlmBackend</code>, <code>Tool</code>, <code>Storage</code>, <code>Sandbox</code>) into one cohesive loading surface.</p> <p>The kernel surface is <strong>unchanged</strong>. Plugin loading produces <code>Arc<dyn Dyn{LlmBackend,Tool,Storage,Sandbox}></code> proxies that the existing <code>Runtime::run</code> / <code>Runtime::run_with_history</code> consume without knowing they are remote. All Phase 0 capability filtering, tracing, and dispatch logic applies to plugin-backed implementations identically.</p> <p>Per QG18, plugin trait boundaries and serve-mode-adjacent IPC schemas require ADRs. This ADR bundles 18 design decisions plus the four ports' IPC bindings plus the supporting tau-pkg / tau-domain amendments, mirroring the <a href="decisions/0006-tau-runtime.html">ADR-0006</a> / <a href="decisions/0007-tau-cli.html">ADR-0007</a> precedent of grouping tightly-coupled cross-crate amendments into one ADR for design coherence. All amendments here are solely motivated by the plugin-loading mechanism; no promiscuous bundling.</p> <p>Relevant Constitution constraints (spec §1.2):</p> <div class="table-wrapper"><table><thead><tr><th>Constraint</th><th>Mechanism's answer</th></tr></thead><tbody> <tr><td><code>forbid(unsafe_code)</code> workspace-wide</td><td>IPC fits without exception — process-level isolation, no FFI at the host boundary.</td></tr> <tr><td><strong>G6</strong> runtime not framework</td><td>Loading produces port proxies the kernel consumes; no new abstraction over the agent loop.</td></tr> <tr><td><strong>G9</strong> observable by default</td><td>Ten new tracing events; plugin-side <code>tracing</code> re-emitted via stderr; protocol recording is built in.</td></tr> <tr><td><strong>G12</strong> sandboxing</td><td>Out-of-scope here (priority 12), but the IPC mechanism is the <em>prerequisite</em> — the process boundary already exists; priority 12 will bolt platform sandbox primitives onto the spawn path.</td></tr> <tr><td><strong>G15</strong> continue-on-fail</td><td>Plugin crashes resolve in-flight calls to <code>RuntimeError::PluginCrashed</code>; host stays up.</td></tr> <tr><td><strong>NG4</strong> no marketplace</td><td>Plugins distribute as git URLs; tau-pkg builds from source; no registry, no signed binaries.</td></tr> <tr><td><strong>NG9</strong> no credential management</td><td>Plugin config is a static map passed at handshake; how plugins source secrets (env, OS keychain) is each plugin's concern, not the loader's.</td></tr> <tr><td><strong>NG10</strong> no telemetry</td><td>Tracing events are local; recording is an explicit user opt-in via <code>--record-protocol</code>.</td></tr> </tbody></table> </div> <p>This is the first sub-project of Phase 1, and the mechanism here is the substrate priorities 2 (real LLM-backend plugin) and 3 (real Tool plugin) build on directly.</p> <h2 id="decision-8"><a class="header" href="#decision-8">Decision</a></h2> <h3 id="1-mechanism-out-of-process-ipc"><a class="header" href="#1-mechanism-out-of-process-ipc">1. Mechanism: out-of-process IPC</a></h3> <p>Plugins run as separate child processes of the host. Communication is over the child's stdio pipes. Picked head-to-head against three alternatives (see <em>Alternatives considered: mechanism</em> below for the full rejection rationale):</p> <ul> <li><strong>dlopen / <code>abi_stable</code></strong> — rejected on <code>forbid(unsafe_code)</code> and on the inability to recover from a plugin crashing without taking the host down.</li> <li><strong>WASM / WASI</strong> — rejected on tooling immaturity in 2026 for long-lived host processes hosting many guests, plus the LLM-client- in-WASM ecosystem still being thin (<code>reqwest</code> doesn't run cleanly).</li> <li><strong>Per-host-process plugin pool with shared memory</strong> — rejected as a premature optimization; the IPC overhead at sub-millisecond scale is invisible next to LLM call latency, and the ergonomics complexity is high.</li> </ul> <p>Out-of-process IPC fits the constitution cleanly: the process boundary is the natural place to bolt G12 sandbox primitives onto later (seccomp / landlock / sandbox-exec / AppContainer), and a plugin crash resolves in-flight calls to <code>RuntimeError::PluginCrashed</code> without taking the host down.</p> <h3 id="2-wire-format-messagepack-rpc-over-stdio-with-length-prefixed-framing"><a class="header" href="#2-wire-format-messagepack-rpc-over-stdio-with-length-prefixed-framing">2. Wire format: MessagePack-RPC over stdio with length-prefixed framing</a></h3> <p>Each message is a length-prefixed MessagePack body:</p> <pre><code>+--------+--------+--------+--------+================+ | big-endian u32 length (excl PFX) | MessagePack | +--------+--------+--------+--------+ message body | +================+ </code></pre> <p>Picked for: binary efficiency (~3–5× over JSON for tau payloads), self-describing structure (lossless round-trip to JSON for debug), serde-derive ergonomics on existing <code>tau-ports</code> types (no parallel schema), and 2026 ecosystem maturity (<code>rmp-serde = "1"</code>).</p> <p>Length-prefix is stricter than vanilla MessagePack-RPC requires (the format is self-delimiting), but it gives three benefits: (1) each message is a discrete chunk in a recording log; (2) non-Rust plugin authors can read N bytes deterministically; (3) defensive resync if the wire is ever corrupted. Max body size 64 MiB, configurable via <code>PluginHostOptions</code>.</p> <p>The MessagePack-RPC frame shapes are:</p> <div class="table-wrapper"><table><thead><tr><th>Frame</th><th>Shape</th></tr></thead><tbody> <tr><td>Request</td><td><code>[0, msgid: u32, method: str, params: array]</code></td></tr> <tr><td>Response</td><td><code>[1, msgid: u32, error: ErrorObj | nil, result: any]</code></td></tr> <tr><td>Notification</td><td><code>[2, method: str, params: array]</code></td></tr> </tbody></table> </div> <p>Alternative (rejected): JSON-RPC over stdio. Smaller payloads in MessagePack matter for streaming chunks and tool-arg blobs; JSON's self-describing-ness is preserved by <code>rmp-serde</code>'s lossless conversion to JSON for debug purposes.</p> <h3 id="3-lifecycle-long-lived-multiplexed-plugin-processes-per-host-session"><a class="header" href="#3-lifecycle-long-lived-multiplexed-plugin-processes-per-host-session">3. Lifecycle: long-lived multiplexed plugin processes per host session</a></h3> <p>One plugin process per (binary, host session) lives for the whole <code>tau run</code> / <code>tau chat</code> invocation. Picked for:</p> <ul> <li><strong>TLS / HTTP keepalive amortization</strong> — a real LLM-backend plugin reuses connections across calls; per-call spawn would force fresh TLS handshakes.</li> <li><strong>REPL responsiveness</strong> — <code>tau chat</code> issues many turns; spawn cost per turn would compound to dozens of seconds.</li> <li><strong>Amortized spawn cost</strong> — the build step (Decision 6) means plugin binaries aren't tiny; spawning once per call would be wasteful.</li> </ul> <p>Per-call spawn was rejected for compounding overhead in chat workloads; shared-pool-across-host-invocations was rejected for v0.1 because it adds a daemon supervision concern that the constitution doesn't motivate yet.</p> <h3 id="4-concurrency-json-rpc-id-correlated-multiplexing-concurrent-by-default"><a class="header" href="#4-concurrency-json-rpc-id-correlated-multiplexing-concurrent-by-default">4. Concurrency: JSON-RPC <code>id</code>-correlated multiplexing; concurrent by default</a></h3> <p>A single plugin process handles multiple in-flight requests by msgid correlation. The SDK's runner dispatches each <code>Request</code> frame on a fresh <code>tokio::spawn</code>, so plugins are concurrent by default. An opt-in serial mode is provided for plugins with non-<code>Send</code> state (e.g., a plugin holding a <code>&mut</code> SQLite connection); the SDK exposes this via a runner option, not a separate runner type.</p> <p>Alternatives rejected:</p> <ul> <li><strong>One request at a time per plugin</strong> — would block REPL streaming on any other in-flight call; trivially wrong for the multi-tool case.</li> <li><strong>Per-port dedicated processes</strong> — already the lifecycle (one process per loaded port); concurrency is orthogonal.</li> </ul> <h3 id="5-streaming-notification-based-via-streamchunk--final-response"><a class="header" href="#5-streaming-notification-based-via-streamchunk--final-response">5. Streaming: notification-based via <code>stream.chunk</code> + final response</a></h3> <p>Streaming <code>llm.stream</code> calls (see Decision 18 below — wire method is <code>llm.stream</code>, not <code>llm.complete_streaming</code> as the spec drafted) are modelled on the LSP <code>partialResult</code> precedent. Host sends an <code>llm.stream</code> request with msgid=N. Plugin emits zero or more <code>stream.chunk</code> notifications referencing N:</p> <pre><code>[2, "stream.chunk", [N, <CompletionChunk>]] </code></pre> <p>Plugin terminates by sending the regular response on msgid=N carrying <code>{ stop_reason, usage }</code>. On error mid-stream, the plugin sends an error response on msgid=N and the host SDK propagates a <code>LlmError</code> into the stream's <code>Err</code> arm.</p> <p>Host-side, a <code>stream_router</code> collects <code>stream.chunk</code> notifications into an mpsc channel terminated by the final response, exposing a <code>Pin<Box<dyn Stream<Item = Result<CompletionChunk, LlmError>>>></code> to the runtime. The runtime consumes it identically to an in-process implementation.</p> <p>Alternative rejected: streaming-over-newline-delimited-JSON on a sidecar pipe. Complexity-for-no-gain; the MessagePack-RPC notification form already covers this case and round-trips cleanly through the recording sink.</p> <h3 id="6-discovery--build-plugin-table--kind--rust-cargo-build-at-install-time"><a class="header" href="#6-discovery--build-plugin-table--kind--rust-cargo-build-at-install-time">6. Discovery + build: <code>[plugin]</code> table + <code>kind = "rust-cargo"</code> build at install time</a></h3> <p>Plugin packages declare a <code>[plugin]</code> table in their <code>tau.toml</code>:</p> <pre><code class="language-toml">[plugin] provides = "llm_backend" # llm_backend | tool | storage | sandbox kind = "rust-cargo" # only kind in v0.1; #[non_exhaustive] bin = "echo-llm" # cargo bin target name </code></pre> <p><code>tau install</code> shells out to <code>cargo build --release --bin <plugin.bin></code> in the cloned package directory at install time. Stdout / stderr stream to host's tracing as <code>target = "tau_pkg::build"</code> (INFO for stdout, WARN for stderr). On non-zero exit, the lockfile is NOT written; the cloned source tree is retained for inspection / <code>tau install --force</code>. Future kinds (<code>PythonPip</code>, <code>NodeNpm</code>, <code>Prebuilt</code>) are additive enum variants on the <code>#[non_exhaustive]</code> <code>PluginKind</code>.</p> <p>Alternatives rejected:</p> <ul> <li><strong>Build at run time, not install time</strong> — would surface compile errors on first <code>tau run</code>, breaking the install-time error contract; would also slow first-run.</li> <li><strong>Pre-built binary distribution</strong> — incompatible with NG4 (no marketplace) at v0.1; deferred until a <code>Prebuilt</code> kind variant lands.</li> <li><strong>Manifest-as-binary-only-distribution</strong> — same as above; no marketplace path means no path to ship binaries.</li> </ul> <h3 id="7-handshake-host-initiated-metahandshake-with-strict-validation"><a class="header" href="#7-handshake-host-initiated-metahandshake-with-strict-validation">7. Handshake: host-initiated <code>meta.handshake</code> with strict validation</a></h3> <p>Host first sends <code>[0, 1, "meta.handshake", [{ protocol_version, port, trace_context, config }]]</code>. Plugin replies with <code>protocol_version</code>, <code>provides</code>, <code>plugin_name</code>, <code>plugin_version</code>, <code>methods</code>, <code>schemas</code>. The host validates:</p> <div class="table-wrapper"><table><thead><tr><th>Rule</th><th>Failure variant</th></tr></thead><tbody> <tr><td><code>protocol_version</code> matches host's</td><td><code>ProtocolVersionMismatch { host, plugin }</code></td></tr> <tr><td><code>provides</code> matches the manifest's <code>[plugin] provides</code></td><td><code>ProvidesMismatch { manifest, plugin_advertised }</code></td></tr> <tr><td><code>methods</code> includes all required for the port</td><td><code>MissingRequiredMethod { method }</code></td></tr> <tr><td>Reply parses as a valid <code>HandshakeResponse</code></td><td><code>Malformed { detail }</code></td></tr> <tr><td>Reply arrives within <code>handshake_timeout_ms</code> (default 5000)</td><td><code>Timeout</code></td></tr> </tbody></table> </div> <p>On any failure: kill the process, return <code>RuntimeError::PluginHandshakeFailed { plugin, reason }</code> with a structured <code>HandshakeFailureReason</code>. The plugin is not given a chance to re-handshake; the contract is strict.</p> <p>The <code>provides</code> cross-check (manifest vs. advertised) is the security- critical step: a tool plugin tagged <code>provides = "llm_backend"</code> in its <code>tau.toml</code> but advertising <code>tool</code> at handshake (or vice versa) would otherwise let one port masquerade as another. Mismatch is fatal at handshake time.</p> <p>Alternative rejected: handshake-less protocol (assume protocol v1, no schema introspection). Foreseeable cost of cross-version handling without a handshake (silent decoding errors mid-call) outweighs the ~5 ms handshake cost amortized over an entire host session.</p> <h3 id="8-shutdown-metashutdown-notification--graceful-timeout-chain"><a class="header" href="#8-shutdown-metashutdown-notification--graceful-timeout-chain">8. Shutdown: <code>meta.shutdown</code> notification + graceful timeout chain</a></h3> <p>Host sends <code>[2, "meta.shutdown", []]</code> on host exit. SDK closes in-flight call handles, runs the plugin's shutdown hook (if implemented), exits within <code>shutdown_timeout_ms</code> (default 2000). After timeout: SIGTERM, wait 500 ms, then SIGKILL. The full sequence is:</p> <ol> <li>Send <code>meta.shutdown</code> notification.</li> <li>Wait for child exit, up to <code>options.shutdown_timeout</code> (default 2 s).</li> <li>If still alive: SIGTERM, wait 500 ms.</li> <li>If still alive: SIGKILL.</li> <li>Tracing event <code>plugin.exited { plugin, exit_code, signal, clean }</code>.</li> </ol> <p>Alternative rejected: closing stdin only and relying on the SDK's read-loop seeing EOF.
