Less explicit, harder to instrument, and asymmetric with the request-shaped lifecycle of every other host→plugin operation. The notification form mirrors <code>meta.handshake</code>'s request-shape and reads naturally in protocol recordings.</p> <h3 id="9-observability-plugin-side-tracing-events-json-encoded-to-stderr"><a class="header" href="#9-observability-plugin-side-tracing-events-json-encoded-to-stderr">9. Observability: plugin-side <code>tracing</code> events JSON-encoded to stderr</a></h3> <p>Plugin SDK ships a <code>tracing-subscriber</code> JSON layer pre-configured to write events to stderr. Host's stderr task reads each line, parses each as a JSON tracing event, and re-emits via <code>tracing::Event::dispatch</code> with <code>target = format!("plugin::{}", plugin_name)</code>. Lines that fail JSON parse are emitted raw at WARN as <code>tracing::warn!(target = "plugin::{name}::raw", "{line}")</code>.</p> <p>This means a tau user setting <code>RUST_LOG=tau=debug,plugin::echo-llm=debug</code> sees the plugin's own tracing alongside host tracing in one stream, properly leveled, with no special configuration on the plugin author's side. The SDK provides the layer; the plugin author writes <code>tracing::info!("turn ready")</code> and it shows up in the host log.</p> <p>Alternative rejected: sidecar tracing transport (separate file, IPC channel). Cost of separate channel ≫ value: stderr is already there, already lossless, and already conventionally used for diagnostic output.</p> <h3 id="10-trace-context-flat-trace_context-field-in-handshake"><a class="header" href="#10-trace-context-flat-trace_context-field-in-handshake">10. Trace context: flat <code>trace_context</code> field in handshake</a></h3> <p>The <code>meta.handshake</code> request carries <code>trace_context: { run_id, agent_id, root_span_id }</code>. Plugin SDK injects these as fields on every tracing event the plugin emits. True distributed-span stitching (per-call parent-span IDs threaded through notifications, span lifecycle propagation) is deferred to G14 perf budgets / priority 13.</p> <p>Alternative rejected: per-call trace context on every Request frame. Substantial wire-overhead for marginal diagnostic value at v0.1; the flat-context-per-handshake form is sufficient because each host session has one run-id. Per-call context lands as an additive future field on Request <code>params</code> when priority 13 motivates it.</p> <h3 id="11-config-delivery-static-in-metahandshake"><a class="header" href="#11-config-delivery-static-in-metahandshake">11. Config delivery: static, in <code>meta.handshake</code></a></h3> <p>Plugin config (the <code>[agents.<id>.config]</code> table from project <code>tau.toml</code> or the equivalent for the active agent) is serialized to JSON and passed once in the handshake. Per-call config overrides are not supported in v0.1 — additive future field on Request <code>params</code> when demand materializes.</p> <p>Alternative rejected: streaming config updates via a notification. Adds a config-mutation surface that the constitution doesn't motivate at v0.1; static handshake-time config is sufficient for echo plugins, HTTP-LLM plugins, and tool plugins anticipated in priorities 2 and 3.</p> <h3 id="12-sandboxing-deferred-to-priority-12"><a class="header" href="#12-sandboxing-deferred-to-priority-12">12. Sandboxing: deferred to priority 12</a></h3> <p>Plugin processes in v0.1 run with full host privileges. Toy plugins are author-trusted; real plugins (priorities 2 and 3) are user-trusted via the install-time provenance of <code>tau install <git-url></code>. OS-level sandbox primitives (seccomp / landlock / sandbox-exec / AppContainer) land in their own sub-project (priority 12). The IPC mechanism here is the <em>prerequisite</em> — the process boundary already exists; priority 12 will bolt platform sandboxing onto the spawn path.</p> <p>Alternative rejected: minimal sandbox at v0.1 (e.g., closing all FDs, clearing env). Half-measures invite false security claims; better to ship full-privilege at v0.1 and document it explicitly than ship a patchwork that gets read as "sandboxed".</p> <h3 id="13-sdk-shape-per-port-generic-runner-functions-no-proc-macros"><a class="header" href="#13-sdk-shape-per-port-generic-runner-functions-no-proc-macros">13. SDK shape: per-port generic runner functions; no proc macros</a></h3> <p>Plugin author implements the <em>same</em> <code>tau_ports::*</code> trait the kernel uses. The SDK exposes a free function per port:</p> <pre><pre class="playground"><code class="language-rust"><span class="boring">#![allow(unused)] </span><span class="boring">fn main() { </span>pub async fn run_llm_backend<T: LlmBackend + Send + Sync + 'static>( plugin: T, ) -> Result<(), SdkError>; pub async fn run_tool<T: Tool + Send + Sync + 'static>(plugin: T) -> Result<(), SdkError>; pub async fn run_storage<T: Storage + Send + Sync + 'static>(plugin: T) -> Result<(), SdkError>; pub async fn run_sandbox<T: Sandbox + Send + Sync + 'static>(plugin: T) -> Result<(), SdkError>; <span class="boring">}</span></code></pre></pre> <p>Plugin author's <code>main.rs</code>:</p> <pre><pre class="playground"><code class="language-rust">#[tokio::main] async fn main() -> Result<(), Box<dyn std::error::Error>> { run_llm_backend(MyBackend::new()).await?; Ok(()) }</code></pre></pre> <p>That's the entire surface. No <code>#[derive(Plugin)]</code>. No <code>#[async_trait]</code>. No magic. Plain Rust.</p> <p>Alternatives rejected:</p> <ul> <li><strong>Proc-macro <code>#[plugin]</code></strong> — adds compile-time dependencies and a parallel trait surface that diverges from the kernel's. Rejected on G6 (runtime not framework) and constitution simplicity bias.</li> <li><strong>Single <code>run_plugin(provides, plugin)</code> runner</strong> — would force a parallel trait union; per-port runners are clearer, type-safer, and the runtime cost of having four <code>async fn</code>s in the SDK is zero.</li> <li><strong>Plugin-as-library with embed-host pattern</strong> — would require the plugin author to write the <code>main</code> themselves and reach into the SDK; per-port runner functions hide the framing / handshake / shutdown loop entirely.</li> </ul> <h3 id="14-configure-trait--two-runner-flavors-per-port"><a class="header" href="#14-configure-trait--two-runner-flavors-per-port">14. <code>Configure</code> trait + two runner flavors per port</a></h3> <p>For plugins that consume the <code>meta.handshake</code> <code>config</code> field, the SDK exposes a <code>Configure</code> trait:</p> <pre><pre class="playground"><code class="language-rust"><span class="boring">#![allow(unused)] </span><span class="boring">fn main() { </span>pub trait Configure { type Config: serde::de::DeserializeOwned; fn from_config(config: Self::Config) -> Result<Self, ConfigError> where Self: Sized; } <span class="boring">}</span></code></pre></pre> <p>Two flavors per port runner: <code>run_llm_backend(plugin)</code> (no config — plugin already constructed) vs <code>run_llm_backend_with_config::<T>()</code> (T impls Configure; runner constructs T from handshake config). Plugin author picks based on whether they need config.</p> <p><code>ConfigError</code> has typed variants: <code>Decode(#[from] serde_json::Error)</code>, <code>MissingField(&'static str)</code>, <code>InvalidValue { field, detail }</code>. No <code>Internal</code> variant — the same discipline as Decision 18 below applies SDK-wide.</p> <p>Alternative rejected: a single runner that accepts a <code>Box<dyn Fn(Value) -> Result<T, ConfigError>></code> constructor. More verbose at the call site and forces the plugin author to box a closure; two named functions are clearer.</p> <h3 id="15-testing-layered-mock-stdio-peer--real-spawn-integration"><a class="header" href="#15-testing-layered-mock-stdio-peer--real-spawn-integration">15. Testing: layered (mock stdio peer + real-spawn integration)</a></h3> <p>Tests are layered for correctness vs. mechanism validation:</p> <ul> <li><strong>Mock stdio peer</strong> (<code>FakeStdioPeer</code> in <code>tau-plugin-protocol</code> behind <code>test-support</code> feature): used by <code>tau-plugin-sdk</code> runners and <code>tau-runtime::plugin_host</code> <code>Ipc*</code> adapters to drive each side against a deterministic peer. Fast (~2 s per crate), no subprocess overhead, full control over crash / timeout / malformed responses.</li> <li><strong>Real-spawn integration</strong> in <code>tau-cli</code>: <code>cargo build</code> → <code>tau run echo-agent "..."</code> against the real <code>echo-llm</code> / <code>echo-tool</code> processes. Slower (~10 s) but proves the full mechanism end-to-end including the build step, handshake, dispatch, streaming, shutdown, and tracing re-emit.</li> <li><strong>Phase 0 <code>test-mock</code> feature is retired</strong>: <code>tau-cli</code>'s <code>cfg(feature = "test-mock")</code> blocks are deleted; <code>cmd::run</code> and <code>cmd::chat</code> rewire through <code>plugin_host</code> exclusively. The <code>no-default-features-cli</code> CI job continues to run unchanged (it never relied on <code>test-mock</code>).</li> </ul> <p>Alternatives rejected:</p> <ul> <li><strong>Real-spawn only</strong> — would slow per-crate test feedback to unacceptable levels; the mock peer covers ~80% of correctness cases.</li> <li><strong>Mock peer only</strong> — would leave the build step, the actual stdio framing, and the <code>Command::spawn</code> path untested. Phase 0's bias against trigger-pathless code disallows this.</li> </ul> <h3 id="16-toy-plugins-echo-llm--echo-tool-under-cratestau-plugins"><a class="header" href="#16-toy-plugins-echo-llm--echo-tool-under-cratestau-plugins">16. Toy plugins: <code>echo-llm</code> + <code>echo-tool</code> under <code>crates/tau-plugins/</code></a></h3> <p>Two toy plugins ship in this sub-project as workspace members:</p> <ul> <li><strong><code>echo-llm</code></strong>: <code>LlmBackend</code> plugin returning canned responses from config (static <code>canned_text</code> or scripted <code>script[turn]</code>). Test-only modes (<code>crash_after_handshake</code>, <code>delay_response_ms</code>, <code>error_on_method</code>) gate via config flags for deterministic failure- path testing.</li> <li><strong><code>echo-tool</code></strong>: <code>Tool</code> plugin echoing its <code>text</code> arg back as a text content block.</li> </ul> <p>Storage and Sandbox toy plugins are explicitly deferred — <code>tau-runtime</code> doesn't wire those ports into the agent loop in v0.1, so their toy plugins land alongside their host-wiring sub-project.</p> <p>Toy plugins build under <code>cargo build --workspace</code>; CI catches breakage immediately. They are excluded from any <code>--release</code> artifact tau might publish (they're test fixtures, not products).</p> <p>Alternative rejected: ship toy plugins for all four ports. Storage and Sandbox aren't kernel-exercised in v0.1, so toy plugins for them would test a mechanism with no consumer — dead-code-shaped tests that earn nothing.</p> <h3 id="17-debug-tier-protocol-recording--live-decode--3-new-subcommands"><a class="header" href="#17-debug-tier-protocol-recording--live-decode--3-new-subcommands">17. Debug tier: protocol recording + live decode + 3 new subcommands</a></h3> <p>Five debug capabilities ship in v0.1:</p> <ol> <li><strong>Protocol recording</strong> (<code>--record-protocol <path></code>): every plugin process spawned during this <code>tau</code> invocation has its host-side framer wrapped in a <code>RecordingTap</code> that mirrors all frames to the path as JSONL. Format includes <code>{ts, plugin, dir, msgid, method, frame: <base64>}</code>. Replayable.</li> <li><strong>Live wire-decode tracing</strong>: when <code>RUST_LOG=tau_runtime::plugin_host::wire=debug</code>, the read-loop and writer-mutex emit a tracing event per frame with the decoded body pretty-printed as JSON. Decode happens lazily; at higher log levels the tracing subscriber's filter rejects the event before any decode work happens.</li> <li><strong><code>tau plugin protocol decode <path></code></strong>: human-readable transcript reader for recording files. Filters by plugin / method / time.</li> <li><strong><code>tau plugin run <binary> [--interactive | --script]</code></strong>: standalone plugin runner. Interactive REPL drives method calls and prints responses; scripted form replays a <code>script.jsonl</code>.</li> <li><strong><code>tau plugin describe <name></code></strong>: resolves an installed plugin from the lockfile, spawns it, runs <code>meta.handshake</code>, prints metadata, runs <code>meta.describe</code> on each method, dumps schemas. Plugin shut down cleanly after.</li> </ol> <p>Three of the five (recording, live decode, describe) are nearly free byproducts of the framer + handshake design. Two (decode CLI, interactive runner) are small new subcommands, ~150 LOC each. Total debug-tier surface ~400 LOC; small enough to ship in v0.1 without slipping the sub-project.</p> <p>Alternative rejected: ship debug tier as a separate sub-project. The binary wire format is opaque enough that without these tools, a malformed frame would be near-impossible to debug; shipping the mechanism without them would be hostile to plugin authors.</p> <h3 id="18-errors-four-new-typed-runtimeerror-variants-one-new-installerror-no-new-internal"><a class="header" href="#18-errors-four-new-typed-runtimeerror-variants-one-new-installerror-no-new-internal">18. Errors: four new typed <code>RuntimeError</code> variants; one new <code>InstallError</code>; NO new <code>Internal</code></a></h3> <p><code>tau-runtime::RuntimeError</code> gains four variants:</p> <pre><pre class="playground"><code class="language-rust"><span class="boring">#![allow(unused)] </span><span class="boring">fn main() { </span>PluginSpawnFailed { plugin: String, source: io::Error } PluginHandshakeFailed { plugin: String, reason: HandshakeFailureReason } PluginCrashed { plugin: String, exit_status: ExitStatus, stderr_tail: String } PluginContractViolation { plugin: String, detail: String } <span class="boring">}</span></code></pre></pre> <p><code>HandshakeFailureReason</code> is a structured sub-enum with five variants (per Decision 7).</p> <p><code>tau-pkg::InstallError</code> gains two:</p> <pre><pre class="playground"><code class="language-rust"><span class="boring">#![allow(unused)] </span><span class="boring">fn main() { </span>BuildFailed { exit_status: ExitStatus, stderr_tail: String } CargoNotFound <span class="boring">}</span></code></pre></pre> <p><code>tau-plugin-protocol::ProtocolError</code>, <code>tau-plugin-sdk::SdkError</code>, and <code>tau-plugin-sdk::ConfigError</code> are similarly typed-variant-only.</p> <p><strong>No new <code>Internal</code> variants ship anywhere.</strong> The mechanical CI test <code>crates/tau-domain/tests/escape_hatch_registry.rs</code> continues to gate against accidental additions. This codifies the discipline that <code>PluginContractViolation</code> and <code>Sandbox(_)</code> are not <code>Internal</code> escapes — each new variant has a concrete reachable failure path backed by ≥1 test, per the Phase-0 mid memo and ADR-0007 §17.</p> <h2 id="alternatives-considered-mechanism"><a class="header" href="#alternatives-considered-mechanism">Alternatives considered (mechanism)</a></h2> <p>The single biggest decision in this ADR is Decision 1 (out-of-process IPC). Three alternatives were considered head-to-head before committing.</p> <h3 id="a-dlopen--abi_stable-in-process-dynamic-linking"><a class="header" href="#a-dlopen--abi_stable-in-process-dynamic-linking">A. dlopen / <code>abi_stable</code> (in-process dynamic linking)</a></h3> <p>Dynamically link plugin <code>.so</code> / <code>.dylib</code> / <code>.dll</code> into the host's address space; calls go through <code>abi_stable</code>'s ABI-stable trait objects.</p> <p><strong>Rejected</strong> because:</p> <ul> <li>Workspace's <code>forbid(unsafe_code)</code> would need an exception for the dlopen call site and for <code>abi_stable</code>'s opaque pointer marshalling. Constitution-level workspace lints are not worth bending for one feature.</li> <li>A plugin crashing (<code>abort</code>, segfault, <code>panic</code> across an FFI boundary) takes the entire host down. <code>tau chat</code> evaporating because a tool plugin panic'd is a UX regression we can't accept.</li> <li>ABI evolution is a permanent tax: every <code>tau-ports</code> field addition forces an ABI bump. The IPC mechanism's wire-stable serialization insulates the host crate from this.</li> <li>Loading-time overhead (dlopen + ABI trait construction) is roughly comparable to spawn cost; the supposed in-process performance win is thin once the LLM call dominates.</li> </ul> <h3 id="b-wasm--wasi"><a class="header" href="#b-wasm--wasi">B. WASM / WASI</a></h3> <p>Plugins compile to WASM modules; host instantiates them in wasmtime / wasmer.</p> <p><strong>Rejected</strong> because:</p> <ul> <li>2026 ecosystem maturity for hosting-many-long-lived-guests is still thin. Component-model adoption is patchy.</li> <li>LLM-client-in-WASM (<code>reqwest</code>-style HTTP) doesn't run cleanly without WASI extensions that aren't universally available — defeats the purpose of plugin authors writing real backends.</li> <li>Capability-based security via WASI is a real win, but it's a v0.2+ story; v0.1 priority 12 will deliver OS-level sandboxing on the IPC path with broader scope (not just compute, also network and FS).</li> <li>Build complexity for plugin authors (WASM target, no native crates) is high enough that priority 2's first real LLM backend would have to fight the ecosystem to ship.</li> </ul> <p>WASM remains attractive for a future "untrusted plugin" tier. The IPC mechanism doesn't preclude that direction; it simply doesn't pay the ecosystem cost in 2026.</p> <h3 id="c-shared-memory-ring-buffer-with-one-host-process-and-per-plugin-worker-threads"><a class="header" href="#c-shared-memory-ring-buffer-with-one-host-process-and-per-plugin-worker-threads">C. Shared-memory ring buffer with one host process and per-plugin worker threads</a></h3> <p>Single process, plugins linked statically, communicate over a shared-memory ring buffer.</p> <p><strong>Rejected</strong> because:</p> <ul> <li>Premature optimization: IPC overhead at sub-millisecond scale is invisible next to LLM call latency (typical 200 ms – 5 s). The 100 µs serialize+pipe write cost shows up nowhere in the budget.</li> <li>Static linking forces every plugin into the host's binary; defeats user-supplied plugins entirely.</li> <li>Re-introduces all of (A)'s crash-blast-radius problems with extra ring-buffer reasoning on top.</li> </ul> <h2 id="cross-references-1"><a class="header" href="#cross-references-1">Cross-references</a></h2> <ul> <li><strong>Supersedes</strong> <a href="decisions/0007-tau-cli.html">ADR-0007</a> §18: the "plugin loading deferred to Phase 1+" decision is now closed by this ADR.</li> <li><strong>Builds on</strong> <a href="decisions/0004-tau-pkg.html">ADR-0004</a> §3: the install lifecycle gains a build step (Decision 6) for <code>kind = "rust-cargo"</code> plugin packages. <code>LockedPackage</code> gains an optional <code>plugin: Option<LockedPlugin></code> field; lockfile schema bumps v1 → v2 with auto-upgrade on next install.</li> <li><strong>Follows the pattern of</strong> <a href="decisions/0005-package-source-and-kind-serde.html">ADR-0005</a>: <code>PortKind</code> and <code>PluginKind</code> use custom serde via Display/FromStr, serializing as <code>"llm_backend"</code> / <code>"rust-cargo"</code> strings rather than adjacent-tagged objects. Same ergonomics, same TOML-friendliness.</li> <li><strong>Amends</strong> <a href="decisions/0006-tau-runtime.html">ADR-0006</a> §17 (additive vocabulary): four new <code>RuntimeError::Plugin*</code> variants, the <code>plugin_host</code> module, and ten new tracing events join the kernel's vocabulary. The §6 capability filter remains correct under IPC because it runs <em>before</em> the request crosses the wire — the plugin never sees tools the agent isn't authorized to use. Integration tests verify this.</li> <li><strong>Builds on</strong> <a href="decisions/0007-tau-cli.html">ADR-0007</a> §15: <code>Runtime::run_with_history</code> is the kernel entry point <code>tau chat</code> threads through <code>plugin_host</code>- produced <code>Arc<dyn DynLlmBackend></code> proxies. Both the §14 capability- filter amendment and the §15 <code>run_with_history</code> amendment apply unchanged to plugin-backed implementations.</li> <li><strong>ROADMAP</strong>: closes Phase 1 priority 1; substrate for priorities 2 (real LLM-backend plugin) and 3 (real Tool plugin), each its own sub-project building on this mechanism.</li> </ul> <h2 id="consequences-8"><a class="header" href="#consequences-8">Consequences</a></h2> <h3 id="positive-4"><a class="header" href="#positive-4">Positive</a></h3> <ul> <li>Plugin loading is real. Users can <code>tau install <git-url></code> a plugin package, and the next <code>tau run</code> / <code>tau chat</code> will spawn it as a subprocess and dispatch through it.</li> <li>Two new workspace crates (<code>tau-plugin-protocol</code>, <code>tau-plugin-sdk</code>) are stable, documented, and tested. Plugin authors target plain Rust with the same <code>tau_ports::*</code> traits the kernel uses; no proc macros, no derive, no parallel trait surface.</li> <li>The kernel surface is unchanged. All Phase 0 capability filtering, tracing, dispatch, and <code>Runtime::run_with_history</code> paths apply to plugin-backed implementations identically.</li> <li>Crash isolation is real (G15): a plugin process crashing resolves in-flight calls to <code>RuntimeError::PluginCrashed</code> and the host stays up. <code>tau chat</code> recovers by surfacing the error to the REPL.</li> <li>Observability is real (G9): ten new tracing events on the host side, plugin-side tracing re-emitted via stderr at <code>target = plugin::<name></code>, protocol recording one flag away.</li> <li>Debug tier ships in v0.1: <code>tau plugin describe</code>, <code>tau plugin run</code>, <code>tau plugin protocol decode</code>, plus <code>--record-protocol</code> and live wire decode tracing. Binary wire format opacity is fully addressed.</li> <li>Priorities 2 (real LLM backend) and 3 (real Tool plugin) are unblocked. Each is now its own sub-project building on a stable IPC mechanism.</li> </ul> <h3 id="negative-4"><a class="header" href="#negative-4">Negative</a></h3> <ul> <li><strong>Per-call serde overhead</strong> at sub-millisecond scale (MessagePack encode + pipe write + plugin decode + plugin re-encode + host decode). Invisible next to LLM latency, but real, and visible in micro-benchmarks. Documented; performance budgets land with priority 13.</li> <li><strong>Lockfile schema bump v1 → v2.</strong> Existing v0.1 installations auto-upgrade on next <code>tau install</code>, but older <code>tau</code> binaries reading a v2 lockfile surface <code>LockfileVersionTooNew</code>. Documented in release notes and in the migration section below.</li> <li><strong>Plugin processes run with full host privileges in v0.1.</strong> OS-level sandboxing is priority 12 (a separate sub-project); v0.1 documents this explicitly. Toy plugins are author-trusted; real plugins (priorities 2 and 3) inherit the user-trust of <code>tau install <git-url></code>.</li> <li><strong>One port per package, one binary per port.</strong> Multi-port plugins (one binary providing both an <code>LlmBackend</code> and a related <code>Tool</code>) are deferred for simplicity. Will become an additive future field on <code>PluginManifest</code> if priority 2/3 plugins motivate it.</li> <li><strong>No auto-restart / circuit-breaker.</strong> A crashed plugin returns <code>RuntimeError::PluginCrashed</code> and the user re-invokes. Documented; deferred indefinitely (re-invocation is acceptable for the developer- tool target audience per NG11).</li> <li><strong><code>test-mock</code> feature retired.</strong> Pre-existing tests that gated on <code>feature = "test-mock"</code> rebuild against <code>echo-llm</code> / <code>echo-tool</code>. CI matrix gains three build jobs (<code>tau-plugin-protocol</code>, <code>tau-plugin-sdk</code>, <code>tau-plugins</code>). Total required checks 12 → 15.</li> <li><strong><code>#[tokio::main]</code> already coupled <code>tau-cli</code> to tokio (per ADR-0007 §2);</strong> <code>tau-runtime</code> now expands its <code>tokio</code> features to include <code>process</code> and <code>io-util</code> for the host side. Documented. The runtime stays async-runtime-agnostic via the <code>LlmBackend</code>/<code>Tool</code> traits; only the plugin-host module commits to tokio, mirroring tau-cli's binary-side commitment.</li> </ul> <h3 id="neutral--new-obligations-4"><a class="header" href="#neutral--new-obligations-4">Neutral / new obligations</a></h3> <ul> <li>Future tau-runtime / tau-pkg / tau-domain amendments motivated by their own sub-projects (or a non-plugin-loading consumer) get their own ADRs; no promiscuous bundling.</li> <li>The ten new tracing events join the <a href="decisions/0006-tau-runtime.html">ADR-0006</a> §3.9 vocabulary as additive (non-breaking per ADR-0006 §17). Future renames or removals require an ADR.</li> <li>The wire vocabulary (<code>meta.*</code>, <code>llm.*</code>, <code>tool.*</code>, <code>storage.*</code>, <code>sandbox.*</code>, <code>stream.*</code> method namespaces) is now a public-facing schema. Breaking changes require a <code>protocol_version</code> bump and an ADR; additive method or field additions on existing methods follow the additive-vocabulary discipline.</li> <li>Plugin authors writing against <code>tau-plugin-sdk</code> are bound to the <code>tau_ports::*</code> trait surface — that's deliberate (G6: kernel and plugins share one trait surface, no parallel one).</li> </ul> <h2 id="out-of-scope"><a class="header" href="#out-of-scope">Out of scope</a></h2> <p>The spec's §2.1 explicitly defers the following topics; they belong to their own sub-projects, not this one:</p> <div class="table-wrapper"><table><thead><tr><th>Topic</th><th>Where it lives</th></tr></thead><tbody> <tr><td>Real LLM-backend plugin (Anthropic / OpenAI HTTP)</td><td>Phase 1 priority 2</td></tr> <tr><td>Real Tool plugin (<code>fs-read</code>, <code>shell</code>)</td><td>Phase 1 priority 3</td></tr> <tr><td>Capability override (project tau.toml <code>[agents.<id>.capabilities]</code>)</td><td>Phase 1 priority 4 (tier 2)</td></tr> <tr><td>Transitive <code>requires.tools</code> auto-install</td><td>Phase 1 priority 5 (tier 2)</td></tr> <tr><td>Schema validation for tool args</td><td>Phase 1 priority 6 (tier 2) — <code>RuntimeError::PluginContractViolation</code> activates here</td></tr> <tr><td><code>tau update</code> / <code>tau verify</code> / <code>tau uninstall</code></td><td>Phase 1 priority 7 (tier 2)</td></tr> <tr><td>Streaming LLM responses end-to-end (<code>Runtime::run_streaming</code>)</td><td>Phase 1 priority 8 (tier 2) — protocol-side streaming primitive lands here, but the kernel consumer is priority 8</td></tr> <tr><td>Multi-agent orchestration</td><td>Phase 1 priority 9 (tier 3)</td></tr> <tr><td>Workflow / pipeline runner</td><td>Phase 1 priority 10 (tier 3)</td></tr> <tr><td>REPL persistence</td><td>Phase 1 priority 11 (tier 3)</td></tr> <tr><td>OS-level sandboxing</td><td>Phase 1 priority 12 (tier 3)</td></tr> <tr><td>Performance budgets in CI</td><td>Phase 1 priority 13 (tier 4)</td></tr> <tr><td><code>cargo audit</code> + <code>cargo-deny</code> in CI</td><td>Phase 1 priority 14 (tier 4)</td></tr> <tr><td>Serve mode (JSON-RPC over stdio)</td><td>Phase 1 priority 15 (tier 4) — distinct from this sub-project's IPC; "serve mode" is the <em>kernel</em> exposing JSON-RPC to <em>outer</em> tools, not plugins talking to the kernel</td></tr> <tr><td>Conformance test suite</td><td>Deferred until at least two real implementations exist</td></tr> <tr><td>Auto-restart / circuit breaker around crashed plugins</td><td>Deferred indefinitely</td></tr> </tbody></table> </div> <h2 id="migration"><a class="header" href="#migration">Migration</a></h2> <p>Per spec §11:</p> <div class="table-wrapper"><table><thead><tr><th>Concern</th><th>Path</th></tr></thead><tbody> <tr><td><strong>Lockfile schema</strong></td><td>TOML <code>version = 1</code> → <code>version = 2</code>. v1 lockfiles auto-upgrade on the next <code>tau install</code> (re-read manifests, re-build any <code>[plugin]</code> packages, write v2). Older <code>tau</code> binaries reading a v2 lockfile surface the existing <code>LockfileVersionTooNew</code> error path — no new error variant needed.</td></tr> <tr><td><strong>Existing v0.1 installations</strong></td><td><code>LockedPackage { plugin: None }</code> for legacy installs. <code>tau ls</code> shows them as data-only; <code>tau run</code> referencing them as a plugin fails with <code>RuntimeError::PluginContractViolation { detail: "package is not a plugin (no [plugin] manifest table)" }</code>. Documented in release notes.</td></tr> <tr><td><strong><code>test-mock</code> feature</strong></td><td>Removed from <code>tau-cli/Cargo.toml</code>. <code>cfg(feature = "test-mock")</code> blocks deleted. Tests previously gated on this rebuild against <code>echo-llm</code> / <code>echo-tool</code>. The <code>no-default-features-cli</code> CI job continues to run unchanged (it never relied on <code>test-mock</code>).</td></tr> <tr><td><strong>Existing <code>Runtime::run</code> consumers</strong></td><td>Unchanged. The kernel's signature is identical; the only difference is the type of <code>Arc<dyn DynLlmBackend></code> it receives. All Phase 0 integration tests keep passing.</td></tr> <tr><td><strong>Plugin author distribution</strong></td><td>Pre-amendment: no plugins to distribute. Post-amendment: <code>tau install <git-url></code> clones + builds. No backward-incompatibility because there is no "back".</td></tr> </tbody></table> </div> <h2 id="plan-erratum-carryovers"><a class="header" href="#plan-erratum-carryovers">Plan-erratum carryovers</a></h2> <p>Items discovered during implementation that diverge from the spec text. The wire vocabulary and trait shapes documented elsewhere in this ADR reflect the <strong>as-implemented</strong> truth; this section is the audit trail.</p> <ol> <li><strong><code>tau-ports</code> had no <code>serde</code> feature</strong> at the start of the sub- project (discovered in Task 1, RESOLVED in Task 9). The plan's Cargo.toml templates initially prescribed <code>tau-ports = { workspace = true, features = ["serde"] }</code> for both <code>tau-plugin-protocol</code> and <code>tau-plugin-sdk</code>, but <code>tau-ports/Cargo.toml</code> exposed only <code>default</code> and <code>test-fixtures</code>. Task 1 dropped the non-existent feature flag. Task 9 added the <code>serde</code> feature to <code>tau-ports/Cargo.toml</code> (propagating to <code>tau-domain/serde</code> + <code>uuid/serde</code>), gated all <code>Serialize</code> / <code>Deserialize</code> derives behind it, and restored <code>features = ["serde"]</code> on the two new crates' <code>tau-ports</code> deps. <code>Namespace</code> / <code>Key</code> use <code>serde(into = "String", try_from = "String")</code> to preserve their validating constructors.</li> <li><strong>Wire method <code>llm.complete_streaming</code> is named <code>llm.stream</code></strong> in the implementation. Spec §4.3 / §4.4 / §4.5 / §4.6 reference <code>llm.complete_streaming</code>; those references are stale. The actual <code>tau_ports::LlmBackend</code> trait method is <code>stream</code> (not <code>complete_streaming</code>), so the SDK runner dispatches <code>llm.stream</code> over the wire. The streaming notification method <code>stream.chunk</code> is unchanged. <strong>The canonical wire vocabulary is <code>llm.complete</code>, <code>llm.stream</code>, <code>stream.chunk</code></strong> — this ADR is the authoritative record. Future docs / spec edits should align.</li> <li><strong><code>CompletionChunk::Done</code> is named <code>CompletionChunk::Finish</code></strong> in actual <code>tau-ports</code>. The spec's <code>CompletionChunk::Done { stop_reason, usage }</code> should be read as <code>CompletionChunk::Finish { stop_reason, usage }</code>. The terminal-marker semantics are identical; only the variant name differs.</li> <li><strong><code>Tool</code> is stateful</strong> with an <code>init</code> / <code>invoke</code> / <code>teardown</code> lifecycle (a Phase 0 design decision that the plan did not surface until Task 9). The SDK's <code>run_tool</code> runs the full lifecycle per <code>tool.call</code>. Host-side <code>IpcTool</code> (Task 15) maps a single <code>tool.call</code> RPC into one full plugin-side init→invoke→teardown sequence. The stateless <code>fn(args) -> result</code> model the spec implied is incorrect; the actual contract is the lifecycle the kernel already uses in-process.</li> <li><strong><code>with_dyn_*</code> builder methods on <code>RuntimeBuilder</code></strong> were added in Task 15 (<code>with_dyn_llm_backend</code>, <code>with_dyn_tool</code>, <code>with_dyn_storage</code>, <code>with_dyn_sandbox</code>). Necessary because IPC adapters return <code>Arc<dyn Dyn*></code> (the dyn-compatible shim trait) but the existing <code>with_*</code> methods are bounded on the native <code>LlmBackend</code> / <code>Tool</code> / etc. traits, which IPC adapters can't implement directly (native <code>async fn</code> in trait isn't dyn-compatible). The <code>Dyn*</code> shim traits already exist in tau-runtime per Phase 0 ADR-0006; the new <code>with_dyn_*</code> methods simply expose them as builder entry points. Existing <code>with_*</code> callers are unchanged.</li> </ol> <p>These five carryovers are recorded for fresh-eyes review (Task 25) and for future reference. None of them changes the <em>decisions</em> in this ADR — they document where the implementation's vocabulary diverged from the spec's.</p> <h2 id="implementation-reference"><a class="header" href="#implementation-reference">Implementation reference</a></h2> <p>Tasks 1–22 of the implementation plan (<code>docs/superpowers/plans/2026-04-28-plugin-loading.md</code>) deliver this ADR's decisions:</p> <div class="table-wrapper"><table><thead><tr><th>Tasks</th><th>Decisions</th></tr></thead><tbody> <tr><td>1</td><td>Workspace scaffold; <code>tau-plugin-protocol</code> + <code>tau-plugin-sdk</code> crates</td></tr> <tr><td>2</td><td><code>tau-domain::PluginManifest</code> / <code>PortKind</code> / <code>PluginKind</code> (Decision 6 schema)</td></tr> <tr><td>3–6</td><td>Wire framer, <code>Frame</code> enum, error envelope, handshake/shutdown payload types, <code>FakeStdioPeer</code> (Decisions 2, 5, 7, 8, 15)</td></tr> <tr><td>7–10</td><td>SDK tracing layer, handshake builder, per-port runners, <code>Configure</code> trait (Decisions 9, 10, 13, 14)</td></tr> <tr><td>11–12</td><td>tau-pkg <code>[plugin]</code> manifest parsing, <code>BuildOptions</code>, install-time build, <code>LockedPlugin</code>, lockfile v1→v2 (Decision 6)</td></tr> <tr><td>13–17</td><td>tau-runtime <code>plugin_host</code> module, spawn + handshake + stderr re-emit + shutdown, <code>IpcLlmBackend</code> / <code>IpcTool</code> / <code>IpcStorage</code> / <code>IpcSandbox</code>, <code>stream_router</code>, <code>RecordingSink::JsonlFile</code> (Decisions 1, 3, 4, 5, 7, 8, 9, 17, 18)</td></tr> <tr><td>18</td><td><code>echo-llm</code> + <code>echo-tool</code> toy plugins (Decision 16)</td></tr> <tr><td>19</td><td>Drop <code>test-mock</code> feature; rewire <code>cmd::run</code> + <code>cmd::chat</code> (Decision 15)</td></tr> <tr><td>20</td><td><code>--record-protocol</code> global flag; <code>tau plugin {describe, run, protocol decode}</code> subcommands (Decision 17)</td></tr> <tr><td>21</td><td><code>tau-cli</code> real-spawn integration tests (Decision 15)</td></tr> <tr><td>22</td><td>CI gains three build jobs; branch protection updated (Decision 18 audit gate)</td></tr> <tr><td>23</td><td>This ADR + index update</td></tr> <tr><td>24</td><td>Final local verification + mark PR ready</td></tr> <tr><td>25</td><td>ADR-0008 fresh-eyes review (24 h or self-review per QG22) — flips status from Proposed to Accepted</td></tr> <tr><td>26</td><td>Plan sign-off + ROADMAP + branch-protection update + squash merge</td></tr> </tbody></table> </div> <p>The status of this ADR flips from <strong>Proposed</strong> to <strong>Accepted</strong> at Task 25 sign-off.</p> <div style="break-before: page; page-break-before: always;"></div><h1 id="adr-0009-typed-llmerror-migration-policy--conformance-suite-charter"><a class="header" href="#adr-0009-typed-llmerror-migration-policy--conformance-suite-charter">ADR-0009: Typed <code>LlmError</code> migration policy + conformance suite charter</a></h1> <p><strong>Status:</strong> Accepted <strong>Date:</strong> 2026-04-29 <strong>Deciders:</strong> Titouan Lebocq <strong>Supersedes:</strong> — <strong>Closes:</strong> <a href="decisions/0008-plugin-loading.html">ADR-0008</a> §17 (conformance test suite deferral — "until ≥2 real LLM-backend implementations exist"). <strong>Amends:</strong> — <strong>Refines:</strong> <a href="decisions/0007-tau-cli.html">ADR-0007</a> (escape-hatch registry rule applies to the <code>LlmError::Internal</code> callsite-scope reduction in this sub-project).</p> <h2 id="context-9"><a class="header" href="#context-9">Context</a></h2> <p>Phase 1 sub-project 2c shipped the OpenAI plugin alongside two infrastructure deliverables:</p> <ol> <li>A shared <code>tau-plugin-test-support</code> crate (cassette replayer lifted from anthropic; rule-of-three refactor at N=3 plugins).</li> <li>A <code>tau-plugin-conformance</code> parameterized behavioral test crate.</li> </ol> <p>Both pre-existing plugins (anthropic, ollama) had been mapping every non-2xx HTTP response to <code>LlmError::Internal { message }</code> — a deliberate v0.1 simplification (deferred per spec §1 of both prior sub-projects). At N=3 plugins, the cost of this is concrete:</p> <ul> <li><code>tau_runtime</code> and tool callers cannot branch on retry-eligibility. <code>LlmError::is_retryable()</code> returns <code>true</code> for <code>RateLimited / Transport / Stream / Provider</code> and <code>false</code> for <code>Internal</code> — meaning every 429 / 5xx that should retry was being mis-classified as non-retryable, silently losing the signal.</li> <li>Callers that want to wait <code>Retry-After</code> seconds before the next call must string-grep <code>Internal.message</code>; the typed <code>RateLimited { retry_after_seconds: Option<u32> }</code> variant carries the integer structurally.</li> <li>Error envelope shapes differ across providers (Anthropic typed, OpenAI typed, Ollama bare-string), but consumers expect a uniform surface.</li> </ul> <p><code>tau_ports::LlmError</code> is <code>#[non_exhaustive]</code> and <strong>already</strong> had the typed variants needed (<code>InvalidRequest</code>, <code>RateLimited</code>, <code>Auth</code>, <code>Transport</code>, <code>Stream</code>, <code>Provider</code>). The work was a migration, not a vocabulary expansion.</p> <p>The conformance suite was deferred in ADR-0008 §17 explicitly until two-or-more real plugins existed. Three now do; the parameterized harness becomes high-leverage.</p> <h2 id="decision-9"><a class="header" href="#decision-9">Decision</a></h2> <h3 id="a-typed-error-mapping-policy"><a class="header" href="#a-typed-error-mapping-policy">A. Typed-error mapping policy</a></h3> <p>All <code>tau</code> LLM-backend plugins MUST emit typed <code>LlmError</code> variants for HTTP-mapped failures:</p> <div class="table-wrapper"><table><thead><tr><th>Status</th><th>Typed variant</th></tr></thead><tbody> <tr><td>400</td><td><code>LlmError::InvalidRequest { reason }</code></td></tr> <tr><td>401, 403</td><td><code>LlmError::Auth { message }</code></td></tr> <tr><td>404</td><td><code>LlmError::InvalidRequest { reason }</code> (with remediation embedded in <code>reason</code> when applicable)</td></tr> <tr><td>429</td><td><code>LlmError::RateLimited { retry_after_seconds: Option<u32> }</code> (parsed from <code>Retry-After</code> HTTP header)</td></tr> <tr><td>5xx (except 501)</td><td><code>LlmError::Provider { message }</code> (retryable per <code>is_retryable()</code>)</td></tr> <tr><td>Network / TLS / DNS</td><td><code>LlmError::Transport { message }</code></td></tr> <tr><td>Mid-stream</td><td><code>LlmError::Stream { message }</code> (only emitted from stream items)</td></tr> </tbody></table> </div> <p><code>map_response_error</code> MUST take the signature <code>(status, headers, body)</code>. The <code>headers</code> parameter is required so 429 responses can populate <code>RateLimited.retry_after_seconds</code> from the <code>Retry-After</code> HTTP header. Plugin <code>complete()</code> and <code>stream()</code> methods MUST extract <code>headers</code> BEFORE consuming the response via <code>Response::text()</code> (which moves the response).</p> <p><code>LlmError::Internal { message }</code> is RESERVED for plugin-internal translation errors only (e.g., wrapping a <code>BuildError</code> from <code>request.rs</code> when the typed-tau-domain → JSON conversion fails). It MUST NOT be used for HTTP-mapped paths.</p> <p>The <code>llmerror-internal</code> entry in <a href="decisions/../explanation/escape-hatches.html"><code>docs/explanation/escape-hatches.md</code></a> remains active. Its scope narrows post-migration — <code>Internal</code> callsites now exist only at the BuildError/ParseError translation boundary, not at the HTTP-mapping boundary. The mechanical CI test at <code>crates/tau-domain/tests/escape_hatch_registry.rs</code> continues to gate against accidental NEW <code>Internal</code> / <code>Custom</code> variants in <code>tau-ports</code>. <strong>No new such variants ship in this sub-project.</strong></p> <p><code>LlmError::ModelNotFound</code> (a typed variant we don't yet have) is OUT of scope for v0.1: <code>InvalidRequest { reason }</code> with the remediation hint embedded in <code>reason</code> is sufficient. A future sub-project may promote it when a caller needs to branch on the case structurally.</p> <h3 id="b-conformance-suite-charter"><a class="header" href="#b-conformance-suite-charter">B. Conformance suite charter</a></h3> <p>A new crate <code>tau-plugin-conformance</code> provides <code>ConformanceSuite::default().run(build_plugin, cassettes_dir).await</code>, where <code>build_plugin: Fn(String) -> impl LlmBackend</code> returns a freshly configured plugin pointed at the per-test cassette server's URL.</p> <p>The catalog at v0.1 is FIXED at 6 baseline tests:</p> <ol> <li><code>batch_happy_path</code> — <code>complete()</code> returns Ok; non-empty <code>text</code>; valid <code>stop_reason</code>.</li> <li><code>batch_with_tools</code> — one <code>tool_use</code> with non-empty id+name and Object-typed input.</li> <li><code>streaming_text</code> — at least one <code>Text</code> chunk; exactly one terminal <code>Finish</code>.</li> <li><code>streaming_tool_use</code> — at least one <code>ToolUse</code> chunk before <code>Finish</code>; <code>tu.input</code> is Object.</li> <li><code>error_rate_limited</code> — 429-exhausting cassette → typed <code>LlmError::RateLimited</code>.</li> <li><code>error_auth</code> — 401 cassette → typed <code>LlmError::Auth</code>.</li> </ol> <p>The catalog is conservative by design. The suite tests <strong>mechanical correctness</strong>: request shape, response shape, stream chunk ordering, error typing. The suite does NOT test:</p> <ul> <li><strong>Response quality</strong> (does the model follow the instruction? is the answer right?). <a href="decisions/../../CONSTITUTION.html">Constitution NG7</a> explicitly forbids tau evaluating quality.</li> <li>Specific response text or <code>stop_reason</code> values beyond "valid variant". Plugins differ in how they map provider-specific finish-reasons to <code>tau_ports::StopReason</code>; mandating exact strings would break that flexibility.</li> <li>Specific tool_use ids. Some plugins synthesize ids (Ollama); others preserve provider ids (Anthropic, OpenAI). The suite asserts only "id is non-empty".</li> <li>Specific token counts. Different providers tokenize differently; asserting numeric equality would fail spuriously.</li> </ul> <p>Catalog extension requires a follow-up ADR-amendment. Adding tests is non-trivial because each new test must hold for ALL plugins simultaneously — a stricter contract than per-plugin tests.</p> <p>Per-plugin cassettes live at <code>crates/tau-plugins/<plugin>/tests/conformance-cassettes/<test_name>.yaml</code>, with file names matching the test catalog. Each plugin's <code>tests/conformance.rs</code> is a 5-15-line shim that wires its <code>Configure::from_config</code> into the closure-based suite API.</p> <p>The suite panics on the first assertion failure with a descriptive message including the test name. The caller's <code>#[tokio::test]</code> surface fails accordingly.</p> <h2 id="consequences-9"><a class="header" href="#consequences-9">Consequences</a></h2> <h3 id="positive-5"><a class="header" href="#positive-5">Positive</a></h3> <ul> <li><code>tau_runtime</code>'s retry helper can use <code>LlmError::is_retryable()</code> honestly. Today every variant including <code>Internal</code> is non-retryable; post-migration, <code>RateLimited</code>, <code>Provider</code>, <code>Transport</code>, and <code>Stream</code> correctly mark transient failures as retryable.</li> <li>Future LLM-backend plugin authors get a behavioral test suite for free. Adding sub-project 2d (next provider) is a smaller surface because the conformance shim catches mechanical correctness errors before any plugin-specific tests run.</li> <li>The cassette replayer's centralization (~323 LOC) eliminates drift across plugins. Past sub-projects had to maintain three copies; future plugins import the shared crate.</li> <li>17 → 21 required CI checks gating <code>main</code> (<code>build (openai-plugin)</code>, <code>build (tau-plugin-test-support)</code>, <code>build (tau-plugin-conformance)</code>, <code>test (conformance)</code>).</li> </ul> <h3 id="negative-5"><a class="header" href="#negative-5">Negative</a></h3> <ul> <li>The PR shipping this ADR is large (~3000 LOC churn across 5+ crates). Reviewers must trust the per-task subagent-driven workflow + per-plugin test runs.</li> <li>Conformance cassettes are duplicated across three plugins (each plugin needs its own cassette directory because wire formats differ). 18 cassette YAMLs total. A future cassette record-mode replayer could automate maintenance.</li> <li><code>map_response_error</code>'s 3-arg signature <code>(status, headers, body)</code> is a MINOR breaking change for the in-tree plugins; external plugin authors who copied the 2-arg signature from earlier sub- projects will need to update. Acceptable: no external plugins exist yet at this phase.</li> </ul> <h3 id="neutral"><a class="header" href="#neutral">Neutral</a></h3> <ul> <li>The <code>LlmError::Internal</code> variant remains in <code>tau-ports</code> (no vocabulary deprecation). Callsites narrow but the variant stays — there are still legitimate plugin-internal translation errors that warrant the <code>Internal</code> escape hatch.</li> <li>The conformance suite is <code>dev-dependency</code>-only; it adds no runtime surface to the runtime or any plugin binary.</li> </ul> <h3 id="obligations"><a class="header" href="#obligations">Obligations</a></h3> <ul> <li>Future LLM-backend plugin authors MUST integrate with the conformance suite by adding <code>tests/conformance.rs</code> + a <code>tests/conformance-cassettes/</code> directory.</li> <li>Future plugin authors MUST NOT use <code>LlmError::Internal</code> for HTTP-mapped paths.</li> </ul> <h2 id="alternatives-considered-8"><a class="header" href="#alternatives-considered-8">Alternatives considered</a></h2> <h3 id="alt-a-defer-typed-error-migration-to-a-separate-sub-project"><a class="header" href="#alt-a-defer-typed-error-migration-to-a-separate-sub-project">Alt A: Defer typed-error migration to a separate sub-project</a></h3> <p>Ship OpenAI with <code>Internal</code>-only mapping like 2a/2b; let a follow-up sub-project handle the typed migration across all three plugins.</p> <p><strong>Rejected:</strong> The migration is mechanical (1-for-1 cassette assertion updates) and bundling it with sub-project 2c amortizes the testing overhead — the existing anthropic + ollama integration tests run against the typed mappers as a regression check. Splitting would require running the same tests twice (once with <code>Internal</code>, once typed) for no architectural benefit.</p> <h3 id="alt-b-add-llmerrormodelnotfound-typed-variant"><a class="header" href="#alt-b-add-llmerrormodelnotfound-typed-variant">Alt B: Add <code>LlmError::ModelNotFound</code> typed variant</a></h3> <p>Promote 404 errors to a typed <code>ModelNotFound { model: String }</code> variant.</p> <p><strong>Rejected for v0.1:</strong> Three providers each represent "model not found" differently (OpenAI: <code>code: "model_not_found"</code>; Ollama: <code>error.error: "model 'X' not found"</code>; Anthropic: <code>error.type: "not_found_error"</code>). A typed variant would encode one of these shapes; structurally embedding the model name is non-trivial because not all providers return it consistently. <code>InvalidRequest { reason }</code> with the model name embedded in <code>reason</code> is adequate at v0.1; revisit when a real caller needs to branch on the case.</p> <h3 id="alt-c-conformance-suite-as-a-trait-not-a-closure"><a class="header" href="#alt-c-conformance-suite-as-a-trait-not-a-closure">Alt C: Conformance suite as a trait, not a closure</a></h3> <p><code>pub trait PluginBuilder { type Plugin: LlmBackend; fn build(&self, base_url: String) -> Self::Plugin; }</code> plus <code>ConformanceSuite::run<P: PluginBuilder>(&self, builder: &P, ...)</code>.</p> <p><strong>Rejected:</strong> Yet another trait to define and implement. The closure signature <code>Fn(String) -> impl LlmBackend</code> is idiomatic Rust, requires no boilerplate, and supports the same use cases. Per-plugin shims become 5-15 lines instead of 30+.</p> <h3 id="alt-d-conformance-catalog-extends-to-response-quality-tests"><a class="header" href="#alt-d-conformance-catalog-extends-to-response-quality-tests">Alt D: Conformance catalog extends to response-quality tests</a></h3> <p>Add a "model-follows-instructions" test that asserts the response text contains the requested keywords.</p> <p><strong>Rejected (NG7):</strong> <a href="decisions/../../CONSTITUTION.html">Constitution NG7</a> forbids tau evaluating model quality. Quality tests belong in downstream projects (e.g., <code>stature</code>, the opinionated coding pipeline). The conformance suite is mechanical correctness only; this boundary is explicit in the catalog charter to prevent scope creep.</p> <div style="break-before: page; page-break-before: always;"></div><h1 id="adr-0010-tool-args-schema-validation-policy"><a class="header" href="#adr-0010-tool-args-schema-validation-policy">ADR-0010: Tool-args schema validation policy</a></h1> <p><strong>Status:</strong> Accepted <strong>Date:</strong> 2026-04-30 <strong>Deciders:</strong> Titouan Lebocq <strong>Supersedes:</strong> — <strong>Closes:</strong> <a href="decisions/0006-tau-runtime.html">ADR-0006</a> §3 + Consequences (lines 376-380) — <code>RuntimeError::PluginContractViolation</code> was "wired but not yet trigger-pathed"; <code>deserialize_tool_args</code> was a v0.1 passthrough. <strong>Amends:</strong> — <strong>Refines:</strong> <a href="decisions/0006-tau-runtime.html">ADR-0006</a> §9 (outcome/error dichotomy — this ADR explicitly classifies validation failure modes across the build-time / invoke-time boundary).</p> <h2 id="context-10"><a class="header" href="#context-10">Context</a></h2> <p>Tools today declare an <code>input_schema: tau_domain::Value</code> (a JSON Schema object) via <code>Tool::schema().input_schema</code>, but the runtime never validates the LLM's tool-call args against it before invoking <code>Tool::invoke</code>. Each plugin guards its own arg shape via ad-hoc deserialization (e.g. fs-read's <code>parse_path_arg</code> returning <code>BadArgs</code> if <code>path</code> is missing). The cost of this:</p> <ol> <li>Plugins reimplement the same checks. Drift between schemas and guards is inevitable; the schema becomes documentation, not enforcement.</li> <li>Error message format varies per plugin. When the LLM produces a bad tool call, the recovery message it sees is whatever the plugin author wrote — sometimes precise, sometimes "missing field".</li> <li>The schema isn't validated at registration time. A typo in <code>"type": "objectt"</code> silently ships in <code>tau install</code>, and only blows up when the LLM happens to emit a call that exercises the broken constraint — <em>after</em> tokens have been spent.</li> </ol> <p>ADR-0006 §3 / Consequences (lines 376-380) reserved this work explicitly:</p> <blockquote> <p><code>RuntimeError::PluginContractViolation</code> is wired (Task 10) but the v0.1 implementation does not have a trigger path: <code>deserialize_tool_args</code> is a passthrough today. Phase-1+ schema validation will populate this variant; until then the variant is dead code on every observed run.</p> </blockquote> <p>This ADR closes that reservation by hoisting validation to the kernel.</p> <h2 id="decision-10"><a class="header" href="#decision-10">Decision</a></h2> <p>Five inter-locking commitments:</p> <h3 id="1-dialect-json-schema-draft-7"><a class="header" href="#1-dialect-json-schema-draft-7">1. Dialect: JSON Schema Draft 7</a></h3> <p>Plugin authors write Draft-7-flavored schemas via <code>serde_json::json!{...}</code> literals (or equivalent). The runtime uses the <a href="https://crates.io/crates/jsonschema"><code>jsonschema</code></a> crate configured <code>Draft::Draft7</code>.</p> <p>Rationale: Draft 7 is what every shipped tau plugin's <code>Tool::schema()</code> already uses — <code>type</code>, <code>properties</code>, <code>required</code>, <code>items</code>, <code>minimum</code>, <code>maximum</code>, <code>description</code>, <code>default</code>. It matches the <a href="https://modelcontextprotocol.io/">MCP</a> spec's tool-input format and Anthropic's tool-use API. Migration to Draft 2020-12 is deferred to a future ADR if the ecosystem moves.</p> <p>Trigger to revisit: ecosystem-wide adoption of Draft 2020-12 in LLM tool-use APIs.</p> <h3 id="2-validation-location-tau-runtime-kernel"><a class="header" href="#2-validation-location-tau-runtime-kernel">2. Validation location: tau-runtime kernel</a></h3> <p>Validation runs at <code>tau-runtime::tool_args::validate_tool_args</code>, called from <code>run.rs</code> immediately before <code>Tool::invoke</code>. This replaces the v0.1 <code>deserialize_tool_args</code> passthrough.</p> <p>Rationale: the hook was already in place at <code>run.rs:417</code> with the right signature (post-capability-check, pre-invoke). One enforcement point eliminates plugin/runtime drift. Routing failures through typed error variants (<code>BuildError::ToolSchemaInvalid</code> at build, <code>ToolError::BadArgs</code> at invoke) integrates naturally with the existing <code>RuntimeBuilder::build()</code> / <code>Runtime::run</code> flows.</p> <p>Alternative considered: SDK-side enforcement (<code>tau-plugin-sdk::run_tool_with_io</code>). Rejected at v0.1 because in-process tools (the in-tree path used by every test) wouldn't exercise SDK-side validation, and out-of-process plugins still pay the IPC round-trip before validation fires.</p> <p>Trigger to revisit: an out-of-process plugin lying about its schema in the handshake response (responding with one schema then <code>Tool::invoke</code>-ing under a different one). At that point the runtime gains a parallel SDK-side enforcement path — see decision 5.</p> <h3 id="3-compilation-timing-at-runtimebuilderbuild"><a class="header" href="#3-compilation-timing-at-runtimebuilderbuild">3. Compilation timing: at <code>RuntimeBuilder::build()</code></a></h3> <p>Each registered tool's <code>input_schema</code> is compiled <strong>once</strong> via <code>ToolArgsValidator::compile(&input_schema)</code>. The compiled validator is stored in <code>Runtime.tool_validators: HashMap<String, ToolArgsValidator></code>, a parallel field next to <code>Runtime.tools</code>. Per-invoke validation just runs the compiled matcher (~10–50µs).</p> <p>Failure to compile (malformed schema) returns <code>SchemaCompileError</code>, which the builder maps to <code>BuildError::ToolSchemaInvalid { tool_name, detail }</code> — the build fails before any <code>Runtime::run</code> is called and before any LLM round-trip. This catches plugin-author bugs at the earliest possible point in the lifecycle.</p> <p>Empty schemas (<code>Value::Null</code> or <code>Value::Object(empty)</code>) opt out cleanly — <code>compile</code> returns a validator with <code>compiled: None</code> and <code>validate</code> is a no-op. Tools that genuinely accept arbitrary input declare an empty schema.</p> <p>Rationale: build-once-validate-many is the standard jsonschema pattern. The cost of compilation is non-trivial (regex precompile, type-coercion graph); paying it per-invoke is wasteful for an agent loop that may issue dozens of tool calls.</p> <p>Trigger to revisit: dynamic tool registration mid-run (currently impossible — <code>Runtime</code> is immutable after <code>build()</code>).</p> <h3 id="4-error-semantics-split-by-failure-mode"><a class="header" href="#4-error-semantics-split-by-failure-mode">4. Error semantics: split by failure mode</a></h3> <div class="table-wrapper"><table><thead><tr><th>Failure mode</th><th>Trigger path</th><th>Outcome</th><th>LLM sees</th></tr></thead><tbody> <tr><td>Schema malformed</td><td>Build time, in <code>compile()</code></td><td><code>BuildError::ToolSchemaInvalid</code> (build aborts)</td><td>Nothing — build fails before LLM is called</td></tr> <tr><td>Args mismatch</td><td>Invoke time, in <code>validate()</code></td><td><code>ToolError::BadArgs</code> (recoverable)</td><td>Structured error in conversation; loop continues; LLM self-corrects on next turn</td></tr> </tbody></table> </div> <p>The two failure modes have <strong>genuinely different recoverability profiles</strong>. A malformed schema is a plugin-author bug; the user needs to fix it, and continuing the run wastes tokens. An args mismatch is most likely an LLM hallucination; terminating the run on every hallucinated arg would be hostile to the dominant case.</p> <p><strong>MANDATORY rule (locked at validator boundary):</strong> every <code>ToolError::BadArgs.reason</code> produced by <code>ToolArgsValidator::validate</code> MUST contain three blocks:</p> <ol> <li><code>"You sent: {args_json}"</code> — the args the LLM actually emitted.</li> <li><code>"Expected (input_schema):\n{schema_json}"</code> — the full declared schema the args are failing against.</li> <li><code>"Specific issue(s):\n{validation_errors}"</code> — the per-field diagnostic from jsonschema's <code>iter_errors</code>.</li> </ol> <p>The rule is enforced at <code>ToolArgsValidator::validate</code>'s only return path, so callers cannot short-circuit it. Tests assert the literal substrings <code>"You sent:"</code>, <code>"Expected (input_schema):"</code>, and <code>"Specific issue"</code> are present in every failure-case error.</p> <p>Rationale: the LLM that emitted the bad call is also the one that needs to recover. Without the schema in the error message, the LLM may re-emit the same bad call because it doesn't know what shape is expected. With it, the error is <strong>self-instructive</strong>: the model sees <code>(what-I-sent, what-was-expected, why-it-failed)</code> in one round-trip and can correct.</p> <p>Trigger to revisit: real-world data showing the LLM doesn't recover even with the schema in the error — at which point error formatting becomes a tuning problem rather than a structural one.</p> <h3 id="5-runtimeerrorplugincontractviolation-stays-reserved"><a class="header" href="#5-runtimeerrorplugincontractviolation-stays-reserved">5. <code>RuntimeError::PluginContractViolation</code> stays reserved</a></h3> <p>The existing <code>RuntimeError::PluginContractViolation { plugin, detail }</code> variant remains documented and wired but <strong>does not gain a trigger path in this sub-project</strong>. ADR-0006 documented it as "wired but not yet trigger-pathed"; v0.1 of this work narrows the trigger paths to <strong>build-time <code>ToolSchemaInvalid</code></strong> and <strong>invoke-time <code>BadArgs</code></strong>. The reserved variant becomes the home for a future runtime check: out-of-process plugin lies about its schema in the handshake response, then later violates the declared contract during invoke.</p> <p>Rationale: opening that path requires SDK-side enforcement infrastructure (decision 2's "alternative considered"). Building it speculatively before a real motivating case lands would over- engineer the v0.1 surface.</p> <p>Trigger to revisit: a third-party tool plugin shipped via tau's plugin protocol whose handshake-declared schema diverges from its actual <code>Tool::invoke</code> behavior — at which point a runtime validation path lights up the variant.</p> <h2 id="consequences-10"><a class="header" href="#consequences-10">Consequences</a></h2> <h3 id="negative--new-cost"><a class="header" href="#negative--new-cost">Negative / new cost</a></h3> <ul> <li><code>tau-runtime</code> gains a transitive dep on <code>jsonschema = "0.46"</code> (~1MB compiled, brings <code>regex_syntax</code>, <code>fancy-regex</code>, <code>email_address</code>, <code>ahash</code> into the dep tree). Negligible vs. the existing reqwest / tokio / semver footprint.</li> <li><code>RuntimeBuilder::build()</code> is now O(tools × schema_size) at compile time. For typical agent configs (<10 tools, schemas in the hundreds of bytes) this is well under 1ms. Plugins with pathologically large schemas — e.g., a <code>enum</code> with 10000 entries — could push this; future perf work can address.</li> <li><code>Runtime</code> gains a parallel <code>tool_validators</code> field, increasing the struct size by a HashMap. Memory cost for typical configs is in the noise.</li> </ul> <h3 id="positive-6"><a class="header" href="#positive-6">Positive</a></h3> <ul> <li>Plugin authors stop reimplementing argument shape checks. The <code>parse_*_arg</code> patterns in shipped plugins (e.g., fs-read, shell) become redundant once Phase-2 cleanup lands; for v0.1 they coexist defensively.</li> <li>Plugin-author bugs (schema typos) catch at <code>tau install</code> / <code>tau run</code> startup before any LLM is called. Zero tokens wasted.</li> <li>LLMs get <strong>uniform</strong> structured error feedback across all tools, with the schema embedded for self-correction.</li> </ul> <h3 id="neutral--new-obligations-5"><a class="header" href="#neutral--new-obligations-5">Neutral / new obligations</a></h3> <ul> <li>Future tau-runtime API additions involving validation require their own ADRs (QG18). The MANDATORY-rule template is locked at this ADR; any softening (e.g., subschema-only error slicing) needs a new ADR.</li> <li>The <code>jsonschema</code> crate version is pinned to the major (<code>"0.46"</code>) in <code>[workspace.dependencies]</code>; major upgrades (e.g., 0.47) need to verify the public API surface — past versions of jsonschema have renamed types between minors.</li> </ul> <h2 id="alternatives-considered-9"><a class="header" href="#alternatives-considered-9">Alternatives considered</a></h2> <h3 id="a-hand-roll-a-minimal-draft-7-subset"><a class="header" href="#a-hand-roll-a-minimal-draft-7-subset">A. Hand-roll a minimal Draft 7 subset</a></h3> <p>Rejected. Validate only the keywords actually used by shipped plugins (<code>type</code>, <code>properties</code>, <code>required</code>, <code>items</code>, <code>minimum</code>, <code>maximum</code>). ~150 LOC + tests. Zero deps.</p> <p>Cons: any plugin author using <code>enum</code>, <code>pattern</code>, <code>format</code>, <code>oneOf</code> would silently have those keywords ignored — no compile-time warning, no runtime error, just silently permissive validation. For a system that will accept third-party plugins, this is a footgun.</p> <h3 id="b-schema-engine-valico-instead-of-jsonschema"><a class="header" href="#b-schema-engine-valico-instead-of-jsonschema">B. Schema engine: <code>valico</code> instead of <code>jsonschema</code></a></h3> <p>Rejected. Lighter (~200KB) but Draft-4-only and "lightly maintained" since 2023. Bus-factor risk if we hit a bug, and Draft 4's constraint vocabulary differs from what shipped plugins use (e.g., <code>required</code> was an object property in Draft 4, became a top-level array in Draft 6+).</p> <h3 id="c-validation-location-sdk-runner-only-in-plugin-enforcement"><a class="header" href="#c-validation-location-sdk-runner-only-in-plugin-enforcement">C. Validation location: SDK runner only (in-plugin enforcement)</a></h3> <p>Rejected. See decision 2's "alternative considered". The runtime boundary is the right enforcement point at v0.1; SDK-side adds coverage gaps for out-of-process plugins that bypass the SDK.</p> <h3 id="d-per-invoke-compilation-no-caching"><a class="header" href="#d-per-invoke-compilation-no-caching">D. Per-invoke compilation (no caching)</a></h3> <p>Rejected. See decision 3. Order-of-magnitude slower for busy agent loops; loses the registration-time well-formedness check that's load-bearing for decision 4's "schema malformed" build-fatal path.</p> <h3 id="e-treat-all-validation-failures-as-kernel-fatal"><a class="header" href="#e-treat-all-validation-failures-as-kernel-fatal">E. Treat all validation failures as kernel-fatal</a></h3> <p>(via <code>RuntimeError::PluginContractViolation</code>)</p> <p>Rejected. See decision 4. Args mismatch is dominantly an LLM hallucination (recoverable); terminating the run on every hallucinated arg is hostile to the dominant case. The build-fatal/invoke-recoverable split matches the actual recoverability profile.</p> <h2 id="references-1"><a class="header" href="#references-1">References</a></h2> <ul> <li>Spec: <code>docs/superpowers/specs/2026-04-30-tool-args-schema-design.md</code></li> <li>Plan: <code>docs/superpowers/plans/2026-04-30-tool-args-schema.md</code></li> <li>ADR-0006 §3 + Consequences — the deferral this ADR closes.</li> <li>ADR-0009 (typed-error policy) — new variants follow this policy.</li> <li><code>crates/tau-runtime/src/tool_args.rs</code> — the validator module.</li> <li><code>crates/tau-runtime/src/run.rs:417</code>-area — the call-site integration.</li> <li><code>crates/tau-runtime/src/builder.rs::collect_tools_by_name</code> — the build-time compilation step.</li> </ul> <div style="break-before: page; page-break-before: always;"></div><h1 id="adr-0011-streaming-llm-responses"><a class="header" href="#adr-0011-streaming-llm-responses">ADR-0011: Streaming LLM responses</a></h1> <p><strong>Status:</strong> Accepted <strong>Date:</strong> 2026-04-30 <strong>Deciders:</strong> Titouan Lebocq <strong>Supersedes:</strong> — <strong>Closes:</strong> <a href="decisions/0006-tau-runtime.html">ADR-0006</a> §5 — streaming was a v0.1 deferral: <code>LlmBackend::stream</code> existed and every shipped backend implemented it, but no kernel-level consumer drove it. <strong>Amends:</strong> — <strong>Refines:</strong> <a href="decisions/0006-tau-runtime.html">ADR-0006</a> §9 (outcome/error dichotomy — this ADR refines the streaming-path classification of fatal errors via a new <code>RunEvent::FatalError</code> terminal event that preserves byte-identical batch-API error semantics).</p> <h2 id="context-11"><a class="header" href="#context-11">Context</a></h2> <p>Three of the LLM backends shipped in priorities 2a-2c (Anthropic/Ollama/OpenAI) implement <code>LlmBackend::stream</code>, returning a <code>CompletionStream</code> (<code>Pin<Box<dyn Stream<Item = Result<CompletionChunk, LlmError>> + Send>></code>). The trait has been there since priority 1, and the protocol's <code>llm.stream</code> IPC wire method exists per ADR-0008. Yet <code>Runtime::run_with_history</code> calls <code>LlmBackend::complete</code> exclusively — the entire response materializes before the agent loop sees it.</p> <p>The cost:</p> <ol> <li><strong><code>tau chat</code> REPL feels dead</strong> during long completions. The user types a question, sees nothing for 5-30 seconds, then the full response renders at once.</li> <li><strong><code>tau run</code> cannot drive token-aware UIs.</strong> Scripts piping <code>tau run --json</code> get one final blob; they can't react to text as it arrives.</li> <li><strong>Two distinct codepaths</strong> would emerge if streaming consumers kept calling <code>LlmBackend::stream</code> directly while batch consumers kept calling <code>complete</code>. ADR-0006 §16's "single source of truth for the agent loop" invariant would break.</li> </ol> <p>ADR-0006 §5 reserved this work explicitly:</p> <blockquote> <p>Streaming is deferred to a future ADR. v0.1 ships <code>LlmBackend::stream</code> as a contract for backends but no kernel-level consumer; <code>Runtime::run_with_history</code> is the non-streaming entry point.</p> </blockquote> <p>This ADR closes that reservation.</p> <h2 id="decision-11"><a class="header" href="#decision-11">Decision</a></h2> <p>Five inter-locking commitments:</p> <h3 id="1-api-surface-streamitem--runevent"><a class="header" href="#1-api-surface-streamitem--runevent">1. API surface: <code>Stream<Item = RunEvent></code></a></h3> <p><code>Runtime::run_streaming</code> and <code>run_streaming_with_history</code> are public async methods on <code>impl Runtime</code> that return <code>Result<impl Stream<Item = RunEvent> + 'static, RuntimeError></code>. The caller drives consumption via <code>.next().await</code> or equivalent stream adapters.</p> <p>Rationale: <code>Stream<Item = RunEvent></code> is the idiomatic Rust async iterator. It composes naturally with <code>tokio_stream</code>, <code>futures-util</code>, and any future SSE / WebSocket / long-poll surface. Callbacks and mpsc channels were considered:</p> <ul> <li><strong>Callback</strong> (<code>run_streaming(req, on_event: impl FnMut(...))</code>) puts the kernel in charge of pacing. Caller can't pause / await between events; <code>async</code>-flavored callbacks force the trait to be <code>async fn</code> in trait, which needs <code>async_trait</code> or fights the compiler.</li> <li><strong>mpsc channel</strong> adds a hidden buffer and a second runtime task; the consumer has to learn the channel's bounded/unbounded semantics separately. Pull-based <code>Stream</code> is the simpler primitive.</li> </ul> <p>The lifetime is <code>'static</code>, NOT <code>'_</code>. The stream owns all the data it needs (<code>Arc<dyn DynLlmBackend></code>, owned <code>HashMap<String, Arc<dyn DynTool>></code>, owned <code>Vec<Capability></code>, etc.) so it doesn't borrow from the runtime registry. After construction the stream is independent of <code>&self</code>. The plan-erratum's draft signature <code>+ Send + '_</code> was wrong on both points: the stream owns its data (<code>'static</code>), and it cannot be <code>Send</code> because <code>DynLlmBackend::stream</code> returns a non-<code>Send</code> <code>BoxFuture</code> per the design at <code>crates/tau-runtime/src/builder.rs:45-50</code>.</p> <p>Trigger to revisit: A <code>Send</code>-bounded variant of <code>DynLlmBackend</code> (and sibling traits) is needed before streaming consumers can use <code>tokio::spawn</code> (rather than running on the same task). At that point the public signature gains <code>+ Send</code>.</p> <h3 id="2-event-vocabulary-kernel-translated-runevent"><a class="header" href="#2-event-vocabulary-kernel-translated-runevent">2. Event vocabulary: kernel-translated <code>RunEvent</code></a></h3> <p>The stream yields <strong>kernel-translated</strong> events, not the raw <code>CompletionChunk</code>s from <code>LlmBackend::stream</code>. The <code>RunEvent</code> enum has six variants:</p> <div class="table-wrapper"><table><thead><tr><th>Variant</th><th>Carries</th><th>Fires when</th></tr></thead><tbody> <tr><td><code>TextDelta { delta: String }</code></td><td>one text fragment</td><td>LLM emits <code>CompletionChunk::Text</code></td></tr> <tr><td><code>ToolCallStarted { id, name, args }</code></td><td>the tool the LLM wants to call</td><td>LLM emits <code>CompletionChunk::ToolUse</code> (display intent BEFORE dispatch — see decision 3)</td></tr> <tr><td><code>ToolCallCompleted { id, name, result: Result<ToolResult, String> }</code></td><td>dispatch outcome</td><td><code>Tool::invoke</code> returns OR validation fails (BadArgs is recoverable; <code>result: Err(reason)</code> and the loop continues)</td></tr> <tr><td><code>TurnCompleted { stop_reason, usage, turn }</code></td><td>per-turn summary</td><td>LLM <code>Finish</code> chunk arrives AND all tool dispatches resolved</td></tr> <tr><td><code>RunCompleted { outcome }</code></td><td>final <code>RunOutcome</code></td><td>the run completes (success or agent-level failure: <code>Completed</code>, <code>Failed{PolicyDenied}</code>, <code>Failed{OutOfResources}</code>)</td></tr> <tr><td><code>FatalError { kind, detail, context_json, tool_error_variant }</code></td><td>structured kernel-error payload</td><td>the streaming pump hits an error that the <strong>batch API</strong> must surface as <code>Err(RuntimeError::*)</code> (LLM, Tool::*, ToolNotRegistered)</td></tr> </tbody></table> </div> <p><code>RunEvent</code> is <code>#[non_exhaustive]</code> + <code>#[derive(Debug, Clone)]</code>. Future variants are additive.</p> <p>Rationale: streaming consumers (REPL UIs, JSON event readers) shouldn't have to learn LLM-protocol semantics (raw chunk types, partial-tool-use accumulation, provider-specific finish reasons). The kernel handles the protocol gymnastics; UIs see a clean state machine. The <code>ToolCallStarted</code> / <code>ToolCallCompleted</code> pair is the equivalent abstraction for tool dispatch — the consumer doesn't need to track chunk-by-chunk tool_use accumulation.</p> <p>The <code>FatalError</code> variant is the major <strong>plan-erratum revision</strong> vs. the spec's original 5-variant design. The original "no new error variants" rule (spec §5) was wrong: <code>Runtime::run_with_history</code>'s public batch API returns <code>Result<RunOutcome, RuntimeError></code> where <code>RuntimeError::Tool(ToolError::BadArgs { reason })</code>, <code>RuntimeError::ToolNotRegistered { ... }</code>, and <code>RuntimeError::Llm(...)</code> are all <strong>kernel-error</strong> failures, distinct from agent-level <code>RunOutcome::Failed { kind: PolicyDenied }</code>. To preserve byte-identical batch behavior under Task 7's refactor (where the batch path becomes a thin stream-drainer), the streaming pump needed a way to communicate kernel errors back to the drainer for typed reconstruction. <code>FatalError</code>'s <code>kind: String</code> (e.g. "Tool", "Llm", "ToolNotRegistered") + <code>tool_error_variant: Option<String></code> fields together let the drainer reconstruct the precise typed <code>RuntimeError::*</code> variant the test suite asserts on. Without this variant, either (a) the batch API's typed error variants would have to change (forbidden by spec §4.4's byte-identical requirement) or (b) all errors would collapse into agent-level failures (a UX regression in <code>tau run</code>, where exit code 1 / 2 distinguish agent failure / kernel error).</p> <p>Trigger to revisit: a third-party streaming consumer that wants provider-specific raw chunks (e.g., for a custom debugging UI). At that point an opt-in raw-chunk channel can be added without disturbing the kernel-translated events.</p> <h3 id="3-toolcallstarted-fires-on-llm-emission-not-after-dispatch"><a class="header" href="#3-toolcallstarted-fires-on-llm-emission-not-after-dispatch">3. <code>ToolCallStarted</code> fires on LLM emission, not after dispatch</a></h3> <p>When the LLM streams a <code>CompletionChunk::ToolUse(tu)</code>, the kernel pump yields <code>RunEvent::ToolCallStarted { id, name, args }</code> <strong>immediately</strong> — before any capability check, schema validation, session open, or <code>Tool::invoke</code> call. The matching <code>ToolCallCompleted</code> fires after dispatch resolves.</p> <p>Rationale: REPL UIs need to display intent — "the agent wants to call fs-read with path=foo.txt" — before the dispatch itself begins. If <code>ToolCallStarted</code> fired only after dispatch, slow tools (network calls, long shell commands) would freeze the UI for the dispatch duration with no visible activity. The spec's Q3-A locked this in based on the user-experience requirement.</p> <p>The pump invariant becomes: <strong>every <code>ToolCallStarted</code> is paired with a <code>ToolCallCompleted</code> (same id) before the next <code>TurnCompleted</code>, OR followed by a terminal <code>RunCompleted { Failed }</code> / <code>FatalError</code></strong>.</p> <p>The "OR" is the documented exception:</p> <ul> <li>A capability denial mid-turn yields <code>RunCompleted { Failed { PolicyDenied } }</code> and terminates the run; the offending tool's <code>ToolCallStarted</code> fired but its <code>ToolCallCompleted</code> does NOT.</li> <li>A real plugin invocation crash yields <code>FatalError { kind: "Tool", ... }</code> and terminates the run; same exception.</li> </ul> <p>Trigger to revisit: a UI that requires every Started to have a matching Completed (e.g., a progress bar). At that point a sentinel <code>Aborted</code> ToolCallCompleted variant can be added.</p> <h3 id="4-pure-runevent-items-not-resultrunevent-"><a class="header" href="#4-pure-runevent-items-not-resultrunevent-">4. Pure <code>RunEvent</code> items, not <code>Result<RunEvent, ...></code></a></h3> <p>The stream's item type is <code>RunEvent</code>, not <code>Result<RunEvent, StreamError></code>. There is no separate "stream error" variant; instead, errors surface through:</p> <ul> <li><strong>Construction-time failures</strong> (capability override invalid, LLM backend not registered, tool not registered at build): the <code>Result<impl Stream, RuntimeError></code> returned from <code>run_streaming(...)</code> is <code>Err(RuntimeError::*)</code> BEFORE the stream materializes.</li> <li><strong>Mid-stream agent-level failures</strong> (<code>PolicyDenied</code>, <code>OutOfResources</code>): yielded as <code>RunEvent::RunCompleted { outcome: RunOutcome::Failed { kind, .. } }</code>. The agent-loop terminated cleanly; the agent itself failed.</li> <li><strong>Mid-stream kernel-level failures</strong> (<code>LlmError</code>, <code>ToolError::*</code>, <code>ToolNotRegistered</code>): yielded as <code>RunEvent::FatalError { kind, detail, context_json, tool_error_variant }</code>. The kernel hit an error the batch API surfaces as <code>Err(RuntimeError::*)</code>.</li> </ul> <p>Rationale: a single error path is simpler than a stream-item Result. Construction errors are caught synchronously; mid-stream errors are events the consumer renders alongside text.
