CLIs map kernel-level fatal errors to exit code 2 (kernel error); agent-level failures map to exit code 1 (<code>AgentFailed</code> marker error).</p> <p>Trigger to revisit: a streaming consumer that wants per-chunk recoverable errors (e.g., a partial-text-render path for OpenAI's "content moderation" mid-stream rejections). At that point a <code>RunEvent::Warning</code> or similar non-terminal event variant can be added without changing the terminal event semantics.</p> <h3 id="5-full-cli-scope-kernel--tau-chat--tau-run---stream"><a class="header" href="#5-full-cli-scope-kernel--tau-chat--tau-run---stream">5. Full CLI scope: kernel + <code>tau chat</code> + <code>tau run --stream</code></a></h3> <p>Ship streaming-aware UI in both <code>tau chat</code> and <code>tau run</code> in the same sub-project (not deferred to a follow-up):</p> <ul> <li><strong><code>tau chat</code></strong> streams by default. The new <code>--no-stream</code> flag (<code>ChatArgs.no_stream: bool</code>, default <code>false</code>) opts out for users who prefer the batch render UX. Two-pass rendering: during the stream, raw <code>print!("{delta}")</code> + flush gives a typewriter UX; on <code>RunCompleted</code>, the existing <code>render_final_message</code> helper re-renders the assistant text via termimad (markdown) — the user sees text twice (rough draft → final formatting). Tool annotations go to stderr (<code>→ calling X...</code> / <code>✓ X completed</code>) so stdout stays the agent's text.</li> <li><strong><code>tau run</code></strong> gains a <code>--stream</code> flag (<code>RunArgs.stream: bool</code>, default <code>false</code>) for opt-in streaming. Polarity asymmetry is intentional: <code>tau run</code> is script-friendly by default (one final blob is easier to pipe); <code>tau chat</code> is interactive by default (typewriter UX is the win). Human mode emits text deltas to stdout <ul> <li>tool annotations to stderr; JSON mode emits one canonical event per stdout line:</li> </ul> </li> </ul> <pre><code class="language-json">{"event":"text_delta","delta":"..."} {"event":"tool_call_started","id":"...","name":"...","args":...} {"event":"tool_call_completed","id":"...","name":"...","result":{"ok":true}} {"event":"turn_completed","stop_reason":"...","usage":{...},"turn":N} {"event":"run_completed","outcome":{...}} </code></pre> <p>Rationale: bundling the UX surfaces with the kernel API in one sub-project means the kernel pump is exercised end-to-end (CLI → runtime → backend) before the sub-project closes. A future ADR revising the event shape would touch all three layers consistently. Splitting into kernel-only-now + UI-later would risk landing a kernel API that doesn't fit any actual UI's needs.</p> <p>Trigger to revisit: a third user-facing surface (TUI, web SSE, JSON-RPC over stdio for <code>tau serve</code>). Each surface gets its own ADR section reusing the canonical event shape from this ADR.</p> <h2 id="consequences-11"><a class="header" href="#consequences-11">Consequences</a></h2> <h3 id="negative--new-cost-1"><a class="header" href="#negative--new-cost-1">Negative / new cost</a></h3> <ul> <li><code>tau-runtime</code> gains a transitive dep on <code>async-stream = "0.3"</code> (~50KB compiled). Negligible vs. the existing <code>tokio</code> / <code>futures-core</code> footprint.</li> <li><code>tau-runtime</code> gains a <code>RunEvent</code> enum (6 variants, ~200 LOC) and a <code>run_streaming_inner</code> async generator (~250 LOC). The generator uses <code>async_stream::stream! { ... }</code> macro syntax; future contributors need familiarity. (<code>async-stream</code> is widely used; not a high adoption cost.)</li> <li><code>tau-runtime</code>'s <code>run.rs</code> agent-loop body (~400 LOC at run.rs:111-510 pre-refactor) MOVED into <code>stream.rs</code>'s <code>run_streaming_inner</code>. The batch path (<code>run_with_history</code>) is now a ~50-line stream-drainer with a typed-error reconstruction match for FatalError. Two codepaths collapsed into one source of truth.</li> <li><code>RunEvent::FatalError</code>'s <code>tool_error_variant: Option<String></code> is a string-tagged-variant pattern that's slightly less type-safe than carrying the original <code>ToolError</code> directly. Trade-off: passing <code>ToolError</code> through a <code>Clone</code>-required event variant would force <code>LlmError</code> and <code>ToolError</code> to derive <code>Clone</code>, expanding the public API surface area. The string-tag approach is additive and reversible.</li> <li><code>RunEvent</code> is <code>Clone</code>, which forces every variant to carry only <code>Clone</code> types. This rules out future variants carrying <code>dyn</code> trait objects directly (they'd need to be <code>Arc<dyn ...></code> or owned payloads).</li> </ul> <h3 id="positive-7"><a class="header" href="#positive-7">Positive</a></h3> <ul> <li>The streaming pump is <strong>the single source of truth</strong> for the agent loop. <code>run_with_history</code> is a thin drainer that returns the terminal <code>RunCompleted.outcome</code> (or reconstructs <code>RuntimeError::*</code> from <code>FatalError</code>). The 100+ existing run-loop tests continue to pass unchanged — they're the regression net.</li> <li>LLM-backend plugins' existing <code>stream()</code> impls (priority 2a-2c) are now exercised by every batch-mode <code>tau run</code> and <code>tau chat</code> call, not just opt-in streaming. The 5 test-fixture LLMs that previously panicked on <code>stream()</code> were updated to delegate via <code>tau_ports::batch_to_stream(self.complete(req).await?)</code>.</li> <li><code>tau chat</code> typewriter UX dramatically improves perceived latency on long completions.</li> <li><code>tau run --stream --json</code> enables token-aware downstream tooling (progress bars, partial-render UIs, telemetry pipelines).</li> </ul> <h3 id="neutral--new-obligations-6"><a class="header" href="#neutral--new-obligations-6">Neutral / new obligations</a></h3> <ul> <li>Future tau-runtime API additions involving streaming (cancellation via <code>Drop</code>, parallel tool dispatch, per-event token usage) require their own ADRs (QG18). The MANDATORY-rule template at the schema- validation boundary (ADR-0010) now also fires inside the streaming pump's tool-dispatch flow; the rule is unchanged.</li> <li>The <code>async-stream = "0.3"</code> crate version is pinned to the major in <code>[workspace.dependencies]</code>; major upgrades verify the public API surface.</li> </ul> <h2 id="alternatives-considered-10"><a class="header" href="#alternatives-considered-10">Alternatives considered</a></h2> <h3 id="a-callback-based-api-runtimerun_streamingreq-on_event-impl-fnmut"><a class="header" href="#a-callback-based-api-runtimerun_streamingreq-on_event-impl-fnmut">A. Callback-based API (<code>Runtime::run_streaming(req, on_event: impl FnMut(...))</code>)</a></h3> <p>Rejected. Caller can't pause / await between events; the closure runs synchronously inside the kernel pump's task. To support <code>async fn</code>-flavored callbacks, the trait would need <code>async_trait</code> desugaring. <code>Stream</code> is the more flexible, more idiomatic primitive.</p> <h3 id="b-mpsc-channel-api-runtimerun_streamingreq---mpscreceiverrunevent"><a class="header" href="#b-mpsc-channel-api-runtimerun_streamingreq---mpscreceiverrunevent">B. mpsc channel API (<code>Runtime::run_streaming(req) -> mpsc::Receiver<RunEvent></code>)</a></h3> <p>Rejected. mpsc adds a buffer and a second runtime task; the consumer has to learn the bounded/unbounded semantics. Pull-based <code>Stream</code> is the simpler primitive — the consumer paces by awaiting <code>.next()</code>.</p> <h3 id="c-pass-through-streamingevent-raw-llm-events"><a class="header" href="#c-pass-through-streamingevent-raw-llm-events">C. Pass-through <code>StreamingEvent</code> (raw LLM events)</a></h3> <p>Rejected. Forwarding raw <code>CompletionChunk</code>s would force every streaming consumer to learn:</p> <ul> <li>Per-provider tool_use chunk accumulation (Anthropic deltas vs. OpenAI function_call deltas vs. Ollama's whole-message tool_calls).</li> <li>The kernel's tool-dispatch state machine (which tool_calls the kernel approved, which it denied, which crashed).</li> <li><code>StopReason</code> mapping per provider.</li> </ul> <p>The kernel's job is exactly to translate this into a clean state machine. Punting that to consumers would multiply UI complexity across every consumer and make UI testing harder.</p> <h3 id="d-end-of-turn-only-tool-dispatch-no-toolcallstarted-mid-stream"><a class="header" href="#d-end-of-turn-only-tool-dispatch-no-toolcallstarted-mid-stream">D. End-of-turn-only tool dispatch (no <code>ToolCallStarted</code> mid-stream)</a></h3> <p>Rejected. UI would freeze during long tool calls with no visible activity. <code>ToolCallStarted</code> fires immediately on LLM emission so REPLs can show "→ calling fs-read..." while dispatch proceeds.</p> <h3 id="e-no-streaming-ux-kernel-only-api-defer-cli-ux-to-a-follow-up"><a class="header" href="#e-no-streaming-ux-kernel-only-api-defer-cli-ux-to-a-follow-up">E. No streaming UX (kernel-only API, defer CLI UX to a follow-up)</a></h3> <p>Rejected. See decision 5. Bundling the kernel API with at least one real UI consumer ensures the API actually fits a UI's needs. A kernel-only API would risk landing a shape that doesn't compose with the eventual UI work.</p> <h3 id="f-drop-the-byte-identical-batch-api-requirement-collapse-all-errors-into-runoutcomefailed"><a class="header" href="#f-drop-the-byte-identical-batch-api-requirement-collapse-all-errors-into-runoutcomefailed">F. Drop the byte-identical batch-API requirement; collapse all errors into <code>RunOutcome::Failed</code></a></h3> <p>Rejected. <code>tau run</code>'s exit-code semantics distinguish agent failure (exit 1, <code>AgentFailed</code> marker) from kernel error (exit 2). Collapsing them would make scripts that depend on this distinction silently misbehave. The <code>FatalError</code> variant preserves the distinction.</p> <h2 id="references-2"><a class="header" href="#references-2">References</a></h2> <ul> <li>Spec: <code>docs/superpowers/specs/2026-04-30-streaming-design.md</code></li> <li>Plan: <code>docs/superpowers/plans/2026-04-30-streaming.md</code></li> <li>ADR-0006 §5 — the deferral this ADR closes.</li> <li>ADR-0006 §16 — the "single source of truth for the agent loop" invariant this refactor preserves.</li> <li>ADR-0008 — <code>llm.stream</code> IPC wire method.</li> <li>ADR-0009 — typed-error policy; new error variants follow this.</li> <li>ADR-0010 — schema validation; the streaming pump preserves the MANDATORY-rule template at the validator boundary.</li> <li><code>crates/tau-runtime/src/stream.rs</code> — the streaming module.</li> <li><code>crates/tau-runtime/src/run.rs:111-196</code> — the post-refactor batch drainer (replaces the original ~400 LOC agent-loop body).</li> <li><code>crates/tau-runtime/src/builder.rs::Runtime::run_streaming</code> — the public entry point.</li> <li><code>crates/tau-runtime/tests/run_streaming_e2e.rs</code> — 5 e2e scenarios.</li> <li><code>crates/tau-cli/src/cmd/chat.rs</code> — <code>tau chat</code> two-pass rendering.</li> <li><code>crates/tau-cli/src/cmd/run.rs::run_streaming_path</code> — <code>tau run --stream</code> human + JSON modes.</li> </ul> <div style="break-before: page; page-break-before: always;"></div><h1 id="adr-0012-tau-update--verify--uninstall-lifecycle-commands"><a class="header" href="#adr-0012-tau-update--verify--uninstall-lifecycle-commands">ADR-0012: tau update / verify / uninstall lifecycle commands</a></h1> <p><strong>Status:</strong> Accepted <strong>Date:</strong> 2026-05-01 <strong>Deciders:</strong> Titouan Lebocq <strong>Supersedes:</strong> — <strong>Closes:</strong> <a href="decisions/0007-tau-cli.html">ADR-0007</a> §1 — <code>uninstall</code>, <code>update</code>, <code>verify</code> were explicitly deferred to Phase 1+ when the v0.1 5-subcommand surface (<code>install</code>, <code>list</code>, <code>run</code>, <code>init</code>, <code>chat</code>) was locked. <strong>Amends:</strong> — <strong>Refines:</strong> <a href="decisions/0007-tau-cli.html">ADR-0007</a> §7 (three-bucket exit code policy — this ADR explicitly maps verify-drift and lifecycle errors into the 0/1/2 buckets).</p> <h2 id="context-12"><a class="header" href="#context-12">Context</a></h2> <p>Phase 0 priority 3 shipped <code>tau-pkg</code> and <code>tau install</code>. The <code>LockedVersion.sha256</code> field was reserved for "Phase-1 <code>tau verify</code> content hashing"; the <code>tau_pkg::uninstall(name, version, scope)</code> library function was already implemented at install.rs:612. ADR-0007 §1 deferred the three lifecycle subcommands explicitly:</p> <blockquote> <p>Deferred to Phase 1+: <code>uninstall</code>, <code>update</code>, <code>verify</code>, <code>workflow</code> and any orchestration verbs.</p> </blockquote> <p>After Tier 2 priorities 4 (capability override), 5 (transitive dependency resolution), 6 (tool-args schema validation), and 8 (streaming LLM responses) shipped, only this priority and one Tier 2 slot remained open. This ADR closes priority 7's scope.</p> <p>The constraints driving the four design decisions below:</p> <ol> <li><strong><code>PackageSource</code> is <code>#[non_exhaustive]</code></strong>. Today only the <code>Git</code> variant exists, but the marker explicitly anticipates future variants (registry, tarball, local path). Verify primitives that tie to git operations (<code>git rev-parse HEAD</code>, <code>git status --porcelain</code>) would need redesign for each new source — wrong coupling.</li> <li><strong>The library function <code>tau_pkg::uninstall</code> already exists</strong> and handles whole-package, per-version, active-version-promotion, and lockfile mutation. The CLI is a thin wrapper.</li> <li><strong>Multi-version cohabitation already works</strong> in the lockfile via <code>LockedPackage.installed_versions: Vec<LockedVersion></code>. Update semantics build on top.</li> <li><strong>The exit-code policy from ADR-0007 §7</strong> (0 success, 1 agent failure, 2 kernel error) maps cleanly to verify drift (kernel trust → 2) and lifecycle errors (kernel error → 2).</li> </ol> <h2 id="decision-12"><a class="header" href="#decision-12">Decision</a></h2> <p>Four inter-locking commitments:</p> <h3 id="1-whole-tree-sha-256-verify-source-agnostic"><a class="header" href="#1-whole-tree-sha-256-verify-source-agnostic">1. Whole-tree SHA-256 verify, source-agnostic</a></h3> <p><strong>Decision:</strong> At install time, after the source materializes the package files, compute a whole-tree SHA-256 over the install dir (excluding <code>.git/</code>, <code>target/</code>, and <code>*.tau-tmp/</code>). Store in <code>LockedVersion.sha256</code>. On verify, recompute and compare. Plugin binaries get a separate <code>LockedPlugin.binary_sha256</code> field (introduced in lockfile schema v3).</p> <p><strong>Rationale:</strong></p> <p><code>PackageSource</code> is <code>#[non_exhaustive]</code> — future variants are inevitable. A verify primitive that ties to git operations would need redesign for each new source. Tree-hashing works for any source: clone → hash, unpack tarball → hash, resolve local path → hash, fetch from registry → hash. The recompute step is identical regardless of how the install got there.</p> <p>Sub-100ms for typical packages (~100 files, <1MB). Cheap enough to run on every <code>tau verify</code>, including in CI.</p> <h4 id="11-excluded-paths"><a class="header" href="#11-excluded-paths">1.1. Excluded paths</a></h4> <ul> <li><strong><code>.git/</code></strong> — git-specific noise. Changes on <code>git gc</code>, ref updates, shallow-clone metadata. Not part of what the runtime depends on.</li> <li><strong><code>target/</code></strong> — build artifacts. Recomputed on each <code>cargo build</code>, would always show drift. Plugin binaries are tracked separately via <code>LockedPlugin.binary_sha256</code>.</li> <li><strong><code>*.tau-tmp/</code></strong> — any stale temp dirs from interrupted operations. Defensive.</li> </ul> <h4 id="12-hash-algorithm"><a class="header" href="#12-hash-algorithm">1.2. Hash algorithm</a></h4> <pre><code class="language-text">1. Walk install dir with walkdir, follow_links(false). 2. Skip `.git/`, `target/`, `*.tau-tmp/` directories. 3. Sort entries lexicographically by relative path. 4. For each file: hasher.update(rel_path.as_bytes()); hasher.update(&[0]); hasher.update(file_contents); hasher.update(&[0]); 5. Return format!("{:x}", hash.finalize()) — 64-char lowercase hex. </code></pre> <p>The <code>\0</code> separators prevent path-content ambiguity (e.g. <code>a/bcontent</code> vs <code>a/b\0content</code>). Symlinks are NOT followed; a symlink contributes its target path bytes (not the resolved file content) to the hash — preventing symlink-loop pitfalls during walk.</p> <h4 id="13-plugin-binary-hashing"><a class="header" href="#13-plugin-binary-hashing">1.3. Plugin binary hashing</a></h4> <p><code>LockedPlugin</code> (lockfile schema v2) gains a <code>binary_sha256: String</code> field at v3. Populated at install time after <code>cargo build</code> succeeds, via <code>sha256_of_file(LockedPlugin.binary_path)</code>. Verified separately from the source-tree hash because:</p> <ul> <li>Source tree drift = "did someone tamper with the package code on disk."</li> <li>Binary drift = "did someone replace the runtime artifact." These are different threat models with different remediations (rebuild vs reinstall).</li> </ul> <p>Older <code>LockedPlugin</code> entries from lockfile v2-leftover (no <code>binary_sha256</code>) are flagged <code>unverified</code> for the binary, NOT <code>drift</code>.</p> <h4 id="14-trigger-to-revisit"><a class="header" href="#14-trigger-to-revisit">1.4. Trigger to revisit</a></h4> <ul> <li>Per-file drift diagnosis ("file X changed at line Y") — would require additional manifest storage. Cheap to add later as a <code>--diff</code> flag on <code>tau verify</code>.</li> <li>Cryptographic signing (registry signing keys, GPG, Sigstore) — separate Phase 2+ ADR.</li> <li>Hash algorithm migration (BLAKE3, etc.) — hash field is opaque string; algorithm prefix (<code>sha256:...</code>) could be added later.</li> </ul> <h3 id="2-tau-update-defaults-to-latest-tag"><a class="header" href="#2-tau-update-defaults-to-latest-tag">2. <code>tau update</code> defaults to latest tag</a></h3> <p><strong>Decision:</strong> <code>tau update <pkg></code> re-resolves the package against the source's latest published tag (using priority 5's <code>source_list::list_versions_at_source</code>). <code>tau update <pkg> --version 1.2.3</code> jumps to that exact version. Re-resolves transitive deps. Old versions stay installed by default; opt-in <code>--prune</code> removes the previous active version after the new install succeeds.</p> <p><strong>Rationale:</strong></p> <p>Dominant idiom (npm, cargo, gem). Users expect "give me the new version of X" by default. Multi-version cohabitation already exists in the lockfile (<code>LockedPackage.installed_versions: Vec<LockedVersion></code>); rollback is <code>tau update <pkg> --version <old></code> away.</p> <p>Re-resolving transitive deps means new <code>[[requires.tools]]</code> declarations in the new version automatically install. Priority 5's "highest-compatible" picker handles existing deps that are still satisfied without re-installing.</p> <h4 id="21-behavior-matrix"><a class="header" href="#21-behavior-matrix">2.1. Behavior matrix</a></h4> <div class="table-wrapper"><table><thead><tr><th>Command</th><th>Behavior</th></tr></thead><tbody> <tr><td><code>tau update <pkg></code></td><td>Find latest tag matching package source's rev constraint. If newer than active, install + promote. Old versions kept.</td></tr> <tr><td><code>tau update <pkg> --version <v></code></td><td>Validate <code><v></code> is reachable from source. Install + promote. Error if version not found.</td></tr> <tr><td><code>tau update <pkg> --prune</code></td><td>Same as <code>tau update <pkg></code> plus <code>tau_pkg::uninstall(name, Some(old_active_version), scope)</code> after promotion.</td></tr> <tr><td><code>tau update <pkg> --json</code></td><td>Streaming-style JSON event output (post-call summary; library is synchronous).</td></tr> </tbody></table> </div> <h4 id="22-json-event-shape"><a class="header" href="#22-json-event-shape">2.2. JSON event shape</a></h4> <p>The library function returns synchronously after all work completes, so per-step progress events (resolving / installing / etc.) would require library refactoring. v0.1 emits a two-event pair:</p> <pre><code class="language-json">{"event":"update_started","name":"...","current":"1.0.0"} {"event":"update_completed","name":"...","from":"1.0.0","to":"1.1.0","pruned":true|false,"transitive_deps_changed":[...]} </code></pre> <p>On failure: <code>update_started</code> is emitted, then no <code>update_completed</code> follows. JSON consumers detect failure via exit code 2 + stderr.</p> <h4 id="23-no-tau-update-no-args-at-v01"><a class="header" href="#23-no-tau-update-no-args-at-v01">2.3. No <code>tau update</code> (no args) at v0.1</a></h4> <p>Updating every plugin in one command without per-package review is a footgun. The <code>Default<Risky></code> posture from QG14 says "don't ship defaults that surprise the user with broad effects." <code>tau update</code> with no args is omitted; a future ADR can revisit if there's demonstrated demand.</p> <h4 id="24-trigger-to-revisit"><a class="header" href="#24-trigger-to-revisit">2.4. Trigger to revisit</a></h4> <ul> <li>Batch update (<code>tau update</code> no args) — needs an ADR amendment to lock the trust posture.</li> <li><code>tau update --dry-run</code> — print what would happen without modifying anything.</li> <li>Atomic install-then-prune (rollback on failure) — current design is install-then-prune-best-effort.</li> <li>Per-step progress JSON events — needs library refactoring to expose hooks.</li> </ul> <h3 id="3-tau-uninstall-is-permissive-no-cascade"><a class="header" href="#3-tau-uninstall-is-permissive-no-cascade">3. <code>tau uninstall</code> is permissive (no cascade)</a></h3> <p><strong>Decision:</strong> <code>tau uninstall <pkg></code> operates on the lockfile and install tree only — no cross-project dep tracking. Print a remediation hint pointing to project <code>tau.toml</code>s and <code>tau resolve</code> for self-healing.</p> <p><strong>Rationale:</strong></p> <p>Tau's installed packages aren't a single shared system — they live in scopes (per-user, per-project). The <code>[[requires.tools]]</code> graph lives in <strong>project</strong> files, not the lockfile. <code>tau uninstall</code> operates on the lockfile + install tree; it has no project-level context.</p> <p>Cascade-detection would require scanning the entire user's home for <code>tau.toml</code>s — privacy-invasive and unreliable.</p> <p>Self-healing is the alternative: if a user uninstalls a package they still need, the next <code>tau run</code> / <code>tau chat</code> re-resolves and re-installs (priority 5's lazy resolve). The system "just works" again on next use.</p> <h4 id="31-remediation-hint"><a class="header" href="#31-remediation-hint">3.1. Remediation hint</a></h4> <p>Always printed (informational; ignorable for those who don't need it):</p> <pre><code class="language-text">✓ Uninstalled <pkg>@<v>. Removed: <scope>/packages/<pkg>/<v> Lockfile: <scope>/lock.toml If any project still depends on <pkg>: • Remove or update the [[agents.<id>.requires.tools]] entry for <pkg> in the project's tau.toml. • Or re-install on next run: cd <project> && tau resolve </code></pre> <p>The hint always prints because users can't always remember which projects depend on which packages. Cheap to print, actionable for those who need it.</p> <h4 id="32-behavior-matrix"><a class="header" href="#32-behavior-matrix">3.2. Behavior matrix</a></h4> <div class="table-wrapper"><table><thead><tr><th>Command</th><th>Behavior</th></tr></thead><tbody> <tr><td><code>tau uninstall <pkg></code></td><td>Remove all versions; remove lockfile entry.</td></tr> <tr><td><code>tau uninstall <pkg> --version <v></code></td><td>Remove single version; promote highest remaining as active; remove lockfile entry only if no versions remain.</td></tr> </tbody></table> </div> <p>The library function <code>tau_pkg::uninstall(name, version, scope)</code> already exists at <code>crates/tau-pkg/src/install.rs:612</code> (Phase 0) and handles all these cases — including active-version promotion. The CLI is a thin wrapper.</p> <h4 id="33-trigger-to-revisit"><a class="header" href="#33-trigger-to-revisit">3.3. Trigger to revisit</a></h4> <ul> <li><code>tau uninstall --force</code> to override a future cascade-detection feature.</li> <li><code>tau uninstall --dry-run</code> — preview what would be removed.</li> <li>Cross-scope uninstall (today: scope is determined by CWD's project).</li> </ul> <h3 id="4-verify-exit-codes-reuse-the-3-bucket-policy"><a class="header" href="#4-verify-exit-codes-reuse-the-3-bucket-policy">4. Verify exit codes reuse the 3-bucket policy</a></h3> <p><strong>Decision:</strong> <code>tau verify</code> exits 0 if all packages verified or unverified (v2-leftover); exits 2 if any drift detected (tree, binary, missing). Drift kinds are reported via JSON status field (<code>drift</code> with <code>kind: tree|binary|missing</code>) or human stderr lines.</p> <p><strong>Rationale:</strong></p> <p>Tampered packages are a kernel-trust issue, not an agent issue, so exit 2 (kernel error) is correct per ADR-0007 §7. The 3-bucket policy is:</p> <ul> <li><strong>0</strong> — success: lifecycle command succeeded.</li> <li><strong>1</strong> — agent failure: not applicable to lifecycle commands (reserved for <code>tau run</code>'s <code>RunOutcome::Failed</code>).</li> <li><strong>2</strong> — kernel error: lifecycle error OR verify drift.</li> </ul> <h4 id="41-drift-kinds"><a class="header" href="#41-drift-kinds">4.1. Drift kinds</a></h4> <div class="table-wrapper"><table><thead><tr><th>Kind</th><th>Trigger</th><th>Lockfile sha256</th><th>Disk</th></tr></thead><tbody> <tr><td><code>tree</code></td><td>Source files modified (manifest, src/, etc.)</td><td>populated</td><td>exists, hash differs</td></tr> <tr><td><code>binary</code></td><td>Plugin binary modified</td><td>populated (<code>binary_sha256</code>)</td><td>exists, hash differs</td></tr> <tr><td><code>missing</code></td><td>Install dir deleted</td><td>populated</td><td>absent</td></tr> <tr><td><code>unverified</code></td><td>v2-leftover, hash empty</td><td>empty</td><td>exists, no comparison possible</td></tr> </tbody></table> </div> <p><code>unverified</code> is <strong>informational, not drift</strong> — exit 0 unless other drifts exist. Printed with hint to "re-install <pkg> to populate hash" (deferred polish; current v0.1 just labels the status).</p> <h4 id="42-json-event-shape"><a class="header" href="#42-json-event-shape">4.2. JSON event shape</a></h4> <p>Mirrors ADR-0011's per-line streaming convention:</p> <pre><code class="language-json">{"event":"verify_started","total":N} {"event":"verify_package","name":"...","version":"...","status":"ok"} {"event":"verify_package","name":"...","version":"...","status":"drift","kind":"tree","expected":"...","actual":"..."} {"event":"verify_package","name":"...","version":"...","status":"unverified"} {"event":"verify_completed","total":N,"ok":N,"drift":M,"unverified":K} </code></pre> <h4 id="43-trigger-to-revisit"><a class="header" href="#43-trigger-to-revisit">4.3. Trigger to revisit</a></h4> <ul> <li>Per-file drift diagnosis (which file changed) — <code>--diff</code> flag.</li> <li><code>tau verify --fix</code> to auto-reinstall drifted packages.</li> <li>Parallel verify for many packages (current implementation is sequential).</li> <li>Orphaned install-dir detection (lockfile entry gone but install dir present) — currently scoped out of v0.1; can be added at the CLI layer without changing the library.</li> </ul> <h2 id="consequences-12"><a class="header" href="#consequences-12">Consequences</a></h2> <h3 id="negative--new-cost-2"><a class="header" href="#negative--new-cost-2">Negative / new cost</a></h3> <ul> <li><code>tau-pkg</code> gains transitive deps on <code>sha2 = "0.10"</code> and <code>walkdir = "2"</code> (~150KB compiled total). Negligible vs. existing <code>git2</code>/<code>tokio</code>/etc. footprint.</li> <li><code>tau-pkg</code> gains 3 new modules (<code>tree_hash</code>, <code>verify</code>, <code>update</code>) totaling ~700 LOC + tests. Code organization is clean: one module per logical responsibility.</li> <li><code>LockedPlugin</code> gains a <code>binary_sha256: String</code> field. Lockfile schema bumps v2 → v3. Additive: v2 lockfiles auto-upgrade on next save. v2-leftover entries (empty <code>binary_sha256</code> + empty <code>LockedVersion.sha256</code>) are flagged <code>unverified</code> by <code>tau verify</code>, NOT <code>drift</code>.</li> <li><code>tau install</code> is now O(file-count + file-bytes) at install time for the source-tree hash. Sub-100ms for typical packages; not a measurable regression.</li> <li><code>Runtime::run_with_history</code>-equivalent JSON-event-per-line convention now applies to <code>tau update --json</code> and <code>tau verify --json</code>. Future commands joining the convention should mirror.</li> </ul> <h3 id="positive-8"><a class="header" href="#positive-8">Positive</a></h3> <ul> <li><code>tau verify</code> provides the integrity-check primitive ADR-0006 reserved at v0.1. Source-agnostic by design — future <code>PackageSource</code> variants reuse the verify primitive without redesign.</li> <li><code>tau update <pkg></code> matches user expectations (npm/cargo/gem defaults). <code>--version</code> to pin, <code>--prune</code> to clean up.</li> <li><code>tau uninstall <pkg></code> finally exists as a CLI surface. The library function existed since Phase 0; this just wires it up.</li> <li>Self-healing via lazy resolve (priority 5's lazy install) means <code>tau uninstall <pkg></code> is non-destructive in practice — the next <code>tau run</code> / <code>tau chat</code> re-installs if needed. The remediation hint guides users to the right place.</li> <li>Lockfile schema v2 → v3 is forward-compatible with future drift diagnostics, signing, and per-file hashing.</li> </ul> <h3 id="neutral--new-obligations-7"><a class="header" href="#neutral--new-obligations-7">Neutral / new obligations</a></h3> <ul> <li>Future <code>tau verify</code> extensions (per-file diff, <code>--fix</code>, parallel verify) require their own ADRs (QG18). The hash format is locked at this ADR; any change requires a new ADR.</li> <li>The <code>sha2 = "0.10"</code> and <code>walkdir = "2"</code> workspace dep versions are pinned to the major. Major upgrades verify the public API surface.</li> </ul> <h2 id="alternatives-considered-11"><a class="header" href="#alternatives-considered-11">Alternatives considered</a></h2> <h3 id="a-git-revision-verify-git-rev-parse-head--git-status---porcelain"><a class="header" href="#a-git-revision-verify-git-rev-parse-head--git-status---porcelain">A. Git-revision verify (<code>git rev-parse HEAD</code> + <code>git status --porcelain</code>)</a></h3> <p>Rejected. Reuses git's content addressing for free; cheap to implement (~30 LOC). However: ties verify to the <code>Git</code> variant of <code>PackageSource</code>. Future variants (registry, tarball, local path) would need their own verify primitive. Wrong coupling.</p> <p>The early brainstorm leaned toward this option until the user flagged the non-git futures. Pivoting to whole-tree SHA-256 makes verify source-agnostic from day one.</p> <h3 id="b-per-file-sha-256-manifest-taumanifestjson"><a class="header" href="#b-per-file-sha-256-manifest-taumanifestjson">B. Per-file SHA-256 manifest (<code>.tau/manifest.json</code>)</a></h3> <p>Rejected. Granular ("file X changed at line Y" reachable). Disk overhead per install (~50KB). Implementation complexity (manifest write at install, walk + diff at verify, manifest schema versioning).</p> <p>The whole-tree single-SHA approach is leaner for v0.1: same correctness primitive, smaller disk + code footprint, easier to reason about. Per-file granularity can land later as a <code>tau verify --diff</code> flag if real-world drift reports demand it.</p> <h3 id="c-tau-update-no-args-batch-update"><a class="header" href="#c-tau-update-no-args-batch-update">C. <code>tau update</code> (no args) batch update</a></h3> <p>Rejected. Updating every plugin in one command without per-package review is a footgun. ADR-0007's QG14 (<code>Default<Risky></code>) argues against shipping defaults that surprise users with broad effects. v0.1: explicit per-package update only. Defer the batch case to a future ADR if there's demonstrated demand.</p> <h3 id="d-tau-uninstall-with-cascade-detection"><a class="header" href="#d-tau-uninstall-with-cascade-detection">D. <code>tau uninstall</code> with cascade detection</a></h3> <p>Rejected. Cross-project dep tracking would require scanning the user's entire home directory for <code>tau.toml</code>s — privacy-invasive, unreliable, and slow. Self-healing via priority 5's lazy resolve is the safer default. The remediation hint guides users to the right place if they need it.</p> <h3 id="e-cryptographic-signing-instead-of-or-alongside-hashing"><a class="header" href="#e-cryptographic-signing-instead-of-or-alongside-hashing">E. Cryptographic signing instead of (or alongside) hashing</a></h3> <p>Rejected for v0.1. Signing answers "did the publisher actually release this content?" — different question than "did it change since I installed it?" The hashing approach is the integrity primitive; signing is the authenticity primitive. They compose; ship hashing first. Signing belongs to a future Phase 2+ ADR (registry infrastructure, key management, revocation are all major scope).</p> <h3 id="f-track-lockedpluginbinary_sha256-inline-in-lockedversionsha256"><a class="header" href="#f-track-lockedpluginbinary_sha256-inline-in-lockedversionsha256">F. Track <code>LockedPlugin.binary_sha256</code> inline in <code>LockedVersion.sha256</code></a></h3> <p>Rejected. Conflating source-tree drift with binary drift muddies the threat model. Source = "package authors edited code"; binary = "build artifact replaced." Different remediations (rebuild from source vs reinstall from source). Separating the fields keeps <code>tau verify</code>'s output legible: <code>kind=tree</code> vs <code>kind=binary</code> is informational.</p> <h2 id="references-3"><a class="header" href="#references-3">References</a></h2> <ul> <li>Spec: <code>docs/superpowers/specs/2026-05-01-tau-lifecycle-design.md</code></li> <li>Plan: <code>docs/superpowers/plans/2026-05-01-tau-lifecycle.md</code></li> <li>ADR-0007 §1 — the deferral this ADR closes.</li> <li>ADR-0007 §7 — three-bucket exit code policy reused for verify.</li> <li>ADR-0009 — typed-error policy; new error variants follow this (<code>VerifyError</code>, <code>UpdateError</code>).</li> <li>ADR-0011 — JSON event-per-line streaming convention reused for <code>tau update --json</code> and <code>tau verify --json</code>.</li> <li><code>crates/tau-pkg/src/tree_hash.rs</code> — the source-agnostic walker.</li> <li><code>crates/tau-pkg/src/verify.rs</code> — drift detection.</li> <li><code>crates/tau-pkg/src/update.rs</code> — composition over existing APIs.</li> <li><code>crates/tau-pkg/src/install.rs:612</code> — pre-existing <code>tau_pkg::uninstall</code> from Phase 0.</li> <li><code>crates/tau-pkg/src/lockfile.rs</code> — <code>LockedPlugin.binary_sha256</code> field (lockfile schema v3).</li> <li><code>crates/tau-cli/src/cmd/{update,verify,uninstall}.rs</code> — CLI wrappers.</li> <li><code>crates/tau-cli/tests/cmd_{update,verify,uninstall}.rs</code> — e2e tests via <code>file://</code> git fixtures.</li> </ul> <div style="break-before: page; page-break-before: always;"></div><h1 id="adr-0013-repl-persistence--tau-chat---resume-and-tau-session-group"><a class="header" href="#adr-0013-repl-persistence--tau-chat---resume-and-tau-session-group">ADR-0013: REPL persistence — <code>tau chat --resume</code> and <code>tau session</code> group</a></h1> <p><strong>Status:</strong> Accepted <strong>Date:</strong> 2026-05-02 <strong>Deciders:</strong> Titouan Lebocq <strong>Supersedes:</strong> — <strong>Closes:</strong></p> <ul> <li><a href="decisions/0006-tau-runtime.html">ADR-0006</a> §16 — "REPL persistence" was listed as a Phase 1+ deferral.</li> <li><a href="decisions/0007-tau-cli.html">ADR-0007</a> §11 — <code>/save</code>/<code>/load</code> slash commands were deferred to Phase 1+ at v0.1. This ADR closes that reservation by making auto-save the default (the explicit save/load slash commands become moot). <strong>Amends:</strong> — <strong>Refines:</strong> <a href="decisions/0006-tau-runtime.html">ADR-0006</a> NG6 (no persistent agent memory in core) — this ADR places the persistence concern at the CLI layer; the runtime stays stateless across CLI invocations.</li> </ul> <h2 id="context-13"><a class="header" href="#context-13">Context</a></h2> <p><code>tau chat</code> REPL sessions live entirely in memory. The <code>history: Vec<Message></code> accumulates per turn in the existing turn handler at <code>crates/tau-cli/src/cmd/chat.rs::run_repl</code>, threaded into each <code>Runtime::run_with_history</code> (or <code>run_streaming_with_history</code> after Tier 2 priority 8) call. On <code>/exit</code>, Ctrl-D, or process termination, the history is dropped.</p> <p>ADR-0007 §11 captured this as a deliberate v0.1 limitation:</p> <blockquote> <p>Four slash commands: <code>/exit</code> (quit), <code>/help</code> (show commands), <code>/clear</code> (drop in-memory history), <code>/history</code> (print messages so far). <code>/save</code>, <code>/load</code>, <code>/system</code>, <code>/model</code> etc. are deferred to Phase 1+.</p> </blockquote> <p>ADR-0006 NG6 placed REPL history outside the runtime's responsibilities: persistent agent memory is "not a runtime responsibility." This left the door open for a CLI-side persistence layer to land later.</p> <p>The constraints driving the five design decisions below:</p> <ol> <li> <p><strong>Industry idiom is split</strong>. Terminal LLM tools fall into four camps: JSONL per session (goose, gptme), SQLite single DB (simonw/llm, continue.dev, Cursor), single JSON/YAML per session (mods, aichat), and Markdown append-only (aider). Each has distinct tradeoffs around append cost, crash safety, search, and human inspectability.</p> </li> <li> <p><strong><code>PackageSource</code> is <code>#[non_exhaustive]</code></strong> with only <code>Git</code> today, but future variants (registry, tarball, local path) are anticipated. ADR-0012 made the verify primitive source-agnostic for the same reason; the resume drift check keeps that posture by comparing <code>package.name</code> + <code>package.version</code> strings rather than git commits.</p> </li> <li> <p><strong>Multi-version cohabitation already works</strong> (lockfile schema v3 from ADR-0012). Resume must accept that the user may have several versions of the same package installed; the session header records a single version, and resume validates against it.</p> </li> <li> <p><strong>Three-bucket exit code policy</strong> (ADR-0007 §7) maps cleanly to resume errors: drift → 2, not-found → 2, ambiguous prefix → 2.</p> </li> </ol> <h2 id="decision-13"><a class="header" href="#decision-13">Decision</a></h2> <p>Five inter-locking commitments:</p> <h3 id="1-jsonl-storage-format-source-agnostic-append-only"><a class="header" href="#1-jsonl-storage-format-source-agnostic-append-only">1. JSONL storage format, source-agnostic, append-only</a></h3> <p><strong>Decision:</strong> Sessions are stored as JSONL files at <code><scope.state_path()>/sessions/<uuid>.jsonl</code>. Header on line 1 (<code>{"type":"header",...}</code>); subsequent lines are <code>{"type":"message", "msg": <Message>}</code> and <code>{"type":"turn_summary", "turn": N, ...}</code>. Append-only writes per turn.</p> <p><strong>Rationale:</strong></p> <p>The terminal-LLM tooling landscape splits four ways. Trade-offs:</p> <div class="table-wrapper"><table><thead><tr><th>Concern</th><th>JSONL</th><th>SQLite</th><th>JSON</th><th>Markdown</th></tr></thead><tbody> <tr><td>Append cost (per turn)</td><td>O(1) line append</td><td>O(1) INSERT</td><td>O(history) full rewrite</td><td>O(1) line append</td></tr> <tr><td>Crash safety</td><td>Partial line recoverable</td><td>ACID</td><td>Risk on mid-write</td><td>Crash-safe</td></tr> <tr><td>Cross-session search</td><td>O(N) <code>grep -r</code> / <code>jq</code></td><td>O(log N) indexed query</td><td>O(N) walk + parse</td><td>O(N) <code>grep</code></td></tr> <tr><td>Single-session size scaling</td><td>Streams fine to 100MB+</td><td>Same (with proper schema)</td><td>Reads slow at 10MB+</td><td>Reads slow at 10MB+</td></tr> <tr><td>Dependency cost</td><td>None</td><td>~2MB rusqlite + schema migrations</td><td>None</td><td>None</td></tr> <tr><td>Human-inspectable</td><td><code>cat file.jsonl</code> works</td><td>Need sqlite3 CLI</td><td>Pretty-print</td><td>Just read</td></tr> <tr><td>Migrate later</td><td>Trivial walk + INSERT</td><td>Hard to escape</td><td>Trivial</td><td>Trivial</td></tr> </tbody></table> </div> <p>JSONL wins on every access pattern except cross-session search. SQLite is the right destination if and when search becomes a requirement — and it's not in v0.1's scope. JSONL is also free to migrate to SQLite later: walk all <code>.jsonl</code> files, <code>INSERT</code> rows. Reversible.</p> <p>Tau already has the JSONL precedent at <code>crates/tau-runtime/src/plugin_host/recording.rs</code> (plugin protocol recording). Adopting JSONL for sessions reuses the mental model and tooling.</p> <h4 id="11-file-layout"><a class="header" href="#11-file-layout">1.1. File layout</a></h4> <pre><code class="language-jsonl">{"type":"header","schema":1,"id":"e8b97f2c-...","created_at":"2026-05-01T14:33:21Z","agent_id":"coder","package":{"name":"my-coder-agent","version":"1.0.0","resolved_commit":"abc123..."},"llm_backend":"anthropic","title":null} {"type":"message","msg":{...}} {"type":"message","msg":{...}} {"type":"turn_summary","turn":1,"stop_reason":"EndTurn","input_tokens":523,"output_tokens":187} {"type":"message","msg":{...}} ... </code></pre> <ul> <li>Line 1 is the <strong>mandatory header</strong>. Schema version 1 baseline.</li> <li>Subsequent lines are appended per turn.</li> <li><code>turn_summary</code> lines carry per-turn metadata (stop reason + token usage) for inspection without re-running.</li> </ul> <h4 id="12-schema-versioning"><a class="header" href="#12-schema-versioning">1.2. Schema versioning</a></h4> <p><code>SCHEMA_VERSION = 1</code> baseline. Future bumps require their own ADR amendment. <code>SessionReader::read</code> rejects unsupported versions with <code>SessionError::UnsupportedSchema { schema, supported }</code>.</p> <h4 id="13-crash-recovery"><a class="header" href="#13-crash-recovery">1.3. Crash recovery</a></h4> <p><code>SessionReader::read</code> skips a single trailing malformed line gracefully (logs <code>tracing::warn! name="session.partial_line_skipped"</code>). A REPL crash mid-write leaves the file with a partial last line that the next resume can recover from. Earlier malformed lines return <code>SessionError::Parse</code>.</p> <h4 id="14-trigger-to-revisit-1"><a class="header" href="#14-trigger-to-revisit-1">1.4. Trigger to revisit</a></h4> <ul> <li>Cross-session full-text search → migrate to SQLite (planned destination if/when this lands).</li> <li>Schema breaking change → bump <code>schema</code> field; reader emits upgrade hint.</li> <li>Compression for large sessions (gzip) → tracked here as out of scope.</li> </ul> <h3 id="2-uuid-v7-ids-with-prefix-resolution"><a class="header" href="#2-uuid-v7-ids-with-prefix-resolution">2. UUID v7 ids with prefix resolution</a></h3> <p><strong>Decision:</strong> Session ids are UUID v7 (timestamp-prefixed, sortable). The CLI accepts ≥8-char prefixes at any subcommand that takes <code><id></code>. Prefix resolution finds the longest unique match; ambiguous prefixes return <code>SessionError::AmbiguousPrefix</code> with the candidate list.</p> <p><strong>Rationale:</strong></p> <p>UUID v7 matches the existing <code>AgentInstanceId::new()</code> precedent (<code>crates/tau-domain/src/id.rs:254</code> uses <code>Uuid::now_v7()</code>). Lexicographic sort = chronological sort, so listings are naturally ordered by creation time.</p> <p>8-char prefix gives users a short ergonomic id without collision risk (UUID v7 has timestamp entropy; collisions within a single user's archive are vanishingly rare). Lists display the 8-char prefix; <code>tau chat --resume <prefix></code> and friends resolve to the longest unique prefix automatically.</p> <h4 id="21-trigger-to-revisit"><a class="header" href="#21-trigger-to-revisit">2.1. Trigger to revisit</a></h4> <ul> <li>100k+ sessions per scope → consider longer prefix display (12 chars).</li> <li>User feedback that UUIDs are unfriendly → optional <code>/title <name></code> slash command for human-readable aliases (deferred polish).</li> </ul> <h3 id="3-strict-mode-resume----force-opt-out"><a class="header" href="#3-strict-mode-resume----force-opt-out">3. Strict-mode resume + <code>--force</code> opt-out</a></h3> <p><strong>Decision:</strong> <code>tau chat <agent> --resume <id></code> validates that the agent's <code>agent_id</code>, <code>package.name</code>, <code>package.version</code>, and <code>llm_backend</code> match what the session header recorded. Mismatch errors with <code>SessionError::AgentDrift { field, expected, actual }</code> naming the drifted field. <code>--force</code> bypasses the check with a warning printed to stderr.</p> <p><strong>Rationale:</strong></p> <p>Tau has typed errors for everything else (capability denials, schema validation, install failures). Silent drift on resume is inconsistent with that posture: the user expects "this is a continuation of the same conversation," and silent drift means the agent's tools, system prompt, or backend may have changed between save and resume.</p> <p>The alternative — best-effort resume — would let agent behavior silently change. The other alternative — snapshot resume (pin the package version at session creation; reinstall that exact version if missing) — is over-engineered. Most users won't need byte-identical reproducibility, and it doubles disk usage. If reproducibility becomes a Tier 4+ requirement, snapshot resume can be added as <code>--pin</code> opt-in.</p> <p>The <code>--force</code> opt-out gives users an escape hatch for "I know what I'm doing — resume anyway and accept any breakage."</p> <h4 id="31-drift-fields-checked"><a class="header" href="#31-drift-fields-checked">3.1. Drift fields checked</a></h4> <ul> <li><code>agent_id</code> (the named entry in project tau.toml).</li> <li><code>package.name</code>.</li> <li><code>package.version</code>.</li> <li><code>llm_backend</code>.</li> </ul> <p><code>resolved_commit</code> is recorded in the header but NOT enforced (audit field; commits don't change within a single version).</p> <h4 id="32-trigger-to-revisit"><a class="header" href="#32-trigger-to-revisit">3.2. Trigger to revisit</a></h4> <ul> <li>Real-world friction with strict mode (e.g., users always <code>--force</code>) → consider pin-mode default.</li> <li>Cross-version session migration (<code>tau session migrate <id></code>) → future subcommand if there's demand.</li> </ul> <h3 id="4-auto-save-default-with---ephemeral-opt-out"><a class="header" href="#4-auto-save-default-with---ephemeral-opt-out">4. Auto-save default with <code>--ephemeral</code> opt-out</a></h3> <p><strong>Decision:</strong> Every <code>tau chat <agent></code> invocation auto-creates a session file from turn 1. No opt-in needed. The <code>--ephemeral</code> flag opts out (in-memory only; no file ever written).</p> <p><strong>Rationale:</strong></p> <p>Matches dominant idiom: ChatGPT, Claude Desktop, goose, gptme, simonw/llm. Users have built an expectation that conversations are recoverable. The "I forgot to save the conversation that just gave me the answer" footgun outweighs the "I didn't want this saved" edge case.</p> <p><code>--ephemeral</code> covers the privacy edge case: when the user deliberately does not want the conversation persisted (testing, sensitive content, throwaway exploration).</p> <h4 id="41-privacy-posture"><a class="header" href="#41-privacy-posture">4.1. Privacy posture</a></h4> <p>Sessions persist:</p> <ul> <li>Full message text (user prompts, agent responses).</li> <li>Tool calls (the LLM's intent: "call fs-read with path=X").</li> <li>Tool results (file contents, command output, etc.).</li> <li>Tool errors (paths that were denied, etc.).</li> </ul> <p>Sessions do NOT persist:</p> <ul> <li>Environment variables.</li> <li>API keys (LLM-backend credentials).</li> <li>Plugin process internals.</li> <li>The system prompt is recorded (it's part of the agent's identity, not a secret).</li> </ul> <p>Users handling sensitive content should use <code>--ephemeral</code>. The CLI prints a one-line reminder on session start so the user is aware: <code>✓ Session: <prefix> (will be saved)</code> or <code>⚠ Ephemeral session — not saved to disk</code>.</p> <h4 id="42-file-lifecycle"><a class="header" href="#42-file-lifecycle">4.2. File lifecycle</a></h4> <ul> <li>Open: <code>SessionWriter::create(scope, id, header)</code> on <code>tau chat <agent></code> startup. Writes the header line immediately. File handle held open for the duration of the REPL.</li> <li>Append: each turn appends N message lines + 1 turn_summary line.</li> <li>Close: <code>SessionWriter::close()</code> on REPL exit. Flushes; no metadata rewrite.</li> <li>Crash recovery: see §1.3.</li> </ul> <h4 id="43-trigger-to-revisit-1"><a class="header" href="#43-trigger-to-revisit-1">4.3. Trigger to revisit</a></h4> <ul> <li>Per-session encryption (Phase 2+ ADR).</li> <li>Auto-prune by age or count → ADR-0013 amendment.</li> <li>Tool-result redaction in saved sessions (<code>--no-tool-results</code> flag) → minor flag addition.</li> </ul> <h3 id="5-tau-chat---resume--tau-session-subcommand-group"><a class="header" href="#5-tau-chat---resume--tau-session-subcommand-group">5. <code>tau chat --resume</code> + <code>tau session</code> subcommand group</a></h3> <p><strong>Decision:</strong> Resume invocation lives on <code>tau chat</code> (resuming IS chatting). Session management lives in a new <code>tau session</code> subcommand group (mirrors the existing <code>tau plugin</code> pattern).</p> <p><strong>Rationale:</strong></p> <p>Bundling listing/showing/deleting under <code>--list</code>/<code>--show</code>/<code>--delete</code> flags on <code>tau chat</code> muddies the verb: <code>tau chat --list</code> does not chat. Splitting along the verb boundary keeps each command's purpose clear:</p> <ul> <li><code>tau chat</code> = active sessions (start new, resume existing).</li> <li><code>tau session</code> = archive management.</li> </ul> <h4 id="51-cli-surface"><a class="header" href="#51-cli-surface">5.1. CLI surface</a></h4> <pre><code>tau chat <agent> # new session (auto-create file) tau chat <agent> --resume <id> # resume by id (or 8+ char prefix) tau chat <agent> --resume <id> --force # bypass drift check tau chat <agent> --ephemeral # in-memory only (no file) tau session list [<agent>] [--global] # list sessions [--limit N | --all] [--json] tau session show <id> [--global] # render transcript [--json] # raw JSONL (re-emitted via Output::json) tau session delete <id> [--global] # confirmation prompt [--force] # skip prompt tau session export <id> # convert transcript [--format jsonl|md|json] # default: jsonl [--global] </code></pre> <h4 id="52-slash-command-revision-repl"><a class="header" href="#52-slash-command-revision-repl">5.2. Slash command revision (REPL)</a></h4> <div class="table-wrapper"><table><thead><tr><th>Command</th><th>v0.1 behavior</th></tr></thead><tbody> <tr><td><code>/exit</code></td><td>unchanged (existing)</td></tr> <tr><td><code>/help</code></td><td>unchanged (updated to drop <code>/clear</code>)</td></tr> <tr><td><code>/history</code></td><td>unchanged</td></tr> <tr><td><code>/info</code></td><td><strong>new</strong> — print session id, file path, turn count, started_at, agent + package</td></tr> <tr><td><code>/clear</code></td><td><strong>dropped from active surface</strong> — prints deprecation message and continues. The user exits and re-runs for a fresh session.</td></tr> </tbody></table> </div> <p><code>/clear</code>'s old semantics ("drop in-memory history") are incoherent with persistence: clearing in-memory leaves the file intact, so resume would re-surface the cleared messages. Three options were considered (no-op for the file, rotate to new session, truncate file); option 3 (drop the command, instruct user to /exit + re-run) is the simplest and avoids the semantic murk. Future: a <code>/new</code> or <code>/branch</code> slash command could add in-REPL session rotation if demand surfaces.</p> <h4 id="53-exit-codes-per-adr-0007-7"><a class="header" href="#53-exit-codes-per-adr-0007-7">5.3. Exit codes (per ADR-0007 §7)</a></h4> <div class="table-wrapper"><table><thead><tr><th>Command</th><th>Success</th><th>Failure</th></tr></thead><tbody> <tr><td><code>tau chat --resume <id></code> (drift, no <code>--force</code>)</td><td>n/a</td><td>2</td></tr> <tr><td><code>tau chat --resume <id></code> (id not found)</td><td>n/a</td><td>2</td></tr> <tr><td><code>tau chat --resume <id></code> (prefix ambiguous)</td><td>n/a</td><td>2</td></tr> <tr><td><code>tau session list</code></td><td>0</td><td>2 (scope error)</td></tr> <tr><td><code>tau session show <id></code></td><td>0</td><td>2 (id not found / ambiguous)</td></tr> <tr><td><code>tau session delete <id></code></td><td>0</td><td>2 (id not found)</td></tr> <tr><td><code>tau session export <id></code></td><td>0</td><td>2 (id not found)</td></tr> </tbody></table> </div> <h4 id="54-trigger-to-revisit"><a class="header" href="#54-trigger-to-revisit">5.4. Trigger to revisit</a></h4> <ul> <li>Cross-session search → <code>tau session search <query></code> subcommand (likely SQLite migration).</li> <li>Session rename / alias names → <code>tau session rename <id> <name></code>.</li> <li>Bulk operations → <code>tau session delete --all</code>, <code>tau session delete --older-than 30d</code>.</li> </ul> <h2 id="consequences-13"><a class="header" href="#consequences-13">Consequences</a></h2> <h3 id="negative--new-cost-3"><a class="header" href="#negative--new-cost-3">Negative / new cost</a></h3> <ul> <li><code>tau-cli</code> gains a transitive dep on <code>humantime</code> (~30KB compiled). <code>humantime-serde</code> was already pulled in via <code>humantime</code>'s parent in <code>tau-pkg</code>'s lockfile usage; this just makes it a direct dep.</li> <li><code>tau-cli</code> gains a <code>session</code> module (~1100 LOC across 4 files: id.rs, store.rs, render.rs, mod.rs). Code organization is clean: one module per logical responsibility.</li> <li>The chat REPL's turn handler grows by ~50 LOC for the auto-save side-effect. Both branches (streaming + batch) write to the session file per turn.</li> <li><code>/clear</code>'s behavior change is a soft breaking change for scripts that drove it. The deprecation message guides users to the new workflow.</li> </ul> <h3 id="positive-9"><a class="header" href="#positive-9">Positive</a></h3> <ul> <li>Sessions auto-save by default — matches industry idiom; users recover the conversation that just gave them the answer.</li> <li>Resume is strict by default — the user's mental model is preserved (continuation of the same agent), with <code>--force</code> as the deliberate escape hatch.</li> <li>Source-agnostic by design — future <code>PackageSource</code> variants reuse the resume primitive without redesign.</li> <li>The new <code>tau session</code> subcommand group enables tooling workflows: <code>tau session list --json | jq</code>, <code>tau session show <id> | less</code>, <code>tau session export <id> --format md > file.md</code>.</li> <li>No tau-runtime changes — runtime stays stateless across CLI invocations (NG6 preserved).</li> </ul> <h3 id="neutral--new-obligations-8"><a class="header" href="#neutral--new-obligations-8">Neutral / new obligations</a></h3> <ul> <li>Future <code>tau session</code> extensions (search, rename, bulk operations) require their own ADRs (QG18). The CLI surface is locked at this ADR; any expansion needs a new ADR.</li> <li>The schema version is locked at 1; future bumps require ADR amendment + reader compatibility.</li> </ul> <h2 id="alternatives-considered-12"><a class="header" href="#alternatives-considered-12">Alternatives considered</a></h2> <h3 id="a-sqlite-single-db"><a class="header" href="#a-sqlite-single-db">A. SQLite single DB</a></h3> <p>Rejected for v0.1. Wins on cross-session search (the headline feature for simonw/llm and continue.dev). Costs: ~2MB rusqlite dep, schema migration design, lock contention model. Tau v0.1 doesn't have a cross-session search requirement; defer to a future ADR if/when it lands. JSONL is free to migrate to SQLite later (walk + INSERT).</p> <h3 id="b-single-jsonyaml-file-per-session-mods-aichat"><a class="header" href="#b-single-jsonyaml-file-per-session-mods-aichat">B. Single JSON/YAML file per session (mods, aichat)</a></h3> <p>Rejected. Full rewrite per turn is O(history) — bad for sessions that grow large. Crash safety is worse: a mid-write interrupt can corrupt the entire file. JSONL's append-only model is strictly better.</p> <h3 id="c-markdown-append-only-aider"><a class="header" href="#c-markdown-append-only-aider">C. Markdown append-only (aider)</a></h3> <p>Rejected. Markdown is human-inspectable but breaks structured operations: tool_use args become unreadable text, no ToolResult / ToolError variant distinction, no automated round-trip. JSONL preserves the typed structure.</p> <h3 id="d-best-effort-resume-silent-drift"><a class="header" href="#d-best-effort-resume-silent-drift">D. Best-effort resume (silent drift)</a></h3> <p>Rejected. See decision 3. Silent drift breaks the user's mental model. <code>--force</code> provides the deliberate opt-out for users who explicitly want to ignore drift.</p> <h3 id="e-snapshot-resume-pin-package-version-at-session-creation"><a class="header" href="#e-snapshot-resume-pin-package-version-at-session-creation">E. Snapshot resume (pin package version at session creation)</a></h3> <p>Rejected. See decision 3. Over-engineered for v0.1. Doubles disk usage. Future: <code>--pin</code> opt-in if reproducibility becomes a Tier 4+ requirement.</p> <h3 id="f-explicit-save-save-slash-command"><a class="header" href="#f-explicit-save-save-slash-command">F. Explicit save (<code>/save</code> slash command)</a></h3> <p>Rejected. See decision 4. "I forgot to save" is the dominant footgun. Auto-save aligns with industry idiom (ChatGPT, Claude Desktop, goose, gptme, simonw/llm).</p> <h3 id="g-flags-on-tau-chat-instead-of-tau-session-subcommand-group"><a class="header" href="#g-flags-on-tau-chat-instead-of-tau-session-subcommand-group">G. Flags on <code>tau chat</code> instead of <code>tau session</code> subcommand group</a></h3> <p>Rejected. See decision 5. <code>tau chat --list</code> does not chat; verb muddying. The subcommand-group pattern (mirroring <code>tau plugin</code>) keeps verbs clear.</p> <h3 id="h-keep-clears-old-semantics-no-op-for-the-file"><a class="header" href="#h-keep-clears-old-semantics-no-op-for-the-file">H. Keep <code>/clear</code>'s old semantics (no-op for the file)</a></h3> <p>Rejected. See §5.2. The in-memory clear with the file intact creates a "phantom resume" surprise: the user clears the conversation, exits, resumes, and the cleared messages reappear. Dropping <code>/clear</code> from the active surface (with a deprecation message) is the simplest fix.</p> <h2 id="references-4"><a class="header" href="#references-4">References</a></h2> <ul> <li>Spec: <code>docs/superpowers/specs/2026-05-01-repl-persistence-design.md</code></li> <li>Plan: <code>docs/superpowers/plans/2026-05-01-repl-persistence.md</code></li> <li>ADR-0006 §16 — "REPL persistence" Phase 1+ deferral.</li> <li>ADR-0006 NG6 — "no persistent agent memory in core"; this ADR preserves the boundary by placing persistence at the CLI layer.</li> <li>ADR-0007 §11 — <code>/save</code>/<code>/load</code> slash command deferral; v0.1 REPL stack (rustyline + termimad + in-memory <code>Vec<Message></code>).</li> <li>ADR-0007 §7 — three-bucket exit code policy reused.</li> <li>ADR-0009 — typed-error policy; <code>SessionError</code> follows.</li> <li>ADR-0011 — JSON event-per-line streaming convention reused for <code>tau session list --json</code>.</li> <li>ADR-0012 — three-bucket exit codes for lifecycle commands; source-agnostic verify primitive precedent.</li> <li><code>crates/tau-runtime/src/plugin_host/recording.rs</code> — JSONL writer precedent.</li> <li><code>crates/tau-domain/src/id.rs</code> — <code>AgentInstanceId::new()</code> UUID v7 precedent.</li> <li><code>crates/tau-cli/src/session/</code> — the new module.</li> <li><code>crates/tau-cli/src/cmd/chat.rs</code> — auto-save + resume turn handler.</li> <li><code>crates/tau-cli/src/cmd/session/</code> — the new subcommand group.</li> <li><code>crates/tau-pkg/src/scope.rs::Scope::state_path()</code> — per-scope state directory (<code><scope>/.tau</code> for project, <code>~/.tau</code> for global).</li> </ul> <div style="break-before: page; page-break-before: always;"></div><h1 id="adr-0014-sandboxing--hexagonal-port--linux-native-and-container-adapters"><a class="header" href="#adr-0014-sandboxing--hexagonal-port--linux-native-and-container-adapters">ADR-0014: Sandboxing — hexagonal port + Linux native and container adapters</a></h1> <p><strong>Status:</strong> Accepted <strong>Date:</strong> 2026-05-03 <strong>Deciders:</strong> Titouan Lebocq <strong>Supersedes:</strong> — <strong>Closes:</strong></p> <ul> <li><a href="decisions/0006-tau-runtime.html">ADR-0006</a> §13 — the v0.1 unsandboxed trust posture is now superseded by Layer-4 OS-level enforcement at the plugin spawn site. The capability model (declared in tau.toml, granted via project override, enforced at the runtime kernel) is now backed by real kernel primitives on Linux + container isolation cross-platform.</li> <li>Constitution G12 — "real OS-level sandboxing for plugin processes" is now implementable; activation by default is the next sub-project (see Sub-project A in <a href="decisions/../superpowers/specs/2026-05-03-sandboxing-followups.html">the followups doc</a>). <strong>Amends:</strong> — <strong>Refines:</strong> <a href="decisions/0002-manifest-format.html">ADR-0002</a> — capability declarations in <code>tau.toml</code> now have a typed <code>CapabilityShape</code> companion that adapters declare support for at probe time.</li> </ul> <h2 id="context-14"><a class="header" href="#context-14">Context</a></h2> <p>Phase 0 + Phase 1 (Tiers 1-3 priorities 1-11) shipped a complete agent-loop runtime with capability declarations in plugin manifests, project-level capability narrowing via override, and per-tool <code>SessionContext.granted_capabilities</code> flowing into IPC plugin processes. But the trust boundary stopped at the kernel layer: <code>crate::capability_check</code> gates which tools the AGENT can invoke; the plugin process itself runs unsandboxed and could ignore the capability boundary if it wanted. Constitution G12 reserved this for a future sub-project.</p> <p>Tier 3 priority 12 closes the gap. The constraint set:</p> <ul> <li><strong>Cross-platform:</strong> tau ships on Linux/macOS/Windows. Linux is the CI primary; macOS/Windows must at least compile and probe.</li> <li><strong>Hexagonal:</strong> the runtime should not bind to a specific kernel primitive; new sandbox backends (WASM, remote sandboxes, macOS, Windows) should be additive.</li> <li><strong>Defense in depth:</strong> the agent's capability check + the per-tool deny entries are policy; OS-level sandboxing is the enforcement backstop. Both must coexist.</li> <li><strong>Typed evolution:</strong> capability shapes must evolve additively as new enforcement primitives appear (landlock V2, network egress, syscall arg-filters, etc).</li> </ul> <p>Six discrete decisions follow.</p> <h2 id="decision-1--hexagonal-port--adapter-pattern"><a class="header" href="#decision-1--hexagonal-port--adapter-pattern">Decision 1 — Hexagonal port + adapter pattern</a></h2> <p><strong>Decision:</strong> add a single <code>tau_ports::Sandbox</code> trait that any concrete sandbox impl satisfies. Adapters live in dedicated workspace crates (<code>tau-sandbox-native</code>, <code>tau-sandbox-container</code>, future <code>tau-sandbox-macos</code>, etc). The runtime selects an adapter via a probe-based chain configured in <code><scope>/config.toml</code>.</p> <p><strong>Context:</strong> the alternative was per-platform conditional compilation inside <code>tau-runtime</code> (<code>#[cfg(target_os = "linux")] use linux_sandbox::*; #[cfg(target_os = "macos")] use macos_sandbox::*;</code>). That couples the runtime to every kernel primitive and makes adapter testing impossible in isolation.</p> <p><strong>Consequences:</strong></p> <ul> <li>Each adapter is a separate crate with its own Cargo.toml, deps, feature flags, and test surface. This is the same pattern tau already uses for <code>tau-plugins/anthropic</code>, <code>tau-plugins/ollama</code>, etc.</li> <li>The trait uses <code>async fn</code> (AFIT). AFIT prevents <code>dyn Sandbox</code>, so the runtime's <code>SandboxAdapter</code> enum dispatches to concrete adapters via match. The enum implements <code>Sandbox</code> itself, so downstream callers take <code>&impl Sandbox</code> polymorphically.</li> <li>Future sub-projects add new adapter crates without touching the runtime's selection logic (only the chain config + <code>instantiate</code> match arm).</li> </ul> <p><strong>Alternatives considered:</strong></p> <ul> <li>Single sandbox crate with <code>cfg(target_os)</code> modules — rejected (locks in the dispatch model; adapter authors can't test in isolation).</li> <li>Trait objects (<code>Arc<dyn Sandbox></code>) — blocked by AFIT.</li> <li>Generic-over-<code>S: Sandbox</code> everywhere — works for plan validation (<code>validate_plan_against_adapter<S></code>) but explodes monomorphization cost when the runtime holds the adapter behind <code>Arc</code>.</li> </ul> <h2 id="decision-2--linux-native-first-macos-windows-remote-in-future-sub-projects"><a class="header" href="#decision-2--linux-native-first-macos-windows-remote-in-future-sub-projects">Decision 2 — Linux native first; macOS, Windows, remote in future sub-projects</a></h2> <p><strong>Decision:</strong> v0.1 ships two adapters: <code>tau-sandbox-native</code> (Linux landlock + seccomp + namespaces) and <code>tau-sandbox-container</code> (docker/podman shell-out, cross-platform). macOS sandbox-exec, Windows AppContainer, and remote backends (Vercel Sandbox, Sandcastle) are future sub-projects.</p> <p><strong>Context:</strong> Linux is tau's primary CI target and where the most mature unprivileged kernel sandboxing primitives exist (landlock + seccomp + user namespaces, all stable since kernel 5.13). macOS sandbox-exec requires libsandbox FFI (poorly documented); Windows AppContainer requires WinAPI bindings via <code>windows-rs</code>. Both deserve their own sub-projects rather than rushed parity.</p> <p><strong>Consequences:</strong></p> <ul> <li>Non-Linux hosts probe <code>Unavailable</code> from the native adapter; the default chain falls back to the container adapter (which works on any host with Docker Desktop / Podman installed).</li> <li>macOS/Windows users who don't have a container runtime get a clear "no sandbox adapter available on this platform" error and exit code 2 from <code>tau resolve --check-sandbox</code>. Refusing to start without sandboxing is the correct security posture (see Decision 6).</li> <li>Phase 2 includes <code>tau-sandbox-macos</code> (sub-project J) and <code>tau-sandbox-windows</code> (sub-project K) as named follow-ups.</li> </ul> <p><strong>Alternatives considered:</strong></p> <ul> <li>Ship all three platforms together — rejected (would delay the Linux case for the harder platforms; landlock/seccomp work standalone).</li> <li>macOS via container only — viable today; explicit in the default chain. Documented as the intended posture until sub-project J lands.</li> </ul> <h2 id="decision-3--typed-capabilityshape-vocabulary-not-free-form-strings"><a class="header" href="#decision-3--typed-capabilityshape-vocabulary-not-free-form-strings">Decision 3 — Typed <code>CapabilityShape</code> vocabulary, not free-form strings</a></h2> <p><strong>Decision:</strong> introduce <code>pub enum CapabilityShape</code> in <code>tau-domain</code> with variants for each kernel-level enforcement primitive (<code>FilesystemRead</code>, <code>FilesystemWrite</code>, <code>ProcessExec</code>, <code>NetworkHttp</code>, <code>AgentSpawn</code>, <code>Custom { name }</code>). Adapters declare a <code>CapabilityShapeSet</code> they support; the runtime cross-checks plan-required vs adapter-supported shapes before spawn.</p> <p><strong>Context:</strong> the alternative is matching capabilities to enforcement primitives at every adapter call site via string comparison or ad-hoc enums. That couples each adapter to the full Capability hierarchy and forces every adapter to know how (e.g.) <code>Capability:: Process(Spawn)</code> and <code>Capability::Filesystem(Exec)</code> both reduce to the same kernel surface.</p> <p><strong>Consequences:</strong></p> <ul> <li><code>Capability::required_shape() -> CapabilityShape</code> is the single abstraction layer. Adapters never inspect <code>Capability</code> directly; they only ask "do I support this shape?".</li> <li>Two capabilities can map to the same shape: <code>Filesystem(Exec)</code> and <code>Process(Spawn)</code> both → <code>ProcessExec</code>. This deduplicates kernel work.</li> <li>New shapes (e.g. <code>FilesystemTruncate</code> for landlock V2) land in <code>tau-domain</code> with <code>#[non_exhaustive]</code> evolution. Adapters declare support per-shape via <code>supported_shapes</code>; unsupported shapes return <code>SandboxError::ShapeUnsupported</code> cleanly.</li> <li>All <code>Custom</code> capabilities reduce to <code>CapabilityShape::Custom { name }</code>. Adapters MAY refuse to sandbox custom shapes; the mock and native adapters do, the container adapter rejects via <code>validate_plan</code>.</li> </ul> <p><strong>Alternatives considered:</strong></p> <ul> <li>Match on <code>Capability</code> directly — rejected (couples every adapter to the full domain hierarchy).</li> <li>One enum variant per <code>Capability</code> variant — rejected (loses the deduplication; future shapes become 1:1 with capabilities).</li> </ul> <h2 id="decision-4--pre-flight-validation-hierarchy-4-layers"><a class="header" href="#decision-4--pre-flight-validation-hierarchy-4-layers">Decision 4 — Pre-flight validation hierarchy (4 layers)</a></h2> <p><strong>Decision:</strong> validation runs at four distinct layers, each catching errors closer to runtime:</p> <ol> <li><strong>Plugin author build (<code>cargo build</code>)</strong> — type-state in the SDK (deferred to a future sub-project; <code>#[capabilities(...)]</code> proc macro is optional polish).</li> <li><strong><code>tau install</code></strong> — Layer 2 cross-check between plugin manifest and the binary's <code>CAPABILITIES</code> handshake response (deferred to sub-project B).</li> <li><strong><code>tau resolve --check-sandbox</code> / <code>tau check</code></strong> — Layer 3 static validation: plan-required shapes ⊆ adapter-supported shapes for every plugin in the lockfile. Shipped in v0.1.</li> <li><strong>Plugin spawn</strong> — Layer 4 runtime enforcement: <code>wrap_spawn</code> is called immediately before fork+exec; the OS sandbox catches plugin-vs-declaration drift even if Layers 2-3 missed it.</li> </ol> <p><strong>Context:</strong> "errors found at Layer 4 (runtime) are expensive — the plugin already crashed". Pushing each error class to the earliest layer that can detect it is the project's discipline. Layer 3 specifically lets <code>tau resolve --check-sandbox</code> catch every plan-vs-adapter mismatch in one pass without spawning anything.</p> <p><strong>Consequences:</strong></p> <ul> <li>Layer 3 implementation: <code>validate_plan_against_adapter</code> returns <code>Result<(), Vec<SandboxValidationError>></code> — ALL errors, not just the first. Single CLI invocation surfaces every problem.</li> <li>Layer 4 implementation: <code>Sandbox::wrap_spawn(plan, &mut Command)</code> validates the plan first, then applies adapter-side wrapping (landlock pre_exec hook, container argv rewrite, etc).</li> <li>Layer 2 (install cross-check) is documented as future work in sub-project B; lockfile schema v3 → v4 added the <code>LockedPlugin.required_shapes</code> field but the install path populates it empty for now (with a <code>tracing::warn!</code> migration note for v3 lockfiles).</li> </ul> <p><strong>Alternatives considered:</strong></p> <ul> <li>Single Layer-4-only validation — rejected (every error becomes a spawn cost; bad plans waste minutes).</li> <li>Layer 1 type-state via proc macro at v0.1 — deferred; the SDK evolution tradeoff isn't worth it before the lower layers prove themselves.</li> </ul> <h2 id="decision-5--adapter-chain-with-probe-based-selection"><a class="header" href="#decision-5--adapter-chain-with-probe-based-selection">Decision 5 — Adapter chain with probe-based selection</a></h2> <p><strong>Decision:</strong> the scope's <code>[sandbox]</code> config defines an ordered <code>chain: Vec<SandboxAdapterConfig></code>. At runtime, each adapter is probed in order; the first <code>Available</code> adapter whose tier ≥ <code>minimum_tier</code> is selected. Empty chain → platform default (<code>[native, container]</code>). Mock adapter is opt-in only.</p> <p><strong>Context:</strong> the alternative is per-machine configuration: each user sets the active adapter explicitly in their scope config. That makes the same project config produce different sandboxing on different machines, which violates the "machine-agnostic" principle from the <a href="decisions/../explanation/tau-as-language.html">tau-as-language vision</a>.</p> <p><strong>Consequences:</strong></p> <ul> <li>The same <code><scope>/config.toml</code> works across Linux dev, Linux CI, macOS dev (with Docker), and Windows dev (with Docker Desktop). The probe at startup discovers what the local host can offer.</li> <li><code>minimum_tier</code> is the security floor: a project that says <code>minimum_tier = "Strict"</code> will refuse to start if only Light is available. This is opt-in stricter posture for projects that need it.</li> <li>Adapter probes cache their result behind <code>OnceCell</code> so repeated spawns don't re-probe.</li> <li>The <code>select_adapter</code> function returns <code>NoAdapterAvailable { tried }</code> with per-adapter rejection reasons when no adapter is usable, so the user sees "tried: native (kernel < 5.13), container (no docker on PATH)" rather than just "no adapter available".</li> </ul> <p><strong>Alternatives considered:</strong></p> <ul> <li>Fixed per-platform default — rejected (can't override; can't add Mock for tests; can't compose).</li> <li>User picks adapter by name — rejected (works on dev machine but breaks CI; loses the machine-agnostic guarantee).</li> <li>Auto-probe without config — happens at v0.1 when chain is empty, but the user can opt into explicit chain config when they want control.</li> </ul> <h2 id="decision-6--mock-adapter-is-opt-in-only-never-silent-fallback"><a class="header" href="#decision-6--mock-adapter-is-opt-in-only-never-silent-fallback">Decision 6 — Mock adapter is opt-in only, never silent fallback</a></h2> <p><strong>Decision:</strong> the <code>MockSandbox</code> adapter (which accepts every plan without enforcement) is admissible only when explicitly listed as <code>{ kind = "mock" }</code> in the scope config. The default chain (<code>[native, container]</code>) does NOT include Mock. When neither native nor container is available, the runtime returns <code>SandboxChainError::NoAdapterAvailable</code> with exit code 2 — it does NOT silently fall through to Mock.</p> <p><strong>Context:</strong> the security posture difference between "I asked for sandboxing and got Mock" and "I asked for sandboxing and got an explicit error" is enormous. A silent Mock fallback means a user believes their plugins are sandboxed when they aren't.</p> <p><strong>Consequences:</strong></p> <ul> <li>macOS/Windows users without Docker Desktop see a clear error and must either install Docker or explicitly opt into Mock with full knowledge of the security implications.</li> <li>CLI integration tests need a way to use Mock; this is mediated by the env var <code>TAU_TESTING_ALLOW_MOCK_SANDBOX=1</code> which gates the Mock instantiation in production builds. Documented as a debt item (sub-project H) — a dedicated test-only binary would be cleaner, but the env-var approach is the v0.1 pragmatic solution.</li> <li>The <code>tracing::warn!</code> from <code>unshare_flags_for_plan</code> (when <code>Network(Http)</code> is requested and per-host filtering hasn't shipped yet) follows the same fail-loud principle: under-enforcement is surfaced, not silenced.</li> </ul> <p><strong>Alternatives considered:</strong></p> <ul> <li>Silent fall-through to Mock — rejected (silent under-enforcement is the dangerous failure mode this decision exists to prevent).</li> <li>Build-time feature flag — rejected (every build that didn't enable the flag would silently break tests; runtime opt-in is more honest).</li> <li>Refuse Mock entirely outside <code>cfg(test)</code> — too restrictive; CLI integration tests via <code>cargo_bin("tau")</code> need Mock in some form.</li> </ul> <h2 id="vision"><a class="header" href="#vision">Vision</a></h2> <p>This sub-project lays the foundation for <strong>tau as a compiled language for agentic workflows</strong>. See <a href="decisions/../explanation/tau-as-language.html"><code>docs/explanation/tau-as-language.md</code></a> for the full vision. The sandboxing port + capability shape vocabulary</p> <ul> <li>adapter chain + probe-based machine-agnosticism are the primitives that future Phase 2 sub-projects build on.</li> </ul> <p><strong>Phase 2 sub-projects (named in the vision doc):</strong></p> <ul> <li><strong>A.</strong> <code>tau check</code> standalone command (~3 weeks). Layer 3 validation as a first-class CLI verb, not just a flag on <code>tau resolve</code>.</li> <li><strong>B.</strong> Tau target triple registry (~2 weeks). Formal naming + documented capability matrix per target.</li> <li><strong>C.</strong> <code>tau build --target <triple></code> + bundle format (~6 weeks). Content-hashed deployment artifacts.</li> <li><strong>D.</strong> Capability vocabulary forward-compatibility (~2 weeks). Stability discipline for <code>CapabilityShape</code> evolution across tau major versions.</li> <li><strong>E.</strong> Cross-machine reproducibility verification (~3 weeks).
