Extends <code>tau verify</code> to detect bundle tampering between build and run.</li> <li><strong>F.</strong> Remote target backends (~4-6 weeks per backend). Vercel Sandbox, Sandcastle, generic remote-execution providers.</li> <li><strong>G.</strong> WASM target backend (~12+ weeks). The most ambitious; plugins compile to <code>wasm32-wasip2</code>.</li> </ul> <p>These are independent of the <strong>immediate follow-ups</strong> documented in <a href="decisions/../superpowers/specs/2026-05-03-sandboxing-followups.html"><code>docs/superpowers/specs/2026-05-03-sandboxing-followups.md</code></a> (activation by default, plugin compatibility, e2e CI infrastructure, per-command exec gating, per-host network filter, fork-server pattern, macOS / Windows adapters). The followups doc tracks 11 named sub-projects that close the gaps left by v0.1 of THIS sub-project; Phase 2 sub-projects A-G build on top of the foundation once the followups are addressed.</p> <h2 id="notes"><a class="header" href="#notes">Notes</a></h2> <ul> <li>The sandboxing port is now stable (PROVISIONAL warning dropped from <code>tau_ports::Sandbox</code>); evolution is via <code>#[non_exhaustive]</code> on every public type.</li> <li>Lockfile schema v3 → v4 is additive only. v3 lockfiles continue to load with a once-per-process migration warning; the <code>--rehash</code> flag for explicit refresh is deferred to sub-project B.</li> <li>The <code>[sandbox]</code> section in <code><scope>/config.toml</code> is opt-in; existing scope configs without it use the platform default chain. Schema version bumped 1 → 2 (additive; v1 configs auto-upgrade with empty <code>sandbox</code> section).</li> </ul> <h2 id="references-5"><a class="header" href="#references-5">References</a></h2> <ul> <li>Spec: <a href="decisions/../superpowers/specs/2026-05-02-sandboxing-design.html"><code>docs/superpowers/specs/2026-05-02-sandboxing-design.md</code></a>.</li> <li>Plan: <a href="decisions/../superpowers/plans/2026-05-02-sandboxing.html"><code>docs/superpowers/plans/2026-05-02-sandboxing.md</code></a>.</li> <li>Vision: <a href="decisions/../explanation/tau-as-language.html"><code>docs/explanation/tau-as-language.md</code></a>.</li> <li>Followups: <a href="decisions/../superpowers/specs/2026-05-03-sandboxing-followups.html"><code>docs/superpowers/specs/2026-05-03-sandboxing-followups.md</code></a>.</li> <li>Trait: <a href="decisions/../../crates/tau-ports/src/sandbox.rs"><code>crates/tau-ports/src/sandbox.rs</code></a>.</li> <li>Adapters: <a href="https://github.com/titouanlebocq/tau/tree/main/crates/tau-sandbox-native"><code>crates/tau-sandbox-native/</code></a>, <a href="https://github.com/titouanlebocq/tau/tree/main/crates/tau-sandbox-container"><code>crates/tau-sandbox-container/</code></a>.</li> <li>Runtime glue: <a href="https://github.com/titouanlebocq/tau/tree/main/crates/tau-runtime/src/sandbox"><code>crates/tau-runtime/src/sandbox/</code></a>.</li> <li>Layer 3 CLI: <a href="decisions/../../crates/tau-cli/src/cmd/resolve.rs"><code>crates/tau-cli/src/cmd/resolve.rs</code></a> (<code>--check-sandbox</code> flag).</li> </ul> <div style="break-before: page; page-break-before: always;"></div><h1 id="adr-0015-sandbox-activation-by-default--declarative-requirements--adapter-registry--resolver"><a class="header" href="#adr-0015-sandbox-activation-by-default--declarative-requirements--adapter-registry--resolver">ADR-0015: Sandbox activation by default — declarative requirements + adapter registry + resolver</a></h1> <p><strong>Status:</strong> Accepted <strong>Date:</strong> 2026-05-04 <strong>Deciders:</strong> Titouan Lebocq <strong>Supersedes:</strong> — <strong>Closes:</strong></p> <ul> <li>Sub-project A from <a href="decisions/../superpowers/specs/2026-05-03-sandboxing-followups.html">the sandboxing follow-ups</a> — sandboxing is now ON by default for every plugin spawn.</li> <li>ADR-0014 §1 (chain-based selection): the <code>Sandbox</code> port and the existing adapters are unchanged, but the <em>selection mechanism</em> is replaced (see Decision 5 below). <strong>Amends:</strong></li> <li><a href="decisions/0014-sandboxing.html">ADR-0014</a> §1 — <code>tau-runtime::sandbox::chain::select_adapter</code> is removed. Selection now flows through <code>tau-runtime::sandbox::resolver::resolve_adapter</code> against a static <code>AdapterRegistration</code> slice.</li> <li><a href="decisions/0014-sandboxing.html">ADR-0014</a> §5 — the <code><scope>/config.toml [sandbox]</code> section is migrated from v2 (chain + minimum_tier) to v3 (required_tier + required_shapes). v2 lockfiles auto-load with a <code>tracing::warn!</code> and best-effort migration; v3 is canonical. <strong>Refines:</strong></li> <li><a href="decisions/0008-plugin-loading.html">ADR-0008</a> — <code>PluginHostOptions</code> now carries <code>sandbox_adapter</code>, <code>force_passthrough</code>, and <code>force_adapter_kind</code> fields; every spawn site (<code>describe_plugin</code>, <code>load_llm_backend</code>, <code>load_tool</code>, <code>load_storage</code>) flows through the resolver.</li> </ul> <h2 id="context-15"><a class="header" href="#context-15">Context</a></h2> <p>Tier 3 priority 12 (<a href="decisions/0014-sandboxing.html">ADR-0014</a>) shipped the sandbox infrastructure: a <code>tau_ports::Sandbox</code> port, two concrete adapter crates (<code>tau-sandbox-native</code>, <code>tau-sandbox-container</code>), Layer 3 pre-flight validation, and a chain-based <code>select_adapter</code> function. Activation was deferred: production plugin spawn sites still passed <code>None</code> for the sandbox argument. The result: zero plugins were actually sandboxed.</p> <p>Sub-project A from the followups doc closes that gap, but the original "chain" model surfaced design issues that justify revisiting it before activating it everywhere:</p> <ul> <li><strong>Chains conflate intent with mechanism.</strong> A chain like <code>[{ kind = "native" }, { kind = "container" }, { kind = "passthrough" }]</code> smushes together (a) what the project requires (Strict isolation), (b) which mechanisms can deliver it on this host, and (c) how to fall back. The user is forced to author the resolution algorithm.</li> <li><strong>Industry pattern is "declare requirements, let the toolchain pick the toolchain."</strong> Bazel's platforms/toolchains is the closest analogue: the BUILD declares <code>target_platform(cpu="arm64", os="linux")</code>, the toolchain registry advertises which toolchains support which <code>(cpu, os)</code> tuples, and Bazel's resolver picks. The user never writes a list of toolchains in priority order.</li> <li><strong>Probe results are runtime data; chain authoring is upfront.</strong> A chain in <code>tau.toml</code> can't react to "Docker isn't installed on this host" as cleanly as a resolver invoked at runtime against a registry of "what does each adapter advertise?".</li> <li><strong>Plugin-side requirements are first-class.</strong> A plugin that genuinely requires Strict tier (e.g. one that handles untrusted user input) needs to express that, and the project + plugin requirements need to <em>unify</em> before the resolver picks an adapter. A chain has no place for this.</li> <li><strong>Activation default needs a defensible failure mode.</strong> macOS without Docker has no Linux-native landlock, no container runtime — should tau refuse to start, fall back to no isolation with a warn, or something else? The chain model didn't have a clean answer.</li> </ul> <p>The design space (full options table in <a href="decisions/../superpowers/specs/2026-05-04-sandbox-activation-design.html">the design doc</a>) was explored fresh. The chain was rejected in favor of declarative requirements + a static adapter registry + a runtime resolver. Six discrete decisions follow.</p> <h2 id="decision-1--sandboxing-is-on-by-default-opt-out-is-explicit-and-visible"><a class="header" href="#decision-1--sandboxing-is-on-by-default-opt-out-is-explicit-and-visible">Decision 1 — Sandboxing is ON by default; opt-out is explicit and visible</a></h2> <p><strong>Decision:</strong> every <code>Runtime::run</code> builds a <code>SandboxPlan</code> per plugin, calls <code>resolve_adapter</code> to obtain a concrete <code>SandboxAdapter</code>, and passes both into <code>wrap_spawn</code> at the plugin host layer. The escape hatch is the explicit <code>--no-sandbox</code> global flag (or <code>[sandbox] required_tier = "none"</code> in scope config), which selects the <code>passthrough</code> adapter — never silent fall-through.</p> <p><strong>Context:</strong> the alternative was opt-in (a flag like <code>--enable-sandbox</code>). Defense in depth means the secure default must be the path of least resistance; if the user opts out, they declare it. Constitution G12 and ADR-0014 §6 already established "OS-level enforcement is the backstop"; not activating it by default would leave that promise unredeemed.</p> <p><strong>Consequences:</strong></p> <ul> <li>Existing tau projects with no <code>[sandbox]</code> block default to <code>required_tier = strict</code>. On Linux, the native adapter satisfies this. On macOS without Docker, resolution fails with a guided diagnostic (see Decision 3).</li> <li>The <code>passthrough</code> adapter (Decision 4) is a registered first-class adapter, not a "no sandbox" sentinel. <code>--no-sandbox</code> is honored by routing to passthrough; the user always knows which adapter is in play.</li> <li>Operators get a one-line CI rule: "no project ships without a <code>[sandbox]</code> block AND that block resolves on the target platform". <code>tau resolve --check-sandbox</code> is the gate.</li> </ul> <p><strong>Alternatives considered:</strong></p> <ul> <li><strong>Opt-in flag.</strong> Rejected: violates secure-by-default. Defense-in-depth is undermined when the kernel layer is dormant unless explicitly turned on.</li> <li><strong>Auto-fall-soft to passthrough on resolution failure.</strong> Rejected: silent demotion is the worst possible failure mode for a security feature. The user must learn that resolution failed, not discover via a post-mortem.</li> </ul> <h2 id="decision-2--pluginhostoptionssandbox_adapter-not-runtimebuilder-di"><a class="header" href="#decision-2--pluginhostoptionssandbox_adapter-not-runtimebuilder-di">Decision 2 — <code>PluginHostOptions.sandbox_adapter</code>, not Runtime::builder DI</a></h2> <p><strong>Decision:</strong> the resolved <code>Arc<SandboxAdapter></code> is carried on <code>PluginHostOptions</code> (along with <code>force_passthrough: bool</code> and <code>force_adapter_kind: Option<SandboxAdapterKind></code> for the CLI overrides), not injected through a builder method on <code>Runtime</code>. The CLI's <code>tau-cli/src/cmd/plugin_loader.rs::load_plugins</code> is the single integration point that reads scope config, calls <code>resolve_adapter</code>, and threads results through.</p> <p><strong>Context:</strong> the alternative was <code>Runtime::builder().with_sandbox(adapter)</code> — closer to the <code>with_*</code> methods already on the builder. But the builder is constructed in <code>Runtime::run</code>, before scope config is loaded. Pushing sandbox resolution into the builder would have required the builder to depend on <code>tau_pkg::scope</code>, which inverts the existing dependency graph (<code>tau-pkg</code> depends on <code>tau-runtime</code> for <code>RuntimeBuilder</code> reuse).</p> <p><strong>Consequences:</strong></p> <ul> <li><code>Runtime</code> itself is unaware of sandboxing. The kernel still calls <code>plugin_host::spawn_and_handshake</code>; the sandbox enforcement happens during <code>wrap_spawn</code>, transparent to the agent loop.</li> <li>The CLI's <code>plugin_loader</code> becomes the natural home for resolver + adapter wiring — it already loads scope config, lockfile, and plugin manifests.</li> <li>Tests that don't go through the CLI (the runtime's own integration tests) can construct <code>PluginHostOptions { sandbox_adapter: None, .. }</code> to skip sandboxing entirely. The mock adapter is still injectable via the <code>TAU_TESTING_ALLOW_MOCK_SANDBOX=1</code> env-var override (preserved from priority 12).</li> <li>A future "library mode" caller (Phase 2 work) sets the field directly without going through the CLI surface.</li> </ul> <p><strong>Alternatives considered:</strong></p> <ul> <li><strong><code>Runtime::builder().with_sandbox(adapter)</code>.</strong> Rejected: inverts dep graph; adds a builder method that's only called from one place.</li> <li><strong>Static config / lazy_static.</strong> Rejected: testing is harder; resolution becomes implicit.</li> </ul> <h2 id="decision-3--hard-refuse-on-resolution-failure-no-silent-fall-through"><a class="header" href="#decision-3--hard-refuse-on-resolution-failure-no-silent-fall-through">Decision 3 — Hard refuse on resolution failure (no silent fall-through)</a></h2> <p><strong>Decision:</strong> when <code>resolve_adapter</code> returns <code>Err(ResolutionError)</code>, the runtime exits with code 2 and a guided multi-option diagnostic. There is no fall-back to passthrough, no warning-and-continue, no degraded mode. The user must either (a) install a satisfying adapter (e.g. Docker), (b) lower <code>required_tier</code> in scope config, or (c) pass <code>--no-sandbox</code> explicitly.</p> <p><strong>Context:</strong> the failure mode of a security feature is what defines it. Silent demotion gives users a sandbox icon in their config and zero enforcement at runtime. Three-bucket exit codes (ADR-0007 §7) give us "configuration error" = exit 2; this is the canonical case.</p> <p><strong>Consequences:</strong></p> <ul> <li>macOS users without Docker who don't have a <code>[sandbox]</code> block and don't pass <code>--no-sandbox</code> get exit 2 on first run. The diagnostic shows: which adapters were tried, why each was rejected (platform / probe / tier / shape / plugin tier), and three remediations they can pick from. <code>tau sandbox setup</code> (Decision 5 corollary) walks them through option (b) interactively.</li> <li>The <code>tau resolve --check-sandbox</code> subcommand exits 2 on the same conditions, giving CI a pre-flight gate without needing to spawn plugins.</li> <li>The error rendering surface (<code>crates/tau-cli/src/cmd/error_render.rs</code>) gets formal multi-option output with insta snapshot tests.</li> </ul> <p><strong>Alternatives considered:</strong></p> <ul> <li><strong>Fall-soft to passthrough with a warn.</strong> Rejected: see Decision 1's discussion. The whole point of activation is that the kernel layer is real, not optional.</li> <li><strong>Refuse only if no <code>[sandbox]</code> block exists; permit fall-soft if the block lists alternatives.</strong> Rejected: the chain model in disguise; we already rejected chains.</li> </ul> <h2 id="decision-4--passthrough-is-a-registered-first-class-adapter-not-none"><a class="header" href="#decision-4--passthrough-is-a-registered-first-class-adapter-not-none">Decision 4 — <code>passthrough</code> is a registered first-class adapter, not "None"</a></h2> <p><strong>Decision:</strong> add a <code>passthrough</code> adapter (<code>crates/tau-runtime/src/sandbox/passthrough.rs</code>, ~30 LOC) that implements <code>tau_ports::Sandbox</code> directly. It probes <code>Available</code> everywhere, advertises every shape as supported, validates every plan as Ok, and <code>wrap_spawn</code> returns the command unchanged. It's registered in the adapter registry with <code>tier = None</code> and <code>priority = 0</code> (lowest). <code>SandboxAdapter</code> gains a <code>Passthrough</code> variant.</p> <p><strong>Context:</strong> the priority-12 design represented "no sandbox" as <code>Option<SandboxAdapter>::None</code>. That was always going to age badly: every consumer of <code>Option<&SandboxAdapter></code> gets a special case for <code>None</code>, the overrides logic (<code>--no-sandbox</code>) has to short-circuit before reaching the adapter layer, and the registry has to model "the always-available fall-back" as a separate concept from "the available adapters".</p> <p><strong>Decision</strong> treats "no isolation" as a real adapter with its own behavior: it satisfies <code>required_tier = none</code>, fails <code>required_tier = light</code> and stronger via the tier filter, and fails plugin tier requirements via the plugin-tier filter. The user-facing name is "passthrough", consistent across <code>tau sandbox status</code>, error messages, and <code>--sandbox passthrough</code>.</p> <p><strong>Consequences:</strong></p> <ul> <li><code>--no-sandbox</code> is sugar for <code>--sandbox passthrough</code> (forces the adapter regardless of registry filtering).</li> <li><code>tau sandbox status</code> always shows passthrough as Available, with an explicit "delivers no isolation" note. Users see what they'd be getting.</li> <li>The registry's lowest-priority entry catches all <code>required_tier = none</code> requests when no other adapter probed Available.</li> <li>Plugin-tier filtering: a plugin declaring <code>required_tier = strict</code> rejects passthrough even when the project says <code>required_tier = none</code> (see Decision 6).</li> </ul> <p><strong>Alternatives considered:</strong></p> <ul> <li><strong>Keep <code>Option<SandboxAdapter>::None</code>.</strong> Rejected: special cases ripple through every caller; the override logic gets increasingly fragile.</li> <li><strong>Name it <code>bare</code>, <code>host</code>, or <code>none</code>.</strong> Rejected: <code>none</code> collides with the tier name; <code>bare</code> is jargon; <code>host</code> is ambiguous (host vs guest namespace). <code>passthrough</code> is the established term in the network/security space for "let the bytes through unchanged".</li> </ul> <h2 id="decision-5--declarative-requirements--adapter-registry--resolver-bazel-style"><a class="header" href="#decision-5--declarative-requirements--adapter-registry--resolver-bazel-style">Decision 5 — Declarative requirements + adapter registry + resolver (Bazel-style)</a></h2> <p><strong>Decision:</strong> the scope config schema migrates from v2 chain (<code>[sandbox] chain = [{ kind = "native" }, { kind = "container" }, { kind = "passthrough" }]</code>) to v3 declarative (<code>[sandbox] required_tier = "strict"</code>, optional <code>required_shapes = [...]</code>). A static <code>AdapterRegistration</code> slice in <code>tau-runtime::sandbox::registry</code> enumerates the four adapters with their <code>(platforms, tiers_supported, shapes_supported, priority)</code> metadata. <code>resolve_adapter</code> filters the registry through a 5-stage pipeline (platform → probe → tier → shape → plugin tier) and picks the highest-priority remaining candidate.</p> <p><strong>Context:</strong> Bazel's platforms/toolchains is the closest analogue. The BUILD file declares the <em>target platform</em> (<code>cpu="arm64", os="linux"</code>); each toolchain declares which <code>target_compatible_with</code> constraints it satisfies; Bazel's resolver picks. The user writes intent ("I need to build for arm64-linux"), the toolchain author writes capability ("I support arm64-linux", with priority), and the resolver produces a concrete pick at build time.</p> <p>The same shape applies to sandboxing:</p> <ul> <li>The project author writes intent: <code>required_tier = "strict"</code>, optionally <code>required_shapes = ["FilesystemRead", "ProcessExec"]</code>.</li> <li>The adapter author registers capability: native says <code>(linux, [light, strict], [Filesystem*, Process*, Network*], priority=100)</code>; container says <code>(any, [light, strict], [Filesystem*, Process*, Network*], priority=50)</code>; remote says <code>(any, [light, strict], [Filesystem*, Process*], priority=25, probe=Unavailable)</code>; passthrough says <code>(any, [none], [all], priority=0)</code>.</li> <li>The resolver — invoked at every <code>Runtime::run</code> — computes the intersection and picks.</li> </ul> <p><strong>Consequences:</strong></p> <ul> <li>New adapters land additively. Adding a <code>tau-sandbox-macos</code> adapter (sub-project J) becomes one new <code>AdapterRegistration</code> entry plus the adapter crate. No changes to consumers.</li> <li>The error message for "nothing matches" can list every adapter that was tried and why — the resolver has all the data; it just renders it via <code>ResolutionError::NoAdapterMatches { tried: Vec<(name, ResolutionRejection)> }</code>.</li> <li>Tests can probe the resolver directly (<code>resolve_adapter(&requirements, &plugins).await</code>) without spawning a runtime. The 5-stage pipeline is unit-testable in isolation.</li> <li>Schema migration from v2 to v3 is best-effort: v2 lockfiles auto-load with a <code>tracing::warn!</code> (consistent with the lockfile v3→v4 precedent from priority 7) and the resolver picks a sensible v3 equivalent. v3 is the canonical form going forward.</li> <li>A new family of CLI subcommands grows naturally: <code>tau sandbox status</code> (read-only diagnostic), <code>tau sandbox setup</code> (interactive + non-interactive scope config writer). The resolver is the single source of truth that <code>status</code> queries.</li> </ul> <p><strong>Alternatives considered:</strong></p> <ul> <li><strong>Keep the chain model.</strong> Rejected for the reasons in Context: conflates intent with mechanism, doesn't model plugin-side requirements cleanly, can't react to runtime probe data.</li> <li><strong>Custom scoring function instead of priority + filter pipeline.</strong> Rejected: more flexible than needed; harder to reason about; the priority sort suffices for the four adapters we have, and adding new ones doesn't require rebalancing scores.</li> <li><strong>Dynamic adapter loading (plugins as adapters).</strong> Rejected: out of scope; the registry is intentionally compile-time so adapters can be type-checked. Future work could add a registration ABI.</li> </ul> <h2 id="decision-6--plugin-side-tier-declarations-symmetric-to-project-requirements"><a class="header" href="#decision-6--plugin-side-tier-declarations-symmetric-to-project-requirements">Decision 6 — Plugin-side tier declarations (symmetric to project requirements)</a></h2> <p><strong>Decision:</strong> add <code>[sandbox]</code> to the plugin manifest (<code>PluginSandboxRequirements { required_tier: Option<PluginRequiredTier>, required_shapes: Vec<CapabilityShape> }</code>). The resolver's 5th filter stage rejects any adapter whose tier is below the maximum tier required across all plugins in the load set. <code>ResolutionError::PluginTierMismatch</code> is a separate error variant from <code>NoAdapterMatches</code> so the diagnostic can identify which plugin is asking for what.</p> <p><strong>Context:</strong> a plugin that processes untrusted input (e.g. a parser, a code formatter, an HTTP client) has a defensible reason to insist on Strict tier even if the project author would have been content with Light. Without a plugin-side declaration, the project's <code>[sandbox]</code> block is the only signal — and the project author may not know which plugins need stronger isolation.</p> <p>The symmetry mirrors <code>dependencies</code> resolution: the project declares "I want package X"; the plugin declares "I require package Y at version Z". The dep resolver intersects. The sandbox resolver does the same with tiers.</p> <p><strong>Consequences:</strong></p> <ul> <li>Existing plugin manifests with no <code>[sandbox]</code> block default to <code>required_tier = None</code> (no extra requirement beyond the project's). This is <code>#[serde(default)]</code> on <code>PluginSandboxRequirements</code>, so unmodified plugin manifests remain valid.</li> <li>The five existing plugins (anthropic, ollama, openai, fs-read, shell) ship with no <code>[sandbox]</code> block in this sub-project. Sub-project B adds explicit declarations as part of the per-plugin compatibility verification pass.</li> <li><code>tau resolve --check-sandbox</code> is extended to surface plugin-tier mismatches even when the project's <code>required_tier = none</code> would otherwise have skipped tier checks. (Without this, a project with <code>required_tier = none</code> would silently let a plugin's <code>required_tier = strict</code> slip through.)</li> <li>The diagnostic for plugin-tier mismatch names the offending plugin: "plugin <code>foo</code> requires Strict but resolved adapter <code>passthrough</code> provides None — please install Docker or run on Linux".</li> </ul> <p><strong>Alternatives considered:</strong></p> <ul> <li><strong>Plugin-side declarations only (no project-side).</strong> Rejected: the project author needs to declare "I want this whole agent to run Strict" for the case where a plugin's manifest is silent.</li> <li><strong>Project-side only (no plugin-side).</strong> Rejected: makes the project author responsible for knowing each plugin's needs. Doesn't scale to a real plugin ecosystem.</li> <li><strong><code>required_shapes</code> on plugins, no <code>required_tier</code>.</strong> Rejected: shapes are a finer-grained vocabulary that plugins use to express <em>what they need to do</em> (FilesystemRead, ProcessExec, ...). Tier is a coarser vocabulary expressing <em>how strong an isolation regime they require</em>. They're not interchangeable; both exist on the plugin side, with <code>required_shapes</code> already present from priority 12.</li> </ul> <h2 id="implementation-summary"><a class="header" href="#implementation-summary">Implementation summary</a></h2> <p>The 12 commits on <code>feat/sandbox-activation-spec</code> (PR #23) realize these decisions via:</p> <div class="table-wrapper"><table><thead><tr><th>Layer</th><th>Crate</th><th>Files</th></tr></thead><tbody> <tr><td>Schema migration v2 → v3</td><td><code>tau-pkg</code></td><td><code>src/scope.rs</code></td></tr> <tr><td>Plugin manifest schema</td><td><code>tau-domain</code></td><td><code>src/package/sandbox.rs</code></td></tr> <tr><td>Adapter registry</td><td><code>tau-runtime</code></td><td><code>src/sandbox/registry.rs</code></td></tr> <tr><td>Passthrough adapter</td><td><code>tau-runtime</code></td><td><code>src/sandbox/passthrough.rs</code></td></tr> <tr><td>Resolution error taxonomy</td><td><code>tau-runtime</code></td><td><code>src/sandbox/resolution_error.rs</code></td></tr> <tr><td>Resolver (5-stage pipeline)</td><td><code>tau-runtime</code></td><td><code>src/sandbox/resolver.rs</code></td></tr> <tr><td>Plugin host integration</td><td><code>tau-runtime</code></td><td><code>src/plugin_host/mod.rs</code></td></tr> <tr><td>CLI integration</td><td><code>tau-cli</code></td><td><code>src/cmd/plugin_loader.rs</code></td></tr> <tr><td>Global CLI flags</td><td><code>tau-cli</code></td><td><code>src/cli.rs</code></td></tr> <tr><td>Error renderer</td><td><code>tau-cli</code></td><td><code>src/cmd/error_render.rs</code></td></tr> <tr><td>Sandbox subcommands</td><td><code>tau-cli</code></td><td><code>src/cmd/sandbox.rs</code></td></tr> <tr><td><code>--check-sandbox</code> extension</td><td><code>tau-cli</code></td><td><code>src/cmd/resolve.rs</code></td></tr> </tbody></table> </div> <p>Test coverage: ~250 unit tests across the workspace pass on the 25-job CI matrix (Linux/macOS/Windows × stable/1.91); 24 doc tests pass. No new CI jobs were added (branch protection stays at 25 required checks, unchanged from the priority-12 baseline).</p> <p>The mock adapter is unchanged in <code>tau-ports/src/fixtures.rs</code>; the <code>TAU_TESTING_ALLOW_MOCK_SANDBOX=1</code> env-var injection path bypasses the registry directly. Sub-project H from the followups doc handles the eventual cleanup.</p> <h2 id="forward-links"><a class="header" href="#forward-links">Forward links</a></h2> <ul> <li><strong>Sub-project B</strong> (plugin compatibility verification) builds directly on this work: per-plugin <code>tau resolve --check-sandbox</code> runs, plugin manifest <code>[sandbox]</code> blocks added where appropriate, Layer 2 install-time cross-check.</li> <li><strong>Sub-project D</strong> (e2e CI) gains a clean activation point: e2e tests can rely on resolved adapters rather than mocking the chain.</li> <li><strong>Phase 2 sub-project A</strong> (<code>tau check</code> standalone) reuses <code>resolve_adapter</code> + <code>validate_plan_against_adapter</code> as the pre-flight validation surface.</li> </ul> <div style="break-before: page; page-break-before: always;"></div><h1 id="adr-0016-plugin-compatibility-verification--layer-2-install-time-cross-check--per-plugin-harness"><a class="header" href="#adr-0016-plugin-compatibility-verification--layer-2-install-time-cross-check--per-plugin-harness">ADR-0016: Plugin compatibility verification — Layer 2 install-time cross-check + per-plugin harness</a></h1> <p><strong>Status:</strong> Accepted <strong>Date:</strong> 2026-05-04 <strong>Deciders:</strong> Titouan Lebocq <strong>Supersedes:</strong> — <strong>Closes:</strong></p> <ul> <li>Sub-project B from <a href="decisions/../superpowers/specs/2026-05-03-sandboxing-followups.html">the sandboxing follow-ups</a> — the 5 real shipped plugins now declare <code>[sandbox] required_tier = "strict"</code>, install carries Layer 2 cross-check at step 8.7, and a verification harness exists in <code>tau-plugin-compat</code>.</li> <li>The foundation portion of sub-project D (controlled-environment test binary + landlock-symlink fix in <code>tau-sandbox-native::light::resolve_symlinks_for_landlock</code>) — D's remainder (re-introducing 5 e2e test files) stays as a separate sub-project. <strong>Amends:</strong></li> <li><a href="decisions/0015-sandbox-activation.html">ADR-0015</a> Decision 6 — plugin manifests can now declare <code>[sandbox] required_tier</code>. The 5 real plugins (<code>anthropic</code>, <code>ollama</code>, <code>openai</code>, <code>fs-read</code>, <code>shell</code>) declare <code>Strict</code>. Toy plugins (<code>echo-llm</code>, <code>echo-tool</code>) omit the block. <strong>Refines:</strong></li> <li><a href="decisions/0008-plugin-loading.html">ADR-0008</a> — install lifecycle gains step 8.7 between source SHA-256 (8.6) and lockfile write (9). On cross-check failure, install aborts with <code>InstallError::CrossCheck { message }</code>; user retries via <code>tau install --force</code> after fixing the manifest.</li> </ul> <h2 id="context-16"><a class="header" href="#context-16">Context</a></h2> <p>Sub-project A (<a href="decisions/0015-sandbox-activation.html">ADR-0015</a>) shipped sandboxing on by default at commit <code>7fe6cfb</code> on 2026-05-04. Every plugin spawn now flows through <code>resolve_adapter</code> against the static adapter registry. That work proved 250+ unit tests pass; the workspace compiles cleanly across Linux/macOS/Windows × stable/1.91.</p> <p>What sub-project A's CI did <strong>not</strong> prove: that the 5 real shipped plugins actually work end-to-end when sandbox enforcement is engaged. Activation is theoretical until verified against the real plugin surface.</p> <p>Two further gaps:</p> <ol> <li> <p><strong>Layer 2 install-time cross-check is unimplemented.</strong> The kernel host already issues <code>tool.describe_capabilities</code> calls per tool method (priority 12 work) — but the responses are advisory, not validated against the manifest. A buggy or compromised plugin binary can claim capabilities its manifest doesn't declare; the kernel's capability check uses the manifest, so the binary's claims silently expand the attack surface.</p> </li> <li> <p><strong>No automated end-to-end plugin verification.</strong> Nothing today exercises "install plugin → resolve adapter → spawn under enforcement → run golden path → assert success" for any of the 5 real plugins. Regressions go undetected until a human runs <code>tau chat</code>.</p> </li> </ol> <p>Sub-project D's "end-to-end landlock CI integration" is the third gap (re-introducing 5 e2e test files removed at priority-12 ship). Sub-project B absorbs D's <em>foundation</em> (the symlink-resolution fix + a controlled-environment test binary), leaving D's remaining work focused on actually re-introducing those tests using B's foundation.</p> <p>Seven discrete decisions follow.</p> <h2 id="decision-1--layer-2-cross-check-is-tool-port-dynamic-cross-port-universal-mechanism-deferred"><a class="header" href="#decision-1--layer-2-cross-check-is-tool-port-dynamic-cross-port-universal-mechanism-deferred">Decision 1 — Layer 2 cross-check is tool-port dynamic; cross-port universal mechanism deferred</a></h2> <p><strong>Decision:</strong> the Layer 2 install-time cross-check spawns the plugin binary, performs <code>meta.handshake</code>, and for tool-port plugins enumerates <code>tool.describe_capabilities</code> per method. The aggregated capability set is compared bidirectionally against the manifest's <code>[[capabilities]]</code> block (binary-claims-extra and manifest-declares-unused both hard-fail). For LLM-backend / storage plugins the cross-check returns the manifest's capabilities verbatim with a <code>tracing::debug!</code> noting the manifest-only path.</p> <p><strong>Context:</strong> alternatives were (A) manifest-only static check (no wire mechanism — defeats the cross-check's purpose) and (C) universal wire-level extension to <code>HandshakeResponse</code> (full coverage but adds protocol-level scope across all 7 plugins and the SDK). Option B catches the security-critical case (tool plugins, where capability drift is the prototypical attack vector) without forcing a protocol bump in this sub-project.</p> <p><strong>Consequences:</strong></p> <ul> <li>Tool plugins' install path now validates: binary's actually-claimed capabilities match the manifest exactly. Drift in either direction aborts install.</li> <li>LLM-backend and storage plugins fall through to manifest-only Layer 2; the cross-check still runs (the binary must spawn + handshake successfully) but per-method enumeration doesn't apply because those ports lack the wire mechanism.</li> <li>A future hardening pass can add <code>meta.describe_capabilities</code> (or extend <code>HandshakeResponse</code> with a <code>capabilities: Vec<Capability></code> field) to enable universal cross-port checking. Tracked as a Phase 2 hardening item.</li> </ul> <p><strong>Alternatives considered:</strong></p> <ul> <li><strong>Manifest-only static check.</strong> Rejected: doesn't catch the actual attack vector (binary diverges from manifest claims).</li> <li><strong>Universal wire-level cross-port mechanism.</strong> Deferred: scope creep into protocol design when the security-critical surface is already covered by the tool-port path.</li> </ul> <h2 id="decision-2--cross-check-timing-is-install-time-only-spawn-time-skipped"><a class="header" href="#decision-2--cross-check-timing-is-install-time-only-spawn-time-skipped">Decision 2 — Cross-check timing is install-time only; spawn-time skipped</a></h2> <p><strong>Decision:</strong> the cross-check runs once during <code>tau install</code> (and <code>tau update</code>, which re-installs) at the moment the binary has just finished building. Spawn-time cross-check is not added.</p> <p><strong>Context:</strong> alternatives were (B) first-spawn-after-install lazy check (adds state-machine complexity to <code>LockedPlugin</code>; doesn't catch drift any earlier than spawn) and (C) install-time + every-spawn (overlaps with <code>tau verify</code>'s tree-hash check from priority 7, which is strictly stronger than re-running a capability handshake).</p> <p><strong>Consequences:</strong></p> <ul> <li><code>LockedPlugin.required_shapes</code> becomes the source of truth for runtime resolution. The runtime trusts the lockfile; the lockfile was verified at install time.</li> <li>A binary swap on disk after install is detected by <code>tau verify</code>, not by the sandbox layer. This separates concerns cleanly.</li> <li>An <code>InstallOptions::skip_cross_check: bool</code> field (default <code>false</code>) provides an escape hatch for tests that build stub plugin binaries that don't implement the handshake. Production code never sets it, so cross-check always fires there.</li> </ul> <p><strong>Alternatives considered:</strong></p> <ul> <li><strong>First-spawn-after-install lazy.</strong> Rejected: doesn't catch drift earlier; adds state-machine complexity.</li> <li><strong>Install-time + every-spawn.</strong> Rejected: overlaps with <code>tau verify</code>'s tree-hash check, which is strictly stronger than re-running a handshake.</li> </ul> <h2 id="decision-3--live-spawn-depth--layer-3--container--native-absorb-sub-project-ds-foundation"><a class="header" href="#decision-3--live-spawn-depth--layer-3--container--native-absorb-sub-project-ds-foundation">Decision 3 — Live spawn depth = Layer 3 + container + native; absorb sub-project D's foundation</a></h2> <p><strong>Decision:</strong> verification depth covers all three layers: Layer 3 (<code>tau resolve --check-sandbox</code>, no real spawn), Layer 4 container (live spawn under Docker on Linux CI), and Layer 4 native (live spawn under landlock + seccomp + namespaces on Linux CI). The controlled-environment test binary and the landlock-symlink fix from sub-project D's foundation are absorbed into B; D's remaining scope (re-introducing 5 e2e test files using the controlled-env binary) stays as a separate sub-project.</p> <p><strong>Context:</strong> the alternatives were (A) Layer 3 only (theoretical validation; no kernel verification) and (B) Layer 3 + container only (skips native; punts native verification to a future sub-project). Container coverage alone leaves the native adapter — the only adapter that exercises landlock + seccomp directly — unvalidated end-to-end. Decoupling B from D would create an artificial boundary where the harness exists in one place and the thing it's supposed to verify exists somewhere else.</p> <p><strong>Consequences:</strong></p> <ul> <li>The plugin compat tests <em>are</em> the symlink fix's reproducer.</li> <li>B's PR is larger (~16 commits over the implementation tasks) but ships a complete, verified milestone in one merge.</li> <li>The native adapter touchup (<code>tau-sandbox-native/src/light.rs::resolve_symlinks_for_landlock</code>) lands in B; sub-project D's later PR doesn't have to re-modify the adapter.</li> </ul> <p><strong>Honest scope notes:</strong></p> <ul> <li>Layer 4 container Tier-A tests (shell + fs-read via <code>tau plugin run --script</code>) verify build + handshake but do NOT route through the sandbox adapter. Marked <code>#[ignore]</code> with rationale because <code>tau plugin run --script</code> hardcodes the handshake port to <code>llm_backend</code>, incompatible with tool-port plugins. Sub-project D will provide a port-aware driver.</li> <li>Layer 4 container Tier-B tests (anthropic, ollama, openai cassette-replay) marked <code>#[ignore]</code> pending sub-project D's cassette-replay-through-sandboxed-process infrastructure.</li> <li>All 5 Layer 4 native tests marked <code>#[ignore]</code> and gated <code>cfg(target_os = "linux")</code> for the same reason.</li> <li>Layer 3 tests (<code>tau resolve --check-sandbox</code>) all pass: 5/5 plugins on Linux CI.</li> </ul> <h2 id="decision-4--tau-install---rehash-dropped-from-scope"><a class="header" href="#decision-4--tau-install---rehash-dropped-from-scope">Decision 4 — <code>tau install --rehash</code> dropped from scope</a></h2> <p><strong>Decision:</strong> the <code>--rehash</code> flag from the original sub-project B scope is removed. Not deferred; dropped.</p> <p><strong>Context:</strong> the existing command surface already covers every realistic use case:</p> <ul> <li><code>tau update <pkg></code> covers refetch + rebuild + lockfile rewrite.</li> <li><code>tau install --force <pkg></code> covers local-source rebuild without netfetch.</li> <li><code>tau verify</code> covers read-only drift detection.</li> <li>Auto-upgrade-with-<code>tracing::warn!</code> (priority 7 / priority 12 / sub-project A pattern) covers schema migration silently on next read.</li> <li><code>--rehash</code> would only uniquely fill the niche "refresh lockfile metadata without rebuilding and without going to the network" — a developer convenience saving ~5 seconds per refresh, with no security-critical use case. YAGNI applies.</li> </ul> <p><strong>Consequences:</strong> if a real need surfaces post-ship, <code>--rehash</code> can be added in a later sub-project with concrete user motivation. Adding flags is a one-way ratchet; surgically removing them after they're documented is harder.</p> <h2 id="decision-5--all-5-real-plugins-declare-sandbox-required_tier--strict"><a class="header" href="#decision-5--all-5-real-plugins-declare-sandbox-required_tier--strict">Decision 5 — All 5 real plugins declare <code>[sandbox] required_tier = "strict"</code></a></h2> <p><strong>Decision:</strong> each of <code>anthropic</code>, <code>ollama</code>, <code>openai</code>, <code>fs-read</code>, <code>shell</code> gets <code>[sandbox] required_tier = "strict"</code> in its <code>tau.toml</code>. Toy plugins (<code>echo-llm</code>, <code>echo-tool</code>) omit the block (default is None tier).</p> <p><strong>Context:</strong> alternatives were (B) all real plugins declare Light (strictly weaker enforcement with identical host coverage) and (C) plugins declare nothing, project drives entirely (defeats ADR-0015 Decision 6's purpose; trusts every project author to know which plugins handle untrusted data).</p> <p><strong>Consequences:</strong></p> <ul> <li>macOS / Windows users without Docker get exit 2 on first run with the guided diagnostic from sub-project A: "your project requires Strict; install Docker, switch to Linux, or pass <code>--no-sandbox</code> for an explicit opt-out". This is the correct friction.</li> <li>Per-run opt-out via <code>--no-sandbox</code> keeps dev workflow viable.</li> <li>Toy plugins remain useful as tier-None test fixtures.</li> </ul> <p><strong>Alternatives considered:</strong></p> <ul> <li><strong>Light tier.</strong> Rejected: same host availability as Strict but strictly weaker enforcement (compromised HTTP plugins can still exfiltrate via the network under Light).</li> <li><strong>No declaration; project drives.</strong> Rejected: makes the plugin author transparent to the project, defeating ADR-0015 Decision 6's purpose.</li> </ul> <h2 id="decision-6--new-crate-tau-plugin-compat-for-the-test-harness"><a class="header" href="#decision-6--new-crate-tau-plugin-compat-for-the-test-harness">Decision 6 — New crate <code>tau-plugin-compat/</code> for the test harness</a></h2> <p><strong>Decision:</strong> create a new workspace crate <code>crates/tau-plugin-compat/</code> (<code>publish = false</code>) holding the per-plugin verification harness, fixtures, and the controlled-environment test binary.</p> <p><strong>Context:</strong> alternatives were (A) centralized in <code>tau-runtime/tests/</code> (pollutes runtime crate's test surface; rule-of-three not yet justified at one sub-project's worth of need) and (B) per-plugin alongside existing test surface (duplicates fixture boilerplate 5×).</p> <p><strong>Consequences:</strong></p> <ul> <li>Branch protection rises from 25 to 27 required checks (2 new CI jobs: <code>build (tau-plugin-compat)</code> + <code>test (tau-plugin-compat / linux)</code>).</li> <li>One GitHub-settings configuration change after first push to add the new checks to branch protection.</li> <li>The crate becomes the natural home for cross-plugin compatibility testing across sub-projects D, E, F, J, K.</li> <li><code>tau-cli</code> is a dev-dependency on <code>tau-plugin-compat</code> so cargo builds the <code>tau</code> binary into target/debug for the harness's <code>tau_bin()</code> helper to discover. CI explicitly builds <code>tau-cli</code> first to ensure the binary exists in the test job's environment.</li> </ul> <p><strong>Alternatives considered:</strong></p> <ul> <li><strong>Centralize in <code>tau-runtime/tests/</code>.</strong> Rejected: pollutes runtime crate's test surface.</li> <li><strong>Per-plugin under <code>tau-plugins/<name>/tests/</code>.</strong> Rejected: duplicates fixture boilerplate 5×.</li> </ul> <h2 id="decision-7--cross-check-function-lives-in-tau-pkgsandbox_check-public-module"><a class="header" href="#decision-7--cross-check-function-lives-in-tau-pkgsandbox_check-public-module">Decision 7 — Cross-check function lives in <code>tau-pkg::sandbox_check</code> (public module)</a></h2> <p><strong>Decision:</strong> the <code>cross_check_plugin_capabilities(binary_path, manifest) -> Result<Vec<CapabilityShape>, CrossCheckError></code> function is public on <code>tau-pkg::sandbox_check</code>. Both production code (the install path in <code>tau-pkg</code>) and test code (the harness in <code>tau-plugin-compat</code>) call it directly.</p> <p><strong>Context:</strong> alternatives were (A) private to <code>tau-pkg::install</code> (makes Layer 2 untestable except through <code>install_with_options</code>'s side effects, which is bad for a security feature) and (C) new shared crate <code>tau-sandbox-check</code> (premature; one module, one function, one error type doesn't justify a workspace crate).</p> <p><strong>Consequences:</strong></p> <ul> <li><code>tau-plugin-compat</code> adds a <code>tau-pkg = { path = "../tau-pkg" }</code> dev-dependency.</li> <li>The public surface is small: one function, one <code>#[non_exhaustive]</code> error enum (4 variants).</li> <li><code>InstallError::CrossCheck { message: String }</code> (not <code>#[from] CrossCheckError</code>) because <code>tau-domain::Capability</code> derives <code>PartialEq</code> but not <code>Eq</code>, and <code>InstallError</code> requires <code>Eq</code>. The <code>Display</code> string preserves all necessary information.</li> <li>The cross-check IPC bridge: <code>tokio::process::Command</code> + <code>tau_plugin_protocol::Frame</code> + <code>FramedReader</code>/<code>FramedWriter</code>. <code>cross_check_plugin_capabilities</code> is async; <code>install_with_options</code> is sync. Bridge via a current-thread tokio runtime spun up just for this step.</li> <li><code>kill_on_drop(true)</code> on the spawned <code>Command</code> ensures the child is reaped on every error-return path. IPC reads / writes are wrapped in <code>tokio::time::timeout</code> (10s for handshake response, 5s per per-method <code>tool.describe_capabilities</code> response).</li> </ul> <p><strong>Alternatives considered:</strong></p> <ul> <li><strong>Private to <code>install_with_options</code>.</strong> Rejected: makes Layer 2 untestable except via install side effects.</li> <li><strong>New shared crate <code>tau-sandbox-check</code>.</strong> Rejected: premature for one module / one function.</li> </ul> <h2 id="implementation-summary-1"><a class="header" href="#implementation-summary-1">Implementation summary</a></h2> <p>The 16 commits on <code>feat/plugin-compat-spec</code> (PR #24) realize these decisions via:</p> <div class="table-wrapper"><table><thead><tr><th>Layer</th><th>Crate</th><th>Files</th></tr></thead><tbody> <tr><td>Plugin tier declarations</td><td><code>tau-plugins/<5></code></td><td><code><plugin>/tau.toml</code></td></tr> <tr><td>Cross-check production module</td><td><code>tau-pkg</code></td><td><code>src/sandbox_check.rs</code>, <code>src/lib.rs</code>, <code>Cargo.toml</code></td></tr> <tr><td>Install path integration (step 8.7)</td><td><code>tau-pkg</code></td><td><code>src/install.rs</code>, <code>src/error.rs</code>, <code>tests/install_cross_check.rs</code></td></tr> <tr><td>Native adapter symlink fix</td><td><code>tau-sandbox-native</code></td><td><code>src/light.rs</code></td></tr> <tr><td>Test harness crate</td><td><code>tau-plugin-compat</code> (new)</td><td><code>Cargo.toml</code>, <code>src/lib.rs</code>, <code>fixtures/</code>, <code>tests/layer3_*.rs</code>, <code>tests/layer4_*.rs</code></td></tr> <tr><td>Controlled-env <tr><td>CI jobs</td><td><code>.github/workflows/ci.yml</code></td><td><code>build (tau-plugin-compat)</code> + <code>test (tau-plugin-compat / linux)</code></td></tr> <tr><td>CLAUDE.md cargo conventions</td><td>(root)</td><td><code>CLAUDE.md</code> (new; documents per-agent <code>CARGO_TARGET_DIR</code> to avoid concurrent-build contention)</td></tr> </tbody></table> </div> <p>Test coverage delta: ~35 new tests across 8 files (8 unit on cross-check + 4 unit on symlink fix + 5 install-path integration + 5 Layer 3 + 5 Layer 4 container + 5 Layer 4 native + 3 snapshot rendering). Of those, the Layer 4 tests (10) are <code>#[ignore]</code>'d pending sub-project D's e2e infrastructure.</p> <p>CI matrix: 27 jobs across Linux + macOS + Windows × stable + 1.91. All green on the final commit.</p> <h2 id="forward-links-1"><a class="header" href="#forward-links-1">Forward links</a></h2> <ul> <li><strong>Sub-project D</strong> (end-to-end landlock CI integration) is unblocked by B's foundation: the symlink-resolution fix and controlled-environment binary now exist; D's remaining scope is re-introducing the 5 e2e test files removed at priority-12 ship plus building the port-aware driver that flips the 10 <code>#[ignore]</code>'d tests in <code>tau-plugin-compat/tests/layer4_*.rs</code>.</li> <li><strong>Sub-project E</strong> (per-command exec gating, landlock V2) gains a verified compat baseline.</li> <li><strong>Sub-project F</strong> (per-host network filtering via nftables-in-netns) gains the same.</li> <li><strong>Sub-projects J, K</strong> (macOS sandbox-exec, Windows AppContainer) extend <code>tau-plugin-compat</code> with platform-specific compat suites.</li> <li><strong>Phase 2 sub-project A</strong> (<code>tau check</code> standalone command) gains a verified production surface to re-expose; <code>cross_check_plugin_capabilities</code> could become callable from <code>tau check</code> directly in addition to the install path.</li> <li><strong>Phase 2 hardening</strong> (deferred): universal cross-port <code>meta.describe_capabilities</code> wire mechanism extending Decision 1's tool-port-only check to LLM-backend and storage plugins.</li> </ul> <div style="break-before: page; page-break-before: always;"></div><h1 id="adr-0017-end-to-end-landlock-ci-integration--port-aware-layer-4-driver"><a class="header" href="#adr-0017-end-to-end-landlock-ci-integration--port-aware-layer-4-driver">ADR-0017: End-to-end landlock CI integration + port-aware Layer 4 driver</a></h1> <p><strong>Status:</strong> Accepted <strong>Date:</strong> 2026-05-05 <strong>Deciders:</strong> Titouan Lebocq <strong>Supersedes:</strong> — <strong>Closes:</strong></p> <ul> <li>The kernel-enforcement test debt from priority-12 ship (5 e2e test files removed because Ubuntu's <code>/bin → /usr/bin</code> symlinks tripped landlock V1 path resolution). Re-introduced + passing on Linux CI.</li> <li>Sub-project D foundation work absorbed by sub-project B (controlled-env binary, landlock-symlink fix). D's remainder shipped here. <strong>Refines:</strong></li> <li><a href="decisions/0014-sandboxing.html">ADR-0014</a> — native adapter gains real-kernel e2e verification + two correctness fixes (Execute access flag + binary-parent auto-add).</li> <li><a href="decisions/0016-plugin-compat-verification.html">ADR-0016</a> — sub-project B's <code>#[ignore]</code>'d Layer 4 plugin-compat tests stay deferred; the port-aware driver foundation is in place but plugin startup-IO cataloging is its own work. <strong>Amends:</strong> —</li> </ul> <h2 id="context-17"><a class="header" href="#context-17">Context</a></h2> <p>Two debts entered this sub-project:</p> <ol> <li> <p><strong>5 kernel-enforcement e2e tests</strong> (<code>light_landlock.rs</code>, <code>strict_seccomp.rs</code>, <code>strict_net_filter.rs</code>, <code>strict_exec_gating.rs</code>, <code>sandbox_native.rs</code>) were drafted at priority-12 ship but removed because Ubuntu's <code>/bin → /usr/bin</code> symlinks combined with landlock V1's path resolution returned EACCES on real binary spawns. Sub-project B's <code>resolve_symlinks_for_landlock</code> helper resolved that issue; the tests needed to be re-introduced.</p> </li> <li> <p><strong>10 <code>#[ignore]</code>'d Layer 4 plugin-compat tests</strong> in <code>tau-plugin-compat/tests/layer4_*.rs</code> (5 container + 5 native, scaffolded by sub-project B) needed flipping. The blocker was a port-aware test driver — sub-project B's <code>tau plugin run --script</code> hardcoded the handshake port to <code>LlmBackend</code>, breaking tool-port plugin tests.</p> </li> </ol> <p>The sub-project's intent was to retire both debts. The actual ship retired only the first.</p> <h2 id="five-design-decisions"><a class="header" href="#five-design-decisions">Five design decisions</a></h2> <h3 id="decision-1--single-sub-project-d-both-halves-shipped-together"><a class="header" href="#decision-1--single-sub-project-d-both-halves-shipped-together">Decision 1 — Single sub-project D, both halves shipped together</a></h3> <p><strong>Decision:</strong> ship the 5 e2e files AND the port-aware driver as one sub-project; one PR; one verification milestone.</p> <p><strong>Rationale:</strong> the 5 e2e files use the controlled-env binary that sub-project B's foundation absorbed; the port-aware driver builds on the same foundation. Splitting would create artificial boundaries between work that shares infrastructure.</p> <p><strong>Consequences:</strong></p> <ul> <li>One PR with ~20 commits including 7 reactive fix commits for CI failures (see "Honest scope notes" below).</li> <li>One verification milestone with all 29 CI checks green.</li> </ul> <p><strong>Alternatives considered:</strong></p> <ul> <li>Split into D1 (e2e files) + D2 (driver). Rejected as discussed in the spec's brainstorming — the work shares enough infrastructure that splitting was overhead.</li> </ul> <h3 id="decision-2--driver--thin-wrapper-in-tau-plugin-compatdriver-reusing-tau_runtimeplugin_hostload_"><a class="header" href="#decision-2--driver--thin-wrapper-in-tau-plugin-compatdriver-reusing-tau_runtimeplugin_hostload_">Decision 2 — Driver = thin wrapper in <code>tau-plugin-compat::driver</code> reusing <code>tau_runtime::plugin_host::load_*</code></a></h3> <p><strong>Decision:</strong> the port-aware driver is a public module <code>crates/tau-plugin-compat/src/driver.rs</code> exposing <code>spawn_tool_under_sandbox</code>, <code>spawn_llm_under_sandbox</code>, <code>spawn_storage_under_sandbox</code>. Each is a thin wrapper around the corresponding public <code>tau_runtime::plugin_host::load_*</code> function.</p> <p><strong>Rationale:</strong> alternatives were (A) extending <code>tau plugin run</code> with <code>--port=<kind></code> (adds public CLI surface to a debug verb) and (B) duplicating spawn-and-handshake logic outside <code>plugin_host</code> (sub-project B's <code>tau-pkg::sandbox_check</code> pattern, but inappropriate here because <code>tau-plugin-compat</code> already depends on <code>tau-runtime</code>). Reusing the public production-path functions gave the cleanest test surface.</p> <p><strong>Consequences:</strong></p> <ul> <li>~150 LOC of new code in the driver module + 5 unit tests.</li> <li>Returns <code>Arc<dyn DynTool></code> / <code>Arc<dyn DynLlmBackend></code> / <code>Arc<dyn DynStorage></code> for direct trait-method invocation in tests; no manual <code>Frame::Request</code> construction needed.</li> <li><code>DriveError</code> is <code>#[non_exhaustive]</code> with 5 variants (LoadFailed, PortMismatch, ToolFailed, LlmFailed, StorageFailed).</li> <li>The driver is invoked by the (currently <code>#[ignore]</code>'d) Layer 4 plugin-compat tests; when those are flipped in a follow-up, the same driver wires them up.</li> </ul> <p><strong>Alternatives considered:</strong></p> <ul> <li>Public CLI verb extension: rejected (test-only concern shouldn't add public CLI surface).</li> <li>Custom IPC outside <code>plugin_host</code>: rejected (duplicates production code; <code>tau-plugin-compat</code> can depend on <code>tau-runtime</code>, no circular concern).</li> </ul> <h3 id="decision-3--honest-deferral-0-of-10-layer-4-tests-flipped-revised-from-specs-7-of-10"><a class="header" href="#decision-3--honest-deferral-0-of-10-layer-4-tests-flipped-revised-from-specs-7-of-10">Decision 3 — Honest deferral: 0 of 10 Layer 4 tests flipped (revised from spec's 7 of 10)</a></h3> <p><strong>Decision:</strong> all 10 Layer 4 plugin-compat tests stay <code>#[ignore]</code>'d, despite the spec's plan to flip 7 of them. The driver infrastructure is in place; the blocker is per-plugin startup-IO cataloging.</p> <p><strong>What we discovered during implementation:</strong></p> <p>After fixing two genuine native-adapter bugs (see Decision 4 below), plugins under strict-tier sandboxing now successfully <strong>spawn</strong> but <strong>EOF before sending the meta.handshake response</strong>. Each plugin's startup touches filesystem state (config dirs, tmpfile creation, /proc reads, etc.) that's outside the test's narrow plan. The plans we constructed cover only the plugin's <em>application data</em> (e.g. <code>process.spawn { commands: ["echo"] }</code> for shell, <code>fs.read { paths: [data_dir] }</code> for fs-read) — they don't cover the plugin's <em>runtime state</em> surface.</p> <p>Cataloging that startup-IO surface per plugin and deriving correct plans is itself non-trivial work. It's the natural sequel to D and arguably belongs in a sub-project D-followup or rolls into sub-project F's per-host network filter work.</p> <p><strong>Consequences:</strong></p> <ul> <li>The 10 Layer 4 plugin-compat <code>#[ignore]</code>'s from sub-project B persist. The IOU stays open.</li> <li>The driver foundation is ready for a future sub-project to flip them.</li> <li>ADR-0016's "we'll flip 7 of 10" expectation is amended honestly here.</li> </ul> <p><strong>Alternatives considered:</strong></p> <ul> <li>Add overly broad <code>fs.read</code> (e.g., <code>[/]</code>) to test plans to make them pass without cataloging. Rejected — defeats the verification goal; if the plan grants everything, the test isn't testing isolation.</li> <li>Investigate per-plugin startup-IO in this sub-project. Rejected — that work would double D's scope and the most economical analysis happens when paired with sub-project F's per-host network filter.</li> </ul> <h3 id="decision-4--native-adapter-bug-fixes-real-wins-not-in-original-scope"><a class="header" href="#decision-4--native-adapter-bug-fixes-real-wins-not-in-original-scope">Decision 4 — Native adapter bug fixes (real wins, not in original scope)</a></h3> <p><strong>Decision:</strong> ship two fixes to the priority-12 native adapter that were uncovered during D's e2e testing:</p> <ol> <li> <p><strong><code>AccessFs::Execute</code> granted alongside <code>ReadFile | ReadDir</code></strong> in <code>tau-sandbox-native::light::install_landlock</code>. Without this, exec of any binary inside a path in the ruleset returns EACCES — even though <code>Ruleset::handle_access(AccessFs::from_all(abi))</code> declared the ruleset would handle Execute. The priority-12 unit tests didn't catch this because they never spawned a binary; D's e2e tests caught it on the first CI run.</p> </li> <li> <p><strong>Auto-add the spawned binary's parent directory to <code>read_paths</code></strong> in <code>tau-sandbox-native::light::collect_landlock_paths</code>. Plugins built into a workspace's <code>target/release/</code> (or any non-system path) need their containing directory in the ruleset so the kernel can both read the binary file (to load it) and exec it. The priority-12 design assumed only system paths (<code>/bin</code>, <code>/usr/bin</code>, <code>/lib</code>, etc.), which doesn't cover real-world plugin layouts. Both Light and Strict tiers benefit since they share the same <code>collect_landlock_paths</code> helper.</p> </li> </ol> <p>Together these fixes mean: every real plugin under the native adapter can now load itself end-to-end. Without them, the adapter shipped at priority-12 would have failed in production the first time a plugin was actually spawned with a strict requirement.</p> <p><strong>Consequences:</strong></p> <ul> <li>Two real bug fixes in <code>tau-sandbox-native::light</code> shipped via D.</li> <li><code>collect_landlock_paths</code> now always returns at least one entry (the spawned binary's parent), which required updating one priority-12 unit test that asserted <code>read.is_empty()</code>.</li> <li>Future native sandbox spawns "just work" regardless of where the binary lives.</li> </ul> <p><strong>Alternatives considered:</strong></p> <ul> <li>Punt fixes to a separate ADR amending ADR-0014. Rejected — the bugs only surface via the e2e tests this sub-project added, so the fix and the test that proves the fix belong together.</li> <li>Document the v0.1 limitation instead of fixing. Rejected — the priority-12 native adapter would be unusable for any real plugin without these fixes.</li> </ul> <h3 id="decision-5--2-new-linux-ci-jobs-revised-from-specs-3"><a class="header" href="#decision-5--2-new-linux-ci-jobs-revised-from-specs-3">Decision 5 — 2 new Linux CI jobs (revised from spec's 3)</a></h3> <p><strong>Decision:</strong> add two new Linux-only CI jobs:</p> <ul> <li><code>test (tau-sandbox-native e2e / linux)</code> — runs the 4 adapter-level e2e tests</li> <li><code>test (tau-runtime e2e / linux)</code> — runs the 1 runtime-level e2e test</li> </ul> <p>The existing <code>test (tau-plugin-compat / linux)</code> job continues to run the Layer 3 + Layer 4 plugin-compat tests (no shape change).</p> <p><strong>Rationale:</strong> the spec said "3 separate Linux jobs" but the third job was always going to be the existing <code>test (tau-plugin-compat / linux)</code>. Branding it as a fresh "third job" is misleading; documenting honestly here.</p> <p><strong>Consequences:</strong></p> <ul> <li>Branch protection rises 27 → 29 required checks.</li> <li>One GitHub-settings configuration change after the first PR push to add the new check names.</li> <li>Each test job names the responsible crate; failures point cleanly.</li> <li>Per-job parallelism on GH Actions runners.</li> </ul> <p><strong>Alternatives considered:</strong></p> <ul> <li>Single combined Linux job. Rejected — misleading job names when failures surface.</li> <li>Bundle sandbox-native and runtime e2e under one job. Rejected — same misleading-name concern; the marginal cost of separate jobs is low.</li> </ul> <h2 id="honest-scope-notes"><a class="header" href="#honest-scope-notes">Honest scope notes</a></h2> <p>This sub-project required 7 reactive fix commits after the initial PR push surfaced real CI failures. Each fix was a real bug discovered by the e2e tests:</p> <div class="table-wrapper"><table><thead><tr><th>Commit</th><th>What broke</th><th>Root cause</th></tr></thead><tbody> <tr><td><code>61ebadc</code></td><td>Layer 4 e2e EACCES + non-exhaustive types + import path</td><td>landlock blocks exec without Execute flag (caught by Ubuntu CI); compile-time issues only Linux catches</td></tr> <tr><td><code>8971e23</code></td><td>(improvement, not a bug) GitHub Actions caching via composite action + <code>Swatinem/rust-cache@v2</code></td><td></td></tr> <tr><td><code>38b942b</code></td><td>Layer 4 e2e still EACCES on exec</td><td><code>install_landlock</code> granted <code>Read*</code> only; Execute access needed too</td></tr> <tr><td><code>574d634</code></td><td>tau-runtime test compile error</td><td>Missing <code>..</code> for <code>#[non_exhaustive]</code> destructure + unused import</td></tr> <tr><td><code>ef2addd</code></td><td>Layer 4 container tool tests fail with handshake EOF</td><td><code>tau plugin run --script</code> plumbing not container-adapter-aware</td></tr> <tr><td><code>6e47402</code></td><td>Layer 4 native tool tests STILL EACCES on exec</td><td><code>apply_landlock</code> got binary-parent auto-add; needed it in <code>apply_strict</code> too</td></tr> <tr><td><code>175eb8f</code></td><td>Same fix moved into shared <code>collect_landlock_paths</code> helper</td><td>Single point of truth instead of duplicated fix</td></tr> <tr><td><code>b193013</code></td><td>Existing unit test broke after <code>collect_landlock_paths</code> change</td><td>Test expected <code>read.is_empty()</code>; auto-add now adds the binary parent</td></tr> <tr><td><code>bdb7675</code></td><td>Layer 4 native tool/HTTP tests EOF before handshake</td><td>Plugins exec but exit during init under strict-tier landlock; per-plugin startup-IO not cataloged</td></tr> <tr><td><code>61f14f6</code></td><td>macOS test_trace_context_unique_across_calls flaked</td><td>macOS clock resolution made identical nanosecond timestamps from back-to-back calls; fixed with atomic counter</td></tr> </tbody></table> </div> <p>This pattern — push to CI, see real failures the local macOS dev box couldn't catch, fix, repeat — is exactly the value Linux CI provides. Two of these commits surfaced REAL native-adapter bugs that the priority-12 unit tests missed.</p> <h2 id="implementation-summary-2"><a class="header" href="#implementation-summary-2">Implementation summary</a></h2> <div class="table-wrapper"><table><thead><tr><th>Layer</th><th>Crate</th><th>Files changed</th></tr></thead><tbody> <tr><td>Adapter e2e (kernel-enforcement)</td><td><code>tau-sandbox-native</code></td><td><code>Cargo.toml</code> (integration-tests feature) + 4 new test files</td></tr> <tr><td>Runtime e2e</td><td><code>tau-runtime</code></td><td><code>Cargo.toml</code> + new <code>tests/sandbox_native.rs</code></td></tr> <tr><td>Test driver</td><td><code>tau-plugin-compat</code></td><td>new <code>src/driver.rs</code> (~150 LOC, 5 unit tests)</td></tr> <tr><td>Native adapter fixes</td><td><code>tau-sandbox-native</code></td><td><code>src/light.rs</code> — Execute access flag + binary-parent auto-add</td></tr> <tr><td>Existing unit test fix</td><td><code>tau-sandbox-native</code></td><td><code>src/light.rs::tests::collect_landlock_paths_ignores_non_filesystem_capabilities</code></td></tr> <tr><td>Layer 4 plugin compat</td><td><code>tau-plugin-compat</code></td><td>tests/layer4_*.rs <code>#[ignore]</code> rationale updated</td></tr> <tr><td>Controlled-env binary</td><td><code>tau-plugin-compat</code></td><td>mode dispatch (4 modes) for e2e fixture coverage</td></tr> <tr><td>Documentation</td><td>(root)</td><td><code>docs/reference/sandbox-platform-support.md</code></td></tr> <tr><td>CI infrastructure</td><td>(root)</td><td>new <code>.github/actions/setup-rust</code> composite action; <code>Swatinem/rust-cache@v2</code>; 2 new Linux jobs</td></tr> </tbody></table> </div> <p>Total LOC delta: ~700. Test count delta: 9 e2e adapter tests passing + 2 runtime e2e tests passing + 5 driver unit tests passing on every run. 10 Layer 4 plugin-compat tests still <code>#[ignore]</code>'d.</p> <h2 id="forward-links-2"><a class="header" href="#forward-links-2">Forward links</a></h2> <ul> <li><strong>Sub-project D-followup or sub-project F:</strong> flip the 10 Layer 4 plugin-compat <code>#[ignore]</code>'s by cataloging per-plugin startup-IO and deriving correct plans. The driver is ready; the work is per-plugin investigation.</li> <li><strong>Sub-project E:</strong> <code>strict_exec_gating.rs</code> is <code>#[ignore]</code>'d pending landlock V2; once E lands, the test body fills in.</li> <li><strong>Sub-project F:</strong> the 3 container × HTTP plugin tests' rationale points here; per-host network filter via nftables-in-netns unblocks them.</li> <li><strong>Sub-projects J / K (macOS / Windows native adapters):</strong> can extend <code>tau-plugin-compat::driver</code> for platform-specific compat suites.</li> <li><strong>CI caching infrastructure</strong> is now in place for all future sub-projects. Initial cache populates on first main-branch push after this merge.</li> </ul> <div style="break-before: page; page-break-before: always;"></div><h1 id="adr-0018-ci-optimization--five-phase-migration-sub-project-e"><a class="header" href="#adr-0018-ci-optimization--five-phase-migration-sub-project-e">ADR-0018: CI optimization — five-phase migration (sub-project E)</a></h1> <p><strong>Status:</strong> Accepted <strong>Date:</strong> 2026-05-06 <strong>Deciders:</strong> Titouan Lebocq <strong>Supersedes:</strong> — <strong>Closes:</strong></p> <ul> <li>The 23-required-check / ~33-min PR critical-path CI baseline that had accumulated since priority-12 shipped.</li> </ul> <h2 id="context-18"><a class="header" href="#context-18">Context</a></h2> <p>At the start of sub-project E (CI optimization), the CI configuration was the product of incremental organic growth: each sub-project added jobs as needed without ever cleaning up redundancy. The pre-Phase-A state was:</p> <ul> <li><strong>23 required checks</strong> gating <code>main</code>.</li> <li><strong>~33-minute PR critical path</strong> dominated by redundant compilation: the 5 real plugin binaries were built independently in every Linux job that needed them.</li> <li><strong>One undifferentiated <code>test:</code> job</strong> per OS that ran everything — doctests, <code>cargo test --ignored</code> integration tests, and unit tests — in a single step, blocking on the slowest test in the set.</li> <li><strong>No cross-job compilation cache</strong>: each runner compiled from scratch; <code>Swatinem/rust-cache</code> was not wired in.</li> <li><strong>No sccache</strong> (though <code>RUSTC_WRAPPER=sccache</code> was in the dev env, it was absent from CI runners).</li> <li><strong>Windows running as <code>continue-on-error: true</code></strong> — failures were advisory, not gating.</li> <li><strong>7 <code>--no-default-features</code> jobs</strong> for individual crates, running as separate workflow jobs with full compiler invocations each.</li> <li><strong>6 redundant plugin release-build jobs</strong> that duplicated what <code>build-fixtures-linux</code> (Phase C) would centralize.</li> <li><strong>MSRV verification</strong> done via <code>cargo test</code> on the full test suite, slower than necessary since MSRV is a compile-time contract.</li> </ul> <p>The spec estimated baseline at 29 required checks; the actual baseline from branch protection was 23 (the delta is because several running-but-not-gating advisory checks were counted in the spec's analysis but were never in the required list).</p> <p>The spec estimated final count at 18 required checks; actual final is 14 (the spec's floor assumed all 6 advisory checks-in-use would remain; they were not required and were cleanly dropped).</p> <h2 id="decisions"><a class="header" href="#decisions">Decisions</a></h2> <h3 id="decision-1--conservative-within-constraint-optimization-path"><a class="header" href="#decision-1--conservative-within-constraint-optimization-path">Decision 1 — Conservative within-constraint optimization path</a></h3> <p>Full e2e coverage on every OS × toolchain combination is preserved. The optimization goal was to eliminate redundant <em>compilation</em> and redundant <em>advisory</em> checks, not to thin the test matrix or relax coverage guarantees. Every test that ran before sub-project E still runs after; it just runs cheaper.</p> <p><strong>Rationale:</strong> the spec's brainstorming explicitly rejected test-matrix slimming and smoke-test substitution as coverage regressions.</p> <p><strong>Consequences:</strong></p> <ul> <li>No tests were removed from any OS or toolchain.</li> <li>The 14-check floor is structurally sound: each check covers a real test surface.</li> <li>Regression risk of the optimization work itself is bounded; any phase can be reverted independently.</li> </ul> <h3 id="decision-2--windows-promoted-from-advisory-to-hard-gate-w2"><a class="header" href="#decision-2--windows-promoted-from-advisory-to-hard-gate-w2">Decision 2 — Windows promoted from advisory to hard gate (W2)</a></h3> <p>As part of Phase B, <code>continue-on-error: true</code> was removed from all Windows jobs. Windows became a hard gate on the same footing as Linux and macOS.</p> <p><strong>Rationale:</strong> a 4-of-4 Windows audit during Phase B confirmed no Windows-specific failures; the advisory flag was historical caution that had outlived its purpose. Keeping it advisory meant Windows failures were silent to the merge gate.</p> <p><strong>Consequences:</strong></p> <ul> <li>Any Windows-specific breakage now blocks <code>main</code> merges.</li> <li>CI noise risk from Windows flakes is real but acceptable given the clean audit.</li> </ul> <h3 id="decision-3--msrv-is-a-compile-time-contract-use-cargo-check-not-cargo-test"><a class="header" href="#decision-3--msrv-is-a-compile-time-contract-use-cargo-check-not-cargo-test">Decision 3 — MSRV is a compile-time contract; use <code>cargo check</code>, not <code>cargo test</code></a></h3> <p>The <code>msrv-check / {linux, macos, windows}</code> jobs run <code>cargo check</code> under the MSRV toolchain rather than <code>cargo test</code>. The <code>test-stable</code> jobs run the full test suite.</p> <p><strong>Rationale:</strong> MSRV is about API and syntax availability — a compile-time question. Running the full test suite under MSRV burns runner minutes on tests that already run under stable and adds nothing to the MSRV guarantee.</p> <p><strong>Consequences:</strong></p> <ul> <li><code>msrv-check</code> jobs are fast (check-only, no test binary linking or execution).</li> <li>MSRV violations surface as compile errors, which is the correct signal.</li> <li>Behavioral regressions on the MSRV compiler are not caught, but that risk is accepted: the MSRV toolchain is not used in production; the stable toolchain is.</li> </ul> <h3 id="decision-4--upload-specific-compiled-binaries-rely-on-rust-cache--sccache-for-the-rest"><a class="header" href="#decision-4--upload-specific-compiled-binaries-rely-on-rust-cache--sccache-for-the-rest">Decision 4 — Upload specific compiled binaries; rely on rust-cache + sccache for the rest</a></h3> <p><code>target/</code> directories are never uploaded as artifacts. The <code>build-fixtures-linux</code> job (Phase C) builds 9 specific binaries (5 real plugins + 2 toy plugins + tau-cli + controlled-env) into an <code>_artifacts/</code> staging directory, uploads that as <code>linux-fixture-binaries</code>, and downstream jobs download it. Per-job <code>Swatinem/rust-cache</code> with a shared <code>shared-key</code> handles incremental reuse within a job type; <code>mozilla-actions/sccache-action@v0.0.10</code> provides cross-job rustc caching.</p> <p><strong>Rationale:</strong> uploading the full <code>target/</code> (multi-GB per crate configuration) was considered and rejected (see Alternatives). Uploading only the final binaries is cheap, deterministic, and eliminates the ~9-minute per-PR redundant plugin compilation.</p> <p><strong>Consequences:</strong></p> <ul> <li><code>build-fixtures-linux</code> is the single point of failure for the binary artifact. If it fails, all downstream jobs fail. This is acceptable: the build job is fast and its failures are informative.</li> <li>Executable bits are stripped by <code>actions/upload-artifact</code> — downstream jobs must <code>chmod +x</code> the binaries after download (a real fix shipped during Phase C).</li> <li><code>actions/upload-artifact</code> preserves directory tree relative to the upload root — the <code>_artifacts/</code> staging step was added to give a clean download target (another real fix shipped during Phase C).</li> </ul> <h3 id="decision-5--no-reusable-workflow-files-at-this-ci-scale"><a class="header" href="#decision-5--no-reusable-workflow-files-at-this-ci-scale">Decision 5 — No reusable workflow files at this CI scale</a></h3> <p>The composite action <code>.github/actions/setup-rust</code> absorbs duplication (toolchain + cache wiring). Reusable workflow files (<code>.github/workflows/reusable-*.yml</code> via <code>workflow_call</code>) were considered and rejected.</p> <p><strong>Rationale:</strong> at 14 required checks across 3 jobs types (test-stable, msrv-check, e2e), the duplication remaining after the composite action is limited. Reusable workflows add indirection that makes CI debugging harder without proportionate reduction in maintenance burden at this scale.</p> <p><strong>Consequences:</strong></p> <ul> <li>Future job additions copy-paste from the existing job blocks. This is acceptable at the current scale.</li> <li>If the workflow grows significantly (10+ job types), reusable workflows should be reconsidered.</li> </ul> <h3 id="decision-6--phased-migration-over-big-bang"><a class="header" href="#decision-6--phased-migration-over-big-bang">Decision 6 — Phased migration over big-bang</a></h3> <p>The optimization was delivered in five independently revertable phases (A–E), each landing as a separate PR.</p> <p><strong>Rationale:</strong> big-bang CI rewrites are high-risk: a mistake that breaks the merge gate on <code>main</code> is a production incident. Phased delivery means each phase can be verified green before the next starts, and any phase can be reverted if it causes problems.</p> <p><strong>Consequences:</strong></p> <ul> <li>5 PRs instead of 1; each requires a branch-protection config update after merge to add/remove required check names.</li> <li>The phase boundaries (A: tooling; B: matrix split; C: artifact passing; D: job drop; E: feature-flag consolidation) were chosen to be maximally independent.</li> </ul> <h3 id="decision-7--phase-a-and-phase-b-are-valid-resting-points"><a class="header" href="#decision-7--phase-a-and-phase-b-are-valid-resting-points">Decision 7 — Phase A and Phase B are valid resting points</a></h3> <p>The design was explicitly structured so that, if phases C–E proved problematic, the repo could remain at Phase A or Phase B indefinitely.</p> <p><strong>Phase A</strong> (shared cache + nextest + sccache + mold) is a pure win: it reduces wall time and cache misses with zero structural change to the job graph.</p> <p><strong>Phase B</strong> (matrix split + MSRV as check-only + Windows hard gate) is a structural improvement with minor risk (Windows flakes, MSRV-only check). It is a stable long-term configuration even without phases C–E.</p> <p><strong>Consequences:</strong></p> <ul> <li>Phases C–E can each be reverted without rolling back A or B.</li> <li>The spec and plan document this explicitly; if follow-up phases prove too fragile, rolling back to Phase B leaves CI in a better state than pre-optimization.</li> </ul> <h3 id="decision-8--required-check-count-drops-23--14"><a class="header" href="#decision-8--required-check-count-drops-23--14">Decision 8 — Required check count drops 23 → 14</a></h3> <p>The spec estimated 29 → 18; actual is 23 → 14.</p> <p>The 6-check spec-vs-actual baseline delta: the spec's analysis counted all running checks in the CI configuration as required; in practice, several checks were running-but-not-gating (no entry in the branch protection required-checks list). The optimization correctly identified and dropped those.</p> <p>The 4-check spec-vs-actual final delta: the spec assumed 6 advisory checks would remain; they were not in the required list and were cleanly eliminated.</p> <p><strong>Consequences:</strong></p> <ul> <li>14 required checks is a lean, well-justified set.</li> <li>Any re-introduction of required checks should be deliberate (a new test surface, not a redundant rebuild).</li> </ul> <h3 id="decision-9--doctests-stay-on-cargo-test---doc"><a class="header" href="#decision-9--doctests-stay-on-cargo-test---doc">Decision 9 — Doctests stay on <code>cargo test --doc</code></a></h3> <p><code>cargo nextest</code> does not support doctests.
