The <code>test-stable</code> jobs run <code>cargo nextest run</code> for all non-doctest tests AND <code>cargo test --doc</code> for doctests in the same job step.</p> <p><strong>Rationale:</strong> nextest's doctest support is incomplete upstream. Skipping doctests would regress coverage on a class of tests that verifies API documentation is accurate. Running doctests under legacy <code>cargo test</code> for only the doctest invocation is the lowest-friction compatibility path.</p> <p><strong>Consequences:</strong></p> <ul> <li>Two test invocations per <code>test-stable</code> job (nextest for unit/integration, cargo test --doc for doctests).</li> <li>If nextest gains complete doctest support in a future release, the <code>--doc</code> invocation can be dropped.</li> </ul> <h3 id="decision-10--matrix------ignored-integration-test-block-removed-in-phase-b"><a class="header" href="#decision-10--matrix------ignored-integration-test-block-removed-in-phase-b">Decision 10 — Matrix <code>-- --ignored</code> integration test block removed in Phase B</a></h3> <p>The <code>test:</code> matrix had a <code>features: ["-- --ignored"]</code> entry that ran <code>cargo test -- --ignored</code> to exercise <code>#[ignore]</code>'d integration tests. This was removed in Phase B.</p> <p><strong>Rationale:</strong> the <code>-- --ignored</code> block was a legacy holdover from before the dedicated e2e jobs existed. The sub-project D e2e jobs (<code>test (tau-sandbox-native e2e / linux)</code>, <code>test (tau-runtime e2e / linux)</code>, <code>test (tau-plugin-compat / linux)</code>) cover the integration test scope properly, with correct Linux-only gating and <code>integration-tests</code> feature flags. Running them again inside the matrix was redundant and caused <code>cargo nextest</code> to exit 4 on empty filter sets (see Errata).</p> <p><strong>Consequences:</strong></p> <ul> <li>Integration tests run exactly once (in the dedicated e2e jobs), not twice.</li> <li>The <code>--no-tests=pass</code> flag was added to the nextest invocations to guard against the exit-4 edge case on other empty filter sets.</li> </ul> <h2 id="what-diverged-from-the-specplan-errata"><a class="header" href="#what-diverged-from-the-specplan-errata">What diverged from the spec/plan (errata)</a></h2> <p>These are honest departures from the original spec and plan, documented for future reference:</p> <ol> <li> <p><strong>sccache-action version:</strong> spec said <code>v0.0.6</code>; actual install was <code>v0.0.10</code>. The legacy GitHub Actions cache v1 API was sunset in February 2025; v0.0.6 stopped working on GHA runners. Bumped to v0.0.10 which uses the v2 cache API.</p> </li> <li> <p><strong><code>cargo nextest --run-ignored only</code> exits 4 on empty filter sets:</strong> nextest returns exit code 4 when <code>--run-ignored only</code> finds no tests to run (the filter matches nothing). Fixed by adding <code>--no-tests=pass</code> to nextest invocations. This was not anticipated in the spec.</p> </li> <li> <p><strong>macOS test flake exposed by nextest parallelism:</strong> <code>tau-cli::session::store::tests::list_sessions_returns_descending_by_created_at</code> flaked under nextest's parallel execution because nextest runs test binaries in parallel (unlike cargo test's serial execution within a binary). The test relied on monotonic ordering from <code>std::time::SystemTime</code>, which macOS's clock resolution made non-monotonic under tight loops. Fixed by adding <code>.config/nextest.toml</code> with <code>retries = 2</code>. The underlying test was also fixed.</p> </li> <li> <p><strong><code>actions/upload-artifact</code> preserves directory tree:</strong> when uploading files, the artifact contains the full directory tree relative to the repository root. Added an <code>_artifacts/</code> staging directory in the <code>build-fixtures-linux</code> job to give a clean, predictable download root. The spec did not anticipate this behavior.</p> </li> <li> <p><strong><code>actions/upload-artifact</code> strips executable bits:</strong> downloaded binaries lack the executable bit. Added <code>chmod +x</code> after every artifact download step. The spec did not anticipate this behavior.</p> </li> <li> <p><strong>Layer 3 tests hardcode <code>target/debug/tau</code>:</strong> the plugin-compat Layer 3 tests resolve the tau binary as <code>target/debug/tau</code> (not a configurable path). Restored <code>cargo build -p tau-cli --bin tau</code> (debug, not release) in the <code>test-tau-plugin-compat</code> job to satisfy this constraint. The spec assumed only release builds would be needed.</p> </li> <li> <p><strong>Plugin binary names have <code>-plugin</code> suffix:</strong> the spec and plan referred to plugin binary names as <code>anthropic</code>, <code>ollama</code>, <code>openai</code>, <code>fs-read</code>, <code>shell</code>. The actual <code>[[bin]] name</code> values in the Cargo manifests are <code>anthropic-plugin</code>, <code>ollama-plugin</code>, <code>openai-plugin</code>, <code>fs-read-plugin</code>, <code>shell-plugin</code>. All <code>build-fixtures-linux</code> invocations and artifact copy steps use the correct suffixed names.</p> </li> <li> <p><strong>Spec baseline / final check counts:</strong> spec estimated 29 → 18; actual is 23 → 14. Explained fully in Decision 8.</p> </li> </ol> <h2 id="consequences-14"><a class="header" href="#consequences-14">Consequences</a></h2> <p><strong>Positive:</strong></p> <ul> <li>PR critical path reduced from ~33 minutes to ≤25 minutes (estimated; actual varies by cache hit rate).</li> <li>Required check count reduced from 23 to 14 — branch protection is simpler and more meaningful.</li> <li>Windows is now a hard gate, surfacing cross-platform regressions immediately.</li> <li>MSRV verification is fast and unambiguous (compile-time check only).</li> <li><code>cargo nextest</code> runs in CI; local dev can match CI behavior with a one-time <code>cargo install cargo-nextest --locked</code>.</li> <li>sccache provides cross-job rustc caching; per-job rust-cache provides incremental reuse within a job type. Both layers are now active.</li> <li><code>mold</code> linker on Linux reduces link time for large Rust binaries.</li> <li>Plugin binaries are compiled once per PR (in <code>build-fixtures-linux</code>) and reused by all downstream jobs.</li> <li>Each phase was independently verified green; no extended CI outage during migration.</li> </ul> <p><strong>Negative:</strong></p> <ul> <li><code>build-fixtures-linux</code> is a new single point of failure for all Linux e2e jobs. A flake or build failure in that job blocks the entire downstream pipeline.</li> <li>Two test invocations per <code>test-stable</code> job (nextest + <code>--doc</code>) adds minor complexity vs. a single <code>cargo test</code>.</li> <li>The <code>_artifacts/</code> staging step and <code>chmod +x</code> post-download are non-obvious CI idioms that future contributors must maintain.</li> </ul> <p><strong>Neutral:</strong></p> <ul> <li>Branch protection required-check names must be manually updated after any job rename. This is a GitHub limitation, not a workflow issue.</li> <li><code>.config/nextest.toml</code> <code>retries = 2</code> masks parallelism-exposed flakes rather than fixing their root causes. This is an acceptable trade-off for keeping CI green while root-cause fixes are applied.</li> <li>The composite action <code>.github/actions/setup-rust</code> absorbs toolchain + cache setup duplication; it is not a reusable workflow (see Decision 5).</li> </ul> <h2 id="alternatives-considered-13"><a class="header" href="#alternatives-considered-13">Alternatives considered</a></h2> <h3 id="self-hosted-runners"><a class="header" href="#self-hosted-runners">Self-hosted runners</a></h3> <p>Rejected. Self-hosted runners provide more CPU/memory/disk and persistent caches, but they require ongoing infrastructure management (provisioning, rotation, security patching). The sccache + rust-cache combination achieves the cache-sharing goal on GitHub-hosted runners without operational overhead.</p> <h3 id="matrix-slimming-reduce-os--toolchain-combinations"><a class="header" href="#matrix-slimming-reduce-os--toolchain-combinations">Matrix slimming (reduce OS × toolchain combinations)</a></h3> <p>Rejected. Removing macOS or Windows from the test matrix would regress cross-platform coverage. The spec explicitly names this as a non-goal: optimization must not sacrifice coverage.</p> <h3 id="smoke-tests-instead-of-full-e2e-on-all-os"><a class="header" href="#smoke-tests-instead-of-full-e2e-on-all-os">Smoke tests instead of full e2e on all OS</a></h3> <p>Rejected. Smoke tests (running a single representative test instead of the full suite) trade coverage for speed. The failures that sub-project D's e2e tests caught (Execute access flag, binary-parent auto-add) would not have been caught by a smoke test. The optimization achieves its speed goals through compilation reuse, not test reduction.</p> <h3 id="target-artifact-passing-between-jobs"><a class="header" href="#target-artifact-passing-between-jobs"><code>target/</code> artifact passing between jobs</a></h3> <p>Rejected. A compiled <code>target/</code> directory is 2–10 GB per configuration. Uploading it as an artifact would saturate artifact storage and add upload/download overhead that exceeds the compilation time saved. The design uploads only the final binary artifacts (~50 MB total for 9 binaries).</p> <h3 id="cargo-make-or-similar-task-runner"><a class="header" href="#cargo-make-or-similar-task-runner"><code>cargo-make</code> or similar task runner</a></h3> <p>Rejected. <code>cargo-make</code> would add a non-Rust dependency to the developer toolchain and the CI runner setup. The composite action and shell steps in the workflow are sufficient for the current level of CI complexity. The added indirection of a task runner is not justified.</p> <h3 id="cargo-hakari-for-workspace-hack-crate"><a class="header" href="#cargo-hakari-for-workspace-hack-crate"><code>cargo-hakari</code> for workspace-hack crate</a></h3> <p>Rejected. <code>cargo-hakari</code> optimizes feature unification across workspace crates to reduce the number of crate recompilations. At the current workspace size (8 crates), the benefit is marginal compared to the maintenance burden of keeping the workspace-hack crate up to date on every <code>Cargo.toml</code> change.</p> <h2 id="references-6"><a class="header" href="#references-6">References</a></h2> <ul> <li>Spec: <a href="decisions/../superpowers/specs/2026-05-06-ci-optimization-design.html"><code>docs/superpowers/specs/2026-05-06-ci-optimization-design.md</code></a></li> <li>Plan: <a href="decisions/../superpowers/plans/2026-05-06-ci-optimization.html"><code>docs/superpowers/plans/2026-05-06-ci-optimization.md</code></a></li> <li>Phase A PR: <a href="https://github.com/LEBOCQTitouan/tau/pull/26">#26</a> — tooling (shared-key cache + nextest + sccache + mold)</li> <li>Phase B PR: <a href="https://github.com/LEBOCQTitouan/tau/pull/27">#27</a> — matrix split (test-stable + msrv-check) + Windows hard gate</li> <li>Phase C PR: <a href="https://github.com/LEBOCQTitouan/tau/pull/28">#28</a> — build-fixtures-linux + e2e artifact passing</li> <li>Phase D PR: <a href="https://github.com/LEBOCQTitouan/tau/pull/29">#29</a> — drop 6 redundant plugin release-build jobs</li> <li>Phase E PR: <a href="https://github.com/LEBOCQTitouan/tau/pull/30">#30</a> — feature-flag-matrix consolidation + 7 ndf jobs dropped</li> <li>Related: <a href="decisions/0017-e2e-landlock-and-driver.html">ADR-0017</a> — sub-project D, which introduced the e2e job infrastructure this optimization builds on</li> </ul> <div style="break-before: page; page-break-before: always;"></div><h1 id="adr-0019-per-host-network-filter--machinery-shipped-strictrs-integration-deferred-sub-project-f"><a class="header" href="#adr-0019-per-host-network-filter--machinery-shipped-strictrs-integration-deferred-sub-project-f">ADR-0019: Per-host network filter — machinery shipped, strict.rs integration deferred (sub-project F)</a></h1> <p><strong>Status:</strong> Accepted <strong>Date:</strong> 2026-05-06 <strong>Deciders:</strong> Titouan Lebocq <strong>Supersedes:</strong> — <strong>Closes:</strong></p> <ul> <li>Sub-project F from the priority-12 followups — per-host network filtering machinery (<code>probe</code>, <code>validate</code>, <code>resolve</code>, <code>netns</code>, <code>rules</code>, <code>handle</code>, <code>orchestrator</code>). Full strict.rs integration deferred to task 6.5. <strong>Refines:</strong></li> <li><a href="decisions/0014-sandboxing.html">ADR-0014</a> — the v0.1 <code>unshare_flags_for_plan</code> over-permissive fallback is still in place; task 6.5 will wire <code>apply_per_host_filter</code> into <code>wrap_spawn</code>.</li> </ul> <h2 id="context-19"><a class="header" href="#context-19">Context</a></h2> <h3 id="the-v01-gap"><a class="header" href="#the-v01-gap">The v0.1 gap</a></h3> <p>Priority-12 sandboxing (ADR-0014) stripped <code>CLONE_NEWNET</code> when <code>Network(Http)</code> was in the plan, leaving the child in the parent's network namespace. This meant any plugin with an HTTP capability could reach any host — the plan's <code>hosts</code> allow-list was declared but not enforced at the kernel level. <code>tau-sandbox-native::net::unshare_flags_for_plan</code> recorded a <code>tracing::warn!</code> once-per-process to document this over-permissive behavior.</p> <p>The priority-12 followups doc (written 2026-05-03) identified sub-project F — per-host egress filtering via nftables-in-netns — as the fix.</p> <h3 id="sub-project-fs-design"><a class="header" href="#sub-project-fs-design">Sub-project F's design</a></h3> <p>The spec (<code>docs/superpowers/specs/2026-05-06-sandbox-net-filter-design.md</code>) and plan (<code>docs/superpowers/plans/2026-05-06-sandbox-net-filter.md</code>) describe a layered approach:</p> <ol> <li>Keep <code>CLONE_NEWNET</code> always; child runs in fresh empty netns.</li> <li>Create a veth pair in the parent and move one end to the child netns, assign IPs.</li> <li>Resolve hostnames in <code>Capability::Network(NetCapability::Http { hosts })</code> to IPs (DNS lookup with timeout, multi-record A + AAAA).</li> <li>Generate an nftables ruleset in the child netns: allow egress to resolved IPs + DNS; drop everything else.</li> <li>Require <code>CAP_NET_ADMIN</code> inside the user namespace.</li> <li>Hard-refuse when prerequisites (nft/ip/nsenter binaries, CAP_NET_ADMIN-in-userns) are absent.</li> </ol> <h3 id="what-shipped-pr-35-commit-d4438ae"><a class="header" href="#what-shipped-pr-35-commit-d4438ae">What shipped (PR #35, commit d4438ae)</a></h3> <p>The full machinery module <code>tau-sandbox-native::net_filter</code> was implemented and unit-tested:</p> <ul> <li><code>probe</code> — checks nft/ip/nsenter binaries and CAP_NET_ADMIN-in-userns availability.</li> <li><code>validate</code> — rejects wildcard hosts (<code>*</code>, <code>*.x.y</code>) at plan validation time.</li> <li><code>resolve</code> — multi-record (A + AAAA) DNS lookup per host via <code>tokio::net::lookup_host</code>.</li> <li><code>netns</code> — veth/netns setup helpers (create netns, veth pair, move peer, assign IPs).</li> <li><code>rules</code> — nftables ruleset generation (deterministic nft DSL, verified by insta snapshots).</li> <li><code>handle</code> — <code>NetFilterHandle</code> RAII guard that tears down the veth/netns on Drop.</li> <li><code>orchestrator</code> — <code>apply_per_host_filter(plan, child_pid)</code> composing probe → resolve → netns → rules → apply.</li> </ul> <p>26+ unit tests across these modules. A dedicated CI job (<code>test-net-filter / linux</code>) exercises the real probe + resolve + helpers inside privileged Docker.</p> <h3 id="what-did-not-ship--the-task-65-deferral"><a class="header" href="#what-did-not-ship--the-task-65-deferral">What did NOT ship — the task 6.5 deferral</a></h3> <p>Task 6 originally specified wiring <code>apply_per_host_filter</code> into <code>strict.rs::apply_strict</code>. During implementation it became clear this requires a structural change to the <code>Sandbox</code> trait:</p> <ul> <li><code>Sandbox::wrap_spawn</code> returns a <code>pre_exec</code> closure that runs <strong>inside the forked child</strong>, before <code>execve</code>. The child PID is not yet known at this point.</li> <li><code>apply_per_host_filter</code> needs the <strong>child PID</strong> to move the veth peer into the child's netns (via <code>ip link set <peer> netns <pid></code>).</li> </ul> <p>The clean solution is a new trait method <code>Sandbox::apply_post_spawn(plan, child_pid) -> NetFilterHandle</code> that runs <strong>concurrently with the child's pre_exec phase</strong> while the child blocks on a sync pipe. The child unblocks the pipe only after the parent has completed <code>apply_post_spawn</code>. This "parent-side post-spawn hook with sync pipe rendezvous" pattern is more than a single task — it requires extending the <code>Sandbox</code> trait in <code>tau-ports</code> and updating all adapters + the runtime's <code>plugin_host</code>. Task 6.5 will land this integration.</p> <p>Until task 6.5 ships, <code>unshare_flags_for_plan</code> retains its v0.1 fallback behavior.</p> <h2 id="five-design-decisions-1"><a class="header" href="#five-design-decisions-1">Five design decisions</a></h2> <h3 id="decision-1--q1a-hard-refuse-on-prerequisite-miss"><a class="header" href="#decision-1--q1a-hard-refuse-on-prerequisite-miss">Decision 1 — Q1.A: Hard refuse on prerequisite miss</a></h3> <p><strong>Decision:</strong> When <code>nft</code>, <code>ip</code>, or <code>nsenter</code> binaries are absent, or when <code>CAP_NET_ADMIN</code> cannot be granted inside an unprivileged user namespace, the sandbox returns <code>SandboxError::NetFilter { message: String }</code> rather than silently falling back to the v0.1 over-permissive behavior.</p> <p><strong>Rationale:</strong> A security primitive that silently degrades to "allow everything" is not a security primitive. Operators who deploy tau on systems without nftables (e.g. Alpine with only iptables) must explicitly configure an alternative adapter. A hard refuse surfaces the configuration gap immediately rather than silently violating the <code>hosts</code> allow-list.</p> <p><strong>Consequences:</strong></p> <ul> <li>Deployments on nftables-free Linux distros will see a clear error and must configure the container adapter or an alternative.</li> <li>GHA host runners block uid_map writes, making CAP_NET_ADMIN-in-userns unavailable on standard CI — this forced the privileged Docker CI strategy (see Errata).</li> </ul> <p><strong>Alternatives considered:</strong></p> <ul> <li>Probe-and-skip (fallback to v0.1): less rigorous; the <code>hosts</code> allow-list would be silently unenforced. Rejected.</li> </ul> <h3 id="decision-2--q2a-nft--ip--nsenter-cli-shell-out-not-rust-bindings"><a class="header" href="#decision-2--q2a-nft--ip--nsenter-cli-shell-out-not-rust-bindings">Decision 2 — Q2.A: <code>nft</code> + <code>ip</code> + <code>nsenter</code> CLI shell-out (not Rust bindings)</a></h3> <p><strong>Decision:</strong> All netns and nftables operations use shell-out to the <code>nft</code>, <code>ip</code>, and <code>nsenter</code> system binaries, mirroring the container adapter's pattern of shell-outing to <code>docker</code>/<code>podman</code>.</p> <p><strong>Rationale:</strong> The <code>rustables</code> and <code>nftnl-rs</code> crates are less mature than the system binaries and would require C library FFI bindings or unsafe netlink code. The system binaries are present on any modern Linux system that meets tau's other requirements. Shell-out is auditable (the exact commands are visible in logs), keeps the Rust code surface small, and follows the precedent set by <code>tau-sandbox-container</code>.</p> <p><strong>Consequences:</strong></p> <ul> <li>Three binary probes are required at startup: <code>nft --version</code>, <code>ip version</code>, <code>nsenter --version</code>.</li> <li>Shell-out errors produce <code>SandboxError::NetFilter { message }</code> via <code>error.to_string()</code> conversion.</li> <li>The nft DSL generated is deterministic and verified by insta snapshots.</li> </ul> <p><strong>Alternatives considered:</strong></p> <ul> <li><code>rustables</code> / <code>nftnl-rs</code>: larger surface, less mature, more code. Rejected per spec Q2.A.</li> </ul> <h3 id="decision-3--q3a-one-shot-dns-resolution-at-wrap_spawn-time"><a class="header" href="#decision-3--q3a-one-shot-dns-resolution-at-wrap_spawn-time">Decision 3 — Q3.A: One-shot DNS resolution at wrap_spawn time</a></h3> <p><strong>Decision:</strong> Hostname resolution happens once at <code>apply_per_host_filter</code> invocation time (i.e., at wrap_spawn / post-spawn time). Multi-record (A + AAAA) per host. TTL refresh is deferred.</p> <p><strong>Rationale:</strong> One-shot resolution is sufficient for the majority of plugin workloads (a plugin that needs to call <code>api.anthropic.com</code> will resolve the same IPs throughout its lifetime). TTL refresh would require a background task that updates nftables rules while the plugin is running — significantly more complex and deferred to a future sub-project.</p> <p><strong>Consequences:</strong></p> <ul> <li>A plugin running for many hours might encounter DNS changes mid-run. Accepted as a known limitation.</li> <li><code>tokio::net::lookup_host</code> was added to <code>tau-sandbox-native</code>'s production dependencies (the <code>net</code> feature of the <code>tokio</code> workspace dep).</li> </ul> <p><strong>Alternatives considered:</strong></p> <ul> <li>TTL-respecting refresh: deferred as described.</li> </ul> <h3 id="decision-4--q4aa1-reject-wildcards-at-plan-validation"><a class="header" href="#decision-4--q4aa1-reject-wildcards-at-plan-validation">Decision 4 — Q4a.A1: Reject wildcards at plan validation</a></h3> <p><strong>Decision:</strong> Wildcard hosts (<code>*</code> and <code>*.x.y</code> forms) are rejected by <code>validate</code> with a clear error at plan-validation time, before any network setup begins.</p> <p><strong>Rationale:</strong> Wildcards would require per-DNS-response dynamic rule updates to be meaningful. A static nftables ruleset cannot meaningfully enforce "any IP that resolves from <code>*.example.com</code>". Rejecting wildcards eagerly makes the constraint explicit.</p> <p><strong>Consequences:</strong></p> <ul> <li>Plans that declare <code>hosts: ["*"]</code> (the "any host" escape hatch) will fail validation when the per-host filter is active.</li> <li>Plugin authors who need unrestricted network access should declare no Network capability and use a non-strict tier.</li> </ul> <p><strong>Alternatives considered:</strong></p> <ul> <li>Allow wildcards and expand at resolution time: impractical with static nftables rules. Rejected.</li> </ul> <h3 id="decision-5--q4bb2-tests-bind-on-parent-veth-ip-via-env-var"><a class="header" href="#decision-5--q4bb2-tests-bind-on-parent-veth-ip-via-env-var">Decision 5 — Q4b.B2: Tests bind on parent-veth IP via env var</a></h3> <p><strong>Decision:</strong> Integration tests for the netns + veth + nftables setup bind a mock server on the parent-side veth IP (injected via <code>TAU_NET_PARENT_VETH_IP</code> environment variable) rather than via DNAT auto-routing.</p> <p><strong>Rationale:</strong> DNAT auto-routing requires configuring a NAT rule in the parent netns, which adds complexity and requires additional capabilities. Injecting the parent-veth IP via env var is simpler and sufficient for test coverage. The <code>TAU_NET_PARENT_VETH_IP</code> pattern mirrors the <code>TAU_TESTING_ALLOW_MOCK_SANDBOX</code> pattern already established in the codebase.</p> <p><strong>Consequences:</strong></p> <ul> <li>Tests that require live HTTP responses bind on the parent-veth IP directly.</li> <li>The env var is documented in <code>crates/tau-sandbox-native/src/net_filter/INTEGRATION.md</code>.</li> </ul> <p><strong>Alternatives considered:</strong></p> <ul> <li>DNAT-based routing: more complex, higher-privilege requirement. Rejected per spec Q4b.B2.</li> </ul> <h2 id="errata-vs-spec-and-plan"><a class="header" href="#errata-vs-spec-and-plan">Errata vs. spec and plan</a></h2> <h3 id="1-sandboxerror-lacks-non_exhaustive-and-derives-clonepartialeqeq"><a class="header" href="#1-sandboxerror-lacks-non_exhaustive-and-derives-clonepartialeqeq">1. <code>SandboxError</code> lacks <code>#[non_exhaustive]</code> and derives <code>Clone+PartialEq+Eq</code></a></h3> <p>The spec proposed <code>SandboxError::NetFilterError { source: io::Error }</code>. During implementation it became clear that <code>io::Error</code> does not implement <code>Clone</code>, <code>PartialEq</code>, or <code>Eq</code>, and <code>SandboxError</code> must derive all three (it is used in test assertions throughout <code>tau-ports</code>). Embedding <code>io::Error</code> directly is impossible.</p> <p><strong>Plan correction:</strong> the single new variant is <code>SandboxError::NetFilter { message: String }</code>. The rich <code>NetFilterError</code> enum stays internal to <code>net_filter::*</code>; the conversion at the orchestrator boundary is <code>NetFilterError</code> → <code>error.to_string()</code> → <code>SandboxError::NetFilter { message }</code>.</p> <h3 id="2-phase-0-finding-gha-host-runners-block-uid_map-writes"><a class="header" href="#2-phase-0-finding-gha-host-runners-block-uid_map-writes">2. Phase 0 finding: GHA host runners block uid_map writes</a></h3> <p>The spec assumed the <code>test-net-filter / linux</code> job could run on a standard <code>ubuntu-latest</code> GHA runner. During Phase 0 verification (PR #34, closed), uid_map writes returned "Operation not permitted" on the host runner — the kernel permits user namespaces but the GHA sandbox blocks writing to <code>/proc/<pid>/uid_map</code> after namespace creation.</p> <p>A privileged Docker container (<code>docker run --privileged rust:1.95-bookworm</code>) DOES allow uid_map writes. This is the CI strategy selected during Phase 0 by the project owner.</p> <p><strong>Impact:</strong> the <code>test-net-filter / linux</code> job in <code>.github/workflows/ci.yml</code> runs inside privileged Docker. This is documented in the job definition and in <code>crates/tau-sandbox-native/src/net_filter/INTEGRATION.md</code>.</p> <h3 id="3-f-task-65-deferral--architectural-reason"><a class="header" href="#3-f-task-65-deferral--architectural-reason">3. F task 6.5 deferral — architectural reason</a></h3> <p>Task 6 originally assumed <code>apply_per_host_filter</code> could be wired into <code>strict.rs::apply_strict</code> using the existing <code>Sandbox::wrap_spawn</code> machinery. The architectural conflict:</p> <ul> <li><code>wrap_spawn</code> provides a <code>pre_exec</code> hook that runs in the forked child BEFORE execve. The child PID is not accessible from within <code>pre_exec</code> (it is the PID of the current process at that point, not what the parent sees).</li> <li>The veth peer must be moved into the child's netns using <code>ip link set <peer> netns <pid></code> — a parent-side operation that requires the child's PID as seen from the parent.</li> </ul> <p>These two requirements are fundamentally incompatible with the current <code>Sandbox::wrap_spawn</code> API surface. The correct fix is:</p> <pre><code>trait Sandbox { // Existing fn wrap_spawn(&self, plan: &SandboxPlan, cmd: &mut Command) -> Result<Box<dyn SandboxHandle>>; // New in task 6.5 fn apply_post_spawn( &self, plan: &SandboxPlan, child_pid: u32, ) -> Result<Box<dyn SandboxHandle>>; } </code></pre> <p>The <code>plugin_host</code> orchestrator would:</p> <ol> <li>Call <code>wrap_spawn</code> to install the pre_exec hooks (landlock + seccomp namespaces).</li> <li>Spawn the child; the child blocks on a sync pipe.</li> <li>Call <code>apply_post_spawn(plan, child_pid)</code> to run the per-host filter setup.</li> <li>Signal the sync pipe; the child unblocks and proceeds to execve.</li> </ol> <p>This requires extending the <code>Sandbox</code> trait in <code>tau-ports</code>, updating all adapter implementations, updating the <code>plugin_host</code> spawn orchestration, and updating the <code>MockSandbox</code> fixture. Task 6.5 will land this integration.</p> <h2 id="consequences-15"><a class="header" href="#consequences-15">Consequences</a></h2> <h3 id="positive-10"><a class="header" href="#positive-10">Positive</a></h3> <ul> <li>All sub-project F machinery is in place and unit-tested (~26 tests across probe, validate, resolve, netns, rules, handle).</li> <li>Insta snapshots verify the nft DSL is deterministic — a regression in rule generation will surface immediately.</li> <li>The CI job <code>test-net-filter / linux</code> exercises the real probe + resolve + helpers in privileged Docker.</li> <li>The <code>SandboxError::NetFilter { message: String }</code> variant in <code>tau-ports</code> provides a clean error boundary between the internal <code>NetFilterError</code> hierarchy and the public port API.</li> <li>The task 6.5 integration scope is clearly bounded: extend <code>Sandbox</code> trait, wire <code>apply_post_spawn</code> in <code>plugin_host</code>, add sync pipe, update adapters and mock.</li> </ul> <h3 id="negative-6"><a class="header" href="#negative-6">Negative</a></h3> <ul> <li>Per-host filtering is NOT yet enforced at runtime — <code>strict.rs</code> still uses the v0.1 fallback (drops <code>CLONE_NEWNET</code> when <code>Network(Http)</code> is in plan; child inherits parent netns).</li> <li>The 3 <code>#[ignore]</code>'d Layer 4 container × HTTP plugin tests in <code>tau-plugin-compat/tests/layer4_container.rs</code> remain ignored (they need real F integration at the strict.rs level).</li> <li>4 integration tests in <code>tests/strict_net_filter.rs</code> are <code>#[ignore]</code>'d stubs pending task 6.5.</li> <li>CI infrastructure requires privileged Docker for the <code>test-net-filter / linux</code> job — a slightly elevated CI privilege level.</li> </ul> <h3 id="neutral-1"><a class="header" href="#neutral-1">Neutral</a></h3> <ul> <li>The followups doc gap row "per-host network filtering is over-permissive" stays open until task 6.5 ships.</li> <li><code>tokio</code> <code>net</code> feature was added to <code>tau-sandbox-native</code> production deps; this is a small dependency surface increase.</li> <li>Required CI checks rise 14 → 15 (new <code>test-net-filter / linux</code> job).</li> </ul> <h2 id="alternatives-considered-14"><a class="header" href="#alternatives-considered-14">Alternatives considered</a></h2> <h3 id="rustables--nftnl-rs-rust-bindings-instead-of-nft-cli-shell-out"><a class="header" href="#rustables--nftnl-rs-rust-bindings-instead-of-nft-cli-shell-out"><code>rustables</code> / <code>nftnl-rs</code> Rust bindings instead of <code>nft</code> CLI shell-out</a></h3> <p>Rejected. The Rust netfilter binding crates are less mature than the system binaries, require C library FFI or unsafe netlink code, and don't meaningfully reduce the privilege requirements. Shell-out mirrors the container adapter's proven pattern. Rejected per spec Q2.A.</p> <h3 id="embed-netfiltererror-directly-in-sandboxerror"><a class="header" href="#embed-netfiltererror-directly-in-sandboxerror">Embed <code>NetFilterError</code> directly in <code>SandboxError</code></a></h3> <p>Impossible due to <code>Clone+Eq</code> derive requirements on <code>SandboxError</code>. <code>io::Error</code> does not implement <code>Clone</code> or <code>Eq</code>. The <code>message: String</code> flattening at the boundary is the correct approach. Rejected per plan errata above.</p> <h3 id="probe-and-skip-contingency-for-ci-fallback-to-v01-on-gha"><a class="header" href="#probe-and-skip-contingency-for-ci-fallback-to-v01-on-gha">Probe-and-skip contingency for CI (fallback to v0.1 on GHA)</a></h3> <p>Considered during Phase 0 when the uid_map write failure was discovered. Rejected because it would make the test suite contingent on a capability that varies across environments — privileged Docker provides a clean, reproducible test surface. Path B (privileged Docker) was selected by the project owner.</p> <h3 id="larger-scope-for-task-6-full-strictrs-integration"><a class="header" href="#larger-scope-for-task-6-full-strictrs-integration">Larger scope for task 6 (full strict.rs integration)</a></h3> <p>The architectural conflict (child PID unavailable during <code>wrap_spawn</code> / <code>pre_exec</code>) was identified early. Absorbing the <code>Sandbox</code> trait surgery into task 6 would have significantly expanded scope. Deferring to a focused task 6.5 keeps the PR reviewable and the machinery independently testable.</p> <h2 id="references-7"><a class="header" href="#references-7">References</a></h2> <ul> <li>Spec: <a href="decisions/../superpowers/specs/2026-05-06-sandbox-net-filter-design.html"><code>docs/superpowers/specs/2026-05-06-sandbox-net-filter-design.md</code></a></li> <li>Plan: <a href="decisions/../superpowers/plans/2026-05-06-sandbox-net-filter.html"><code>docs/superpowers/plans/2026-05-06-sandbox-net-filter.md</code></a></li> <li>INTEGRATION.md: <code>crates/tau-sandbox-native/src/net_filter/INTEGRATION.md</code> — deleted with the <code>net_filter</code> module per ADR-0020.</li> <li>PR #35 (merged 2026-05-06 at commit d4438ae): per-host network filter machinery</li> <li>Phase 0 verification PR #34 (closed): GHA uid_map write failure discovery</li> <li>ADR-0014: <a href="decisions/0014-sandboxing.html"><code>0014-sandboxing.md</code></a> — original sandbox design</li> <li>Followups doc: <a href="decisions/../superpowers/specs/2026-05-03-sandboxing-followups.html"><code>../superpowers/specs/2026-05-03-sandboxing-followups.md</code></a></li> </ul> <h2 id="addendum-2026-05-06-f-task-65-shipped--native-adapter-integration"><a class="header" href="#addendum-2026-05-06-f-task-65-shipped--native-adapter-integration">Addendum (2026-05-06): F task 6.5 shipped — Native adapter integration</a></h2> <p>Sub-project F task 6.5 wired the per-host network filter machinery into the Native sandbox adapter's spawn lifecycle. Phase 1 PR #37 lands the architectural changes:</p> <h3 id="trait-extension"><a class="header" href="#trait-extension">Trait extension</a></h3> <p>A new <code>Sandbox::apply_post_spawn(&self, plan, child_pid, &mut handle) -> Result<(), SandboxError></code> trait method runs concurrently with the child's <code>pre_exec</code> phase while the child blocks on a sync pipe. The default no-op implementation covers <code>Mock</code> / <code>Container</code> / <code>Light</code> / <code>Passthrough</code>. Only <code>NativeSandbox</code> overrides it.</p> <p><code>SandboxHandle</code> gains (cfg(unix)):</p> <ul> <li><code>sync_write_fd: Option<OwnedFd></code> — when present, dropping the handle closes the fd, releasing the child with EOF on its blocking read.</li> <li><code>nest_handle(Box<dyn Send>)</code> — append nested cleanup guards. The <code>NetFilterHandle</code> is nested here so the parent veth tears down LIFO-ordered after the child's process exits.</li> <li><code>signal_post_spawn_complete() -> io::Result<()></code> — writes 1 byte to the sync pipe, releasing the child.</li> </ul> <h3 id="native-adapter-wiring"><a class="header" href="#native-adapter-wiring">Native adapter wiring</a></h3> <p><code>apply_strict</code> (in <code>crates/tau-sandbox-native/src/strict.rs</code>):</p> <ul> <li>Pre-allocates a <code>VethSubnet</code> if the plan has <code>Network(Http)</code> (the impure <code>setup_veth_pair_with_subnet</code> runs later, in <code>apply_post_spawn</code>).</li> <li>Sets <code>TAU_NET_PARENT_VETH_IP</code> env var on the spawned <code>Command</code> BEFORE <code>cmd.spawn()</code> so the child can read its parent's bind IP.</li> <li>Creates a sync pipe via <code>nix::unistd::pipe()</code>; the child reads 1 byte in <code>pre_exec</code> between <code>unshare</code> and <code>seccomp</code>, blocking until the parent signals completion.</li> <li>Returns <code>(SandboxHandle, Option<VethSubnet>)</code> so <code>wrap_spawn</code> can stash the subnet.</li> </ul> <p><code>NativeSandbox</code>:</p> <ul> <li>Caches the F probe result in a <code>OnceLock<Result<(), NetFilterError>></code> (probe runs once at first <code>validate_plan</code> call for a <code>Network(Http)</code> plan).</li> <li><code>validate_plan</code> hard-refuses <code>Network(Http)</code> plans on F-unavailable hosts (no nft binary, no CAP_NET_ADMIN-in-userns, etc.) — surfaces a clear <code>SandboxError::NetFilter</code> instead of silently degrading.</li> <li>Per-spawn <code>Mutex<HashMap<RawFd, VethSubnet>></code> keyed by <code>sync_write_fd</code> lets <code>apply_post_spawn</code> look up the pre-allocated subnet for each child.</li> <li><code>apply_post_spawn</code> override: looks up the subnet, calls <code>apply_per_host_filter(plan, child_pid, subnet)</code>, nests the returned <code>NetFilterHandle</code> in the <code>SandboxHandle</code>.</li> </ul> <p><code>unshare_flags_for_plan</code> is flipped: ALWAYS returns <code>CLONE_NEWUSER | CLONE_NEWNET</code>. The v0.1 over-permissive fallback (drop <code>CLONE_NEWNET</code> when <code>Network(Http)</code> is in plan, leaving the child in the parent netns) is removed.</p> <h3 id="runtime-caller"><a class="header" href="#runtime-caller">Runtime caller</a></h3> <p><code>tau-runtime::plugin_host::process::spawn_and_handshake</code> now calls <code>adapter.apply_post_spawn(plan, child_pid, &mut handle).await</code> followed by <code>handle.signal_post_spawn_complete()</code> after <code>cmd.spawn()</code>. All three post-spawn failure modes (child.id None, apply_post_spawn error, signal error) map uniformly to <code>RuntimeError::SandboxWrapFailed { plugin, source }</code> so callers can match on a single variant.</p> <h3 id="out-of-scope--carried-over-follow-ups"><a class="header" href="#out-of-scope--carried-over-follow-ups">Out of scope — carried-over follow-ups</a></h3> <p>Two items did NOT ship in Phase 1 and are tracked as gap rows in <code>docs/superpowers/specs/2026-05-03-sandboxing-followups.md</code>:</p> <ol> <li> <p><strong>Container-adapter network filtering</strong>: the 3 <code>layer4_container.rs</code> HTTP plugin tests (anthropic / ollama / openai cassette-replay) remain <code>#[ignore]</code>'d. They use the Container adapter (Docker), which inherits the trait's no-op <code>apply_post_spawn</code>. F's veth IP is a NativeSandbox construct; inside a Docker container the host is not reachable at that IP. Container-adapter network plumbing is a separate sub-project.</p> </li> <li> <p><strong>strict_net_filter integration tests hang in CI</strong>: all 4 <code>strict_net_filter.rs</code> tests are <code>#[ignore]</code>'d. When <code>test-net-filter / linux</code> (privileged Docker) actually ran them, all 4 hung past 60s. Notably <code>no_network_cap_socket_denied_by_seccomp</code> also hangs (no <code>Network(Http)</code> in plan, no <code>apply_post_spawn</code> runs), suggesting the hang is in the seccomp <code>KillProcess</code> / <code>cmd.output()</code> propagation path on Linux — not in F-specific code. Needs a real-Linux debugging session to repro and fix.</p> </li> </ol> <p>The <code>unshare_flags_for_plan</code> flip + <code>validate_plan</code> hard-refuse + post-spawn integration are validated by the lib unit tests + clippy under both default and <code>integration-tests</code> features.</p> <h2 id="addendum-2026-05-07-superseded-by-adr-0020"><a class="header" href="#addendum-2026-05-07-superseded-by-adr-0020">Addendum (2026-05-07): Superseded by ADR-0020</a></h2> <p>The veth + nftables + CAP_NET_ADMIN design has been replaced by a userspace HTTP-CONNECT proxy (see <a href="decisions/0020-sandbox-proxy.html">ADR-0020 — Sandbox proxy</a>). The <code>tau-sandbox-native::net_filter</code> module described in this ADR was deleted in PR <TBD>. Reasons: privileged-Docker friction, 7 <code>#[ignore]</code>'d tests it left blocked, and a hang in the strict_net_filter integration tests under privileged-Docker CI.</p> <div style="break-before: page; page-break-before: always;"></div><h1 id="adr-0020-sandbox-proxy--replaces-fs-vethnft-per-host-filtering"><a class="header" href="#adr-0020-sandbox-proxy--replaces-fs-vethnft-per-host-filtering">ADR-0020: Sandbox proxy — replaces F's veth+nft per-host filtering</a></h1> <p><strong>Status:</strong> Accepted <strong>Date:</strong> 2026-05-07 <strong>Deciders:</strong> Titouan Lebocq <strong>Supersedes:</strong> <a href="decisions/0019-per-host-network-filter.html">ADR-0019 — Per-host network filter</a></p> <h2 id="context-20"><a class="header" href="#context-20">Context</a></h2> <p>ADR-0019 shipped F's per-host network filter (veth + nftables + CAP_NET_ADMIN-in-parent). Field experience surfaced four problems:</p> <ol> <li>Privileged-Docker requirement in CI made tests slow and brittle</li> <li>The 4 strict_net_filter integration tests hung in privileged Docker (suspected cmd.output() / seccomp KillProcess interaction)</li> <li>The 3 layer4_container HTTP plugin tests couldn't be un-<code>#[ignore]</code>'d because Docker networking ≠ veth IP</li> <li>Production tau required root or CAP_NET_ADMIN — friction for deployers</li> </ol> <p>Research (sub-project H) found that Anthropic's own sandbox-runtime uses a userspace proxy pattern that avoids all four pain points. This ADR adopts that pattern.</p> <h2 id="decision-14"><a class="header" href="#decision-14">Decision</a></h2> <p>Replace the <code>tau-sandbox-native::net_filter</code> module wholesale with a userspace HTTP-CONNECT proxy + small bridge binary. Both Native and Container adapters share the same proxy module via a new <code>tau-sandbox-proxy</code> crate.</p> <p>Architecture: a tokio task in tau's parent address space accepts CONNECT requests on a temp Unix socket file. The strict-tier child runs in <code>unshare(CLONE_NEWUSER | CLONE_NEWNET)</code> — empty netns, no internet. The <code>tau-net-bridge</code> binary brings <code>lo</code> up, listens on <code>127.0.0.1:8443</code>, splices to the inherited Unix socket file. Plugin's HTTPS_PROXY env points at the bridge's TCP listener.</p> <p>Pass-through CONNECT: proxy does NOT terminate TLS. SNI in the TLS ClientHello must match the CONNECT host (closes domain-fronting hole).</p> <h2 id="consequences-16"><a class="header" href="#consequences-16">Consequences</a></h2> <p>Positive:</p> <ul> <li>Zero kernel privileges in the parent (drops CAP_NET_ADMIN requirement)</li> <li>CI runs on stock ubuntu-latest (no privileged Docker)</li> <li>7 <code>#[ignore]</code>'d sandbox tests become runnable (4 strict_net_filter replaced by strict_proxy + 3 layer4_container HTTP plugin tests un-ignored)</li> <li>~640 LOC of F's machinery removed; net code reduction</li> <li>F's sync-pipe machinery in tau-ports also removed (~80 more LOC + trait field)</li> <li>New shared crate tau-sandbox-proxy enables future Container/Native parity work</li> </ul> <p>Negative:</p> <ul> <li>Pass-through CONNECT proxy can't enforce HTTP method/path (matches today's enforcement; future iteration if richer capabilities land)</li> <li>Non-HTTP egress (raw TCP, UDP) no longer covered (no current plugin uses; future iteration if needed)</li> <li>Container adapter's deployment story now requires <code>tau-net-bridge</code> binary at a known path (resolved via TAU_NET_BRIDGE_PATH env var)</li> </ul> <h2 id="references-8"><a class="header" href="#references-8">References</a></h2> <ul> <li>Spec: <code>docs/superpowers/specs/2026-05-07-sandbox-proxy-design.md</code></li> <li>Plan: <code>docs/superpowers/plans/2026-05-07-sandbox-proxy.md</code></li> <li>Production precedent: Anthropic sandbox-runtime (Oct 2025)</li> <li>ADR-0019 (superseded)</li> </ul> <div style="break-before: page; page-break-before: always;"></div><h1 id="adr-0021-per-plugin-container-images"><a class="header" href="#adr-0021-per-plugin-container-images">ADR-0021: per-plugin container images</a></h1> <p><strong>Status:</strong> Accepted (2026-05-08)</p> <p><strong>Supersedes:</strong> the implicit "single base image + bind-mounted plugin binary" approach used by the Container adapter through sub-project H.</p> <h2 id="context-21"><a class="header" href="#context-21">Context</a></h2> <p>The Container sandbox adapter spawned plugins via <code>docker run <base-image> <host-path-to-plugin></code>. The host path doesn't exist inside the container, so exec failed and the plugin host saw EOF before the plugin's handshake could be sent. Five integration tests in <code>crates/tau-plugin-compat/tests/layer4_container.rs</code> were <code>#[ignore]</code>'d — three from sub-project H's HTTP work, two from sub-project D's earlier fs/shell work — all sharing this symptom.</p> <h2 id="decision-15"><a class="header" href="#decision-15">Decision</a></h2> <p>Replace the bind-mount approach with <strong>per-plugin Docker images</strong> built on a shared <code>tau-plugin-base</code> image. Each plugin has its own multi-stage Dockerfile. The Container adapter resolves the image name as <code>tau-plugin-<bin>:dev</code> from the <code>Command</code>'s program path, runs it, and overrides ENTRYPOINT to <code>tau-net-bridge</code> for HTTP plans.</p> <p>This is <strong>Phase 1</strong> of a four-phase roadmap:</p> <ol> <li><strong>Phase 1 (this ADR):</strong> existing 5 plugins baked into images; CI builds via <code>cargo xtask build-plugin-images</code> with GHA buildx cache; Debian-slim base; host-arch builds only; convention-based image discovery.</li> <li><strong>Phase 2:</strong> native-deps plugin support (image build infra grows to handle <code>apt-get install</code>, <code>pip install</code>, etc.).</li> <li><strong>Phase 3:</strong> public plugin SDK / third-party authoring story; manifest schema gains an optional <code>[sandbox.container] image = "..."</code> override field; image conventions become the public contract.</li> <li><strong>Phase 4:</strong> production-grade distribution — GHCR push, sigstore signing, SBOM generation, multi-arch matrix (linux/amd64 + linux/arm64), distroless base swap, plugin lockfile pins image digest.</li> </ol> <h2 id="consequences-17"><a class="header" href="#consequences-17">Consequences</a></h2> <ul> <li>Container adapter no longer bind-mounts the plugin binary or <code>tau-net-bridge</code>; both live inside the per-plugin image.</li> <li>Plugin builds happen twice during a CI run: once for the host artifact pipeline (used by the Native adapter), once inside the Dockerfile builder stage. Locked decision 5: optimise only if profiling demands.</li> <li>Local dev iteration adds a <code>cargo xtask build-plugin-images</code> step before container tests run.</li> <li>CI pins <code>TAU_CONTAINER_RUNTIME=docker</code> (job-level env) so xtask + adapter agree on which runtime owns the per-plugin image storage. Local dev leaves it unset → both default to podman.</li> <li>ADR-0020 (sandbox proxy) unchanged. ADR-0019 (per-host net filter) remains superseded.</li> </ul> <h2 id="tests-closed-by-this-adr"><a class="header" href="#tests-closed-by-this-adr">Tests closed by this ADR</a></h2> <p>All 5 originally-<code>#[ignore]</code>'d Container-adapter integration tests in <code>crates/tau-plugin-compat/tests/layer4_container.rs</code> close:</p> <div class="table-wrapper"><table><thead><tr><th>Test</th><th>Status</th></tr></thead><tbody> <tr><td><code>shell_layer4_container_runs_echo_hello</code></td><td>✅</td></tr> <tr><td><code>fs_read_layer4_container_reads_data_file</code></td><td>✅</td></tr> <tr><td><code>anthropic_layer4_container_completes_via_cassette</code></td><td>✅</td></tr> <tr><td><code>ollama_layer4_container_completes_via_cassette</code></td><td>✅</td></tr> <tr><td><code>openai_layer4_container_completes_via_cassette</code></td><td>✅</td></tr> </tbody></table> </div> <p>The 2 non-HTTP tests close via the per-plugin-image fix alone — the plugin binary now lives at a known in-image path and exec succeeds.</p> <p>The 3 HTTP cassette tests required two further fixes layered on top of the image work, both shipped in sub-project I (under PR #41 — initially deferred to sub-project J, then reopened and fixed in the same PR series):</p> <ol> <li> <p><strong>Plain-HTTP forwarding in <code>tau-sandbox-proxy</code></strong> — the existing CONNECT path is HTTPS-only; cassette servers speak plain HTTP. The proxy now detects the first request line and dispatches CONNECT or HTTP. The HTTP path validates the <code>Host</code> against the allowlist, opens TCP, and rewrites the request line to RFC 7230 origin-form before splicing. Production-relevant: plugins talking to local services (Ollama, etc.) now route through the proxy with allowlist enforcement, not just HTTPS.</p> </li> <li> <p><strong>Container runs as root (uid 0) when the plan has <code>Network(Http)</code></strong> — the bridge inside the container needs to dial the host-bound proxy Unix socket. Docker Desktop on macOS presents bind-mounted Unix sockets as <code>root:root 660</code> regardless of host-side permissions; Linux Docker preserves host UIDs but those won't match <code>nobody</code> (65534) either. Running as root inside the container is safe because <code>--cap-drop=ALL</code> + <code>--security-opt=no-new-privileges</code></p> <ul> <li><code>--read-only</code> + seccomp-default keep the security envelope essentially equivalent to <code>nobody</code>. Non-HTTP plans still run as <code>nobody</code>.</li> </ul> <p>Plus a defence-in-depth chmod on the host: <code>tau-sandbox-proxy</code> sets the proxy socket to <code>0666</code> after binding, so a sandbox-container running as a non-root UID could still dial it on Linux Docker (where bind-mount UIDs are preserved). Belt-and-braces.</p> </li> </ol> <p>The investigation that found the second fix — running root vs. nobody — was bounded by <code>scripts/test-linux-integration.sh</code> (Linux Podman DooD) and a one-off reqwest probe binary; root cause surfaced when the bridge's <code>proxy connect failed: Permission denied</code> warning finally became visible against Docker Desktop.</p> <p>See <code>docs/superpowers/specs/2026-05-08-per-plugin-images-design.md</code> for the full design including locked decisions 1-8 and Phase 1 risks.</p> <div style="break-before: page; page-break-before: always;"></div><h1 id="adr-0022-macos-sandbox-exec-adapter"><a class="header" href="#adr-0022-macos-sandbox-exec-adapter">ADR-0022: macOS sandbox-exec adapter</a></h1> <p><strong>Status:</strong> Accepted <strong>Date:</strong> 2026-05-09 <strong>Deciders:</strong> Titouan Lebocq <strong>Related:</strong> <a href="decisions/0014-sandboxing.html">ADR-0014 — Sandboxing</a>, <a href="decisions/0020-sandbox-proxy.html">ADR-0020 — Sandbox proxy</a></p> <h2 id="context-22"><a class="header" href="#context-22">Context</a></h2> <p>Through ADR-0014..0021 the strict-tier sandbox shipped on Linux only (landlock + seccomp + namespaces, layered with the userspace proxy from ADR-0020). On macOS, <code>RegistryKind::Native</code> resolved to "no adapter", so plugins fell back to <code>passthrough</code> — the same as <code>--no-sandbox</code>. The followups doc had reserved this as sub-project J ("macOS sandbox-exec adapter").</p> <p>macOS does not expose a syscall-level filter analogous to seccomp, but it does ship <code>/usr/bin/sandbox-exec</code> and the SBPL (Sandbox Profile Language) S-expression dialect. The <code>tau-sandbox-proxy</code> crate from ADR-0020 is platform-agnostic for the parent-side accept loop, so the Linux-side defense-in-depth (proxy gates outbound HTTP) ports to macOS unchanged.</p> <h2 id="decision-16"><a class="header" href="#decision-16">Decision</a></h2> <p>Add <code>tau-sandbox-darwin</code>, a third <code>Sandbox</code> adapter parallel to <code>tau-sandbox-native</code> and <code>tau-sandbox-container</code>. Strict tier only; Light tier deliberately omitted because SBPL has no equivalent of landlock's per-path read/write granularity short of strict mode.</p> <p>Architecture:</p> <ul> <li><code>cfg(target_os = "macos")</code>-gated runtime; pure-logic modules (<code>profile.rs</code>, <code>baseline.rs</code>) compile on any platform so unit tests run everywhere.</li> <li><code>wrap_spawn</code> builds an SBPL profile from the <code>SandboxPlan</code>, writes it to <code>/tmp/tau-darwin-<pid>-<n>.sb</code>, then replaces the original command with <code>sandbox-exec -f <profile> <orig-cmd></code>.</li> <li>Network plans validated through <code>tau-sandbox-proxy::validate_hosts</code> (no IPs except loopback, no wildcards). Profile permits outbound network only to <code>127.0.0.1:8443</code> — the proxy port. Plugin's reqwest routes via <code>HTTPS_PROXY=http://127.0.0.1:8443</code>.</li> <li>SBPL baseline (<code>baseline.rs::SBPL_BASELINE</code>) covers libc / dyld bootstrap (<code>process*</code>, <code>mach-lookup</code>, <code>sysctl-read</code>, <code>/usr/lib</code> subpath, etc.). <code>process*</code> rather than narrower verbs because <code>sandbox-exec</code> rejects with "execvp() failed: Operation not permitted" when limited to <code>process-fork</code>.</li> <li>Runtime registry: <code>instantiate(RegistryKind::Native)</code> returns <code>DarwinSandbox</code> on macOS, <code>NativeSandbox</code> on Linux, <code>Unavailable</code> elsewhere.</li> </ul> <h2 id="consequences-18"><a class="header" href="#consequences-18">Consequences</a></h2> <p>Positive:</p> <ul> <li>macOS plugin spawns now run under a real OS-level sandbox, matching Linux strict-tier security envelope (modulo per-syscall filtering, which macOS lacks).</li> <li>Defense-in-depth network containment via the same proxy as Linux — one allowlist surface, not two.</li> <li><code>tau-sandbox-darwin</code> is small (~370 LOC of runtime + 270 LOC of pure profile generation with 7 unit tests + 4 macOS integration tests).</li> </ul> <p>Negative:</p> <ul> <li><code>sandbox-exec</code> is officially deprecated by Apple. App Sandbox + entitlements is the modern path but requires a signed <code>.app</code> bundle. Acceptable: Apple still ships and supports <code>sandbox-exec</code>; if/when that changes we migrate to App Sandbox in a separate sub-project.</li> <li>SBPL baseline allowlist may drift across macOS versions; locked in <code>baseline.rs</code> and tests fail loudly if a new macOS version breaks bootstrap.</li> <li>No per-syscall filtering — the SBPL coarse model is what we get.</li> </ul> <h2 id="references-9"><a class="header" href="#references-9">References</a></h2> <ul> <li>Spec: <code>docs/superpowers/specs/2026-05-09-sandbox-darwin-design.md</code></li> <li>PR: #45 (<code>feat(sandbox-darwin): macOS sandbox-exec adapter (strict tier via SBPL)</code>)</li> <li>Commit: <code>597db89</code></li> </ul> <div style="break-before: page; page-break-before: always;"></div><h1 id="adr-0022--tau-workflow-linear-pipeline-runner"><a class="header" href="#adr-0022--tau-workflow-linear-pipeline-runner">ADR-0022 — tau-workflow: linear pipeline runner</a></h1> <p><strong>Status:</strong> Accepted 2026-05-12. <strong>Branch / PR:</strong> <code>feat/tau-workflow</code> (PR pending). <strong>Spec:</strong> <code>docs/superpowers/specs/2026-05-12-tau-workflow-design.md</code>.</p> <h2 id="context-23"><a class="header" href="#context-23">Context</a></h2> <p>ROADMAP §10 calls for a "deterministic step-by-step pipeline" runner. Until now, tau composes multi-step behavior only inside an agent's tool-loop, which mixes LLM decisions with deterministic glue. A first-class workflow primitive lets users compose multiple agents (and direct tool calls) into a single artifact that is sandboxed, persisted, and resumable.</p> <h2 id="decision-17"><a class="header" href="#decision-17">Decision</a></h2> <p>Ship a new <code>tau-workflow</code> crate that defines the workflow data model, runs steps via <code>tau_runtime::Runtime</code>, and persists each step's output as append-only JSONL. <code>tau-cli</code> exposes <code>tau workflow {list, run, log, resume}</code>. Step kinds for v1 are <code>agent.run</code> and <code>tool.call</code>; templates are <code>${input}</code> and <code>${steps.<id>.output}</code> (string substitution only).</p> <p>Persistence mirrors the REPL-session pattern (<code>.tau/sessions/*.jsonl</code>), giving us free <code>tau workflow log <run-id></code> history and inspectable post-mortem state.</p> <h2 id="alternatives-considered-15"><a class="header" href="#alternatives-considered-15">Alternatives considered</a></h2> <ol> <li><strong>Bake it into <code>tau-runtime</code>.</strong> Smaller diff but mixes orchestration with the plugin-host kernel. Rejected.</li> <li><strong>Bake it into <code>tau-cli</code>.</strong> Smallest diff but locks the runner to the CLI surface; a future serve-mode (Tier 4 §15) couldn't reuse it.</li> <li><strong>DAG runner for v1.</strong> Adds parallel branches and fan-in/out. More flexible but bigger design surface (~3× the LOC); we don't yet know whether users will need DAG capabilities. Earmarked as sub-project "workflow-DAG".</li> <li><strong><code>agent.run</code> only for v1.</strong> Tool calls could compose via dummy "tool-runner" agents. Adds an LLM round-trip per tool call. Rejected in favor of <code>tool.call</code>, which adds <code>Runtime::invoke_tool</code> (small reusable API).</li> </ol> <h2 id="consequences-19"><a class="header" href="#consequences-19">Consequences</a></h2> <ul> <li>New <code>Runtime::invoke_tool</code> API in <code>tau-runtime</code>. Pure addition; no behavior change for existing callers.</li> <li>Workflows are a first-class artifact at the project level (<code>workflows/*.toml</code>), peer to <code>tau.toml</code> agent definitions.</li> <li>Sandboxing is inherited: every step runs through the same sandboxed plugin host as <code>tau run</code>, with the workflow's referenced agents providing the capability grants.</li> <li>The JSONL log format is committed-to: any future schema change requires an additive migration with a once-per-process warn (same model as the lockfile v3→v4 transition).</li> </ul> <h2 id="v1-limitations-to-revisit"><a class="header" href="#v1-limitations-to-revisit">v1 limitations (to revisit)</a></h2> <ul> <li><code>tau-cli::cmd::workflow::build_runtime_for_workflow</code> builds a single Runtime from the first referenced agent's plugin config. Workflows whose agents use different LLM backend plugins will work but share one backend instance; revisit if users hit this.</li> <li>No DAG; no conditionals; no per-step capability overrides; no scheduled workflows; no public library API beyond <code>tau-cli</code>.</li> </ul> <h2 id="out-of-scope-deferred-follow-ups"><a class="header" href="#out-of-scope-deferred-follow-ups">Out of scope (deferred follow-ups)</a></h2> <ul> <li>DAG / parallel branches / fan-out / fan-in.</li> <li>Conditionals, loops, variable assignment beyond <code>${steps.<id>.output}</code>.</li> <li>Per-step capability overrides.</li> <li>Cron-style scheduled workflows.</li> <li><code>tau workflow runs gc</code> cleanup command.</li> </ul> <div style="break-before: page; page-break-before: always;"></div><h1 id="adr-0023-windows-appcontainer-adapter--phase-1-scaffold"><a class="header" href="#adr-0023-windows-appcontainer-adapter--phase-1-scaffold">ADR-0023: Windows AppContainer adapter — Phase 1 scaffold</a></h1> <p><strong>Status:</strong> Accepted (scaffold only — Phase 2 deferred) <strong>Date:</strong> 2026-05-09 <strong>Deciders:</strong> Titouan Lebocq <strong>Related:</strong> <a href="decisions/0014-sandboxing.html">ADR-0014 — Sandboxing</a>, <a href="decisions/0022-sandbox-darwin.html">ADR-0022 — macOS sandbox-exec adapter</a></p> <h2 id="context-24"><a class="header" href="#context-24">Context</a></h2> <p>After ADR-0022 shipped a macOS adapter, Windows remained the last host without a <code>RegistryKind::Native</code> resolution. The followups doc reserved this as sub-project K ("Windows AppContainer adapter").</p> <p>The Windows analogue of landlock + seccomp is <strong>AppContainer</strong> — a Win32 kernel primitive (Windows 8+) that runs a process under a restricted SID with capability-based access controls. Microsoft's <code>windows</code> crate provides safe FFI bindings (MIT/Apache-2 licensed — FOSS-compliant).</p> <p>Two structural blockers prevent landing the full adapter in one PR:</p> <ol> <li><strong><code>tau-sandbox-proxy</code> is <code>cfg(unix)</code>-gated</strong> — uses <code>tokio::net::UnixListener</code> for the parent-side accept loop. Windows needs a TCP-loopback or named-pipe variant before the macOS defense-in-depth pattern ports across.</li> <li><strong><code>std::process::Command</code> on Windows can't be intercepted at spawn time</strong> — there is no <code>pre_exec</code> analogue. To attach <code>PROC_THREAD_ATTRIBUTE_SECURITY_CAPABILITIES</code> to the new process the adapter must call <code>CreateProcessAsUserW</code> directly, which means either refactoring <code>tau-runtime::plugin_host::process</code> to support per-adapter spawn customisation or replacing <code>Command::spawn</code> entirely on the Windows path.</li> </ol> <p>The dev environment is also a constraint: AppContainer is a Windows kernel primitive that Wine doesn't reproduce, so iteration on this adapter is push-to-CI only (~5–7 min per <code>windows-latest</code> cycle) until a UTM Windows 11 ARM VM lands as a separate sub-project.</p> <h2 id="decision-18"><a class="header" href="#decision-18">Decision</a></h2> <p>Ship Phase 1 — <strong>the scaffold</strong> — now, defer Phase 2 (real Win32 calls) to a follow-up PR.</p> <p>Phase 1 ships:</p> <ul> <li><code>crates/tau-sandbox-windows</code> workspace member.</li> <li><code>profile.rs::build_appcontainer_caps(plan)</code> — pure function that translates a <code>SandboxPlan</code> into <code>AppContainerCaps { fs_read_paths, fs_write_paths, has_http, has_process_spawn }</code>. 7 unit tests; runs on any platform.</li> <li><code>acl.rs</code> — Win32-shape API (<code>create_appcontainer_profile</code>, <code>delete_appcontainer_profile</code>, <code>grant_access</code>, <code>revoke_access</code>) but <strong>stub implementations</strong> that return <code>Ok(())</code> without calling Win32. No <code>windows</code> crate dep.</li> <li><code>spawn.rs::register_appcontainer_for_command</code> — stub; documents the spawn-side blocker.</li> <li><code>WindowsSandbox</code> impl <code>Sandbox</code>. <strong>Probe returns <code>Unavailable</code> on Windows</strong> explicitly — Phase 1 is honest that this adapter doesn't yet sandbox anything. <code>wrap_spawn</code> returns <code>SandboxError::Unavailable</code> for HTTP plans (proxy needs UDS→TCP conversion).</li> <li>Runtime registry wired: <code>SandboxAdapter::Windows</code> cfg-gated to Windows; <code>instantiate(RegistryKind::Native)</code> returns <code>Windows</code> on Windows. The resolver still falls back to <code>Passthrough</code> because the probe declines, so behaviour is unchanged from today.</li> </ul> <p>Phase 2 (deferred) needs three coupled changes:</p> <ol> <li>Real Win32 calls in <code>acl.rs</code> via the <code>windows</code> crate (<code>CreateAppContainerProfile</code>, <code>DeriveAppContainerSidFromAppContainerName</code>, <code>SetEntriesInAclW</code>, <code>SetNamedSecurityInfoW</code>, <code>DeleteAppContainerProfile</code>).</li> <li>UDS→TCP (or named-pipe) variant of <code>tau-sandbox-proxy</code>.</li> <li><code>CreateProcessAsUserW</code> spawn integration (either refactor <code>plugin_host::process</code> for per-adapter spawn, or bypass <code>Command</code> on Windows).</li> </ol> <h2 id="consequences-20"><a class="header" href="#consequences-20">Consequences</a></h2> <p>Positive:</p> <ul> <li>Workspace structure, cfg-gating, and runtime registry routing land ahead of the platform-specific work; Phase 2 is purely additive.</li> <li>Pure-logic profile generation is testable on any host, so Phase 2 can iterate against existing tests without <code>windows-latest</code> cycles for the translation logic.</li> <li>Spec at <code>docs/superpowers/specs/2026-05-09-sandbox-windows-design.md</code> documents all four phases and risks; Phase 2 has a clear starting point.</li> </ul> <p>Negative:</p> <ul> <li>Phase 1 doesn't sandbox anything on Windows — the probe is honest about this, so users see <code>Unavailable</code> rather than thinking they're protected. Documented as the trade-off for shipping the scaffold early.</li> <li>Phase 2 requires either a Windows dev environment or push-to-CI iteration. UTM Windows 11 ARM VM is the future unlock.</li> </ul> <h2 id="references-10"><a class="header" href="#references-10">References</a></h2> <ul> <li>Spec: <code>docs/superpowers/specs/2026-05-09-sandbox-windows-design.md</code></li> <li>PR: #46 (<code>feat(sandbox-windows): scaffold Windows AppContainer adapter</code>)</li> <li>Commit: <code>6a58c53</code></li> </ul> <div style="break-before: page; page-break-before: always;"></div><h1 id="adr-0024--multi-agent-orchestration-primitives"><a class="header" href="#adr-0024--multi-agent-orchestration-primitives">ADR-0024 — Multi-agent orchestration primitives</a></h1> <p><strong>Status:</strong> Accepted 2026-05-12. <strong>Branch / PR:</strong> <code>feat/multi-agent-orchestration</code> (PR pending). <strong>Spec:</strong> <code>docs/superpowers/specs/2026-05-12-multi-agent-orchestration-design.md</code>.</p> <h2 id="context-25"><a class="header" href="#context-25">Context</a></h2> <p>ROADMAP §9 — "Multi-agent orchestration (G10's deferred half)." Until now, tau composes multi-step behavior only via the linear <code>tau-workflow</code> runner. A first-class runtime-level primitive set lets agents spawn, coordinate with, and observe other agents — without the runtime imposing any particular orchestration pattern.</p> <h2 id="decision-19"><a class="header" href="#decision-19">Decision</a></h2> <p>Implement the v1 primitive set in <code>tau-runtime::orchestration</code> (new submodule). Six entities (Identity, Capability, Agent, Task, TraceEvent, Run), three verb classes (think/call/complete; virtual tools; host-emitted), three channels (sync return, shared state, trace), six invariants (capability subset, lock exclusivity, LLM-context immutability, trace monotonicity, run termination, budget enforcement). Coordination via shared TaskList with hierarchical task ids + locks (owner + lease + heartbeat). No bus, no inbox, no push-into-LLM. CLI output is npm/cargo-style line-feed.</p> <h2 id="alternatives-considered-16"><a class="header" href="#alternatives-considered-16">Alternatives considered</a></h2> <ol> <li><strong>Separate <code>tau-orchestration</code> crate.</strong> Rejected — most operations are kernel-adjacent (capability checks, plugin dispatch), and serve-mode can import tau-runtime directly.</li> <li><strong>Message bus / inbox stacks.</strong> Rejected — tree topology, not many-to-many; LLM coherence breaks under unsolicited push.</li> <li><strong>Background / monitor tools (claude-code-style).</strong> Rejected for v1 — different primitive class (Channel D + BackgroundTool entity); tracked as deferred sub-project in ROADMAP.</li> <li><strong>Plan DAG (CrewAI-style task dependencies).</strong> Rejected for v1 — linear hierarchy is enough; deferred sub-project.</li> </ol> <h2 id="consequences-21"><a class="header" href="#consequences-21">Consequences</a></h2> <ul> <li><code>Capability::TaskList { mode }</code> + <code>Capability::Plan { mode }</code> variants added to tau-domain. Pure addition; no behavior change for existing callers.</li> <li>New <code>Runtime::spawn_root_agent</code> entry point. Single-agent <code>Runtime::run</code> is preserved.</li> <li>The JSONL log at <code><scope>/.tau/runs/<run_id>.jsonl</code> is committed-to; future schema changes require additive migration.</li> <li>Sandboxing is preserved: every spawned child runs under its own sandbox plan; child grant must be a subset of parent grant.</li> <li>Three of the five spec patterns compose end-to-end on v1: linear (single agent + task list), worker pool (host pre-populates the task list, worker agents claim+complete), and plan-revise (orchestrator manages the task list and inspects results). The supervisor/critic and hierarchical patterns require agent.<kind>.spawn recursive dispatch and ship in the v1.1 follow-up.</li> </ul> <h2 id="v1-implementation-limits"><a class="header" href="#v1-implementation-limits">v1 implementation limits</a></h2> <ul> <li><code>agent.<kind>.spawn</code> is validated (parent.Agent::Spawn check + capability subset law via <code>check_capability_subset</code>) but recursive <code>Runtime::run</code> invocation from inside the streaming tool-dispatch loop is deferred. v1 returns a <code>ToolResult { is_error: true, ... }</code> with text explaining the limitation. Follow-up tracked in ROADMAP.</li> <li>Live trace rendering during a run is not yet wired into the CLI — the CLI prints a summary from the <code>RunSnapshot</code> after the run completes. The JSONL log at <code><scope>/.tau/runs/<run-id>.jsonl</code> is the source of truth for replay/inspection. Follow-up tracked in ROADMAP.</li> <li>Pattern integration tests for the 5 spec patterns are skeletons that depend on multi-turn <code>MockLlmBackend</code> fixture wiring; they're added as the implementer is able.</li> </ul> <h2 id="out-of-scope-deferred-to-follow-ups-all-tracked-in-roadmap"><a class="header" href="#out-of-scope-deferred-to-follow-ups-all-tracked-in-roadmap">Out of scope (deferred to follow-ups, all tracked in ROADMAP)</a></h2> <ul> <li>Background tools / monitors (claude-code Monitor pattern; new channel + entity).</li> <li>Inter-agent message bus / inbox stacks.</li> <li>Pull-status tool (<code>agent.<kind>_status()</code>).</li> <li>Output schemas / typed tool returns.</li> <li>Plan DAG with task dependencies.</li> <li>Cross-run memory.</li> <li>Group chat / mediator agent.</li> <li>Workflow-DAG (extension of tau-workflow v1).</li> </ul> <h2 id="references-11"><a class="header" href="#references-11">References</a></h2> <ul> <li>Anthropic claude-code: <code>TodoWrite</code>, <code>Task</code> (synchronous subagent spawn).</li> <li>LangGraph: typed shared <code>State</code>, checkpoints, subgraphs.</li> <li>CrewAI: agents + tasks + memory tiers + hierarchical process.</li> <li>AutoGen / Magentic-One: orchestrator + specialists with a shared Ledger.</li> <li>OpenAI Swarm: handoffs + context_variables.</li> </ul> <div style="break-before: page; page-break-before: always;"></div><h1 id="adr-0025--skills-foundation-manifest-extension"><a class="header" href="#adr-0025--skills-foundation-manifest-extension">ADR-0025 — Skills foundation (manifest extension)</a></h1> <p><strong>Status:</strong> Accepted 2026-05-13. <strong>Branch / PR:</strong> <code>feat/skills-1-manifest-extension</code> (PR pending). <strong>Spec:</strong> <code>docs/superpowers/specs/2026-05-12-skills-1-manifest-design.md</code>. <strong>Plan:</strong> <code>docs/superpowers/plans/2026-05-13-skills-1-manifest-extension.md</code>.</p> <h2 id="context-26"><a class="header" href="#context-26">Context</a></h2> <p>ROADMAP §16 — "Skills as first-class packages." Constitution G10 commits to Skills being first-class in core ("Skills and MCP are first-class concepts in core. Tau understands the Agent Skills spec natively"). <code>kinds::SKILL = "skill"</code> has been a recognized <code>PackageKind</code> since the v0.1 manifest design, but no runtime concept, manifest block, parser, or install pipeline has existed.</p> <p>Skills-1 is the first of six sub-projects that close this gap. It ships the manifest types + parser + interpolation-variable constant in <code>tau-domain</code> only — no <code>tau-pkg</code>, <code>tau-runtime</code>, or <code>tau-cli</code> changes. Skills-2 (install pipeline), Skills-3 (discovery), Skills-4 (runtime invocation), Skills-5 (Agent Skills spec compliance), and Skills-6 (reference packages + docs) follow as separate PRs.</p> <h2 id="decision-20"><a class="header" href="#decision-20">Decision</a></h2> <p>A tau skill package is a <strong>directory with two manifest files</strong>:</p> <ul> <li><strong><code>SKILL.md</code></strong> — content. Pure Anthropic skill format: YAML frontmatter + Markdown body. Bit-identical to what claude-code / claude.ai / any compliant runtime expects. Zero tau-specific extensions in this file.</li> <li><strong><code>tau.toml</code></strong> — packaging. Capability declaration, tool / skill dependencies, version, source. The same shape as a plugin or any other tau package, with a new <code>[skill]</code> block.</li> </ul> <p>A tau skill IS an Anthropic skill (strip <code>tau.toml</code>, ship to claude-code). An Anthropic skill becomes a tau skill by adding <code>tau.toml</code>. No translation; no two-spec divergence.</p> <p>Skills-1 lands:</p> <ul> <li><code>tau-domain::package::skill</code> module with <code>SkillManifest</code>, <code>SkillFrontmatter</code>, <code>SkillContent</code>, <code>SkillContentError</code>.</li> <li><code>parse_skill_md</code> function: frontmatter splitter (handles <code>---</code> delimiters + CRLF) + <code>serde_yaml</code>-driven YAML parse + required- field validation (<code>name</code>, <code>description</code>).</li> <li><code>UncheckedManifest.skill: Option<SkillManifest></code> field, defaulting to <code>None</code> (mirrors the existing <code>plugin: Option<PluginManifest></code> pattern).</li> <li><code>PackageManifest::skill()</code> accessor.</li> <li><code>SKILL_DIR_VAR = "${SKILL_DIR}"</code> public constant for the interpolation variable. Symbolic in v1; substitution lives in Skills-4.</li> </ul> <h2 id="alternatives-considered-17"><a class="header" href="#alternatives-considered-17">Alternatives considered</a></h2> <p>During the brainstorm, three alternatives were considered before landing on the two-layer design:</p> <ol> <li><strong>Typed <code>[skill]</code> block embedding <code>system_prompt</code> inline.</strong> Rejected: TOML triple-quoted strings are awkward for long prompts; the format diverges from the Anthropic ecosystem; no cross-runtime portability.</li> <li><strong>Metadata-only <code>[skill]</code> + separate prompt file in a tau-specific layout.</strong> Rejected: invents a layout convention that diverges from Anthropic skills for no benefit. The chosen design is this option except the layout convention IS the Anthropic format.</li> <li><strong>Adopt the Agent Skills spec format verbatim as the only manifest.</strong> Rejected as the <em>only</em> manifest: would require either replacing <code>tau.toml</code> or splitting capability declarations across two manifest files. The chosen design adopts the Anthropic format for content (<code>SKILL.md</code>) while keeping tau's packaging machinery (capabilities, tool deps, lockfile) in <code>tau.toml</code> — best of both.</li> </ol> <h2 id="consequences-22"><a class="header" href="#consequences-22">Consequences</a></h2> <ul> <li><code>serde_yaml</code> (MIT/Apache-2.0) is now a tau-domain optional dep behind the <code>serde</code> feature. Allow-listed under cargo-deny.</li> <li>The public re-export surface of <code>tau_domain</code> grows by ~6 items (the new types + parse function + constant).</li> <li>Skills-2 can now wire <code>tau install <skill-pkg></code> through the install pipeline using the parser + manifest field added here.</li> <li>Skills-3 / Skills-4 can read <code>SkillManifest</code> via the existing manifest serde flow.</li> </ul> <h2 id="out-of-scope-deferred-to-skills-2"><a class="header" href="#out-of-scope-deferred-to-skills-2">Out of scope (deferred to Skills-2+)</a></h2> <ul> <li>The <code>tau install</code> install-time validation pipeline (Skills-2).</li> <li><code>${SKILL_DIR}</code> runtime substitution (Skills-4).</li> <li>Cross-field validation that <code>kind = "skill"</code> rejects <code>[plugin]</code> block (Skills-2 — closer to where the install-time error message is rendered).</li> <li>Lockfile schema migration for cached frontmatter + content_sha256 (Skills-2).</li> </ul> <h2 id="references-12"><a class="header" href="#references-12">References</a></h2> <ul> <li>Constitution G10 (Skills + MCP as first-class).</li> <li>Spec: <code>docs/superpowers/specs/2026-05-12-skills-1-manifest-design.md</code>.</li> <li>Priority queue: <code>docs/superpowers/specs/2026-05-12-post-multi-agent-priority-queue.md</code>.</li> <li>ROADMAP §16.</li> </ul> <div style="break-before: page; page-break-before: always;"></div><h1 id="adr-0026--skills-install-pipeline-skills-2"><a class="header" href="#adr-0026--skills-install-pipeline-skills-2">ADR-0026 — Skills install pipeline (Skills-2)</a></h1> <p><strong>Status:</strong> Accepted 2026-05-13. <strong>Branch / PR:</strong> <code>feat/skills-2-install-pipeline</code> (PR pending). <strong>Spec:</strong> <code>docs/superpowers/specs/2026-05-12-skills-2-install-pipeline-design.md</code>. <strong>Plan:</strong> <code>docs/superpowers/plans/2026-05-13-skills-2-install-pipeline.md</code>. <strong>Depends on:</strong> ADR-0025 (Skills-1 foundation).</p> <h2 id="context-27"><a class="header" href="#context-27">Context</a></h2> <p>Second of 6 sub-projects from ROADMAP §16 (Skills as first-class packages, Constitution G10). Skills-1 (ADR-0025, PR #63) shipped the manifest types + parser + interpolation-variable constant in tau-domain only — no install pipeline integration. Skills-2 wires <code>tau install <skill-pkg></code> end-to-end through tau-pkg so a skill package fetches, validates SKILL.md content + frontmatter, resolves transitive deps, computes a content SHA-256 + caches frontmatter, and writes to the lockfile.</p> <h2 id="decision-21"><a class="header" href="#decision-21">Decision</a></h2> <p>A new module <code>tau-pkg::skill_check</code> mirrors <code>tau-pkg::sandbox_check</code>. Single entry point <code>cross_check_skill_package(install_dir, manifest)</code> runs a 4-step flow:</p> <ol> <li>Read <code>SKILL.md</code> from <code>install_dir/<content_path></code> (default <code>"SKILL.md"</code>, from Skills-1's <code>SkillManifest.content</code>).</li> <li>Parse via <code>tau_domain::parse_skill_md</code> (Skills-1).</li> <li>Validate <code>frontmatter.name == manifest.name</code>.</li> <li>Reference lint (<strong>hard-fail</strong>): scan body for <code>${SKILL_DIR}/<rel-path></code> substrings; if no <code>[[capabilities]] kind = "fs.read"</code> glob covers, reject.</li> </ol> <p><code>install_with_options</code> dispatches on <code>manifest.kind()</code>:</p> <ul> <li><code>kind = "plugin"</code> → existing Layer 2 <code>sandbox_check</code> (unchanged)</li> <li><code>kind = "skill"</code> → new <code>skill_check</code>, then compute SHA-256 of SKILL.md bytes + snapshot frontmatter into a new <code>LockedSkill</code> lockfile entry</li> <li>other kinds → neither (existing behavior unchanged)</li> </ul> <p>The Layer 2 sandbox cross-check is skipped for skill packages because skills have no plugin process to spawn.</p> <p>Lockfile schema bumps v4 → v5. New <code>LockedPackage.skill: Option<LockedSkill></code> field. <code>LockedSkill { content_sha256: String, frontmatter: SkillFrontmatterSnapshot }</code>. Auto-upgrade follows the standard <code>was_pre_vN</code> + <code>tracing::warn</code> once-per-process pattern (v2→v3 precedent).</p> <p><code>tau verify</code> gains a <code>VerifyStatus::SkillContentDrift { name, expected, got }</code> variant parallel to <code>BinaryDrift</code>.
