Re-hashes SKILL.md on verify, compares to the cached <code>content_sha256</code>.</p> <p>tau-domain rejects packages combining <code>kind = "skill"</code> with a <code>[plugin]</code> block at parse time via the new <code>PackageManifestError::SkillCannotHavePluginBlock</code>. Cross-field validation runs in <code>UncheckedManifest::validate()</code>.</p> <h2 id="alternatives-considered-18"><a class="header" href="#alternatives-considered-18">Alternatives considered</a></h2> <h3 id="inline-skill_check-logic-in-install_with_options"><a class="header" href="#inline-skill_check-logic-in-install_with_options">Inline <code>skill_check</code> logic in <code>install_with_options</code></a></h3> <p>Rejected: <code>sandbox_check</code> is its own module for the same reasons (size of <code>install.rs</code>, future shareability, testability in isolation). The shared <code>parse_skill_md</code> parser + the discrete 4-step flow benefit from being callable from Skills-3 (<code>tau skill list / show</code> — reads frontmatter on demand) and Skills-4 (runtime invocation — reads body) without dragging install.rs along.</p> <h3 id="warn-only-reference-lint"><a class="header" href="#warn-only-reference-lint">Warn-only reference lint</a></h3> <p>The initial Skills-2 spec draft (commit <code>78f4352</code> in PR #62) had a warn-only lint. Rejected on review (commit <code>6176e18</code> in PR #62):</p> <ul> <li>True-positive cost (caught at runtime when the agent gets a capability-denied error mid-task) is severe — confusing failure mode for the agent's LLM, no clear remediation path from the runtime error alone.</li> <li>False-positive cost (skill author adds one <code>[[capabilities]]</code> line or removes a stale reference) is trivial.</li> <li>Hard-fail at install time matches how the rest of tau handles capability declarations: explicit > implicit. Warn-only would be the outlier.</li> </ul> <h3 id="keep-lockfile-schema-unchanged"><a class="header" href="#keep-lockfile-schema-unchanged">Keep lockfile schema unchanged</a></h3> <p>The initial Skills-2 spec draft had no lockfile migration — <code>tau skill list</code> would re-read every <code>SKILL.md</code> from disk on demand. Rejected on the same PR #62 review:</p> <ul> <li>A scope with 30-50 installed skills incurs 30-50 file opens per list. Noticeable latency, compounds across CLI surfaces.</li> <li>Drift is solved by the same SHA-256 mechanism that protects plugin binaries today (<code>tau verify</code>).</li> <li>Cached frontmatter is ~200 bytes per skill — negligible lockfile growth.</li> </ul> <h2 id="consequences-23"><a class="header" href="#consequences-23">Consequences</a></h2> <ul> <li><code>tau-pkg</code>'s public surface grows by <code>cross_check_skill_package</code> + <code>verify_skill_content</code> + <code>LockedSkill</code> + <code>SkillFrontmatterSnapshot</code>.</li> <li>4 new <code>InstallError</code> variants.</li> <li>1 new <code>PackageManifestError</code> variant.</li> <li>1 new <code>VerifyStatus</code> variant (the inner enum on <code>VerifyReport</code>).</li> <li>Lockfile schema v4 → v5 auto-upgrade. v4 lockfiles load cleanly; skill packages installed pre-v5 will surface as "unverified" via <code>tau verify</code> until reinstalled.</li> <li><code>tau install <skill-pkg></code> is now fully functional end-to-end.</li> <li>Skills-3 / Skills-4 unblocked.</li> </ul> <h2 id="out-of-scope-deferred-to-skills-3"><a class="header" href="#out-of-scope-deferred-to-skills-3">Out of scope (deferred to Skills-3+)</a></h2> <ul> <li><code>tau skill list</code> / <code>tau skill show</code> CLI subcommands → Skills-3 (consumes the cached frontmatter added here).</li> <li>Runtime invocation (<code>agent.<skill>.spawn</code> resolves to installed manifest; SKILL.md body becomes spawned child's system_prompt) → Skills-4.</li> <li>Agent Skills spec export / import → Skills-5.</li> <li>Plugin-package symmetry (<code>kind = "plugin"</code> rejecting <code>[skill]</code> block) — Skills-5 if needed.</li> </ul> <h2 id="references-13"><a class="header" href="#references-13">References</a></h2> <ul> <li>Spec: <code>docs/superpowers/specs/2026-05-12-skills-2-install-pipeline-design.md</code></li> <li>Plan: <code>docs/superpowers/plans/2026-05-13-skills-2-install-pipeline.md</code></li> <li>Skills-1 ADR: <code>docs/decisions/0025-skills-foundation.md</code></li> <li>ROADMAP §16</li> </ul> <div style="break-before: page; page-break-before: always;"></div><h1 id="adr-0027--skills-discovery-skills-3"><a class="header" href="#adr-0027--skills-discovery-skills-3">ADR-0027 — Skills discovery (Skills-3)</a></h1> <p><strong>Status:</strong> Accepted 2026-05-13. <strong>Branch / PR:</strong> <code>feat/skills-3-discovery</code> (PR pending). <strong>Spec:</strong> <code>docs/superpowers/specs/2026-05-13-skills-3-discovery-design.md</code>. <strong>Plan:</strong> <code>docs/superpowers/plans/2026-05-13-skills-3-discovery.md</code>. <strong>Depends on:</strong> ADR-0025 (Skills-1), ADR-0026 (Skills-2).</p> <h2 id="context-28"><a class="header" href="#context-28">Context</a></h2> <p>Third of 6 sub-projects from ROADMAP §16 (Skills as first-class packages, Constitution G10). Skills-1 (ADR-0025) shipped the manifest types + parser; Skills-2 (ADR-0026) wired the install pipeline + lockfile cache. Skills-3 surfaces installed skills to the user via <code>tau skill list</code> and <code>tau skill show <name></code>.</p> <h2 id="decision-22"><a class="header" href="#decision-22">Decision</a></h2> <p>Two subcommands:</p> <ul> <li><strong><code>tau skill list</code></strong> — enumerate installed skills (lockfile only; zero per-skill disk reads, consumes Skills-2's <code>LockedSkill.frontmatter</code> cache).</li> <li><strong><code>tau skill show <name></code></strong> — inspect one skill (lockfile + one <code>tau.toml</code> disk read; optional <code>--body</code> adds one <code>SKILL.md</code> read).</li> </ul> <p>Both subcommands support <code>--json</code> for canonical machine-readable output (matches existing <code>tau resolve --json</code> / <code>tau verify --json</code> convention). Both default to human-formatted terminal output.</p> <p><code>show --body</code> <strong>renders markdown via termimad by default</strong>, matching <code>tau chat</code>'s precedent. <code>--raw</code> flag opts out for pipe / grep / diff workflows. The trade-off favors the interactive default (most users running <code>tau skill show --body</code> are reading interactively, not piping).</p> <p>Unknown-name handling: Levenshtein distance ≤ 2 surfaces a "did you mean…?" suggestion; otherwise prints the full installed list. Exit 2 in both cases (matches existing <code>tau install</code> not-found convention).</p> <p>No new lockfile schema bump in Skills-3. <code>tau.toml</code> is re-read from disk on each <code>show</code> invocation (small + fast). Caching capabilities</p> <ul> <li>requires_tools + requires_skills in the lockfile would require Skills-2 schema churn for a marginal perf gain — rejected.</li> </ul> <h2 id="alternatives-considered-19"><a class="header" href="#alternatives-considered-19">Alternatives considered</a></h2> <h3 id="default-to-raw-markdown-for---body"><a class="header" href="#default-to-raw-markdown-for---body">Default to raw markdown for <code>--body</code></a></h3> <p>Considered: pipe-friendly out of the box, no rendering hop. Rejected:</p> <ul> <li>Tau's existing precedent (<code>tau chat</code> streams rendered markdown) is render-by-default. Skills should match.</li> <li>The interactive case is the most common one. Render makes content scannable; raw markdown forces the user to mentally parse.</li> <li><code>--raw</code> is one flag away for scripting workflows.</li> </ul> <h3 id="tau-skill-uninstall-name-alias"><a class="header" href="#tau-skill-uninstall-name-alias"><code>tau skill uninstall <name></code> alias</a></h3> <p>Considered: discoverability — a user running <code>tau skill list</code> might look for a parallel <code>tau skill uninstall</code>. Rejected:</p> <ul> <li>Pure alias for the generic <code>tau uninstall <name></code> — no skill-specific behavior.</li> <li>API surface bloat.</li> </ul> <h3 id="cache-capabilities--requires_tools--requires_skills-in-lockfile"><a class="header" href="#cache-capabilities--requires_tools--requires_skills-in-lockfile">Cache <code>capabilities</code> + <code>requires_tools</code> + <code>requires_skills</code> in lockfile</a></h3> <p>Considered: would make <code>show</code> zero-disk-read like <code>list</code>. Rejected:</p> <ul> <li>Skills-2 just shipped lockfile schema v5. Bumping to v6 for marginal perf is churn-without-justification.</li> <li><code>tau.toml</code> reads are fast; one file, small payload.</li> <li>Drift would require another sha256 cache (Skills-2 has one for SKILL.md content; adding another for <code>tau.toml</code> is more surface).</li> </ul> <h3 id="--format-template-flag"><a class="header" href="#--format-template-flag"><code>--format <template></code> flag</a></h3> <p>Considered: power-user feature for scripting. Rejected:</p> <ul> <li><code>--json | jq</code> covers the same use case better.</li> <li>Template language is its own design problem.</li> <li>YAGNI for v1.</li> </ul> <h3 id="--sortinstalled-atversionname"><a class="header" href="#--sortinstalled-atversionname"><code>--sort=installed-at|version|name</code></a></h3> <p>Considered: useful for "what did I install recently?" workflows. Rejected for v1:</p> <ul> <li>Feature surface for the initial ship.</li> <li>Easy additive enhancement when a user asks.</li> <li>Alphabetic by name is the most predictable default.</li> </ul> <h2 id="consequences-24"><a class="header" href="#consequences-24">Consequences</a></h2> <ul> <li><code>tau-cli</code>'s public surface grows by <code>Command::Skill</code> + <code>SkillSubcommand</code> + <code>SkillListArgs</code> + <code>SkillShowArgs</code>.</li> <li>New <code>crates/tau-cli/src/cmd/skill/</code> module tree (5 files).</li> <li>No <code>tau-pkg</code> or <code>tau-domain</code> changes. Skills-2's <code>LockedSkill</code> schema is consumed read-only.</li> <li><code>cargo-deny</code> allow-list unchanged (no new external deps).</li> <li><code>tau install <skill-pkg></code> + <code>tau skill list</code> + <code>tau skill show</code> now form a complete user-facing workflow for skill packages.</li> <li>Skills-4 (runtime invocation) is unblocked.</li> </ul> <h2 id="out-of-scope-deferred-to-skills-4"><a class="header" href="#out-of-scope-deferred-to-skills-4">Out of scope (deferred to Skills-4+)</a></h2> <ul> <li><strong>Runtime invocation</strong> — <code>agent.<skill-name>.spawn</code> resolution → Skills-4 (the most strategic remaining sub-project).</li> <li><strong>Agent Skills spec export / import</strong> → Skills-5.</li> <li><strong>Reference skill packages + user docs</strong> → Skills-6.</li> <li><strong><code>--sort</code> / filter flags</strong> — additive enhancement when needed.</li> <li><strong>User-customizable termimad skins</strong> — Skills-5 or separate ROADMAP item.</li> </ul> <h2 id="references-14"><a class="header" href="#references-14">References</a></h2> <ul> <li>Spec: <code>docs/superpowers/specs/2026-05-13-skills-3-discovery-design.md</code></li> <li>Plan: <code>docs/superpowers/plans/2026-05-13-skills-3-discovery.md</code></li> <li>Skills-1 ADR: <code>docs/decisions/0025-skills-foundation.md</code></li> <li>Skills-2 ADR: <code>docs/decisions/0026-skills-install-pipeline.md</code></li> <li>ROADMAP §16</li> </ul> <div style="break-before: page; page-break-before: always;"></div><h1 id="adr-0028--docs-deployment-github-pages-auto-cd"><a class="header" href="#adr-0028--docs-deployment-github-pages-auto-cd">ADR-0028 — Docs deployment (GitHub Pages auto-CD)</a></h1> <p><strong>Status:</strong> Accepted 2026-05-13. <strong>Branch / PR:</strong> <code>feat/docs-publish</code> (PR pending). <strong>Spec:</strong> <code>docs/superpowers/specs/2026-05-13-docs-deploy-design.md</code>. <strong>Plan:</strong> <code>docs/superpowers/plans/2026-05-13-docs-deploy.md</code>.</p> <h2 id="context-29"><a class="header" href="#context-29">Context</a></h2> <p>Documentation lives in <code>docs/</code> (Diátaxis structure per QG8) as plain markdown. There is no published site. Contributors and users read docs by browsing the repository on github.com. This is acceptable for a pre-1.0 project but creates two problems as the project matures:</p> <ol> <li>There is no per-version snapshot. A user on <code>tau 0.5</code> reading docs at <code>HEAD</code> sees behavior that may not match their installed version.</li> <li>ADRs, the Constitution, and the cheatsheet are not navigable as a single site with search.</li> </ol> <h2 id="decision-23"><a class="header" href="#decision-23">Decision</a></h2> <p>Publish <code>docs/</code> as a versioned <a href="https://rust-lang.github.io/mdBook/">mdBook</a> site on GitHub Pages. The site lives on a <code>gh-pages</code> branch with this layout:</p> <ul> <li><code>/</code> redirects to <code>/latest/</code>.</li> <li><code>/latest/</code> is the most recently released build (overwritten each release).</li> <li><code>/v0.X/</code> (pre-1.0) or <code>/vX/</code> (post-1.0) are frozen per-tag builds.</li> <li><code>/preview/pr-NNN/</code> are ephemeral PR-preview builds.</li> <li><code>/versions.json</code> is a manifest for a future version-picker UI.</li> </ul> <p>Deploys are triggered by:</p> <ol> <li><strong>Release tag push</strong> matching <code>v[0-9]+.0.0</code> or <code>v0.[0-9]+.0</code> (major-equivalent bump per QG11): build → publish <code>/vX/</code> + replace <code>/latest/</code>.</li> <li><strong>Push to <code>main</code> with <code>[publish-docs]</code> in the commit message</strong>: replace <code>/latest/</code> only. Force-publish for hot-fixing docs without cutting a release.</li> <li><strong>PR labeled <code>docs:publish</code></strong>: publish ephemeral <code>/preview/pr-NNN/</code>, comment URL on the PR. NEVER touches <code>/latest/</code>.</li> <li><strong><code>workflow_dispatch</code></strong>: manual run.</li> </ol> <p>The deploy uses <code>peaceiris/actions-gh-pages@v3</code> with <code>keep_files: true</code> to overlay builds into per-version subdirectories without disturbing sibling directories. <code>/latest/</code> and <code>/preview/pr-NNN/</code> are wiped before the overlay (because they represent a single "current" state); <code>/vX/</code> are write-once.</p> <p>A separate PR gate workflow (<code>docs-check.yml</code>) runs <code>mdbook build</code> plus <code>mdbook-linkcheck</code> on every PR that touches <code>docs/**</code> or either workflow file. The gate does not deploy.</p> <h2 id="consequences-25"><a class="header" href="#consequences-25">Consequences</a></h2> <p><strong>Positive:</strong></p> <ul> <li>Users on a specific tau version can read docs that match.</li> <li>The full site is searchable, navigable, and link-checked.</li> <li>Force-publish marker lets us fix doc typos without a release.</li> <li>PR previews make rendered-doc review possible before merge.</li> </ul> <p><strong>Negative:</strong></p> <ul> <li>A second markdown source-of-truth surface exists (<code>SUMMARY.md</code>) that must be updated when files are added. Mitigated by the PR gate failing when <code>SUMMARY.md</code> references a missing file.</li> <li>The <code>gh-pages</code> branch must be created manually once before the first deploy.</li> <li>Fork PRs cannot trigger preview deploys (we use <code>pull_request</code> not <code>pull_request_target</code> for security). Acceptable trade-off.</li> </ul> <p><strong>Neutral:</strong></p> <ul> <li>This is a docs-publishing concern only; no Rust code changes.</li> <li>rustdoc is not published as part of this ADR. A follow-up may publish <code>cargo doc</code> output under <code>/api/</code>.</li> </ul> <h2 id="alternatives-considered-20"><a class="header" href="#alternatives-considered-20">Alternatives considered</a></h2> <ul> <li><strong>MkDocs / MkDocs Material</strong>: nicer default theme, Python-based. Rejected because it pulls Python into the docs pipeline of an otherwise pure-Rust project, and mdBook is the idiomatic choice (Rust Book, Cargo Book, rustc dev guide all use it).</li> <li><strong>Docusaurus</strong>: built-in versioning and i18n, MDX support. Rejected as overkill — drags Node into docs, far more configuration surface than the project needs.</li> <li><strong>Jekyll (GitHub Pages default)</strong>: zero CI required, but very limited theming and search; harder to extend later.</li> <li><strong><code>actions/deploy-pages</code> with <code>actions/upload-pages-artifact</code></strong>: cleaner atomic single-artifact model, but forces rebuilding the entire multi-version tree on every deploy. Rejected in favor of the overlay model on <code>gh-pages</code>.</li> <li><strong>Single-version (always overwrite)</strong>: simplest, but loses historical docs. Rejected because per-tag snapshots are the motivating use case.</li> </ul> <div style="break-before: page; page-break-before: always;"></div><h1 id="adr-0028--skills-runtime-invocation-skills-4"><a class="header" href="#adr-0028--skills-runtime-invocation-skills-4">ADR-0028 — Skills runtime invocation (Skills-4)</a></h1> <p><strong>Status:</strong> Accepted 2026-05-14. <strong>Branch / PR:</strong> <code>feat/skills-4-runtime-invocation</code> (PR pending). <strong>Spec:</strong> <code>docs/superpowers/specs/2026-05-14-skills-4-runtime-invocation-design.md</code> (merged at PR #69). <strong>Plan:</strong> <code>docs/superpowers/plans/2026-05-14-skills-4-runtime-invocation.md</code>. <strong>Depends on:</strong> ADR-0025 (Skills-1), ADR-0026 (Skills-2), ADR-0027 (Skills-3), ADR-0024 (multi-agent orchestration v1.1 + v1.2).</p> <h2 id="context-30"><a class="header" href="#context-30">Context</a></h2> <p>Fourth of 6 sub-projects from ROADMAP §16 (Skills as first-class packages, Constitution G10). The runtime piece that makes installed skills usable by agents.</p> <p>When an agent emits a <code>skill.<name>.spawn</code> virtual tool call, the runtime resolves <code><name></code> to an installed skill, builds a child agent run from the skill's declared <code>system_prompt</code> + capabilities (with <code>${SKILL_DIR}</code> substituted + optional caller <code>scope_paths</code> narrowing), and recursively invokes <code>Runtime::run_with_history</code> via the v1.1 agent-spawn machinery shipped in PR #60.</p> <h2 id="decision-24"><a class="header" href="#decision-24">Decision</a></h2> <p>Three locked decisions (from brainstorming):</p> <h3 id="d1-separate-uri-namespace--capability-variant"><a class="header" href="#d1-separate-uri-namespace--capability-variant">D1: Separate URI namespace + capability variant</a></h3> <p><code>skill.<name>.spawn</code> parallel to existing <code>agent.<kind>.spawn</code>. New <code>Capability::Skill(SkillCapability::Spawn { allowed_skills })</code>.</p> <p>TOML form:</p> <pre><code class="language-toml">[[capabilities]] kind = "skill.spawn" allowed_skills = ["critic", "fact-checker"] </code></pre> <p>No namespace collision possible between custom agent kinds and skill names. Authorization (parent has <code><name></code> in <code>allowed_skills</code>) is enforced in <code>validate_skill_spawn</code>, independent of the agent-spawn authorization path.</p> <h3 id="d2-caller-scope_paths-optionvecstring-narrows-fs-paths-only"><a class="header" href="#d2-caller-scope_paths-optionvecstring-narrows-fs-paths-only">D2: Caller <code>scope_paths: Option<Vec<String>></code> narrows fs.* paths only</a></h3> <p>Per-kind intersection; hard-fail on uncovered <code>scope_path</code> (typo detection); non-fs capabilities pass through unchanged. Caller cannot add new capabilities or change capability kinds — skill author owns the capability contract; caller can tighten scope only.</p> <p>Semantics (per <code>apply_scope_paths</code>):</p> <ul> <li>For each <code>fs.*</code> capability the skill declares, the child's effective paths = intersect(declared paths, <code>scope_paths</code>). Non-fs caps unchanged.</li> <li>If a <code>scope_path</code> is not covered by ANY declared fs.* path → <code>SkillScopePathNotCovered</code> error (typo detection).</li> <li>If intersection is empty for a given fs.* kind → drop that capability entirely.</li> </ul> <h3 id="d3-full-multi-turn-mockllmbackend-test-fixture-in-this-pr"><a class="header" href="#d3-full-multi-turn-mockllmbackend-test-fixture-in-this-pr">D3: Full multi-turn <code>MockLlmBackend</code> test fixture in this PR</a></h3> <p>Lifts the existing <code>ScriptedLlm</code> pattern from <code>tests/run_with_tool_calls.rs</code> into reusable <code>crates/tau-runtime/tests/common/mock_llm.rs</code>. Builder API: <code>MockLlmBackend::new(name).add_text("...").add_tool_call(name, args).add_end()</code>.</p> <p>Bonus: 5 <code>#[ignore]</code>'d orchestration pattern test skeletons from PR #59 are un-ignored using this fixture (Tasks 9 patterns: linear, worker-pool, supervisor-critic, hierarchical, plan-revise).</p> <h2 id="alternatives-considered-21"><a class="header" href="#alternatives-considered-21">Alternatives considered</a></h2> <ul> <li><strong>Reuse <code>agent.<kind>.spawn</code> URI for skills</strong> (Option A in brainstorm): namespace collision risk with custom kinds; capability conflation between agent-defined and skill-installed children.</li> <li><strong>Caller-supplied <code>grant: Vec<Capability></code> override</strong> (Option B in brainstorm): too much rope; precedence rules become unnecessary public surface; skill author no longer owns capability contract.</li> <li><strong>No caller knob at all</strong> (Option X in brainstorm): loses per-spawn narrowing use cases (one skill, multiple project scopes).</li> <li><strong>Defer MockLlmBackend to follow-up PR</strong>: weaker Skills-4 coverage; fixture has to be built eventually for the multi-agent pattern tests anyway.</li> </ul> <h2 id="consequences-26"><a class="header" href="#consequences-26">Consequences</a></h2> <ul> <li><code>tau-domain</code> public surface grows by <code>SkillCapability</code> + <code>Capability::Skill</code> variant + <code>CapabilityShape::SkillSpawn</code>.</li> <li><code>tau-pkg</code> public surface grows by <code>find_installed_skill</code> + <code>InstalledSkill</code> + <code>FindSkillError</code>.</li> <li><code>tau-runtime</code> adds <code>orchestration::skill_resolve</code> module + 5 <code>OrchestrationError</code> variants + <code>validate_skill_spawn</code> + <code>is_skill_spawn</code> branch in <code>run_streaming_inner</code>.</li> <li><code>crates/tau-runtime/tests/common/mock_llm.rs</code> is the canonical multi-turn LLM test fixture — future test suites can reuse. Copied verbatim into <code>crates/tau-cli/tests/common/mock_llm.rs</code> for cross-crate test reuse (~180 LOC; not a real maintenance burden, but ROADMAP-tracked for future shared-test-support extraction).</li> <li>5 previously-<code>#[ignore]</code>'d pattern tests from PR #59 are now running, providing real e2e coverage of multi-agent orchestration patterns.</li> <li>No new external deps.</li> <li>No CI changes.</li> </ul> <h2 id="discovered-during-implementation"><a class="header" href="#discovered-during-implementation">Discovered during implementation</a></h2> <p>Skills-4 T8 e2e tests surfaced three gaps in <code>capability_satisfies</code>:</p> <ol> <li> <p><strong><code>Capability::Skill</code> arm missing</strong> — fixed in this PR. Added <code>skill_satisfies</code> helper with <code>string_subset</code> semantics matching <code>agent_satisfies</code>. Without this fix, every <code>skill.<name>.spawn</code> would silently PolicyDeny.</p> </li> <li> <p><strong><code>Capability::TaskList</code> / <code>Capability::Plan</code> arms missing</strong> — fixed independently on main (merged before this PR rebased; visible in <code>capability.rs</code> as <code>task_list_satisfies</code> + <code>plan_satisfies</code> helpers with mode-rank subsumption). Merge resolved by keeping both branches' arms.</p> </li> <li> <p><strong><code>check_capability_subset()</code> uses literal JSON string comparison</strong> (<code>tau-runtime/src/orchestration/virtual_tools.rs</code>): subset law check compares JSON serialisations rather than semantic capability comparison. Means a narrowed <code>agent.spawn(["coder","tester"])</code> isn't recognized as subset of <code>agent.spawn(["team-lead","coder","tester"])</code>. <strong>Still deferred</strong> — T9 pattern D works around by granting the child the full grant. Deserves its own ROADMAP entry.</p> </li> </ol> <h2 id="out-of-scope-deferred-to-skills-5"><a class="header" href="#out-of-scope-deferred-to-skills-5">Out of scope (deferred to Skills-5+)</a></h2> <ul> <li><strong>Agent Skills spec export / import</strong> → Skills-5</li> <li><strong>Reference skill packages + user docs</strong> → Skills-6</li> <li><strong>Sub-skill <code>requires_skills</code> runtime enforcement</strong> — advisory only</li> <li><strong>Body parse caching across spawns</strong> — YAGNI</li> <li><strong>Caller-side capability merge (<code>grant_extend</code>)</strong> — add when use case surfaces</li> </ul> <h2 id="references-15"><a class="header" href="#references-15">References</a></h2> <ul> <li>Spec: <code>docs/superpowers/specs/2026-05-14-skills-4-runtime-invocation-design.md</code></li> <li>Plan: <code>docs/superpowers/plans/2026-05-14-skills-4-runtime-invocation.md</code></li> <li>Skills-1 ADR: <code>docs/decisions/0025-skills-foundation.md</code></li> <li>Skills-2 ADR: <code>docs/decisions/0026-skills-install-pipeline.md</code></li> <li>Skills-3 ADR: <code>docs/decisions/0027-skills-discovery.md</code></li> <li>Multi-agent ADR: <code>docs/decisions/0024-multi-agent-orchestration.md</code></li> <li>Multi-agent v1.1 PR: #60 (recursive <code>agent.<kind>.spawn</code>)</li> <li>Multi-agent v1.2 PR: #61 (per-spawn <code>system_prompt</code>)</li> <li>ROADMAP §16</li> </ul> <div style="break-before: page; page-break-before: always;"></div><h1 id="adr-0029--skills-anthropic-interop-skills-5"><a class="header" href="#adr-0029--skills-anthropic-interop-skills-5">ADR-0029 — Skills Anthropic interop (Skills-5)</a></h1> <p><strong>Status:</strong> Accepted 2026-05-16. <strong>Branch / PR:</strong> <code>feat/skills-5-anthropic-interop-design</code> (PR #102). <strong>Spec:</strong> <code>docs/superpowers/specs/2026-05-15-skills-5-anthropic-interop-design.md</code>. <strong>Plan:</strong> <code>docs/superpowers/plans/2026-05-15-skills-5-anthropic-interop.md</code>. <strong>Depends on:</strong> ADR-0025 (Skills-1), ADR-0026 (Skills-2), ADR-0027 (Skills-3), ADR-0028 (Skills-4).</p> <h2 id="context-31"><a class="header" href="#context-31">Context</a></h2> <p>Fifth of 6 sub-projects from ROADMAP §16. Skills-1 established the two-layer architecture ("a tau skill IS an Anthropic skill plus tau.toml"). Skills-5 ships the tooling that makes that bidirectional in practice: import vanilla Anthropic skills into tau, export tau-installed skills back to vanilla Anthropic format, and validate Anthropic-conformance of installed skills.</p> <h2 id="decision-25"><a class="header" href="#decision-25">Decision</a></h2> <p>Five locked decisions:</p> <h3 id="d1--bidirectional-scope-export--import--conformance"><a class="header" href="#d1--bidirectional-scope-export--import--conformance">D1 — Bidirectional scope (export + import + conformance)</a></h3> <p>Picked from a 4-option scope question (export-only / bidirectional / conformance-only / extension-key full-interop). Bidirectional gives ergonomic UX for the common "consume an Anthropic skill from GitHub" flow; conformance closes the validation loop. The <code>x-tau-capabilities</code> YAML extension for round-trippable export of capability-bearing skills was rejected as premature — only export-without-capabilities use case is concrete today.</p> <h3 id="d2--both-auto-detect-inside-tau-install-and-explicit-tau-skill-import"><a class="header" href="#d2--both-auto-detect-inside-tau-install-and-explicit-tau-skill-import">D2 — Both auto-detect inside <code>tau install</code> AND explicit <code>tau skill import</code></a></h3> <p><code>tau install <src></code> detects Anthropic format and synthesizes a <code>tau.toml</code> transparently (ergonomic happy path). <code>tau skill import <src> --output <dir></code> produces an editable directory so users can inspect or customize the synthesized tau.toml before installing.</p> <h3 id="d3--capabilities-dropped-on-export"><a class="header" href="#d3--capabilities-dropped-on-export">D3 — Capabilities dropped on export</a></h3> <p>Synthesized manifests start <code>capabilities = []</code>. Skill authors who want capabilities must add them by hand (via <code>tau skill import</code> + edit). On export, capabilities (and <code>requires_skills</code>) are silently dropped from the output with an stderr note. <code>tau skill export --strict</code> makes drops a hard error.</p> <p>For non-SKILL.md content (refs/, assets/, etc.), export uses a simple <strong>copy-everything-except-tau.toml</strong> strategy. <code>SkillManifest</code> does not currently carry a <code>files</code> glob (Skills-1 schema), so this is the natural approach: the install pipeline already copies the full source tree into <code><scope>/.tau/packages/<name>/<version>/</code>, and export walks that directory verbatim minus <code>tau.toml</code>.</p> <h3 id="d4--lockfile-schema-v5--v6-with-synthesized_from"><a class="header" href="#d4--lockfile-schema-v5--v6-with-synthesized_from">D4 — Lockfile schema v5 → v6 with <code>synthesized_from</code></a></h3> <p><code>LockedPackage.synthesized_from: Option<SynthesizedSource></code> records the manifest origin. Enum currently has one variant: <code>SynthesizedSource::Anthropic</code>. Field defaults to <code>None</code> for v5 entries on read; lockfile auto-upgrades to v6 on next write (existing pattern from v4→v5 in PR #64). <code>tau skill show</code> displays <code>Source format: synthesized (Anthropic Agent Skills)</code> when the field is <code>Some</code>.</p> <h3 id="d5--tau-verify---anthropic-strict"><a class="header" href="#d5--tau-verify---anthropic-strict">D5 — <code>tau verify --anthropic-strict</code></a></h3> <p>New flag on the existing <code>tau verify</code> command. Without the flag, behavior unchanged. With the flag, additionally checks each installed skill against Anthropic SKILL.md conformance:</p> <ul> <li>Frontmatter must parse as valid YAML with required <code>name</code> + <code>description</code></li> <li><code>description</code> must be non-whitespace</li> <li>Body must be non-whitespace</li> </ul> <p>Emits <code>VerifyStatus::AnthropicConformance { skill_name, issue }</code> with <code>AnthropicConformanceIssue::{MissingDescription, EmptyBody, MalformedFrontmatter}</code> failure modes.</p> <h2 id="alternatives-considered-22"><a class="header" href="#alternatives-considered-22">Alternatives considered</a></h2> <ul> <li><strong>Conformance-only Skills-5</strong> (no commands, just validation in <code>tau install</code> + <code>tau verify --anthropic-strict</code>). Rejected: import is the highest-leverage ergonomic feature; defers the most valuable UX gain.</li> <li><strong>Export-only Skills-5</strong> (no import). Rejected for the same reason.</li> <li><strong>Auto-detect only inside <code>tau install</code></strong> (no explicit <code>tau skill import</code>). Rejected: power users want to inspect/edit the synthesized tau.toml; without explicit import, they'd have to edit the on-disk install location post-fact (awkward).</li> <li><strong>Explicit <code>tau skill import</code> only</strong> (no auto-detect). Rejected: forces every user to know about format mismatch and run extra steps; common case should Just Work.</li> <li><strong><code>x-tau-capabilities</code> YAML extension key for round-trippable export.</strong> Rejected: YAGNI; no real use case yet for round-trip with capability preservation.</li> <li><strong>Plural-format <code>--format <foo></code> flag.</strong> Rejected: only Anthropic format is in scope; premature plumbing.</li> <li><strong>Bulk export (<code>tau skill export --all</code>).</strong> Rejected: YAGNI; trivially scriptable via <code>tau skill list --json | jq | xargs</code>.</li> </ul> <h2 id="consequences-27"><a class="header" href="#consequences-27">Consequences</a></h2> <ul> <li><strong><code>tau-domain</code></strong> public surface grows by <code>SkillFormat</code>, <code>detect_format</code>, <code>synthesize_manifest_from_skill_md</code>, <code>SynthesizeError</code>.</li> <li><strong><code>tau-pkg</code></strong> public surface grows by new <code>synthesize</code> module (<code>synthesize_anthropic_skill</code> + tau-pkg's own <code>SynthesizeError</code>) + <code>SynthesizedSource</code> + 2 new <code>InstallError</code> variants (<code>NotASkillPackage</code>, <code>SynthesizeFailed</code>) + <code>AnthropicConformanceIssue</code> + new <code>VerifyStatus::AnthropicConformance</code> variant + <code>verify_all_with_options(scope, anthropic_strict)</code> entry point. Existing <code>verify_all</code> preserved as a delegating wrapper.</li> <li><strong><code>tau-pkg::install</code></strong>: Anthropic-format installs now write the synthesized <code>tau.toml</code> to disk at <code><scope>/.tau/packages/<name>/<version>/tau.toml</code> — surfaced during T7 integration as a gap; without it <code>tau skill show</code> + <code>tau skill export</code> couldn't operate on Anthropic-installed packages.</li> <li><strong><code>tau-cli</code></strong> public surface grows by <code>SkillSubcommand::{Import, Export}</code> + <code>--anthropic-strict</code> flag on <code>tau verify</code>.</li> <li><strong>Lockfile schema v6</strong> (additive); v5 reads cleanly with <code>synthesized_from = None</code>; v5→v6 upgrade is automatic on next write.</li> <li><strong><code>tau skill import</code> URL handling</strong>: All Git-scheme URLs (including <code>file://</code>) route through <code>git clone</code>. Only bare local paths (no scheme) use filesystem copy. This was a T7 integration fix.</li> <li><strong>No new external dependencies.</strong> No CI changes.</li> </ul> <h2 id="discovered-during-implementation-1"><a class="header" href="#discovered-during-implementation-1">Discovered during implementation</a></h2> <p>Two T7 integration gaps surfaced and were fixed in scope:</p> <ol> <li> <p><strong>Synthesized <code>tau.toml</code> was never written to the install directory.</strong> T3 added the in-memory manifest synthesis path but kept the install behavior unchanged in terms of what landed on disk. <code>tau skill show</code> + <code>tau skill export</code> failed for Anthropic-installed skills because they require <code>tau.toml</code> to exist. Fixed by writing the synthesized manifest to the staging directory before the staging→final rename.</p> </li> <li> <p><strong><code>tau skill import</code> treated <code>file://</code> URLs as local-path fs copies.</strong> For bare git repos, this copied <code>.git/</code> metadata instead of working-tree content. Fixed by routing all Git-scheme URLs (including <code>file://</code>) through <code>git clone</code>; only bare local paths now use fs copy.</p> </li> </ol> <p>Both gaps blocked the Skills-5 user story end-to-end. T7's roundtrip e2e tests caught them; the fix landed in scope so the un-ignored tests pass.</p> <h2 id="out-of-scope-deferred-to-skills-6--future"><a class="header" href="#out-of-scope-deferred-to-skills-6--future">Out of scope (deferred to Skills-6+ / future)</a></h2> <ul> <li><strong>Reference skill packages</strong> themselves — Skills-6.</li> <li><strong>Sub-skill <code>requires_skills</code> cross-format mapping</strong> — silently dropped on export (advisory only).</li> <li><strong>Conformance against future Anthropic spec revisions</strong> — re-evaluate when the next major spec lands.</li> <li><strong><code>tau skill convert</code></strong> as an alias or alternative to import/export — Skills-5 v2 if requested.</li> <li><strong>MCP-adjacent interop</strong> (consuming MCP server descriptors as tau skills) — separate sub-project; out of ROADMAP §16 scope.</li> <li><strong><code>x-tau-capabilities</code> YAML extension key</strong> for capability preservation across export — revisit if a concrete use case emerges.</li> </ul> <h2 id="references-16"><a class="header" href="#references-16">References</a></h2> <ul> <li>Spec: <code>docs/superpowers/specs/2026-05-15-skills-5-anthropic-interop-design.md</code></li> <li>Plan: <code>docs/superpowers/plans/2026-05-15-skills-5-anthropic-interop.md</code></li> <li>Skills-1 ADR: <code>docs/decisions/0025-skills-foundation.md</code></li> <li>Skills-2 ADR: <code>docs/decisions/0026-skills-install-pipeline.md</code></li> <li>Skills-3 ADR: <code>docs/decisions/0027-skills-discovery.md</code></li> <li>Skills-4 ADR: <code>docs/decisions/0028-skills-runtime-invocation.md</code></li> <li>ROADMAP §16</li> <li>Priority queue: <code>docs/superpowers/specs/2026-05-12-post-multi-agent-priority-queue.md</code></li> </ul> <div style="break-before: page; page-break-before: always;"></div><h1 id="adr-0030--skills-reference-packages--user-docs-skills-6"><a class="header" href="#adr-0030--skills-reference-packages--user-docs-skills-6">ADR-0030 — Skills reference packages + user docs (Skills-6)</a></h1> <p><strong>Status:</strong> Accepted 2026-05-16. <strong>Branch / PR:</strong> <code>feat/skills-6-reference-packages</code> (PR #115). <strong>Spec:</strong> <code>docs/superpowers/specs/2026-05-16-skills-6-reference-packages-design.md</code>. <strong>Plan:</strong> <code>docs/superpowers/plans/2026-05-16-skills-6-reference-packages.md</code>. <strong>Depends on:</strong> ADR-0025 (Skills-1), ADR-0026 (Skills-2), ADR-0027 (Skills-3), ADR-0028 (Skills-4), ADR-0029 (Skills-5).</p> <h2 id="context-32"><a class="header" href="#context-32">Context</a></h2> <p>Final sub-project of ROADMAP §16. Skills-1 through Skills-5 built the infrastructure; Skills-6 ships the <strong>content</strong> that turns the infrastructure into a complete, usable product:</p> <ul> <li>3 exemplary skill packages under <code>skills/</code> (critic, fact-checker, pr-reviewer) covering pure-prompt / fs.read / process.spawn axes.</li> <li>6 mdBook documentation pages filling all four Diátaxis quadrants.</li> <li>9 end-to-end integration tests proving the user story works in CI across Linux, macOS, Windows.</li> </ul> <p>After Skills-6, a new contributor can clone tau, build it, install a reference skill, render it, and export it back to Anthropic format — the entire Skills track makes sense end-to-end without prior knowledge.</p> <h2 id="decision-26"><a class="header" href="#decision-26">Decision</a></h2> <p>Three locked decisions:</p> <h3 id="d1--three-reference-skills-covering-three-capability-axes"><a class="header" href="#d1--three-reference-skills-covering-three-capability-axes">D1 — Three reference skills covering three capability axes</a></h3> <ul> <li><code>critic</code> (no capabilities) → Anthropic-roundtrip proof</li> <li><code>fact-checker</code> (fs.read on <code>${SKILL_DIR}/references/**</code>) → substitution + multi-file</li> <li><code>pr-reviewer</code> (process.spawn on git + rg) → third axis</li> </ul> <p>Rejected: 1-skill (too minimal) and 2-skill (skips the process.spawn axis).</p> <h3 id="d2--add-only-no-refactor-of-existing-tempdir-test-fixtures"><a class="header" href="#d2--add-only-no-refactor-of-existing-tempdir-test-fixtures">D2 — Add-only: no refactor of existing tempdir test fixtures</a></h3> <p>Skills-1–5 inline-synthesize critic fixtures in 10+ test files. Refactoring them to reference <code>skills/critic/</code> would risk subtle regressions and merge conflicts with parallel Claude sessions for marginal benefit. Skills-6 ADDS new integration tests against the in-tree skills; existing fixtures stay as-is.</p> <h3 id="d3--full-diátaxis-mdbook-documentation"><a class="header" href="#d3--full-diátaxis-mdbook-documentation">D3 — Full Diátaxis mdBook documentation</a></h3> <p>mdBook is already wired with the four Diátaxis quadrants (tutorials / how-to / reference / explanation). Skills-6 fills each quadrant: tutorial (narrative walkthrough), 3 how-to recipes, manifest schema reference, two-layer architecture explanation. Auto-deploys to GitHub Pages via PR #67's existing workflow.</p> <p>Rejected: in-repo README only (under-invests in user-facing surface); how-to + reference only (lacks tutorial narrative + explanation anchoring).</p> <h2 id="alternatives-considered-23"><a class="header" href="#alternatives-considered-23">Alternatives considered</a></h2> <ul> <li>1-skill scope (just critic). Rejected: doesn't prove capability story.</li> <li>2-skill scope (critic + fact-checker, no pr-reviewer). Rejected: skips the process.spawn capability axis.</li> <li>Refactor existing test fixtures. Rejected: 10+ files touched, refactor risk, merge-conflict risk.</li> <li>Separate <code>tau-skills</code> git repo. Rejected: in-tree is fine for proof-of-concept; external repo addressable when external versioning needs emerge.</li> <li>In-repo README only. Rejected: mdBook is already wired + auto-deploys.</li> <li>Tutorial-only docs. Rejected: reference + explanation are load-bearing for authoring + understanding.</li> <li><code>tau skill new <name></code> scaffolding command. Rejected: useful but separate sub-project; not blocking the user story Skills-6 ships.</li> </ul> <h2 id="consequences-28"><a class="header" href="#consequences-28">Consequences</a></h2> <ul> <li><strong>New top-level <code>skills/</code> directory</strong> (sibling to <code>crates/</code>). Future reference skills land here.</li> <li><strong>New <code>docs/tutorials/build-your-first-skill.md</code></strong>, three <code>docs/how-to/</code> recipes, <code>docs/reference/skill-manifest-schema.md</code>, <code>docs/explanation/two-layer-skills.md</code>. All indexed in <code>docs/SUMMARY.md</code>.</li> <li><strong>9 new integration tests</strong> across <code>crates/tau-pkg/tests/</code> and <code>crates/tau-cli/tests/</code>. Existing tests untouched.</li> <li><strong><code>.gitattributes</code></strong> forces LF on <code>skills/**/SKILL.md</code> to keep the byte-identical export roundtrip test passing on Windows.</li> <li><strong>No new external dependencies. No CI changes.</strong> The new tests run under the existing <code>test-stable</code> matrix.</li> </ul> <h2 id="closes-roadmap-16"><a class="header" href="#closes-roadmap-16">Closes ROADMAP §16</a></h2> <p>Skills-6 is the final sub-project of the Skills track. ROADMAP §16 is complete after this PR merges. Future Skills work is additive (more reference packages, <code>tau skill new</code>, marketplace, etc.) and sits outside §16.</p> <h2 id="references-17"><a class="header" href="#references-17">References</a></h2> <ul> <li>Spec: <code>docs/superpowers/specs/2026-05-16-skills-6-reference-packages-design.md</code></li> <li>Plan: <code>docs/superpowers/plans/2026-05-16-skills-6-reference-packages.md</code></li> <li>Predecessor ADRs: 0025 (foundation), 0026 (install pipeline), 0027 (discovery), 0028 (runtime invocation), 0029 (Anthropic interop)</li> <li>ROADMAP §16</li> </ul> <div style="break-before: page; page-break-before: always;"></div><h1 id="tau-dev-environment--linux-pre-commit--pre-push-gate"><a class="header" href="#tau-dev-environment--linux-pre-commit--pre-push-gate">tau dev environment — Linux pre-commit + pre-push gate</a></h1> <p>Goal: catch cross-platform build/runtime issues locally before pushing, so CI is confirmation rather than discovery. Also unblocks local debugging of F task 6.5 follow-ups (strict_net_filter integration test hang, Container-adapter network filtering).</p> <p>This iteration covers <strong>Linux only</strong> (running on Apple Silicon Mac). Windows + macOS legs are deferred to follow-up PRs.</p> <h2 id="tldr--one-time-setup"><a class="header" href="#tldr--one-time-setup">TL;DR — one-time setup</a></h2> <pre><code class="language-bash"># 1. Use rustup, not Homebrew rust (see "Toolchain setup" below if you have Homebrew rust installed). # rustup honors rust-toolchain.toml and auto-provisions cross-targets. # 2. Install tools (FOSS only) brew install lefthook podman brew install filosottile/musl-cross/musl-cross # for cross-compile-check (x86_64 included by default) # 3. Initialize Podman's hidden Linux VM (--rootful required for caps) podman machine init --cpus 4 --memory 8192 --rootful podman machine start # 4. Wire git hooks lefthook install # 5. Verify lefthook run pre-commit --all-files # ~30-60s, must exit 0 lefthook run pre-push --all-files # ~3-5min cold, must exit 0 </code></pre> <p>After this, every <code>git commit</code> runs the fast checks; every <code>git push</code> runs the deep Linux gate.</p> <h2 id="toolchain-setup--rustup-not-homebrew-rust"><a class="header" href="#toolchain-setup--rustup-not-homebrew-rust">Toolchain setup — rustup, not Homebrew rust</a></h2> <p>This project requires the rustup-managed Rust toolchain. <code>rust-toolchain.toml</code> declares the channel, components, and cross-compile targets that rustup auto-provisions.</p> <p><strong>If you have Homebrew rust installed, remove it before installing rustup:</strong></p> <pre><code class="language-bash">which cargo # should be ~/.cargo/bin/cargo # if it shows /opt/homebrew/bin/cargo, fix below brew list rust 2>/dev/null && brew uninstall rust curl --proto '=https' --tlsv1.2 -sSf https://sh.rustup.rs | sh # Restart your shell, or `source ~/.cargo/env`. which cargo # now ~/.cargo/bin/cargo cargo --version # should NOT say "(Homebrew)" </code></pre> <p>If you can't or won't uninstall Homebrew rust, ensure <code>~/.cargo/bin</code> precedes <code>/opt/homebrew/bin</code> in <code>$PATH</code>:</p> <pre><code class="language-bash">echo 'export PATH="$HOME/.cargo/bin:$PATH"' >> ~/.zshrc source ~/.zshrc which cargo # confirm rustup's cargo wins </code></pre> <p>The <code>check-linux-x86</code> pre-commit step requires the musl stdlib for the <code>x86_64-unknown-linux-musl</code> target. Homebrew rust doesn't ship this stdlib; rustup auto-installs it from <code>rust-toolchain.toml</code>'s <code>targets</code> list. Skipping this prerequisite means <code>check-linux-x86</code> will fail with "can't find crate for <code>core</code>".</p> <h2 id="architecture"><a class="header" href="#architecture">Architecture</a></h2> <pre><code>┌──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐ │ Apple Silicon Mac (host) │ │ │ │ git commit ──── lefthook pre-commit ─── ~30-60s (host, no VM) │ │ • cargo fmt --all -- --check │ │ • cargo clippy --workspace --all-targets │ │ • cargo nextest run --workspace --all-targets │ │ • cargo check --target x86_64-unknown-linux-musl│ │ │ │ git push ─────── lefthook pre-push ──── ~3-5min (Linux VM) │ │ │ │ ┌────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐ │ │ │ Podman machine (Linux VM, persistent) │ │ │ │ │ │ │ │ ephemeral container per pre-push run: │ │ │ │ podman run --rm │ │ │ │ --cap-add SYS_ADMIN --cap-add NET_ADMIN │ │ │ │ --security-opt seccomp=unconfined │ │ │ │ --security-opt apparmor=unconfined │ │ │ │ -v $WORKSPACE:/workspace │ │ │ │ -v cargo-cache:/usr/local/cargo/registry │ │ │ │ -v target-cache:/workspace/target/lefthook-podman │ │ │ │ rust:1.82-bookworm │ │ │ │ bash -c 'cargo nextest run --workspace --all-targets' │ │ │ └────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘ │ └──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘ </code></pre> <h2 id="interactive-linux-debugging"><a class="header" href="#interactive-linux-debugging">Interactive Linux debugging</a></h2> <p>When you need to investigate a test failure or reproduce a bug interactively (e.g., the strict_net_filter integration test hang from F task 6.5 follow-ups), use the same image and caps as the gate, just with <code>bash</code> instead of <code>cargo nextest</code>:</p> <pre><code class="language-bash">podman run -it --rm \ --cap-add SYS_ADMIN --cap-add NET_ADMIN \ --security-opt seccomp=unconfined \ --security-opt apparmor=unconfined \ -v "$PWD":/workspace:Z \ -v cargo-cache:/usr/local/cargo/registry \ -v target-cache:/workspace/target/lefthook-podman \ -w /workspace \ docker.io/library/rust:1.82-bookworm \ bash </code></pre> <p>Inside the container, <code>apt-get install -y iproute2 nftables</code> then run cargo commands directly. Same kernel, same caps, same crate cache as the automated gate — what fails interactively will fail in the gate, and vice versa.</p> <h2 id="bypassing-the-gate-emergencies-only"><a class="header" href="#bypassing-the-gate-emergencies-only">Bypassing the gate (emergencies only)</a></h2> <pre><code class="language-bash">git commit --no-verify # skip pre-commit git push --no-verify # skip pre-push </code></pre> <p>Don't do this routinely. The gate exists so CI doesn't have to find the bugs.</p> <h2 id="architecture-mismatch-known-gaps"><a class="header" href="#architecture-mismatch-known-gaps">Architecture mismatch (known gaps)</a></h2> <p>Apple Silicon is arm64; CI Linux runners are x86_64. The local gate will catch:</p> <ul> <li>✅ All cfg-gating bugs (<code>cfg(unix)</code>, <code>cfg(target_os)</code>)</li> <li>✅ All build-time API mismatches (the <code>std::os::fd</code> class)</li> <li>✅ Most Linux runtime regressions (sandbox tests, IPC, syscall behavior on arm64 Linux)</li> <li>✅ Privilege drift (selective-cap regressions)</li> </ul> <p>The local gate will NOT catch:</p> <ul> <li>❌ Arch-specific runtime bugs that only manifest on x86_64 (struct alignment, atomic ordering, syscall numbers in raw asm — landlock syscall numbers differ between x86_64 and arm64 Linux)</li> <li>❌ glibc-version differences (Podman ships current Debian; CI ships Ubuntu)</li> <li>❌ Windows-specific issues (deferred to follow-up PR)</li> <li>❌ macOS-specific issues that require a fresh macOS VM (deferred indefinitely; Mac coverage stays via the host)</li> </ul> <p>These remaining gaps are caught by CI. The pre-push gate covers ~95% of the cross-platform pain points; CI handles the rest.</p> <h2 id="troubleshooting"><a class="header" href="#troubleshooting">Troubleshooting</a></h2> <p><strong><code>lefthook: command not found</code></strong>: open a new shell after <code>brew install lefthook</code> to pick up <code>$PATH</code> updates.</p> <p><strong><code>check-linux-x86</code> fails with "can't find crate for <code>core</code>"</strong>: Homebrew's <code>cargo</code> is shadowing rustup's shim on <code>$PATH</code>, and Homebrew rust doesn't ship the musl stdlib. Fix: see "Toolchain setup" above. Verify with <code>which cargo</code> — it should show <code>~/.cargo/bin/cargo</code>, not <code>/opt/homebrew/bin/cargo</code>.</p> <p><strong><code>podman machine</code> is non-rootful</strong>: privileged-style containers won't work. Recreate:</p> <pre><code class="language-bash">podman machine stop podman machine rm podman machine init --cpus 4 --memory 8192 --rootful podman machine start </code></pre> <p><strong>Pre-push hangs at apt-get</strong>: the container is a fresh Debian — <code>apt-get update</code> reaches Debian mirrors. If you're behind a corporate proxy, configure Podman to use it (<code>podman machine ssh</code> then add proxy env vars to <code>/etc/profile.d/</code>).</p> <p><strong>Pre-push fails with permission denied on a syscall</strong>: a test is using a cap outside the documented list. Either expand the cap list in <code>lefthook.yml</code> (with a justifying comment) or fix the test to not need that cap. Never silently widen to <code>--privileged</code> — that defeats the gate.</p> <p><strong>Pre-commit hook didn't run</strong>: check <code>.git/hooks/pre-commit</code> exists. If not, re-run <code>lefthook install</code>.</p> <p><strong>Cargo target dir collision</strong>: lefthook uses <code>target/lefthook/{fmt,clippy,test,check-linux}</code> and <code>target/lefthook-podman</code>. These don't collide with <code>target/main</code> (main agent) or <code>target/agent-*</code> (sub-agents) per <a href="../CLAUDE.html">CLAUDE.md Rule 1</a>. If you see lock contention, ensure your bare cargo invocations are using the right <code>CARGO_TARGET_DIR</code>.</p> <p><strong>Container-VM disk space fills up</strong>: <code>podman machine</code> defaults are conservative. If you hit "no space left on device", increase the machine disk size:</p> <pre><code class="language-bash">podman machine stop podman machine set --disk-size 100 podman machine start </code></pre> <p><strong>QEMU <code>rustc</code> SIGSEGV during compilation</strong>: the Podman container is running aarch64 Linux natively (not x86_64 emulation), so this shouldn't happen. If you've added <code>--platform linux/amd64</code> somewhere and hit rustc crashes, remove it — Apple Silicon QEMU x86_64 emulation is unstable for rustc workloads.</p> <h2 id="what-this-enables"><a class="header" href="#what-this-enables">What this enables</a></h2> <p>After this PR ships:</p> <ol> <li>F task 6.5 follow-up #2 (strict_net_filter integration test hang) becomes debuggable locally — <code>podman run -it ...</code> reproduces the privileged-Linux environment for interactive <code>gdb</code>/<code>strace</code> work.</li> <li>F task 6.5 follow-up #1 (Container-adapter network filtering) becomes debuggable locally via the same mechanism.</li> <li>The cfg(unix) / cfg(target_os) class of bug is caught at commit time, not CI time.</li> <li>Privilege drift is caught at commit/push time, not silently masked by CI's previous <code>--privileged</code>.</li> </ol> <h2 id="out-of-scope-follow-up-prs"><a class="header" href="#out-of-scope-follow-up-prs">Out of scope (follow-up PRs)</a></h2> <ul> <li><strong>Windows VM (UTM + Windows 11 ARM)</strong> — largest setup; tracked as PR2 candidate.</li> <li><strong>macOS VM (Tart)</strong> — Tart is Fair Source, not OSI FOSS; not pursued.</li> <li><strong>x86_64 Linux runtime via QEMU</strong> — too slow; CI provides x86_64 ground truth.</li> <li><strong>Pre-commit fix mode</strong> — the gate is verify-only (<code>cargo fmt -- --check</code>), not auto-rewrite (<code>cargo fmt</code>).</li> </ul> </main> <nav class="nav-wrapper" aria-label="Page navigation"> <!-- Mobile navigation buttons --> <div style="clear: both"></div> </nav> </div> </div> <nav class="nav-wide-wrapper" aria-label="Page navigation"> </nav> </div> <script> window.playground_copyable = true;
